# Journey to the West - Complete Bilingual Transcript (Episodes 1-108)

**Total Episodes:** 108

---

# Journey to the West · Chapter One: The Monkey

## ①

  From the beginning of time, a rock stood high on top of the mountain. The sun, the moon, heaven and earth, all worked their magic on the rock. One day the rock split open. Inside was a monkey. The monkey stood up and stretched. Suddenly powerful light shot from its eyes. For a moment the light reached the Cloud Palace in heaven.

## ②

  The Jade Emperor, ruler of heaven, sat up. He turned to one of his captains who was standing nearby.
  > "Find out what caused that light," said the Emperor.
  > "Yes, Your Majesty," said the captain.
  The captain rushed out of the hall. He looked out the southern gate of heaven and saw the monkey on earth below.

## ③

  The light was gone. But the captain had magical sight. He could see everything that had just happened.
  > "Interesting," said the captain.
  When the captain returned, the Jade Emperor asked, "What caused the light?"
  > "It was a monkey," said the captain.
  > "A monkey?" asked the Jade Emperor.
  > "Yes," said the captain. "He's on the Fruit and Flower Mountain down on earth. There had been a rock on the mountain. The monkey came from the rock."

## ④

  The light shone from the monkey's eyes. The Emperor thought for a moment and then shrugged.
  > "I'm not surprised. Amazing things happen when heaven and earth work together," he said.
  As time passed, the monkey learned to walk, run, and climb. He drank from streams and ate grasses and leaves. He gathered fruit and explored caves and mountain tops. He became friends with all the other monkeys and apes. At night, he slept under a cliff.

## ⑤

  One very hot morning, all the monkeys and apes were playing in the shade.
  > "It is so hot today!" cried one monkey. "Let's play in the stream."
  > "Good idea!" said another monkey.
  The monkeys and apes ran to the stream.

## ⑥

  The water rolled and bounced over the rocks. The monkeys jumped into the cool water. Everyone splashed and played. After a few minutes, one monkey scratched her head.
  > "We all love this stream," she said. "We drink from it, we swim in it, we know that it flows all the way to the ocean. But does anyone know where the stream begins?"
  They all looked at one another and shook their heads.

## ⑦

  > "We have nothing to do today," the monkey continued, "why don't we follow the stream to find its source?"
  > "That sounds like fun!" said another monkey.
  > "Let's go!" shouted a third monkey.
  Everyone jumped out of the water. They ran alongside the stream and swung from tree to tree.

## ⑧

  They jumped over rocks and climbed up steep cliffs. Higher and higher they went up the mountain until they reached an enormous waterfall. Mist filled the air. The water crashed down, roaring like thunder.
  > "I wonder what's behind that waterfall," said one monkey.
  > "Me too!" said a second monkey.
  But nobody could jump through it.
  > "Whoever can jump through and come back alive will be king," said one of the monkeys.
  > "Is anyone brave enough to try?" All the monkeys looked at one another. They shook their heads.
  > "I'm not going to try," said a tall monkey.
  > "Me neither," said a short monkey.

## ⑨

  A voice called out.
  > "I'll do it!"
  Everyone moved out of the way as the speaker stepped forward. It was the monkey.
  > "Are you sure?" they asked.
  > "It looks dangerous," someone said.
  The monkey laughed.
  > "I'm not afraid of anything. And when I come back, I will be king."

## ⑩

  Monkey took a deep breath and leaped into the waterfall. He splashed through the waterfall and landed in a large cave. His eyes opened wide. The cave was filled with bamboo, trees and beautiful flowers.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一章：石猴出世

## ①

  从远古开始，一块石头高耸于山顶。太阳、月亮、天地都对这块石头施展魔力。一天，石头裂开，里面是一只猴子。猴子站起来伸展身体，突然，强大的光芒从双眼射出。片刻间，光芒直达天宫的云殿。

## ②

  玉皇大帝端坐在天宫宝座上。他转向旁边站着的一位天将。
  > "查清楚那光芒是什么原因。"皇帝说。
  > "是，陛下。"天将回答。
  天将冲出大殿，望向天宫南天门，看到了地上的猴子。

## ③

  光芒消失了。但那位天将拥有神通，能看清刚才发生的一切。
  > "有趣。"天将说。
  玉皇大帝等天将回来时问道："是什么引起的？"
  > "是一只猴子。"天将答道。
  > "是一只猴子？"玉皇大帝问。
  > "是的。"天将答，"它在人间的花果山上。山上原来有块石头，猴子就是从那块石头里出来的。"

## ④

  光芒从猴子的眼睛发出。皇帝想了一会儿，然后耸耸肩。
  > "我并不惊讶。当天地协同作用时，总会发生神奇之事。"他说。
  随着时间的流逝，猴子学会了走路、奔跑和攀爬。他喝溪水，吃草和树叶，采集水果，探索洞穴和山顶。他和其他所有的猴子、猿猴成为朋友。夜晚，他在悬崖下睡觉。

## ⑤

  一个炎热的早晨，所有的猴子、猿猴都在树荫下玩耍。
  > "今天太热了，"一只猴子叫道，"我们去溪水里玩吧。"
  > "好主意。"另一只猴子说。
  猴子们和猿猴们跑向溪边。

## ⑥

  溪水在岩石上翻滚跳跃。猴子们跳进清凉的水中，大家嬉戏打闹，溅起水花。几分钟后，一只猴子挠了挠头。
  > "我们都喜欢这条溪流，"她说，"我们喝它的水，在里面游泳，知道它一直流向大海。可是谁知道溪流的源头在哪里？"
  大家互相看了看，摇了摇头。

## ⑦

  > "我们今天没事做，"那只猴子接着说，"为什么不沿溪流找到它的源头呢？"
  > "听起来很有趣。"另一只猴子说。
  > "我们走吧！"第三只猴子叫道。
  大家跳出水面，沿着溪流奔跑，在树间荡秋千。

## ⑧

  他们跳过岩石，爬上陡峭的悬崖。越爬越高，直到一个巨大的瀑布挡在前面。空中雾气弥漫。水流轰鸣着冲下，如同雷鸣。
  > "我想知道瀑布后面是什么。"一只猴子说。
  > "我也是！"第二只猴子说。
  但谁也跳不进去。
  > "能跳过去并活着回来的，将成为大王。"一只猴子提议。
  > "有谁敢试试吗？" 所有的猴子面面相觑，摇了摇头。
  > "我不试。"一只高个子猴子说。
  > "我也不。"一只矮猴子说。

## ⑨

  > "我来！"一个声音叫道。
  大家纷纷让开，说话者走上前，正是那只猴子。
  > "你确定吗？"有人问。
  > "看起来很危险。"有人说道。
  猴子笑道："我什么都不怕。等我回来，我就要做大王。"

## ⑩

  猴子深吸一口气，跳进了瀑布。猴子穿过瀑布，落在一个大洞穴里。他的眼睛睁得大大的。洞穴里长满了竹子、树木和美丽的花朵。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Two: The Water Curtain Cave

## ①

  The monkey splashed through the waterfall and landed in a large cave. His eyes opened wide. The cave was filled with bamboo, trees, and beautiful flowers. Moss covered the walls. A stream flowed through the cave, and glowing light and mist filled the air. The monkey found a long table with bowls, cups, and plates, and a fireplace against one wall. Deeper in the cave, the monkey found bedrooms with cozy beds.
  Outside, the other monkeys and apes were looking at the waterfall.
  > "Do you think he made it through?" asked one monkey.

## ②

  > "No, I don't think so," said another monkey. "He probably got washed away down the river."
  Suddenly, with a splash, the monkey shot out of the waterfall and landed in front of the group.
  > "Your lives!" said the monkey, laughing. "Yes, and we are very lucky! I found a perfect home for all of us. Follow me!"
  The monkey jumped back through the water. Some of the monkeys scratched their heads.
  > "It still seems dangerous," said one monkey.
  > "Let's go!"
  He leaped through the waterfall. After that, another monkey jumped through. Then more followed. Soon all of the monkeys and apes were inside the cave. Everyone ran around, marveling at all the wonderful things.
  > "This cave is beautiful!" said one of the monkeys.
  Some of the monkeys and apes began fighting and arguing. They grabbed plates and bowls from one another. Others fought over the bedrooms.
  > "I saw this bed first!" yelled one monkey.
  > "I did!" yelled another.
  Monkey watched his friends for a moment and then folded his arms.
  > "Stop!" he called. All the monkeys and apes stopped what they were doing and looked at him.
  > "I found this cave for us," said Monkey. "That means I am now your king. Why aren't you bowing to me?"
  > "He's right!" they bowed to Monkey and said, "All hail the Monkey King!" Everyone else bowed. "Hail the Monkey King!" they shouted.

## ③

  They cheered. Many years went by. During the day, the monkeys and apes played in the forest and the stream. Every night they slept safely in their cave. One night the monkeys and apes held a huge feast.

## ④

  Fruit and nuts covered the table. The king's subjects danced and sang while music played. Monkey sat on his throne and smiled. But then his smile faded. Soon he was frowning.

## ⑤

  One of the monkeys rushed over.
  > "Your Majesty," he said, "you look sad. What's wrong?"

## ⑥

  Monkey sighed. "Our life here is perfect."
  > "Yes, that's true," said the monkey. "So why are you sad?"

## ⑦

  Monkey was quiet for a moment. Then he said, "Someday our lives will end. I wish this perfect life could last forever."
  The monkey's eyes lit up.

## ⑧

  > "Oh," said the monkey. "You want to live forever?"
  > "I do," said Monkey.

## ⑨

  The monkey rubbed his chin.
  > "Then you must study with a sage," he said. "Sages are very wise people. They can transform themselves into other animals. They can fly through the sky."

## ⑩

  > "And they know how to live forever," he added.
  Monkey smiled again.
  > "Where can I find a sage?" he asked.
  > "You must find a land with people," said the monkey. "That's where you'll find a sage."

## ⑪

  The next morning, Monkey built a raft and loaded food onto it. He pushed the raft into the stream and jumped on. As the raft began to float away, Monkey waved to his friends.

## ⑫

  > "Don't worry," he called. "After I learn how to live forever, I will return."

---

# 🇨🇳 第二章：水帘洞天

## ①

  猴子溅着水穿过瀑布，落进一个巨大的洞穴，双眼圆睁。洞穴里长满了竹子、树木和美丽的花朵。苔藓覆盖着岩壁。一条溪流穿洞而过，光芒与雾气弥漫空中。猴子发现一张长桌，摆着碗、杯、盘子，壁炉靠墙。洞穴深处，猴子发现了带有舒适床铺的卧室。

## ②

  外面，众猴正望着瀑布。
  > "你觉得他成功了吗？"一只猴子问。
  > "不，不会吧，"另一只猴子说，"他可能被河水冲走了。"
  突然，噗通一声，猴子从瀑布中射出，落在群猴面前。
  > "各位，"猴子笑着说道，"是的，我们非常幸运！我为全体同胞找到了一个完美的家园。跟我来！"
  猴子跳回水中。有些猴子挠了挠头。
  > "还是很危险，"一只猴子说。
  > "我们走！"
  于是，又有猴子跳了进去。接着，更多猴子跟上。很快，所有猴子、猿猴都进了洞穴。大家四处奔跑，欣赏着奇妙的一切。
  > "这个洞穴真美，"某只猴子说。
  一些猴子、猿猴开始争吵打闹，互相抢夺盘碗；另一些则为卧室争执。
  > "这张床是我先发现的，"一只猴子嚷道。
  > "明明是我，"另一只喊道。
  > "是我的！"
  猴子观察朋友们一会儿，然后双臂交叉，大喝一声。所有猴子、猿猴停下动作，望着他。
  > "这个洞穴是我为你们找到的，"猴子说，"从今往后，我就是你们的大王。还不行礼吗？"
  > "他说得对！"他们向猴子鞠躬，喊道："全体参见猴王！"其他人也跟着行礼："参见大王！"

## ③

  他们齐声欢呼。许多年过去了。白天，猴子们在森林和溪流中嬉戏，每晚都安全地睡在洞穴里。一天晚上，猴子们举行了一场盛大的宴会。

## ④

  水果和坚果铺满了桌子。猴王的臣子们随着音乐跳舞歌唱。猴王坐在宝座上微笑着，但笑容渐渐消失，很快皱起了眉头。

## ⑤

  某只猴子急忙上前。
  > "陛下，"他说，"您看起来不开心。怎么了？"

## ⑥

  猴王叹了口气。
  > "我们的生活在这里很完美。"
  > "确实如此，"那只猴子说，"那您为什么伤心？"

## ⑦

  猴王沉默片刻，然后说："总有一天我们的生命会终结。我希望这完美的生活能永远持续。"那只猴子的眼睛亮了起来。
  > "哦，"他说，"你想永生吗？"
  > "是的，"猴王说。

## ⑧

  那只猴子摸了摸下巴。
  > "那你必须去拜师学艺。仙人非常有智慧，能变化形态，还能在空中飞翔。"

## ⑨

  > "他们还懂得如何获得永生。"
  猴王再次微笑。
  > "我在哪里能找到仙人？"他问。
  > "你必须去有人烟的地方，"那只猴子说。"那才是你能找到仙人的地方。"

## ⑩

## ⑪

  第二天一早，猴王扎了一个木筏，装满食物。他把木筏推入溪流，跳了上去。木筏漂离时，猴王向朋友们挥手告别。

## ⑫

  > "别担心，"他喊道，"等我学会永生之术，我一定会回来。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Three: Subodhi
## ①

  The monkey drifted across the ocean for a long time and finally set foot on a new land. He traveled for many years, visiting towns and meeting many people, but never found a sage. Later he came to a dense forest on a high mountain. He followed a steep mountain trail and soon heard the sound of chopping. A woodcutter was chopping wood.
  > "Hello," called the monkey. "Are there any sages in these mountains?"

## ②

  The woodcutter dropped his axe.
  > "You're a monkey," he said. "And you can talk."
  > "Yes," replied the monkey. "I want to live forever. Do you know where I can find a sage?"
  The woodcutter scratched his head.
  > "Well, yes," he said. "Follow me."

## ③

  > "A sage named Subhuti lives on this mountain," said the woodcutter. "He is very wise."
  Monkey was excited.
  > "Where can I find him?" he asked.
  > "Just follow this trail and you will come to his home," said the woodcutter.
  > "Thank you," said the monkey.
  The monkey thanked the woodcutter and ran up the trail. Soon he saw a temple built into the side of the mountain. Subhuti was sitting with his students in the main room of his temple, meditating.

## ④

  Subhuti looked at his oldest student.
  > "Please go to the door," said Subhuti. "A new student is about to arrive. Let him in."
  The student looked confused.
  > "Okay, master," he said.
  The student got up and went to the door of the temple. He looked outside.
  > "Please come in," he said.

## ⑤

  Monkey stood outside the door and called, "I have heard that the great sage Subhuti is here."
  A moment later, Monkey was standing before the sage.
  > "I want to be your student," said Monkey.
  > "You're just a monkey," said Subhuti. "How can you be my student?"
  > "I may be a monkey," said Monkey, "but I can walk and talk and do many other things."

## ⑥

  > "I traveled almost 13 years to get here. I'm sure I can be your student," said Monkey.
  Subhuti stared at Monkey for a moment.
  > "Who are your parents?" he asked.
  > "I don't have parents," said Monkey. "I was born from a rock."
  > "Interesting," said Subhuti.

## ⑦

  > "You were probably created by heaven and earth. I may accept you as a student, but I need to give you a name," said Subhuti.
  He thought for a moment.
  > "I will call you Sun Wukong."
  For the next seven years, Sun Wukong lived in Subhuti's temple. The monkey spent his days meditating, listening to his teacher's lessons, and doing chores.
  One day, while Subhuti was giving a lesson, Wukong started to dance.
  Subhuti stood up.
  > "How dare you dance while I'm teaching?" he shouted.

## ⑧

  > "Master, please calm your anger," said Wukong. "I was so happy I couldn't help dancing."
  Subhuti's tone softened.
  > "You're happy?" he asked.
  > "Yes," said Wukong. "I love studying with you."
  Subhuti continued:
  > "Wukong, you've been here a long time. What would you like to learn from me?"

## ⑨

  Subhuti asked.
  Wukong shrugged.
  > "I don't know," he said. "You tell me what I should learn."
  > "I can teach you to tell the future," said Subhuti. "Would you like that?"
  > "Maybe," asked Wukong. "Will it make me live forever?"

## ⑩

  > "Of course not," replied Subhuti.
  > "Then forget it," said Wukong. "Teach me something else."
  > "How about some magic breathing exercises?" said Subhuti.
  > "Will they make me live forever?" asked Wukong.
  > "No," said Subhuti.

## ⑪

  > "Then I'm not interested," said Wukong.
  Subhuti flew into a rage. He stood up and knocked Wukong on the head three times, then stormed out of the room.
  > "Wukong," said another student, "you are very rude to Master."
  The other students all agreed.

## ⑫

  Wukong, however, smiled. None of the other students knew why.
  > "Let's all slowly reveal our true forms," said Wukong.
  Another student chimed in, "Alright, let's show our forms."
  Yet another student said, "Okay."
  Afterwards, each displayed their abilities, cheering together.

---

# 🇨🇳 第三章：菩提祖师

## ①

  猴子在海上漂泊了很久，终于踏上一片新大陆。他走了许多年，游历城镇，遇见许多人，却始终未遇仙人。后来他来到茂林深山，沿着陡峭山路前行，不久便听见砍柴声。一位樵夫正在砍柴。
  > "你好，"猴子叫道，"这山里可有什么仙人？"

## ②

  樵夫放下斧头。
  > "你是一只猴子，"他说，"而且你会说话。"
  > "是的，"猴子回答，"我想长生不老。你知道哪里能找到仙人吗？"
  樵夫挠了挠头。
  > "嗯，有。跟我来。"

## ③

  > "这山上有位仙人叫须菩提，非常高明。"
  猴子兴奋地问：
  > "他在哪儿？"
  > "沿着这条路走，就能到他住处，"樵夫说。
  > "谢谢。"猴子道谢后沿路跑去。
  不久，见一座寺庙嵌在山腰上。须菩提正与弟子们在寺中打坐。

## ④

  须菩提看向年长的弟子。
  > "去开门，"须菩提说，"有新弟子到了，请进。"
  弟子一脸茫然。
  > "师父，好的。"
  弟子起身走到寺门前，探望一番后说："请进。"

## ⑤

  猴子在门外喊道："晚辈听说须菩提大仙在此。"
  片刻，猴子便站到仙人面前。
  > "我想做您的弟子，"猴子说。
  > "你只是一只猴，"须菩提道，"如何能做我的弟子？"
  > "我虽是猴，却能走、能言，还会许多伎俩。"

## ⑥

  > "我走了将近十三年才到这儿，一定能成为好弟子。"
  须菩提盯着猴子瞧了一会儿。
  > "你父母是谁？"他问。
  > "我没有父母，"猴子说，"我是从石头里蹦出来的。"
  > "有趣。"

## ⑦

  须菩提说道："你应是天地所生。我可收你为徒，不过得给你取个名字。"
  他想片刻。
  > "你就叫孙悟空吧。"
  此后七年，孙悟空住在须菩提的寺庙里，每日打坐、听课、劳作。一日，须菩提讲经时，悟空高兴得手舞足蹈。须菩提起身怒喝：
  > "你怎敢在我讲学时跳舞？"

## ⑧

  > "师父息怒，"悟空忙说，"弟子太高兴，忍不住舞了起来。"
  须菩提语气稍缓。
  > "你很开心？"他问。
  > "是的，"悟空道，"弟子爱极了学习。"
  须菩提又道：
  > "悟空，你来了这么久，想跟我学点什么？"

## ⑨

  须菩提问。
  悟空耸耸肩。
  > "弟子不知，请师父示知。"
  > "那我教你未卜先知如何？"须菩提说。
  > "能长生吗？"悟空问。
  > "也许吧，"悟空说，"这能长生不老吗？"

## ⑩

  > "不能。"须菩提答。
  > "那算了，"悟空说，"教点别的。"
  > "嗯，教你些呼吸法术如何？"须菩提道。
  > "能长生吗？"悟空问。
  > "不能。"须菩提皱眉道。

## ⑪

  > "那我更没兴趣了。"悟空说。
  须菩提大怒，起身在悟空头上连敲三下，然后拂袖离去。
  > "悟空，"有弟子斥责，"你对师父太无礼了。"
  其他弟子纷纷附和。

## ⑫

  悟空却笑了。众人皆不知其意。
  > "咱们慢慢显形吧，"悟空说。
  另一弟子也应和："好，咱们显形吧。"
  又有弟子说："好。"
  随后大家各自展现本领，齐声喝彩。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Four: Secret Formulas

## ①

  That night, after the other students went to bed, Wukong stayed awake. At three o'clock in the morning, he crept quietly through the dark temple and entered Subhuti's room.
  > "Wukong, what are you doing here?" asked the sage.
  > "I understood your secret message," said Wukong. "You hit me on the head three times. That meant you wanted me to visit you at three o'clock. Now, will you teach me how to live forever?"
  Subhuti smiled faintly.
  > "I knew you would understand. Tell the other students to leave."
  Subhuti whispered into Wukong's ear. The sage whispered prayers and secret formulas about the universe and nature. As the monkey listened to his teacher's words, powerful light filled the room. Now Wukong knew how to live forever.

## ②

  For the next few years, Wukong meditated and practiced the secret formulas. While the other students slept at night, Wukong stayed up. Soon his mind and body became powerful; he could change shape, transform into other animals, and soar through the sky on clouds.

## ③

  One day, all the students were sitting outside.
  > "Wukong," said one student, "you've been busy lately."
  > "That's true," said another student, "what have you been doing?"
  > "I've been meditating and practicing secret formulas," answered Wukong.
  > "Secret formulas?" asked the first student.
  Everyone looked very interested and leaned in closer to Wukong.
  > "Yes," said the monkey. "Our master taught them to me."
  > "He did?" said a student. "You must be special. He doesn't teach those formulas to everyone. What did he teach you?"
  Wukong smiled.
  > "He taught me how to live forever. He also taught me how to change into other things."
  > "Show us what you can do," said the students.

## ④

  Wukong stood up. He muttered a spell and made a sign with his hands. Suddenly—POOF!—the monkey was gone. In his place stood an enormous pine tree.
  > "What do you think?" came a curious voice from the tree.
  The students clapped and cheered.
  > "That's amazing!" said one. "The monkey is truly powerful," said another.
  The noise disturbed Subhuti. He ran outside and saw the enormous pine tree.
  > "What's going on out here?" he shouted.
  Everyone stopped cheering. Wukong quickly turned back into himself. Subhuti's eyes flashed with anger.
  > "Everyone but Wukong, go inside!" he yelled.

## ⑤

  Subhuti waited for the other students to leave.
  > "I taught you the secret formulas so you could live forever," said the sage, "not so you could show off."
  > "I'm sorry," said Wukong.
  Subhuti continued.
  > "Now all the students have seen what you can do. They will want to know how to do it too. If you don't tell them, they might harm you. It's not safe for you to stay here any longer. You must go."
  Wukong started to cry.
  > "But Master, where will I go?"
  > "Go back to the Mountain of Flowers and Fruit," said Subhuti.
  > "But you taught me so much," said Wukong. "I must repay you first."
  > "You don't need to repay me," said Subhuti. "Just try to stay out of trouble."
  The sage looked at Wukong for a moment.
  > "I can see you will do evil things someday. Don't tell anyone you are my student. Now go."
  Wukong hung his head.
  > "Goodbye, Master."
  He leaped onto a cloud and left.

## ⑥

  After a short journey, Wukong arrived at the Mountain of Flowers and Fruit.
  > "I have returned!" he called.

---

# 🇨🇳 第四章：秘传法术

## ①

  那晚其他弟子睡下后，悟空仍醒着。凌晨三点，他悄悄潜入黑暗的寺庙，进入须菩提的房间。
  > "悟空，你在这里做什么？"仙人问道。
  > "我明白您的暗号，"悟空说，"您在我头上打了三下，意思是让我三点钟来找您。现在，您愿意教我长生不老之法吗？"
  须菩提微微一笑。
  > "我早知道你领会了。让这些弟子都离开。"
  须菩提凑近悟空耳边，传授关于宇宙与自然的咒语和秘法。当猴子聆听师父教导时，强大的光芒充满房间。此刻悟空已明了长生之道。

## ②

  接下来的几年里，悟空打坐修炼秘法。其他弟子夜间安睡时，悟空却总在修行。不久他的身心变得强大，能够变化形态，还可化身为各类动物，驾云在天空翱翔。

## ③

  一天，所有弟子正在户外坐着。
  > "悟空，"一名弟子说，"你最近很忙啊。"
  > "确实，"另一名弟子说，"你都在做什么？"
  > "我一直在打坐、修炼秘法，"悟空回答。
  > "秘法？"第一名弟子问。
  众人显得非常感兴趣，纷纷凑近悟空。
  > "是的，"猴子说，"师父把这些教给了我。"
  > "真的吗？"有弟子说，"你一定特别受宠。师父可不会把这些秘法教给任何人。他都教你什么了？"
  悟空微微一笑。
  > "他教我如何长生不老，还教我如何变化成其他事物。"
  > "给我们展示一下你的本领吧，"弟子们说。

## ④

  悟空站起身，念动咒语，双手结印。忽然——啪！猴子消失无踪，取而代之的是一棵高大的松树。
  > "怎么样？"树中传来好奇的声音。
  弟子们纷纷喝彩。
  > "太神奇了！"一名弟子说。
  > "这只猴子真是力大无穷，"另一名说道。
  喧闹声惊动了须菩提。他跑出来看到那棵巨大的松树。
  > "外面怎么回事？"他喝道。
  众人停止欢呼。悟空迅速变回原形。须菩提眼中怒火闪动。
  > "除了悟空，其他人统统进去！"他吼道。

## ⑤

  须菩提等其他弟子离开。
  > "我教你秘法是为了让你长生不老，"仙人说，"不是为了让你炫耀。"
  > "对不起，"悟空说道。
  须菩提继续说道。
  > "如今所有弟子都看到了你的本事。他们也会想知道如何做到。若你不告诉他们，他们可能会加害于你。你再留在这里不安全了。你必须离开。"
  悟空开始哭泣。
  > "可是师父，我该去哪里？"
  > "回你的花果山去吧，"须菩提说。
  > "可您教会了我这么多，"猴子说，"我必须先报答您。"
  > "你不必报答我，"须菩提道，"只要今后少惹麻烦就行。"
  仙人注视悟空片刻。
  > "我能看出你将来会做恶事。不要告诉任何人你是我的弟子。去吧。"
  悟空低下头。
  > "弟子告辞，师父。"
  他纵身跳上云朵，离去。

## ⑥

  经过一段短途飞行，悟空回到了花果山。
  > "我回来啦！"他高声喊道。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Five: The Demon of Chaos

## ①

  > "Your Majesty!" the king reported. "Something terrible has happened."
  > "What happened here?" asked Wukong.
  Several more monkeys and apes gathered around, looking frightened.
  > "A demon attacked us," said the king. "We tried to fight him, but he was too powerful. He stole most of our things and kidnapped many of our people."
  Wukong was furious.
  > "Who is he? Where does he live?" he demanded.
  > "He calls himself the Demon of Chaos," replied the king. "He came from the north."

## ②

  > "Wait here," ordered Wukong. "I will deal with the demon."
  > "The demon is very powerful," the king warned.
  > "I learned many things from a sage," Wukong replied. "I am now as powerful as a god. I am not afraid of any demon. I'll be back soon."
  He leaped into the air and flew north. His subjects stared in amazement.
  > "Our king can fly!" exclaimed the king.

## ③

  Wukong soon spotted a gloomy mountain with dark clouds hanging over it.
  > "That looks like a demon's lair," he thought.
  He landed on the mountain and found a cave. Two guards stood at the entrance, practicing sword fighting.
  > "I am the king of the Fruit and Flower Mountain!" Wukong yelled. "The Demon of Chaos attacked my subjects. I seek revenge!"
  The guards shrieked and ran into the cave.

## ④

  The Demon of Chaos was sitting at a table, eating.
  > "Disaster!" one guard cried, running in.
  > "What sort of disaster?" asked the demon.
  > "There's a monkey outside," said the other guard. "He says he's the king of the Fruit and Flower Mountain. You attacked his subjects, and now he wants revenge."
  > "The monkeys on the Fruit and Flower Mountain spoke of a king," said the demon. "He left to find a sage. So he's back."
  The demon stood up.
  > "Does the monkey have any weapons?" he asked.
  > "No," replied the guard.
  > "Then bring me my armor and sword," ordered the demon.
  A moment later, the Demon of Chaos walked outside. He looked at Wukong and laughed.
  > "You're just a little monkey," he said.
  Wukong looked up at the huge demon.
  > "I am small," he said, "but I am more powerful than you can imagine. I am not afraid of you."
  The demon swung his sword. Wukong jumped out of the way and then pounced on the demon.
  Bam! Wukong hit the demon on the nose.

## ⑤

  > "Ah!" cried the demon.
  Wukong pulled out a handful of his own hair and blew on it. Each strand turned into a duplicate of Wukong, exactly like him. All at once, the duplicates attacked the demon, punching and kicking.
  > "What's going on?" the demon cried, trying to fight off the clones.
  > "It's a magic spell," said Wukong, smiling. "It's called 'Body Beyond the Body.'"
  The Demon of Chaos was soon destroyed.

## ⑥

  Wukong chased away the guards and then entered the cave. He found all the monkeys and apes that the demon had kidnapped. When they saw him, they cheered.
  > "Your Majesty!" they cried. "You came to rescue us!"
  Wukong smiled.
  > "I will take you home," he said.

## ⑦

  The next morning, Wukong woke early.
  > "Other demons might attack us," he thought. "We must be ready to defend ourselves."
  He spent the day teaching his subjects how to fight. They practiced with swords and spears. Before long, the monkeys and apes had become a fierce army.
  > "No demon will dare bother us now," said the king.
  > "That's true," said Wukong, "but there's still one problem."
  > "What's that?" asked the king.
  > "I can't use any of these weapons," said Wukong. "They're too light for me."

---

# 🇨🇳 第五章：混沌魔王

## ①

  > "陛下！"猴王跑来报告，"出大事了。"
  > "这里发生了什么事？"悟空问猴王。
  又有几只猴子、猿猴围拢过来，他们一脸惊恐。
  > "有个妖怪袭击我们，"猴王说，"我们试图抵抗，但他太厉害了。他抢走了大部分财物，还绑架了许多同伴。"
  悟空勃然大大怒。
  > "他是谁？住在哪里？"
  > "他自称混沌魔王，"猴王道，"从北方来的。"

## ②

  > "你们在这儿等着，"悟空下令，"我来对付那妖怪。"
  > "那妖怪非常厉害，"猴王警告道。
  > "我从仙人那里学了好多本事，"悟空回答，"我现在法力如神，什么妖怪都不怕。我很快就回来。"
  他腾空而起，向北飞去。臣民们惊讶得目瞪口呆。
  > "我们的国王会飞啊！"猴王惊叹道。

## ③

  悟空很快发现一座阴暗的山峰，乌云笼罩。
  > "这定是妖魔的巢穴，"他想。
  悟空降落到山上，找到一个洞穴。洞口站着两个守卫，正在练习剑术。
  > "我是花果山之王！"悟空大喝道，"混沌魔王袭击我的子民，我要报仇！"
  守卫们尖叫着跑进洞中。

## ④

  混沌魔王正坐在桌旁用餐。
  > "大事不好！"一名守卫慌张跑入。
  > "什么灾难？"魔王问。
  > "洞外有只猴子，"另一名守卫说，"他说他是花果山之王。您袭击了他的子民，他要来复仇。"
  > "花果山的猴子们曾说起有位国王，"魔王道，"他离开去寻访仙人了。原来他回来了。"
  魔王站起身。
  > "那猴子有武器吗？"
  > "没有，"守卫答。
  > "那就给我拿盔甲和剑来，"魔王吩咐。
  片刻后，混沌魔王走出洞外。他看着悟空，冷笑起来。
  > "你不过是一只小猴子，"他说。
  悟空仰视着庞大的魔王。
  > "我虽小，"悟空道，"但我的力量超乎你想象。我不怕你。"
  魔王挥剑劈来。悟空灵巧躲开，随即扑向魔王。
  砰！悟空一拳击中魔王的鼻子。

## ⑤

  > "啊！"魔王惨叫一声。
  悟空拔下一把毛发，吹了一口气。每一根毛发立刻变成一只假悟空，一模一样。霎时间，假悟空们群起进攻，拳打脚踢。
  > "怎么回事？"魔王惊慌失措，试图抵挡众多假悟空。
  > "这是我的法术，"悟空笑道，"名叫'身外化身'。"
  混沌魔王很快就被消灭了。

## ⑥

  悟空赶走守卫，进入洞穴。他发现所有被绑架的猴子、猿猴。他们见到悟空，纷纷欢呼。
  > "大王！"猴子、猿猴们齐声喊道，"您回来救我们了！"
  悟空微笑。
  > "我送你们回家。"

## ⑦

  第二天一早，悟空早早醒来。
  > "其他妖魔可能还会来犯，"他想，"我们必须做好防御准备。"
  悟空花了一整天教导子民们战斗技巧。他们练习刀剑和长矛。不久，猴子、猿猴们成了一支勇猛之师。
  > "现在没有妖魔敢来骚扰我们了，"猴王说。
  > "是的，"悟空道，"但还是有个问题。"
  > "什么问题？"猴王问。
  > "我们现有的兵器我都没法用，"悟空说。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Six: The Dragon King

## ①

  > "What's wrong with our swords and spears?" asked the king.
  > "They're fine for ordinary monkeys and apes," said Wukong, "but I am very strong and need a much heavier weapon."
  The king thought for a moment.
  > "A Dragon King lives at the bottom of the Eastern Sea," he said. "Maybe he has a weapon you can use."
  > "That's a good idea," said Wukong. "I'll go right away and be back soon."
  He cast a quick spell so he could breathe underwater, then dived into the stream. He swam to the ocean and went deeper and deeper. Soon he arrived at a grand palace.

## ②

  The Dragon King and the Dragon Queen were sitting at a table, drinking tea. When Wukong walked in, the Dragon King looked over.
  > "Who are you?" asked the Dragon King.
  > "I am the king of the Fruit and Flower Mountain," replied Wukong. "My name is Sun Wukong."
  > "Nice to meet you," said the Queen. "Would you like some tea?"
  > "No, thank you," said Wukong. "I need a heavy weapon because my strength is like that of a god. I would like one of yours."
  > "Well," said the Dragon King, "I suppose we could find a weapon for you."
  He glanced at a turtle soldier.
  > "Find a heavy weapon for Sun Wukong."

## ③

  The turtle left the room. Soon he returned, slowly dragging an enormous sword. He dropped it and then fell, out of breath.
  Wukong picked up the sword with no trouble at all.
  Swish! Swish! He waved the sword through the air, pretending to fight.
  > "This sword is too light," said Wukong. "Find me a better weapon."

## ④

  > "This monkey is rude," the Dragon Queen whispered to her husband.
  > "You're right, dear," the Dragon King whispered back. "Let's find him something quickly so he'll leave."
  A few minutes later, several turtles and octopuses dragged an enormous spear into the room.
  > "There," said the Dragon King. "That looks like a very heavy weapon, right, Wukong?"
  Wukong lifted the spear and stabbed at the air a few times. He shook his head.
  > "This is still too light."
  The Dragon King snorted.
  > "That spear is very heavy. How can you say it's too light?"
  > "To me it's light," said Wukong. "Find me something else."
  > "We don't have anything else," said the Dragon King. "That's the heaviest weapon we have."
  Wukong stomped his foot.
  > "I'm not leaving until I get what I want!"
  > "This is an outrage!" cried the Dragon King.
  The Queen whispered to him again.
  > "What about the magical iron bar in the treasury? I'm sure that's heavy enough."
  > "We can't give you that," said the Dragon King. "It's a treasure from heaven."
  > "Who cares?" said the Queen. "I just want this monkey out of my palace."
  The Dragon King sighed.
  > "Wukong, we might have something heavy enough for you."
  > "Bring it here," said Wukong.
  > "We can't," replied the Dragon King. "It's too heavy for anyone to lift. But if you can lift it, we'll let you have it."
  > "Show me where it is," said Wukong.
  The group went to the treasury. In the center of the room stood an enormous iron pillar, radiating beams of golden light.
  > "That pillar was used to measure all the oceans and rivers," said the Dragon King.
  Wukong went closer and looked up at the massive piece of iron. The Dragon King folded his arms.
  > "If you can pick it up, you can have it."

## ⑤

---

# 🇨🇳 第六章：龙王相助

## ①

  > "我们的刀剑和长矛怎么了吗？"猴王问。
  > "它们对普通猴子、猿猴来说够用，"悟空说，"但我非常有力，需要更重的武器。"
  猴王思索片刻。
  > "东海龙王住在海底，"他说，"他也许有你能用的武器。"
  > "好主意，"悟空道，"我这就去，很快回来。"
  他念了一道咒语，以便在水中呼吸，然后潜入溪流，游向大海，越潜越深。不一会儿，来到一座宏伟的宫殿。

## ②

  龙王与龙后正坐在桌旁品茶。悟空走进来时，龙王抬眼望去。
  > "你是谁？"龙王问。
  > "我是花果山之王，"悟空答，"我叫孙悟空。"
  > "幸会，"龙后说道，"您要喝杯茶吗？"
  > "不用了，多谢，"悟空说，"我需要一件沉重的武器，因为我的力量如神一般。我想要你们的一件兵器。"
  > "好吧，"龙王道，"我派人给你找找看。"
  龙王看向一只龟将。
  > "给孙悟空找一件沉重的武器。"

## ③

  龟将退出房间。很快又回来了，慢慢拖着一把巨剑。他丢下剑，便累得气喘吁吁。
  悟空轻而易举地举起剑。
  嗖！嗖！他在空中挥舞了几下，假装战斗。
  > "这剑太轻了，"悟空道，"给我找件更好的。"

## ④

  > "这猴子真无礼，"龙后低声对丈夫说。
  > "你说得对，亲爱的，"龙王低声回应，"快点给他找件东西，让他赶紧走人。"
  几分钟后，几只海龟和章鱼拖着一杆巨矛进入房间。
  > "这个，"龙王说，"看起来是很沉的武器，对吧，悟空？"
  悟空举起长矛，朝空中刺了几下，摇摇头。
  > "还是太轻。"
  龙王哼了一声。
  > "那杆矛非常沉，你怎么说太轻？"
  > "对我来说，它还是轻，"悟空道，"再找别的。"
  > "我们没有什么别的了，"龙王说，"这是最重的武器了。"

## ⑤

  悟空跺跺脚。
  > "我拿不到想要的武器就不走！"
  > "真是无理取闹！"龙王怒道。
  龙后再次在他耳边低语。
  > "宝库里的那根定海神针呢？那肯定够沉。"
  > "我们不能给你，"龙王道，"那是天界的宝物。"
  > "谁在乎？"龙后说，"我只要这猴子离开我的宫殿。"
  龙王叹了口气。
  > "悟空，我们也许有足够沉的东西适合你。"
  > "拿来看看，"悟空说。
  > "我们拿不动，"龙王回答，"它太重了，没人能举起。但如果你能举起，我们就送给你。"
  > "带我去看看，"悟空道。
  一行人来到宝库。房间中央矗立着一根巨大的铁柱，金光闪闪。
  > "这根铁柱是用来测量四海四方的，"龙王说。
  悟空走近，仰望着巨大的铁块。龙王双手抱胸。
  > "如果你能拿得起来，就归你了。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seven: The Land of Darkness

## ①

  Wukong touched the iron pillar and felt it move.
  > "Hmm," he thought, "this piece of iron is truly magical. I bet it will do whatever I wish."
  > "Shrink!" commanded Wukong.
  The pillar shrank. Wukong was now just a little taller than before. He lifted it and swung it around.
  > "This is a perfect weapon for me," he said.
  > "I can't believe he can lift it," exclaimed the Dragon Queen.
  Wukong made the bar even smaller. It became as tiny as a needle. He placed it inside his ear.
  > "I've got what I want," said Wukong. "Goodbye."
  He turned to leave.
  > "He was very rude," said the Dragon Queen.
  The Dragon King clenched his fists.
  > "I'm going to report him to the Jade Emperor."

## ②

  Back at the Mountain of Flowers and Fruit, the others were amazed by Wukong's new weapon.
  > "No one will ever attack us again!" declared Wukong.
  The monkeys and apes cheered. They held a great feast that lasted until late at night. Wukong went to bed happily. But as he fell asleep, two spirits seized him.
  > "What are you doing?" demanded Wukong. "Let go of me!"
  He kicked and struggled, but the spirits dragged him out of the cave. They walked toward a dark and eerie city. A sign above the gate read: **Land of Darkness**.

## ③

  > "The Land of Darkness?" cried Wukong. "That's where people go when they die. I'm supposed to live forever!"
  He pulled his arms free.
  > "No way!" he roared. The iron bar quickly grew.
  Whack! He knocked out the first spirit. Crack! He knocked out the second.
  > "Who can stop me now?" he shouted.
  He marched toward the Palace of Darkness, swinging his iron bar. Demons and ghosts fled. A tall spirit stepped out of the palace.

## ④

  > "What's going on out here?" asked the spirit.
  > "Who are you?" demanded Wukong.
  > "I am the Judge of the Dead," replied the spirit. "Why are you causing all this trouble?"
  > "I want answers," said Wukong. "I was brought here. Tell me now!"
  The Judge raised his hands.
  > "If you were brought here, it means your time on earth is over."

## ⑤

  > "No way!" yelled Wukong. "I'm going to live forever!"
  The Judge looked nervous.
  > "Let's check the directory," he said. "The directory contains the name and age of every creature on earth. It states when each creature will die."

## ⑥

  Inside the palace, the Judge opened a large book.
  > "What is your name?" he asked.
  Wukong told him. The Judge flipped through the pages.
  > "Here it is," said the Judge. "It says: Sun Wukong, born from a rock 300 years ago. Died today."
  Wukong shook his head.
  > "No. I'm going to live forever."
  > "The directory isn't wrong," said the Judge. "You'll have to stay here now."

## ⑦

  Wukong raised his iron bar and glared at the Judge.
  > "Give me that book."
  The Judge hesitated.
  > "I can't give it to you."
  > "Now," said Wukong.
  The Judge handed the book to Wukong. Wukong pulled two of his hairs and blew on them. They turned into a brush and a jar of ink. He drew a line through his name.
  > "You can't do that!" cried the Judge.
  > "Yes, I can," said Wukong.
  Next, Wukong found the names of all the other monkeys and apes. He crossed out their names as well.
  > "Now I really will live forever," said Wukong. "And so will all of my subjects!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第七章：地府销籍

## ①

  悟空伸手摸了摸铁柱，感觉到它在移动。
  > "嗯，"他想，"这件铁器真是神奇。我敢打赌它会随我心意。"
  > "变小！"悟空命令道。
  铁柱立刻缩小。悟空的身高只比原来高一点。他举起铁柱，挥舞了两下。
  > "这对我来说简直是完美的武器，"他说。
  > "我简直不敢相信他竟然能举起来，"龙后惊叹道。
  悟空让铁棒变得更小。悟空小得如同一枚针。他将铁棒塞进耳朵里。
  > "我要的东西到手了，"悟空道，"告辞。"
  他转身离开。
  > "他太无礼了，"龙后说道。
  龙王握紧拳头。
  > "我要去禀告玉皇大帝。"

## ②

  回到花果山，众人对悟空的新武器惊讶不已。
  > "以后再也没谁敢攻击我们了！"悟空宣称。
  猴子、猿猴们齐声欢呼。他们举办了盛宴，一直热闹到深夜。悟空快活地上床睡觉。但刚入睡，两个小鬼抓住了他。
  > "你们干什么？"悟空喝问，"放开我！"
  他拳打脚踢，却仍被小鬼拖出洞府。他们走向一座阴暗诡异的城市，城门上挂着一块牌子：**地府**。

## ③

  > "地府？"悟空惊呼，"人死后才去的地方。我可是要永生不死的！"
  他猛地挣脱双臂。
  > "休想！"他吼道。铁棒迅速变长。
  砰！第一鬼被打晕。咔嚓！第二鬼也被打翻。
  > "现在谁能挡住我？"他喝道。
  他朝地府宫殿走去，一路挥舞铁棒。妖魔鬼怪四散奔逃。一个高大的鬼差从宫殿里走出来。

## ④

  > "外面乱哄哄的怎么回事？"鬼差问道。
  > "你是谁？"悟空喝问。
  > "我是阎王，"鬼差答，"你在此地胡闹什么？"
  > "我来问个明白，"悟空道，"我被带来这里，立刻告诉我！"
  阎王举起双手。
  > "如果你被带来这里，那就表示你在阳间的寿命已尽。"

## ⑤

  > "没门！"悟空吼道，"我要永生不死！"
  阎王有些慌张。
  > "我们查一下生死簿，"他说，"生死簿上记载着阳间每一个生灵的姓名和寿数，何时命终都有记录。"

## ⑥

  宫殿内，阎王翻开一本大书。
  > "你叫什么名字？"他问道。
  悟空告知。阎王翻阅书页。
  > "找到了，"阎王说，"上面写着：孙悟空，石头所生，三百年前出生，今日身亡。"
  悟空摇头。
  > "不，我要永生不死。"
  > "生死簿不会错，"阎王道，"你现在必须留在这里。"

## ⑦

  悟空举起铁棒，怒视阎王。
  > "把书给我。"
  阎王犹豫不决。
  > "我不能给你。"
  > "现在就给！"悟空喝道。
  阎王无奈，只得将书递上。悟空拔下两根毫毛，吹了一口气，毛发变成笔和墨汁。他用力划去自己的名字。
  > "你不能这样做！"阎王惊呼。
  > "我当然能，"悟空答道。
  接着，悟空又找到所有猴子、猿猴的名字，一一划去。
  > "这下我真的永生不死了，"悟空道，"我的所有子民也都能永生！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eight: A Job in Heaven

## ①

  The Jade Emperor was sitting on his throne in the Cloud Palace. A messenger ran into the court.
  > "Your Majesty!" he reported. "The Dragon King of the Eastern Sea requests an audience."
  > "Let him in," said the Emperor.
  The Dragon King entered and bowed.
  > "Your Majesty, I have a matter to report. Sun Wukong came to my palace and demanded I give him a weapon. He was very rude."
  Another messenger came in.
  > "The Judge of the Dead wishes to see you, Your Majesty."
  The Judge entered and bowed.
  > "There is a monkey named Sun Wukong who crossed out his name in the directory. I beg you to punish him."
  The Jade Emperor rubbed his chin.
  > "Who is this Sun Wukong? And how did he become so powerful?"
  The Emperor's captain stepped forward.
  > "Sun Wukong is the monkey who was born from a rock 300 years ago. I don't know how he became so powerful."
  > "I remember him now," said the Jade Emperor. "I don't care how powerful he is. He has caused too much trouble on earth. Gather troops and go down to the Fruit and Flower Mountain. I want Sun Wukong arrested."

## ②

  The spirit of Venus stepped forward.
  > "Your Majesty," said Venus. "Perhaps we could give Wukong a position here in heaven."
  The Jade Emperor raised his eyebrows.
  > "Why would we do that?"
  > "If he's here, we can keep an eye on him," said Venus. "It will be easy to keep him out of trouble."
  > "Very well," said the Emperor. "Invite Wukong to come and live in heaven. He will be put in charge of the royal peach garden."

## ③

  Wukong was telling his subjects about his adventure in the Land of Darkness.
  > "After I crossed out my name," he said, "I crossed out all of your names too. We will all live forever."
  The monkeys and apes cheered.
  When Wukong returned, he saw a spirit standing nearby. He pulled out his iron bar.
  > "Who are you?" he demanded.
  > "I am Venus," said the spirit. "I have an invitation from the Jade Emperor. He would like you to come and live in heaven."
  > "Wukong smiled. 'At last he has invited me!'"
  When Wukong arrived at the royal court in the Cloud Palace, he did not bow.
  > "You're supposed to bow before the Emperor," Venus whispered.

## ④

  > "I'm just as powerful as he is. Maybe he should bow before me."
  Everyone but the Jade Emperor gasped. Wukong looked at the Emperor.
  > "I'm glad you invited me. I guess you finally realized I should be living up here with all of you."
  > "Show some respect," said Venus quietly.
  The Jade Emperor looked at Venus and smiled.
  > "Wukong, I know you. He can be excused for not acting the right way," he said, looking at Wukong. "I am putting you in charge of the royal peach garden. You will have a home here in heaven. I hope you won't cause any more trouble."

## ⑤

  > "That sounds perfect," said Wukong.
  The next morning, a gardener showed Wukong the peach garden. Bright, glowing peaches hung from every branch.
  > "The peaches in this garden are not like peaches on earth," said the gardener. "These peaches take thousands of years to become ripe. Anyone who takes a bite of one will live forever."
  Each morning Wukong inspected the trees in the garden. He took his job very seriously.
  > "These peaches look delicious," he thought. He looked at the tree. He looked around. None of the gardeners were in sight.
  > "Maybe I'll eat one."

---

# 🇨🇳 第八章：天庭封官

## ①

  玉皇大帝正坐在云宫宝座上。一位使臣气喘吁吁跑进大殿。
  > "陛下，"他禀报道，"东海龙王求见。"
  > "让他进来，"皇帝说道。
  龙王进宫，躬身行礼。
  > "陛下，臣有一事禀告。孙悟空跑到我龙宫，强索兵器，态度极其无礼。"
  又来了一位使臣。
  > "阎君求见陛下。"
  阎君进来，鞠躬行礼。
  > "有一只名叫孙悟空的猴子，在生死簿上勾掉了自己的名字。恳请陛下治他的罪。"
  玉皇大帝抚摸下巴。
  > "这孙悟空究竟是何方神圣？竟有如此神通？"
  皇帝的将领站出来。
  > "孙悟空是三百年前从石头里诞生的那只猴子。我不知道他如何获得如此法力。"
  > "我想起来了，"玉帝说，"不管他有多厉害，他在人间惹是生非太多。集合天兵，下到花果山，把孙悟空给我抓来。"

## ②

  金星的仙灵走上前来。
  > "陛下，"金星说道，"也许我们可以给悟空在天庭安排一个职位。"
  玉皇大帝扬起眉毛。
  > "我们为何要这么做？"
  > "如果他在这里，我们可以就近监视他，"金星说，"这样容易防止他生事。"
  > "好，"玉帝道，"邀请悟空来天庭居住。就让他管理王母的蟠桃园。"

## ③

  悟空正在向子民们讲述他在地府的经历。
  > "我勾掉自己的名字后，"他说，"也把你们所有人的名字都勾掉了。我们大家都能长生不死了。"
  猴子、猿猴们欢呼雀跃。
  悟空返回来时，看见附近站着一位仙灵。他抽出铁棒。
  > "你是谁？"
  > "我是金星，"仙灵答道，"我受玉帝之邀，来请你上天庭居住。"
  > "悟空笑道，'他终于邀请我了！'"
  悟空来到云宫大殿时，并未行礼。
  > "见到陛下理应行礼，"金星小声提醒。

## ④

  > "我的法力与他相当，说不定他该向我行礼才是。"
  除玉帝外，所有人都倒吸一口凉气。悟空看着皇帝。
  > "很高兴你能邀请我。我想你终于意识到我该和你们一起住在天上了。"
  > "放尊重些，"金星低声说道。
  玉帝看了看金星，微微一笑。
  > "悟空，我了解你。他不懂规矩，姑且原谅。不过，"玉帝看着悟空，"我委派你管理蟠桃园。你在天庭已有居所。希望你不要再生事端。"

## ⑤

  > "听起来很不错，"悟空答道。
  第二天一早，一位园丁带悟空参观蟠桃园。光芒闪闪的桃子挂满枝头。
  > "这院子里的桃子与凡间不同，"园丁说，"这些桃子要经过千年方能成熟。任何人只要咬一口，就能长生不老。"
  悟空每天早上都要巡视园中桃树。他工作非常认真。
  > "这些桃子看起来真好吃，"他想。他看了看桃树，又环顾四周，不见园丁踪影。
  > "也许我可以尝一个。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Nine: The Peach Garden

## ①

  Wukong plucked a peach from a branch and bit into it. It was so juicy and sweet.

  He said, "It is delicious!" He ate another peach. And then he ate another one. Each morning after that, Wukong secretly ate more and more peaches. After eating, he climbed into a tree and took a nap. Time went by, and Wukong enjoyed his life in heaven.

## ②

  Meanwhile, the queen of heaven was busy. It was almost time for the annual peach festival. She called for her maidens, Red Gown and Blue Gown.

> "How may we help you?" asked Red Gown.

> "The peach festival is tomorrow," said the queen. "All the important gods and spirits in heaven will be here. I also invited the bodhisattva Guanyin, the goddess of mercy. Go to the peach garden now and pick plenty of ripe peaches."

  Red Gown and Blue Gown went to the garden. As soon as they went through the gate, both maidens gasped.

> "Where are all the peaches?" cried Red Gown.

> "They're gone," cried Blue Gown.

> "This is terrible," said Red Gown. "The queen will be angry."

## ③

  Wukong had been sleeping up on a branch. When he heard the maidens, he woke up.

> "Who is making all this noise?" he asked, jumping down to the ground. "I am trying to sleep."

  The maidens were startled.

> "We are sorry to wake you, sir," said Red Gown. "We came to pick peaches for the peach festival. Do you know what happened to all the peaches?"

> "The peach festival?" said Wukong. His eyes lit up. "I did not hear about that."

> "Oh, it is a wonderful festival," said Blue Gown. "All the important gods and spirits will be there."

> "That sounds like fun," said Wukong. "I am sure I am invited, right?"

  Red Gown bit her lip.

> "Um, I don't think so."

  Wukong was furious.

> "The queen did not invite me? I am just as important as any other spirit or god!"

  The maidens looked nervous.

> "Sir," said Blue Gown. "Where are the peaches?"

> "I ate them," Wukong said. "I ate all of them, every single one. And they were delicious."

> "Oh no!" cried Red Gown. "We must tell the queen!"

> "No, you are not going to tell the queen," said Wukong. He quickly cast a spell. Instantly, Red Gown and Blue Gown fell asleep.

  Wukong looked at all the empty peach trees. He shook his head.

  "I am in big trouble."

## ④

  When Red Gown and Blue Gown woke up, they ran back to the Cloud Palace.

> "Your Majesty," cried Red Gown. "Something terrible has happened. Sun Wukong ate all the peaches."

> "He got very angry and cast a spell on us," added Blue Gown. "When we woke up, he was gone."

  The queen's eyes flashed with anger. She went to the royal court and told the Jade Emperor.

> "That horrible monkey!" cried the Emperor. He turned to his captain. "Gather 100,000 soldiers. I want Wukong arrested."

  The captain nodded and then left the palace.

## ⑤

  Meanwhile, the bodhisattva Guanyin left her home on Mount Potalaka in the South Sea. She soon arrived at the Cloud Palace.

> "I am sorry to tell you this," said the queen. "But there will not be a peach festival."

> "Why not?" asked Guanyin.

> "A monkey named Sun Wukong ate all the peaches," said the Emperor. "I sent 100,000 soldiers to arrest him. They will bring him back to heaven soon."

  Just then, a messenger ran into the court.

> "We need more soldiers, Your Majesty!"

> "What?" cried the Emperor.

> "Wukong defeated the entire army," said the messenger.

  The Jade Emperor put his head in his hands.

> "We do not have any more soldiers."

---

# 🇨🇳 第九章：蟠桃园

## ①

  悟空从树枝上摘下一个桃子，咬了一口。汁水四溢，香甜可口。

  他说："太好吃了！"他又吃了一个，接着又吃了一个。从那以后，每天早晨，悟空都偷偷地吃越来越多的桃子。吃完之后，他就爬上树去睡个午觉。日子一天天过去，悟空在天庭享受着快乐的生活。

## ②

  与此同时，王母娘娘正忙着。一年一度的蟠桃盛会马上就要到了。她召来了她的侍女红袄和蓝袄。

> "娘娘有什么吩咐？"红袄问道。

> "蟠桃盛会明天就要举行了，"王母说。"天上所有重要的神仙都会来。我还请了南海观世音菩萨。你们现在就去蟠桃园，多摘些熟透的桃子来。"

  红袄和蓝袄来到了桃园。一进园门，两位侍女都倒吸了一口凉气。

> "桃子都到哪里去了？"红袄惊叫道。

> "全都不见了，"蓝袄叫道。

> "这可糟了，"红袄说。"娘娘一定会生气的。"

## ③

  悟空正睡在一根树枝上。听到侍女们的声音，他醒了过来。

> "是谁在这儿这么吵闹？"他一边问，一边跳到地上。"我正睡觉呢。"

  侍女们吓了一跳。

> "惊扰了您，真对不起，"红袄说。"我们来为蟠桃盛会摘桃子。您知道桃子都到哪里去了吗？"

> "蟠桃盛会？"悟空说。他眼睛一亮。"我可没听说啊。"

> "那可是一个了不起的盛会呢，"蓝袄说。"所有重要的神仙都会到场。"

> "听起来真好玩，"悟空说。"我肯定也在邀请之列，对吧？"

  红袄咬了咬嘴唇。

> "嗯，我想恐怕没有。"

  悟空勃然大怒。

> "王母娘娘没有邀请我？我和任何神仙一样重要！"

  侍女们看起来很紧张。

> "大人，"蓝袄说。"桃子在哪里？"

> "被我吃了，"悟空说。"全都吃了，一个不剩。而且都好吃极了。"

> "糟了！"红袄叫道。"我们必须禀告娘娘！"

> "不行，你们不能去禀告娘娘，"悟空说。他迅速施了一个法术。红袄和蓝袄立刻睡着了。

  悟空看着光秃秃的桃树，摇了摇头。

  "这下我可惹了大麻烦了。"

## ④

  红袄和蓝袄醒来后，急忙跑回了天宫。

> "娘娘，"红袄哭喊道。"出大事了。孙悟空把所有的桃子都吃光了。"

> "他非常生气，还对我们施了法术，"蓝袄接着说。"我们醒来的时候，他已经不见了。"

  王母娘娘眼中怒火闪烁。她来到凌霄宝殿，禀告了玉皇大帝。

> "这只可恶的猴子！"玉帝大叫。他转向天将。"点起十万天兵天将，我要把悟空捉拿归案。"

  天将点了点头，随即离开天宫。

## ⑤

  与此同时，观世音菩萨从南海普陀洛迦山出发。她很快就赶到了天宫。

> "很抱歉告诉您，"王母娘娘说。"蟠桃盛会办不成了。"

> "为什么呢？"观音问道。

> "一个叫孙悟空的猴子吃光了所有的桃子，"玉帝说。"我已经派了十万天兵天将去捉拿他。很快就能把他带回天庭了。"

  就在这时，一个信使跑进大殿。

> "陛下，我们需要更多兵马！"

> "什么？"玉帝惊叫。

> "悟空打败了整个天军，"信使说。

  玉皇大帝以手扶额。

> "我们再也没有更多的兵马了。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Ten: The Powerful Sage

## ①

  The story begins in the heavenly court. The Jade Emperor sat upon his throne, furious.

> "How will we defeat Sun Wukong?" he asked.

  A general stepped forward.

> "Your Majesty," said the general, "I sent our entire army and they couldn't arrest him."

  Guanyin spoke up from among the immortals.

> "Perhaps we can ask the Sage of Plum Mountain to capture him," said Guanyin.

> "Yes," said the Jade Emperor. "Erlang is very powerful."

  He turned to the messenger.

> "Go to Plum Mountain. Ask Erlang if he will help us."

## ②

  Wukong stood in front of the waterfall with his cheering subjects.

> "My king, you have just defeated an entire army from heaven!" said one of the monkeys.

> "I hope the Jade Emperor has learned his lesson," said Wukong.

> "He and his army are no match for me!"

  A deep voice boomed from above. Wukong looked up. A large man was coming down from the sky. Some of the other monkeys ran and hid.

> "I am Erlang Shen," said the man. "The Jade Emperor sent me to arrest you."

  Wukong laughed.

> "The Jade Emperor's entire army couldn't defeat me. What do you think you're going to do?"

> "I am going to take you back to heaven," said Erlang. "And you will be punished."

  Wukong raised his iron bar and leaped into the air.

> "Come on!"

  Erlang blocked the bar with his sword and then struck back.

## ③

  Wukong jumped onto a cloud to get out of the way. Erlang leaped into the air. He shook his body and suddenly grew much bigger.

  Wukong laughed.

> "I can do that too!"

  He shook his body and grew just as big as Erlang. Clouds and wind blew as the two giants fought in the sky. Their weapons banged together through the night. They were still fighting when the sun rose the next morning.

  This fight could last forever, thought Wukong. I should try a different plan.

  Wukong struck the ground one last time, and then jumped fast down to earth. He turned himself into a sparrow and perched on a branch.

  Erlang will never find me now, thought Wukong.

  He looked up and saw a hawk.

  Danger! thought Wukong. Better run!

  Wukong dived into a stream. He turned himself into a fish and swam in the water. But then a crane flew over the stream. The crane swooped down at the water, its mouth wide open.

  Wukong shot out of the stream. He changed back into himself and ran down a hill.

> "I'll turn myself into a temple," he thought. "Then, if Erlang tries to enter, I'll bite him."

  Wukong's eyes became windows and his mouth became a door. He turned his tail into a flagpole.

## ④

  A moment later, Erlang came down the hill. When he saw the temple, he scratched his head.

> "Hmm," said Erlang. "I never saw a temple with a flagpole before. This must be Wukong. I'll kick in that door!"

  Oh no! thought Wukong. You'll break all my teeth!

  Wukong changed back into himself and ran. Erlang was right behind him.

## ⑤

  Up in heaven, the Jade Emperor, the Queen Mother, and Guanyin watched the chase. The Sage Laozi came over to them.

> "What's going on?" he asked, looking down.

> "That monkey, Sun Wukong, ate all the peaches from the garden," said the Jade Emperor. "Then he defeated our entire army. Erlang is trying to catch him now."

> "I can help," said Laozi.

  He took a metal ring off his arm. He aimed carefully and hurled it down to earth.

> "Go!"

  The ring hit Wukong on the head. The monkey felt dizzy for a moment and then fell to the ground. The powerful Sage had been captured.

---

# 🇨🇳 第十章：神通广大的神仙


## ①

  故事从天庭开始。玉皇大帝坐在宝座上，勃然大怒。

> "我们怎样才能打败孙悟空？"他问道。

  一位天将走上前来。

> "陛下，"天将说，"我派了整个天兵天将，都没能捉住他。"

  观音菩萨在众神仙中开口了。

> "也许我们可以请灌江口的二郎神来捉他，"观音说。

> "好，"玉皇大帝说，"二郎神法力高强。"

  他转向信使。

> "去灌江口，请二郎神来帮我们。"

## ②

  悟空站在瀑布前，猴儿们正在为他欢呼。

> "大王，您刚刚打败了天庭的整个军队！"一只猴子说。

> "希望玉皇大帝已经吸取了教训，"悟空说。

> "他和他的军队根本不是我的对手！"

  天空中传来一个洪亮的声音。悟空抬头一看，一个高大的人正从天而降。一些猴子吓得跑开躲了起来。

> "我是二郎神，"那人说，"玉皇大帝派我来捉拿你。"

  悟空大笑。

> "玉皇大帝的整个军队都打不过我。你以为你能怎么样？"

> "我要把你带回天庭，"二郎神说，"你将受到惩罚。"

  悟空举起金箍棒，纵身一跃。

> "来吧！"

  二郎神用三尖刀挡住了铁棒，随即反击。

## ③

  悟空跳上云头躲避。二郎神腾空而起，摇身一变，突然变得巨大无比。

  悟空大笑。

> "我也会这招！"

  他也摇身一变，变得和二郎神一样高大。云雾翻腾，狂风大作，两个巨人在天空中大战。兵器叮叮当当地碰撞，整整打了一夜。到了第二天太阳升起的时候，他们还在打。

  这样打下去永远没完没了，悟空想。我得换个法子。

  悟空朝地上猛击一棒，然后飞快地跳到下界。他摇身一变，变成一只麻雀，停在树枝上。

  二郎神这次肯定找不到我了，悟空想。

  他抬头一看，却看见一只老鹰。

  不好！悟空想。快跑！

  悟空一头扎进溪流里，变成一条鱼在水中游。可是，一只仙鹤飞到了溪流上空。仙鹤俯冲向水面，嘴张得大大的。

  悟空从溪水里窜出来，现出原形，朝山下跑去。

> "我变成一座土地庙吧，"他想，"等二郎神想进去的时候，我就一口咬住他。"

  悟空的眼睛变成了窗户，嘴巴变成了门，尾巴变成了一根旗杆。

## ④

  不一会儿，二郎神来到了山下。他看见这座庙，挠了挠头。

> "嗯？"二郎神说，"我还从没见过庙旗杆竖在后面的呢，这一定是孙悟空变的。看我砸烂他的门！"

  哎呀！悟空想。你会把我牙齿都打掉的！

  悟空现出原形就跑，二郎神紧紧追在后面。

## ⑤

  在天庭上，玉皇大帝、王母娘娘和观音正看着这场追逐。太上老君走了过来。

> "怎么回事？"他低头问道。

> "那只猴子孙悟空，吃光了蟠桃园里所有的桃子，"玉皇大帝说，"然后又打败了我们整个军队。现在二郎神正在捉他。"

> "我来帮忙，"老君说。

  他从手臂上取下一个金钢琢，瞄准了，朝下界扔了下去。

> "去吧！"

  金钢琢正中悟空的脑袋。猴子一阵头晕目眩，摔倒在地上。神通广大的大圣，终于被捉住了。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eleven: Trouble in Heaven

## ①

  The soldiers quickly tied up Wukong and brought him up to Heaven.

  "I want Sun Wukong destroyed," said the Jade Emperor.

  The soldiers tied Wukong to a pillar in a courtyard. They struck him with swords. But his body was as hard as a diamond. Wukong laughed.

  "Your swords can't hurt me!" he said.

## ②

  The Jade Emperor turned to a messenger.

  "Bring in the fire gods!" he ordered.

  Several fire gods entered the courtyard and threw balls of flame at Wukong. The courtyard filled with smoke. But when the smoke cleared, not one hair on Wukong's body was burned.

  "Thank you," Wukong laughed. "I was feeling a little cold!"

## ③

  "Gather the Thunder Gods," said the Jade Emperor.

  Several Thunder Gods entered the courtyard. The Jade Emperor smiled as lightning bolts shot towards Wukong. But even the lightning couldn't harm the monkey.

  "That tickles!" said Wukong with a smile.

  The Jade Emperor shook his head. "It seems that Wukong can't be destroyed."

  "That's because he ate all the peaches," said Laozi. "Just one peach would make someone live forever. He ate every peach in the garden."

  The Emperor frowned. "Then how will we get rid of him?"

  "I have an idea," said Laozi. "I'll put him in the large pot I use for making potions. Maybe we can burn him up slowly."

  "Perfect," said the Jade Emperor.

## ④

  Soldiers brought Wukong to a room in Laozi's palace. A large pot sat in the middle of the room. Laozi put Wukong into the pot and closed the lid. Then he started a fire under the pot. Day and night, he attended the fire. He kept it burning for forty-nine days.

  "Wukong must have been destroyed by now," thought Laozi.

  He slowly took the lid off the pot. Smoke poured from the opening, and the pot fell over. Burning pieces of coal flew everywhere. Wukong staggered out, and he was coughing.

  "That smoke was horrible!" he cried.

  He pushed Laozi, knocking the old sage onto his back. Wukong pulled out his iron bar and smashed everything in the room.

## ⑤

  "Somebody stop him!" cried Laozi.

  Wukong ran out of Laozi's palace. Gods and spirits fled as Wukong smashed everything in his path. Laozi ran into the cloud palace.

  "Your Majesty, Wukong is causing trouble all over Heaven!" he said.

  "What?" cried the Emperor. "He's alive?"

  "Yes," said Laozi. "I took the lid off the pot because I thought he was burned up. But the fire didn't hurt him at all."

  "This is an outrage," said the Jade Emperor. "What are we going to do with that monkey?"

  The Emperor thought for a moment. "We must ask Buddha for help," he said.

  He turned to a messenger. "Go to the Western Paradise quickly. See if Buddha can come to help us."

## ⑥

  Flying as fast as he could, the messenger headed toward the Western Paradise.

  Meanwhile, everybody hid behind doors as Wukong ran through Heaven. Using his iron bar, he smashed doors and windows and knocked over statues. Suddenly, he stopped. Before him was a huge figure, glowing with golden light.

  "Who are you?" said Wukong.

  "I am Buddha," said the figure. "And who are you, and why are you causing all this trouble?"

  Wukong smiled. "I am Sun Wukong, King of the Mountain of Fruit and Flowers. I should be the King of Heaven too. I am going to the Cloud Palace to tell the Jade Emperor to leave. If he doesn't, I'll never stop causing trouble!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第十一章：大闹天宫

## ①

  天兵天将迅速绑住悟空，把他押上了天庭。

  "我要把孙悟空除掉。"玉皇大帝说。

  士兵们把悟空绑在庭院的一根柱子上，用刀剑砍他。可他的身体坚硬如钻石。悟空哈哈大笑。

  "你们的刀枪伤不了我！"他说。

## ②

  玉皇大帝转身对一名传令官说。

  "去把火神请来！"他下令道。

  几位火神进入庭院，朝悟空投掷火球。庭院里顿时浓烟滚滚。可是当烟雾散去时，悟空身上一根毫毛也没有被烧伤。

  "谢谢你们，"悟空笑着说，"我正觉得有点冷呢！"

## ③

  "把雷神们都召来。"玉皇大帝说。

  几位雷神进入庭院。玉皇大帝微笑着，只见一道道闪电射向悟空。然而，即便是闪电也伤不了这只猴子。

  "真舒服呀！"悟空笑着说。

  玉皇大帝摇了摇头。"看来悟空是消灭不了了。"

  "那是因为他吃了所有的仙桃，"太上老君说，"只要吃一个仙桃就能长生不老。他把园里的仙桃全都吃光了。"

  玉帝皱起眉头。"那我们怎么才能除掉他呢？"

  "我有一个主意，"太上老君说，"我把他放进我炼丹用的大炉子里。也许我们可以慢慢把他炼死。"

  "太好了。"玉皇大帝说。

## ④

  士兵们把悟空带到太上老君的宫殿里。屋子中间放着一口大炉子。太上老君把悟空放进炉中，盖上盖子，然后在炉子下面生起火来。他日夜不停地添柴加火，一连烧了四十九天。

  "悟空这下一定被消灭了吧，"太上老君心想。

  他缓缓揭开炉盖。烟雾从炉口涌出，大炉子翻倒在地，燃烧的煤块四处飞溅。悟空摇摇晃晃地爬了出来，不停地咳嗽着。

  "这烟太呛人了！"他喊道。

  他一把推倒太上老君，从炉中翻出身来。悟空掏出金箍棒，把屋里的东西砸了个稀巴烂。

## ⑤

  "快拦住他！"太上老君大喊道。

  悟空冲出太上老君的宫殿。众神和天将纷纷逃窜，悟空所到之处，一切都被他砸得粉碎。太上老君急忙跑进凌霄宝殿。

  "陛下，悟空在天庭到处大闹！"他说。

  "什么？"玉帝惊叫道，"他还活着？"

  "是的，"太上老君说，"我以为他已经被炼化了，就揭开了炉盖。谁知道那火根本伤不到他。"

  "真是岂有此理！"玉皇大帝说，"我们拿这只猴子到底怎么办？"

  玉帝沉思了一会儿。"我们只好请如来佛祖来帮忙了，"他说。

  他转身对一名传令官说。"快去西天极乐世界，看看如来佛祖能不能来帮我们。"

## ⑥

  传令官以最快的速度向西天极乐世界飞去。

  这时，众人都躲在门后，悟空在天庭横冲直撞。他挥起金箍棒，砸门破窗，推倒神像。突然，他停了下来。在他面前出现了一个巨大的身影，浑身散发着金色的光芒。

  "你是谁？"悟空问。

  "我是如来佛祖，"那身影说，"你又是谁？为什么在这里大闹天宫？"

  悟空微微一笑。"我是孙悟空，花果山之王。我也应该做这天庭之王。我要去凌霄宝殿告诉玉皇大帝，让他把位子让给我。如果他不让，我就永远不停手！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Twelve: The Bet with Buddha

## ①

  Buddha smiled at Wukong.

  "How did you get so powerful?"

  "A sage taught me secret formulas," said Wukong. "I practiced them for many years. I am now equal to the Jade Emperor."

  "The Jade Emperor has been practicing the same formulas for many lifetimes," said Buddha. "How can you think you are equal to him? Go back to your mountain now and behave yourself."

  "I am not leaving until I get to rule heaven," said Wukong.

## ②

  Buddha thought for a minute.

  "Sun Wukong, what powers do you have?"

  "I can change into other animals," said Wukong. "I can soar through the sky on clouds. I can do anything I want."

  "Then let us make a bet," said Buddha. "If you win, you can rule heaven. The Jade Emperor will come to live with me in the Western Paradise. But if you lose, you will be punished severely."

  "What do I have to do?" asked Wukong.

## ③

  "It is simple," said Buddha. He held out his hand. "You just have to jump off my hand."

  Wukong laughed. "That is easy. I can jump across entire oceans."

  Buddha smiled. "Well then, let us see you do it."

  Wukong stepped up onto Buddha's palm. "You are a fool," he said to Buddha. "I am going to jump farther than you could ever imagine. When I return, I will be the ruler of heaven."

## ④

  Wukong leaped and soared through the air. After a long time, he saw five enormous pillars. He landed in front of them.

  "This must be the end of the world," he said to himself. "I will go back now and tell Buddha to take the Jade Emperor away. Heaven is mine."

  Wukong was just about to jump back when he thought of something.

  "There is nobody around. How will I prove that I was here?"

  He tapped his chin. "I will write a note on this pillar. Buddha can come here and check."

## ⑤

  Wukong plucked two hairs and turned them into a brush and a jar of ink. On one of the pillars he wrote: *Sun Wukong was here.*

  "There," said Wukong. "Now I will go and tell Buddha how far I jumped."

  Wukong leaped once more. After a long time he landed on Buddha's palm again.

  "I am back!" said Wukong. "Tell the Jade Emperor to leave."

## ⑥

  Buddha put on a frown. "How can you say you are back? You never left my hand."

  Wukong was confused. "Yes, I did. I reached the end of the world. There were five enormous pillars. I even wrote on one. Come with me and I will show you."

  "There is no need to go anywhere," said Buddha. "Just look down."

  Wukong looked down. Near the bottom of Buddha's middle finger was the note: *Sun Wukong was here.*

## ⑦

  Wukong stamped his foot. "It is a trick! You used some sort of magic."

  "It is not a trick," said Buddha. "You never left my palm."

  "I did! I did! I did! I jumped all the way to—"

  "You lost the bet, Sun Wukong," said Buddha. "And now you will be punished."

  Holding Wukong tightly, Buddha reached down to earth. His hand turned into a mountain, which he placed on top of the monkey. Wukong grunted and pushed with all his strength. The mountain started to rise. Buddha pulled a small sheet of magic paper from his sleeve. He laid the paper on top of the mountain. The mountain crashed back down.

  Buddha turned to the Jade Emperor. "Sun Wukong cannot lift the mountain now," he said. "He will be trapped until his punishment is over."

---

# 🇨🇳 第十二章：与如来之赌

## ①

  佛祖微笑着看着悟空。

  "你是怎么变得这么厉害的？"

  "一位神仙教了我秘诀，"悟空说，"我练了很多年，现在已经和玉皇大帝一样厉害了。"

  "玉皇大帝同样修行了许多世代，"佛祖说，"你怎么能和他平起平坐呢？回到你的山上去，安分守己吧。"

  "我非要统治天庭不可，"悟空说，"不然我绝不走。"

## ②

  佛祖沉思了一会儿。

  "孙悟空，你有什么本事？"

  "我会七十二变，能变成各种动物，"悟空说，"我能腾云驾雾。我想做什么就做什么。"

  "那我们打个赌吧，"佛祖说，"如果你赢了，你就可以统治天庭，玉皇大帝就跟我到西天极乐世界去住。但如果你输了，就要受到严厉的惩罚。"

  "我要做什么？"悟空问。

## ③

  "很简单，"佛祖说。他伸出一只手，"你只要跳出我的手心就行了。"

  悟空哈哈大笑。"那太容易了，我一个筋斗就能翻过整片大海。"

  佛祖微微一笑。"那好，就让我看看吧。"

  悟空纵身跳上佛祖的手掌。"你可真傻，"他对佛祖说，"我要跳到一个你想都想不到的地方。等我回来的时候，我就是天庭之王了。"

## ④

  悟空纵身一跃，翱翔空中。过了很久，他看到了五根巨大的柱子。他落在柱子前面。

  "这一定就是世界的尽头了，"他自言自语道，"现在回去吧，叫佛祖把玉皇大帝带走。天庭是我的了。"

  悟空正准备跳回去，忽然想到了一件事。

  "周围一个人也没有，我怎么证明自己来过这里呢？"

  他摸了摸下巴。"我在这根柱子上写几个字吧。佛祖可以亲自来看看。"

## ⑤

  悟空拔下两根毫毛，变成一支毛笔和一罐墨水。他在一根柱子上写下：*孙悟空到此一游。*

  "好了，"悟空说，"现在回去告诉佛祖我跳了多远。"

  悟空又是一个筋斗。过了很久，他重新落在佛祖的手掌上。

  "我回来了！"悟空说，"快叫玉皇大帝搬走吧。"

## ⑥

  佛祖皱起眉头。"你怎么说你已经回来了？你从来没有跳出过我的手心。"

  悟空糊涂了。"我明明跳出去了！我到了世界的尽头，那里有五根巨大的柱子，我还在上面写了字呢。你跟我去看看就知道了。"

  "不必去了，"佛祖说，"你低头看看吧。"

  悟空低头一看。佛祖的中指根部，赫然写着一行字：*孙悟空到此一游。*

## ⑦

  悟空跺了跺脚。"这是骗术！你使了什么魔法。"

  "不是骗术，"佛祖说，"你从来没有跳出过我的手掌。"

  "我跳了！我跳了！我明明跳了——"

  "你赌输了，孙悟空，"佛祖说，"现在你要受到惩罚了。"

  佛祖牢牢抓住悟空，向下落到人间。他的手变成一座大山，压在猴子身上。悟空咬紧牙关，使出浑身力气去推。大山开始松动上升。佛祖从袖中抽出一张小小的符纸，贴在大山顶上。大山轰然落下，重新把悟空压住。

  佛祖转身对玉皇大帝说。"孙悟空现在搬不动这座山了，"他说，"他要被压在山下，直到惩罚期满为止。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Thirteen: The True Scriptures

## ①

  Five hundred years passed. Wukong stayed trapped under the mountain. A thick layer of moss covered the mountain.

  One day Buddha sat in the Thunderclap Monastery in the Western Paradise. He was talking to his students.

  "The people in the East, in the Tang Empire, need our help," said Buddha. "They lie, cheat and steal. They are greedy and constantly fighting." He held up a bundle of scrolls. "These are the true Scriptures. They will teach the people in the East to act better."

  "Wonderful," said one student. "Let us bring the Scriptures to the Tang Empire."

  Buddha shook his head. "No," he said. "A true believer, a monk, needs to come here to get them. Will anyone go to the East to find a worthy monk?"

  Guanyin stepped forward. "I will go."

## ②

  The Tang Emperor sat as his head monk read to a small group of people. The monk was reading old religious texts. A woman approached the monk.

  "Why are you reading those old texts?" she asked. "Don't you know about the true Scriptures?"

  The Emperor stood up. "How dare you interrupt my—"

  "It is okay," said the monk. He walked over to the woman. "What are the true Scriptures?"

  The woman looked at the monk carefully. "They contain many lessons. People who learn the lessons never have to suffer again."

  "Do you have them here?" asked the monk.

## ③

  "No," said the woman. "They are with Buddha in the Western Paradise. Someone must travel to the Thunderclap Monastery to get them. But only a true believer may make the journey."

  She took a robe out of her bag. "Put this on."

  The monk put on the robe. Beams of light shone from it.

  "You are a true believer," said the woman. "Will you make the journey?"

  "Yes," said the monk, looking down at the glowing robe. "It will be an honor."

  "The journey will be very difficult," said the woman. "Wide rivers and steep mountains will block your path. Fierce creatures and evil demons will try to attack you. But do not fear. You will have help from me."

  Suddenly the room filled with blinding light. The woman rose into the air and changed form.

  "It is the Bodhisattva Guanyin!" someone cried.

  The Emperor and everyone else in the room bowed. Guanyin rose higher and then disappeared.

## ④

  The next morning there was a huge feast. The Tang Emperor sat next to the monk.

  "Your journey will help our empire greatly," said the Emperor. "No longer will our people suffer or treat each other badly. From now on I will think of you as my brother. You will be called the Tang Monk."

  "Thank you, Your Majesty," said the Tang Monk.

  "How long will the journey take?" asked the Emperor.

  "I will return in a few years," said the monk.

  Later that day the Tang Monk got ready for his journey. He put the special robe into a bag. He put dry foods into another bag. A big crowd gathered to say goodbye.

  "Good luck, my brother," said the Tang Emperor.

  The Tang Monk climbed onto a horse and rode toward the west.

## ⑤

  He had traveled for over a month when he came to a big mountain. Slowly his horse walked up a steep trail.

  "I have a bad feeling," said the Tang Monk. He looked around uneasily. "I hope there are not any demons here."

  Suddenly a voice boomed. "Who is walking on my mountain?"

---

# 🇨🇳 第十三章：真经

## ①

  五百年过去了。悟空被困在山下整整五百年。山上覆盖着厚厚的一层青苔。

  有一天，佛祖坐在西天极乐世界的雷音寺中，正和弟子们讲话。

  "东土大唐的人需要我们帮忙，"佛祖说，"他们撒谎、行骗、偷盗，贪婪成性，争斗不断。"他举起一卷经书，"这些就是真经。它们可以教导东土的人民向善。"

  "太好了，"一名弟子说，"我们把经书送到大唐去吧。"

  佛祖摇了摇头。"不行，"他说，"必须要一位虔诚的信徒，一位僧人，亲自来这里取经。谁能去东土找到合适的人选？"

  观音菩萨走上前来。"我去。"

## ②

  大唐皇帝坐在那里，听他的御弟法师给一小群人诵经。那位法师正在诵读古老的经文。一位女子走到法师面前。

  "你为什么读这些旧经文？"她问，"你不知道有真经吗？"

  皇帝站了起来。"你怎么敢打断朕的——"

  "没关系，"法师说。他走过去问那个女子。"什么是真经？"

  女子仔细打量了法师一番。"真经里有许多道理。懂得这些道理的人就再也不用受苦了。"

  "你们这里有吗？"法师问。

## ③

  "没有，"女子说，"真经在西天极乐世界的如来佛祖那里。必须要有人到雷音寺去取。可是只有虔诚的信徒才能走到那里。"

  她从包中取出一件袈裟。"穿上吧。"

  法师披上袈裟。袈裟上放射出万道金光。

  "您是一位虔诚的信徒，"女子说。"您愿意去取经吗？"

  "我愿意，"法师低头望着发光的袈裟说，"这是我的荣幸。"

  "这条路会很艰难，"女子说，"宽阔的江河、陡峭的高山会挡住你的去路。凶猛的野兽、邪恶的妖怪会来攻击你。但是不要怕，我会帮助你的。"

  忽然房间里亮起耀眼的光芒。女子腾空而起，变成了菩萨的法相。

  "是观音菩萨！"有人喊道。

  皇帝和房间里的所有人都跪下叩拜。观音菩萨越升越高，然后消失了。

## ④

  第二天早晨，宫中设下了盛大的宴会。唐太宗与法师并肩而坐。

  "你的旅程会大大地帮助我们的国家，"皇帝说，"从此再也不会让百姓受苦、再也不会让别人欺负自己人了。从今以后我把你当做御弟，你就叫唐僧吧。"

  "感谢陛下，"唐僧说。

  "这趟路要走多久？"皇帝问。

  "几年后我会回来，"法师说。

  当天晚些时候，唐僧收拾行装，将袈裟装进一个包袱，又把干粮装进另一个包袱。一大群人赶来送行。

  "一路平安，好兄弟，"唐太宗说。

  唐僧翻身上马，向西面驰去。

## ⑤

  走了一个多月，唐僧来到了一座大山前。他的马缓缓走在陡峭的山路上。

  "我有一种不祥的预感，"唐僧说。他不安地环顾四周，"我希望这里没有妖怪。"

  突然，一个声音轰然响起。"是什么人在我山上走动？"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fourteen: A Promise to Protect

## ①

  The Tang Monk trembled with fear. The angry voice spoke again.

  "Who is walking on my mountain?"

  "Oh!" cried the Tang Monk. He fell off his horse and tumbled down the mountain.

  At the bottom, he saw a crack between the rocks. The monk looked in and saw a moss-covered monkey peering out at him.

  "My name is Sun Wukong," said the monkey. "I am King of the Fruit and Flower Mountain."

  "Why are you in there?" asked the Tang Monk. He stood up.

  "Buddha put me here," said Wukong. "I am being punished for causing trouble in Heaven. Who are you?"

  "I am just a monk," said the Tang Monk. "I am going to the Western Paradise to get scriptures from Buddha."

## ②

  Wukong's eyes lit up. "You are the Tang Monk!" he cried. "I am supposed to go with you."

  The Tang Monk took a step back. Was this strange monkey telling the truth?

  "The Bodhisattva Guanyin visited me," Wukong went on. "She said I would be set free if I promised to protect you on the journey. Set me free and I will go with you to the West."

  The Tang Monk relaxed. He looked at the rocks. "How can I free you?"

  "There is a small piece of paper on top of this mountain," said Wukong. "You must remove it."

## ③

  The Tang Monk went back up the mountain. He pushed aside shrubs and brambles and pulled himself over large boulders. Finally, he reached the mountain's peak.

  The monk picked up the paper. Right away a breeze swept it from his hand. The paper floated up and then disappeared among the clouds.

  "The paper floated away," he said to the monkey.

  "It returned to Buddha," said Wukong. "Step back. Go farther," said Wukong. The monk took another step back. "Go farther," said Wukong again.

  The Tang Monk went far from the mountain.

## ④

  He gasped as the top of the mountain rose into the air. Wukong stood under the mountain, holding it up with his hands. He jumped out and the mountain crashed down behind him.

  Wukong grabbed the Tang Monk's hands. "Thank you, Master. I will help you reach the Western Paradise."

  The Tang Monk rode the horse as Wukong walked. The monkey told the monk about himself.

  "The Jade Emperor's entire army could not defeat me," he laughed. "So I said I should be in charge of Heaven."

  "What powers do you have?" asked the Tang Monk.

  "I can become other animals," said Wukong. "Watch this."

  He quickly changed into a tiger. The Tang Monk gulped. Wukong changed into a snake, a bird, and then back into himself.

## ⑤

  "And that is not all," he said. "I can grow big."

  The monkey's body grew so big that his head reached the clouds.

  "I can become tiny too," said Wukong. He shrank to the size of a bean and hopped onto the saddle. He changed back to his normal size. His iron bar appeared from his ear. The monkey spun it around and then struck a huge boulder. The boulder exploded into tiny pieces. The Tang Monk watched in horror.

  Wukong laughed. "Do not look so scared, Master. I am protecting you."

## ⑥

  The two traveled farther until they saw a group of men blocking the road. The men looked rough and mean. They all had weapons. One man stepped forward.

  "Give us your money, or you will all be sorry!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第十四章：护行之诺

## ①

  唐僧吓得浑身发抖。那个愤怒的声音又响了起来。

  "是什么人在我山上走动？"

  "哎呀！"唐僧大叫一声，从马上摔了下来，顺着山坡滚了下去。

  在山脚，他看到岩石间有一道裂缝。他探头朝里张望，看见一只长满青苔的猴子正望着他。

  "我叫孙悟空，"猴子说，"我是花果山之王。"

  "你为什么被压在这里？"唐僧问。他站了起来。

  "是如来佛祖把我压在这里的，"悟空说，"因为我在天庭惹了大祸，这是对我的惩罚。你是什么人？"

  "我只是个普通和尚，"唐僧说，"我要去西天极乐世界，向如来佛祖取经。"

## ②

  悟空的眼睛一亮。"你就是唐僧！"他叫道，"我应该跟你一起走。"

  唐僧后退了一步。这只奇怪的猴子说的会是真话吗？

  "观音菩萨来看过我，"悟空接着说，"她说只要我答应保护你去西天取经，就会有人来放我。救我出来吧，我跟你一起向西走。"

  唐僧放松了一些。他看了看压在悟空身上的山石。"我怎么救你呢？"

  "这座山顶上有一张小小的纸符，"悟空说，"你把它拿走就行了。"

## ③

  唐僧又往山上爬去。他拨开灌木和荆棘，翻过大块的巨石，终于登上了山顶。

  和尚把那张纸拿起来。顿时一阵风把纸从他手中吹走。纸飘上天空，消失在云层里。

  "纸被风吹走了，"他对猴子说。

  "它回到佛祖那里去了，"悟空说，"往后退，再退远些。"

  唐僧又退了几步。"再远一点，"悟空又说了一遍。

  唐僧离山远远地站定了。

## ④

  只见山顶轰然升起。悟空站在山下，双手托住了大山。他纵身一跃跳了出来，身后的山轰隆一声塌了下去。

  悟空一把握住唐僧的手。"多谢师父，我一定帮你到西天取得真经。"

  唐僧骑上马，悟空在前面步行。这只猴子向师父讲述了自己的经历。

  "玉皇大帝的整支天兵天将都打不过我，"他大笑着说，"所以我说这管天庭的位子应该让给我坐。"

  "你都有什么本事？"唐僧问。

  "我会七十二变，能变成各种动物，"悟空说，"你看好了。"

  他摇身一变变成了一只老虎。唐僧倒吸一口凉气。悟空又变成了一条蛇、一只飞鸟，然后变回了自己的模样。

## ⑤

  "还不止呢，"他说，"我能变得很高大。"

  悟空的身体越长越大，头顶直穿云霄。

  "我也能变得很小，"悟空说。他缩小到一粒豆子那么大，跳上了马鞍，然后恢复正常大小。他的金箍棒从耳朵里出现。悟空抡起棒子，朝一块巨石打过去。巨石爆炸，碎成无数小块。唐僧看得目瞪口呆。

  悟空哈哈大笑。"别害怕，师父，我是来保护你的。"

## ⑥

  两个又走了一程，忽然看见一群人在前头拦住了去路。那些人面目凶恶，个个手拿兵器。其中一个人走上前来。

  "把钱财交出来，不然有你们好看！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifteen: The Tight Headband

## ①

  The Tang Monk looked at the robbers. He was shaking.

  "I am sorry," he said, "but we are just monks. We do not have any money."

  "Then give us whatever else you have," said one robber. He came closer.

  "Please, sir," said the monk.

  Wukong put up his hand. "I will deal with these robbers, Master."

  Wukong approached the men. They all laughed.

  "Look at the little monkey," said one of them.

  Wukong laughed too. "Yes, I am a monkey. And I am rather small. It is true."

## ②

  He removed the iron bar from his ear. "But you should be scared of me anyway."

  His iron bar grew and his eyes flashed red with anger.

  "The monkey is a spirit!" cried one man.

  "Run!" cried another.

  The robbers tripped over one another, trying to get away.

  Wukong raised the iron bar, ready to strike.

  "Stop, Wukong!" cried the Tang Monk. "Do not hurt them."

  Wukong turned around as the men ran away. "Why not?" he asked. "They were going to hurt us."

  "A Buddhist monk never hurts people," said the monk. "I would rather get hurt than hurt someone else."

  Wukong laughed. "That is ridiculous. We should have beaten them up."

## ③

  The Tang Monk shook his head. "You are cruel and violent, Wukong."

  Wukong was angry. "I just saved your life!" he cried. "And dare you scold me?" He paused. "I do not have to accept this treatment. I am leaving."

  Wukong leaped into the air and was gone.

  The Tang Monk sighed and continued his journey.

  Later that day he saw an old woman.

  "Monk," said the woman. "Where are you going?"

  "I am going to the Western Paradise," said the Tang Monk.

  "Do not you have anyone with you?" asked the woman. "You cannot go there alone."

## ④

  "I did have a companion," said the Tang Monk. "But he got angry when I scolded him for being violent. He left."

  "Your companion will come back," said the woman. "When he does, trick him into putting this on."

  She pulled a metal headband out of her bag. "Whenever he misbehaves, recite the Tight Headband Spell."

  The old woman whispered a magical spell to the Tang Monk.

  "Thank you," said the Tang Monk. "But how did you—"

  There was a flash of bright light and the woman rose into the air.

  "The Bodhisattva Guanyin!" cried the Tang Monk. He got down from his horse and bowed.

## ⑤

  Meanwhile, Wukong sat in the palace of the Dragon King of the Eastern Sea. He and the Dragon King were drinking tea.

  "I hope you have learned from your punishment," said the Dragon King.

  "Yes, I have," said Wukong. "I will not cause any more trouble for the Jade Emperor."

  The Dragon King sipped his tea. "What will you do now?"

  "I was traveling west with a monk to get scriptures from Buddha," said Wukong. "I promised Guanyin I would do it."

  The Dragon King smiled. "That is wonderful."

  Wukong shrugged. "Yes, well, I am not doing it anymore."

## ⑥

  The Dragon King put down his tea cup. "Why not?"

  "The monk had a bad attitude," said Wukong. "He yelled at me. He said I was cruel and violent."

  The Dragon King coughed nervously. "Well, Wukong, the monk has a point."

  Wukong glared at the king. "What do you mean?"

  The king hesitated and then said, "You are violent sometimes."

  Wukong folded his arms and looked at the ground.

  The Dragon King continued, "Not only that, but you made a promise to Guanyin. Perhaps, Wukong, it is you who has a bad attitude."

## ⑦

  Wukong looked at the Dragon King and sighed.

  "You are right. I did make a promise to Guanyin."

  He put down his tea cup and stood up. "Thank you, my friend. I will visit again soon."

  The Dragon King smiled. "Good luck, Wukong."

  The monkey hurried out of the Dragon King's palace. He found the Tang Monk traveling alongside a stream.

  "Master! I have returned!" he called.

  "I am glad you are back, Wukong," said the monk. "I am hungry. I will find a village and beg for some food for you."

## ⑧

  "You do not need to do that," said the monk. "There is rice in the bag. You can cook that."

  The monk got down from the horse. Wukong opened the bag. When he looked inside, his eyes opened wide. He pulled out the headband.

  "This headband is marvelous," said Wukong.

  The monk watched the monkey closely. "Do you like it?"

  "Yes!" said Wukong.

  "Try it on," said the monk.

  "Really?" asked Wukong.

  The monk nodded. Wukong put the headband on. He looked at his reflection in the stream.

  "I look handsome," said Wukong. "Thanks for—"

  The monkey grabbed the sides of his head and fell over. His eyes bulged.

  "He is going to explode!" he cried. He saw the Tang Monk talking quietly.

---

# 🇨🇳 第十五章：紧箍咒

## ①

  唐僧看着那些强盗，浑身发抖。

  "对不起，"他说，"我们只是出家人，身上没有钱。"

  "那就把别的值钱的东西交出来，"一个强盗说。他走近了一步。

  "求求您了，好汉，"唐僧说。

  悟空举了举手。"师父，让我来对付这些强盗。"

  悟空走到那帮人面前。他们都笑了。

  "看那只小猴子，"其中一个说。

  悟空也笑了。"没错，我是猴子，而且个头确实不大。这是事实。"

## ②

  他从耳朵里掏出金箍棒。"不过，你们还是应该害怕我。"

  金箍棒越长越大，悟空的眼睛因怒而通红。

  "这猴子是神仙！"一个人喊道。

  "快跑！"另一个喊道。

  强盗们连滚带爬，争先恐后地逃跑了。

  悟空举起金箍棒，正要打下去。

  "住手，悟空！"唐僧大喊道，"不要伤害他们。"

  悟空转过身来，看着逃跑的强盗们。"为什么？"他问，"他们本来要伤害我们的。"

  "出家人从不伤害别人，"唐僧说，"我宁可自己受伤也不伤害别人。"

  悟空哼了一声。"太荒唐了，我们就应该把他们打一顿。"

## ③

  唐僧摇了摇头。"悟空，你又残忍又暴躁。"

  悟空气坏了。"我刚救了你的命！"他叫道，"你倒来骂我？"他顿了顿，"我不受你这等气，我走了。"

  悟空纵身一跃飞上天，转眼不见了。

  唐僧叹了一口气，独自继续赶路。

  那天晚些时候，他看见一位老妇人。

  "和尚，"老妇人说。"你要去哪里？"

  "我要去西天取经，"唐僧说。

  "难道你是一个人吗？"妇人问，"你一个人可去不了。"

## ④

  "我原本有一个同伴，"唐僧说，"可是我骂他太暴躁了，他就生气了，走了。"

  "你的同伴会回来的，"妇人说，"等他回来了，你让他把这个戴上。"

  她从包袱里取出一个金属头箍。"以后他要是不听话，你就念紧箍咒。"

  老妇人凑到唐僧耳边，悄悄教了他一段咒语。

  "谢谢您，"唐僧说。"可是您怎么——"

  一道金光闪过，老妇人腾空而起。

  "是观音菩萨！"唐僧叫道。他急忙下马行礼。

## ⑤

  此时，悟空正坐在东海龙王的龙宫里，和龙王一起喝茶。

  "我希望你从惩罚中吸取了教训，"龙王说。

  "吸取了，"悟空说，"我不会再给玉帝添麻烦了。"

  龙王抿了一口茶。"你以后有什么打算？"

  "我本来跟着一个和尚去西天取经，"悟空说，"我答应过观音菩萨要保护他。"

  龙王微笑着。"那太好了。"

  悟空耸了耸肩。"是啊，不过我不干了。"

## ⑥

  龙王放下了茶杯。"为什么？"

  "那和尚态度不好，"悟空说，"他对我又吼又骂，说我残忍又暴躁。"

  龙王不安地咳了一声。"嗯，悟空，和尚说得也有道理。"

  悟空瞪了龙王一眼。"什么意思？"

  龙王犹豫了一下，然后说。"你有时候确实太暴躁了。"

  悟空交叉双臂，低头看着地面。

  龙王接着说。"不但如此，你还答应过观世音菩萨。悟空啊，也许是你自己的态度不对。"

## ⑦

  悟空看了看龙王，叹了一口气。

  "你说得对。我确实答应过观音菩萨。"

  他放下茶杯，站了起来。"多谢了，老朋友。我改日再来看你。"

  龙王微微一笑。"悟空，祝你好运。"

  悟空匆匆赶出龙宫，找到唐僧正在一条小溪边赶路。

  "师父，我回来了！"他喊道。

  "悟空，你回来就好，"和尚说。"我饿了，我去前面村里给你讨些吃的来。"

## ⑧

  "不用麻烦了，"唐僧说，"包袱里有米，你煮来吃就行。"

  唐僧下了马。悟空打开包袱一看，眼睛顿时睁得大大的。他从里面拿出了一个头箍。

  "这个头箍真好看，"悟空说。

  唐僧紧紧盯着猴子。"你喜欢吗？"

  "喜欢！"悟空说。

  "戴上试试吧，"唐僧说。

  "真的吗？"悟空问。

  唐僧点了点头。悟空把头箍戴在头上，低头看着溪水里的倒影。

  "我戴着真好看，"悟空说。"谢谢你——"

  忽然悟空双手抱住脑袋，摔倒在地。他的眼球都鼓了出来。

  "他要炸了！"他大叫。只见唐僧在一旁小声念着咒语。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixteen: Who Will Come Get Sticks

## ①

  The monkey grabbed the sides of his head and fell over. His eyes bulged.

  "He is going to explode!" he cried. He saw the Tang Monk talking quietly.

  "What? What are you saying?" cried Wukong.

  The Tang Monk stopped talking and the pain stopped.

  "The Bodhisattva Guanyin taught me a spell," said the monk. "She gave me the headband to force you to be good."

  Wukong pulled at the headband. But it would not come off.

## ②

  "Good gosh!" cried the monkey. He stamped his foot. "You tricked me!"

  "It is for your own good," said the monk. "You were being violent."

  Wukong pulled out his iron bar and lunged at the Tang Monk. The monk recited the Tight Headband Spell again. Wukong fell to the ground and rolled around in pain.

  "My head hurts!" he cried. "Stop. I will not try to hurt you again."

  The Tang Monk stopped and the monkey stood up.

  "Now will you cook some rice?" asked the monk.

  "Start a fire first," said Wukong.

## ③

  The monkey waited until the Tang Monk had turned his back. Again, he raised the iron bar. But the Tang Monk saw Wukong's shadow.

  "Wukong!" cried the Tang Monk once again, and Wukong fell to the ground.

  The Tang Monk looked furious as he recited the spell. Wukong's head pounded.

  "Stop!" cried the monkey.

  The Tang Monk stopped reciting the spell.

  "Do not try to hit me again," said the monk. "If you do, I will recite the spell until your head really does explode."

  "I am sorry, Master," said Wukong. "I will be good."

## ④

  The two traveled for a few more weeks. They arrived at a wide river.

  "How will we cross this river?" asked the monk.

  "It is too bad you are not a spirit," said Wukong. "I can leap over this river, but I cannot take you with me."

  "Why not?" asked the Tang Monk.

  "You are a human," said the monkey. "So you must make the journey all by yourself. I can only protect you. I cannot carry you."

  "What will we do then?" asked the monk.

## ⑤

  Before Wukong could answer, the water swelled and a dragon leaped from it.

  "Look out!" cried the monkey.

  He yanked the Tang Monk off the horse as the dragon struck. But by the time Wukong reacted, it was too late. The dragon swallowed the horse and dived back under water.

---

# 🇨🇳 第十六章：谁愿来取经

## ①

  悟空双手抱住脑袋，摔倒在地。他的眼睛鼓得大大的。

  "他要爆炸了！"他大喊着，看见唐僧在一旁小声念着什么。

  "什么？你在念什么？"悟空叫道。

  唐僧收了咒，悟空也就不疼了。

  "是观音菩萨教了我一段咒，"和尚说，"她把头箍交给我，就是为了让你守规矩。"

  悟空用力去拽头箍，可是怎么也摘不下来。

## ②

  "天哪！"悟空大叫。他跺了跺脚。"你骗我！"

  "这是为了你好，"唐僧说，"你刚才又想动粗。"

  悟空掏出金箍棒，朝唐僧打去。唐僧又念起紧箍咒来。悟空摔在地上，疼得直打滚。

  "疼死我了！"他叫道，"别念了，我再也不敢伤害你了。"

  唐僧停了咒，悟空站了起来。

  "这下你肯去煮饭了吧？"唐僧问。

  "你先去生火，"悟空嘟囔着。

## ③

  悟空等唐僧转过身去，又偷偷举起了金箍棒。可是唐僧从地上看到了悟空的影子。

  唐僧大喝一声，再次念起咒语，悟空又摔倒在地。

  唐僧满脸怒容，不停地念着咒。悟空头痛欲裂。

  "住口！"悟空大叫。

  唐僧停了咒。

  "你下次再敢打我，"和尚说，"我就把咒一直念到你脑袋真的炸开为止。"

  "师父，我错了，"悟空说，"我一定乖。"

## ④

  两个又走了几个星期，来到了一条宽阔的大河前。

  "这河怎么过呢？"唐僧问。

  "你不是神仙，真不方便，"悟空说，"我一个筋斗就能翻过去，可是带不了你。"

  "为什么？"唐僧问。

  "你是凡人，"悟空说，"取经的路只能你自己一步一步走。我只能保护你，不能背你。"

  "那怎么办？"唐僧发愁了。

## ⑤

  悟空还没来得及回答，河水忽然翻涌，一条白龙从水中腾空而起。

  "小心！"悟空大喊。

  他一把拽下唐僧，可是已经来不及了。白龙一口吞下了坐骑白马，转身又一头扎回了水里。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventeen: A Dragon in the River

## ①

  To the West — Chapter 17: A dragon in the river.

  "That dragon ate my horse!" cried the Tang monk. "How will I ever get to the western paradise? There are so many dangers along the way." He fell to his knees in despair.

  Wukong laughed. "Master, you worry too much. There will be many dangers on your journey. But you have me, the Monkey King, to protect you. All of heaven's soldiers couldn't defeat me. So why worry about a dragon?"

## ②

  The monkey stepped into the water and pulled out his iron rod. "I'll get the dragon to come out of the water."

  He looked down at the water and shouted, "Dragon! Get up here right now!"

  The dragon rose from the water. "Oh, there you are. Who are you?"

  "It doesn't matter who I am," shouted Wukong. "Give that horse back!"

## ③

  The monkey attacked the dragon with his iron rod. The dragon spun around, blocking the rod with his tail. Then with a flash, he dove back under the water.

  Wukong jumped his foot and yelled at the river, "Coward!"

  "What will we do?" asked the Tang monk. "I have no horse."

  "And we can't cross the river with that dragon in there," said Wukong. "I'll try another plan."

## ④

  The monkey stirred the water with his iron rod. The water became rough; waves crashed and churned. The water dragged mud up from the river bottom. Soon the river was brown and muddy.

  The dragon appeared again. "What on earth are you doing now?" he cried. "I'm trying to take a nap."

  "Give us back our horse!" demanded Wukong.

  "I can't," cried the dragon. "It's in my stomach."

## ⑤

  The monkey attacked the dragon again. But once more the dragon disappeared under the water. For more than three hours, Wukong yelled at the river. He yelled all kinds of insults, but the dragon would not come back up.

  Wukong climbed up the river bank and sat down next to the Tang monk. "That dragon is tough. I'm not afraid of him, but I can't beat him either. I need help."

  "Who can help you?" asked the Tang monk.

## ⑥

  Wukong thought for a moment. "Guanyin told me I can ask her for help if I need it."

  "Yes," said the Tang monk. "She told me the same thing."

  Wukong felt the headband and shot a look at the monk. "She already did help you. She gave you this tight headband." He sighed. "But it doesn't matter now. You wait here. I'll be back soon."

## ⑦

  Wukong shot into the air and flew south. Soon he came to Mount Potalaka in the South Sea. Guanyin was in a garden next to her pagoda.

  "Hello, Wukong," she said. "How is the journey going? I see you're wearing the headband."

  "Yes, thanks to your dirty tricks," said the monkey.

  Guanyin smiled. "You need that headband, Wukong. You are too violent and cruel."

## ⑧

  Wukong rolled his eyes. "Fine. I'm here because I have a problem. We reached a wide river with a dragon in it. The dragon ate our horse."

  "Did you tell the dragon that you're traveling with the Tang monk?" asked Guanyin.

  "No," said the monkey.

  "Why?" Guanyin sighed. "That dragon was waiting for you. When I met him, he was being punished for setting fire to his father's palace. I told him to help the Tang monk reach the western paradise. That way, he can earn forgiveness."

  Wukong scratched his head. "It's too late for that now. He won't come out of the water."

---

# 🇨🇳 第十七章：黑河遇龙


## ①

  往西去 —— 第十七集：河里的龙。

  "那条龙吃了我的马！"唐僧喊道，"我怎样才能到达西方极乐世界呢？一路上有这么多危险。"他绝望地跪了下来。

  悟空笑道："师父，你太担心了。你的旅途上会有很多危险。但有我齐天大圣保护你。全天的兵将都打不败我。所以何必担心一条龙呢？"

## ②

  悟空跨进水里，掏出他的铁棒，"我去叫那龙从水里出来。"

  他低头朝水里喊道："龙！马上给我上来！"

  龙从水里钻了出来，"哦，你来啦。你是谁？"

  "我是谁不重要，"悟空喊道，"把我的马还来！"

## ③

  悟空用铁棒攻击龙。龙转身用尾巴挡住了铁棒，然后一闪身又潜回了水里。

  悟空跺了跺脚，对着河面大喊："胆小鬼！"

  "我们怎么办呢？"唐僧问，"我没有马了。"

  "那龙在水里，我们也没法过河，"悟空说，"我再想个办法。"

## ④

  悟空用铁棒搅动河水。河水变得汹涌起来，波浪翻滚。河底的泥沙被搅了上来，很快河水变得又浑又黄。

  龙又出现了，"你到底在干什么？"他喊道，"我想睡个觉呢！"

  "把我们的马还来！"悟空命令道。

  "不行啊，"龙喊道，"它在我肚子里呢。"

## ⑤

  悟空再次攻击龙。但龙又一次潜入了水中。悟空对着河面喊了一个多时辰。他骂了各种各样的话，但龙就是不出来。
