> "I married Princess Hundred Flowers thirteen years ago," said the young man. "I found her in a forest just as a tiger was about to attack her. I saved her life and chased the tiger away."

  The king relaxed a little.

> "That was very brave."

> "Yes, it was very brave," said the young man. "However, that tiger has wanted revenge ever since. Some time ago it became a spirit. Now it disguises itself as a monk."

  The young man narrowed his eyes at the Tang Monk and pointed.

> "That monk!"

> "What?" cried the Tang Monk.

## ⑤

  The king frowned.

> "I don't believe you."

> "I'll prove it," said the young man.

  He pointed at the monk again and recited a spell. Light sparkled. Everybody gasped. Now a tiger sat in the Tang Monk's spot.

## ⑥

  Later, in the stable, a boy was giving hay to the Tang Monk's horse.

> "Did you hear about the Tang Monk?" asked another boy. "He was really a tiger spirit."

> "That young man changed him back and locked him up for him. Wow," said the first boy. "Where is the tiger now?"

> "He's locked up in a cage," said the other boy.

## ⑦

  That night, Bajie was sitting alone outside when he heard a voice.

> "Bajie."

  Bajie looked around.

> "Who's calling me?"

  He saw the horse peeking from behind a wall.

> "You're talking?" cried Bajie.

> "Yes," said the horse. "We have a problem. A young man turned the Tang Monk into a tiger. The monk is locked in a cage now."

> "Oh, I know!" cried Bajie. "It's terrible. Master is now a tiger and Wu Jing was captured by a monster." He sighed. "The journey is over. Let's just go home."

## ⑧

  The horse stamped on Bajie's foot with his hoof.

> "Ouch!" cried the pig. "Why did you do that?"

> "We're not going home," said the horse. "The young man is probably just the monster in disguise. We need to defeat him and save our companions."

> "But how?" asked Bajie.

  The horse thought for a minute.

> "You must find Wukong. He can help us."

  Bajie shook his head.

> "He won't help us."

---

# 🇨🇳 第三十五章：拜见国王


## ①

> "百花公主骗了我！"妖怪说道。

  他跺了跺脚，又叹了口气。

> "我对她生不起气来。我太爱她了。可是那头猪跑了，他会回去找国王，国王肯定会派兵的。"

  妖怪想了一会儿，终于有了主意。他来到公主的房间。

> "我的心上人，"妖怪说，"我要去见见你父亲。"

> "什么？"百花公主大吃一惊。

## ②

> "我要去告诉他我是多么好的一个人，"妖怪说，"我们大家都能成为幸福的一家人。"

  公主还没来得及说什么，妖怪已经转身离开了房间。

> "我得伪装一下，"他自言自语。

  他念了个快速咒语，光芒一闪，妖怪变成了一个英俊的年轻小伙子。他得意地笑了。

## ③

  八戒跑回宝象国，告诉国王他和悟净没能救出百花公主。八戒垂下了脑袋。

> "我跑的时候，悟净被妖怪抓住了。"

> "我们必须救回女儿，"国王说。他转向将军，"集合军队！"

  一名信使跑进大殿。

> "陛下，您的驸马来见您了。"信使说。

  国王一脸困惑。

> "我哪来的驸马？"

## ④

  一个英俊的年轻小伙子走进大殿。

> "岳丈大人好。很抱歉我一直没有来拜访您。"

> "你是谁？"国王问道。

> "我十三年前娶了百花公主，"年轻人说，"我在森林里发现她时，一只老虎正要扑向她。我救了她，把老虎赶跑了。"

  国王稍微放松了一些。

> "那倒是很勇敢。"

> "是的，非常勇敢，"年轻人说，"不过那只老虎从那以后一直想报仇。前阵子它修炼成了精，现在变成了一个和尚四处招摇撞骗。"

  年轻人眯起眼睛，指着唐僧。

> "就是那个和尚！"

> "什么？"唐僧大叫。

## ⑤

  国王皱起了眉头。

> "我不相信你。"

> "我来证明给你看，"年轻人说。

  他再次指向唐僧，念起了咒语。光芒一闪，众人大惊失色——坐在唐僧位置上的竟然是一只老虎。

## ⑥

  后来，在马厩里，一个小男孩正在给唐僧的马喂草料。

> "你听说唐僧的事了吗？"另一个男孩问道，"他原来是个老虎精。"

> "那个年轻人把他变回原形关了起来。哇，"第一个男孩说，"老虎现在在哪里？"

> "被关在笼子里了。"另一个男孩说。

## ⑦

  那天晚上，八戒独自坐在外面，忽然听到一个声音。

> "八戒。"

  八戒环顾四周。

> "谁在叫我？"

  他看到那匹马从墙后面探出头来。

> "你会说话？"八戒惊叫道。

> "是的，"马说，"我们遇到大麻烦了。一个年轻人把唐僧变成了老虎。那位师傅现在被关在笼子里。"

> "唉，我知道！"八戒大喊，"太可怕了。师父变成了老虎，悟净又被妖怪抓走了。"他叹了口气，"这趟旅程结束了，咱们还是各回各家吧。"

## ⑧

  马抬起蹄子踩了八戒一脚。

> "哎呦！"八戒叫了起来，"你为什么踩我？"

> "我们不回家，"马说，"那个年轻小伙子八成就是妖怪伪装的。我们必须打败他，救出同伴。"

> "可怎么打呢？"八戒问。

  马想了一会儿。

> "你必须去找悟空，只有他才能帮我们。"

  八戒摇了摇头。

> "他不会帮我们的。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Thirty-Six: Tricked Again

## ①

> "Why won't Wukong help us?" the horse asked Bajie.

  The pig sighed.

> "He told us not to look for him if we needed help. Plus, I kept telling Master to use the Tight Headband Spell. The monkey is really mad at me."

> "That doesn't matter now," said the horse. "You must get Wukong to come back."

  Bajie hesitated for a moment, and then leaped onto a cloud. He soared through the sky and soon arrived at the Fruit and Flower Mountain.

## ②

  He found Wukong sitting beside a big waterfall. Other monkeys and apes were nearby. They held swords and spears. They stared at Bajie silently.

> "Hello, Wukong," said the pig. "This is a lovely mountain."

  Wukong scowled.

> "What are you doing here, Bajie?"

  The pig looked at the ground.

> "The Tang Monk would like you to come back," he mumbled.

## ③

> "Well, that's too bad," said Wukong, standing up. "He told me to leave. I'll never help him again."

> "Please come back," said Bajie. "We all miss you."

> "I don't miss you," said Wukong. "You told Master to use the Tight Headband Spell. I should take out my iron bar and clobber you."

  Bajie forced a laugh.

> "I was just joking, Wukong. I knew you were really just protecting Master."

> "It wasn't funny," said Wukong. "That spell really hurts."

## ④

  The pig began to cry.

> "Please come back. The Tang Monk is in danger. Big danger. A monster turned him into a tiger. And Wu Jing was captured."

  Wukong shrugged.

> "Just tell the monster that you're friends with me, the Monkey King. He'll be scared and leave all of you alone."

> "Oh, I did tell him about you," Bajie lied.

> "Really?" Wukong leaned closer. "What did he say?"

  Bajie bit his lip.

> "He laughed and said that you're a tiny little coward."

## ⑤

  Wukong's eyes blazed with fury.

> "He will regret saying that. Let's go, Bajie!"

  The monster sat in the dining hall, still disguised as a handsome young man. He was eating a meal with the king and the queen. A servant came in and handed a note to the young man.

> "I'm sorry, Your Majesty, but I must go."

  He ran out of the dining hall. From behind a pillar, the servant watched the man leave. Light sparkled, and the servant turned into Bajie. The pig giggled.

> "The monster is going to be so surprised."

## ⑥

  Meanwhile, the young man ran outside and turned back into a monster. He flew through the air and returned to his pagoda. He burst through the door in a panic. Then he saw Princess Hundred Flowers and relaxed.

> "Oh, my sweet!" he cried. "I was so scared. I thought I'd lost you forever."

> "Why did you think that?" asked the princess.

  The monster sighed.

> "I got a note. It said there was a monkey here and he was trying to destroy my pagoda."

## ⑦

> "Oh, the monkey was here earlier," said the princess.

  The monster looked around.

> "He didn't destroy the pagoda. What did he want?"

  The princess hesitated.

> "You are not going to be happy about this. But he freed the Purple Spirit you had captured."

  The monster looked angry.

> "How dare he!"

> "The monkey did something else too," said the princess.

> "What?" asked the monster.

## ⑧

  There was a flash of light. Suddenly, Wukong stood before the monster. The monkey smiled.

> "I freed the princess too."

---

# 🇨🇳 第三十六章：再遭欺骗


## ①

> "悟空为什么不帮我们呢？"马问八戒。

  八戒叹了口气。

> "他说过出了事别去找他。再说呢，我一直怂恿师父念紧箍咒。猴子可被我气坏了。"

> "现在顾不了那么多了，"马说，"你必须去把悟空请回来。"

  八戒犹豫了一会儿，随即纵身跃上云端。他飞越天空，很快就到了花果山。

## ②

  他发现悟空正坐在一道大瀑布旁边。周围还有许多猴子和猿猴。他们拿着刀枪棍棒，默默地盯着八戒。

> "你好啊，悟空，"八戒说，"这座山真漂亮。"

  悟空板起了脸。

> "你来干什么，八戒？"

  八戒低下了头。

> "师父想请你回去，"他小声嘟囔。

## ③

> "哼，那可不行，"悟空站起来说，"他叫我走人的。我再也不会帮他的忙了。"

> "求你回去吧，"八戒说，"我们都很想你。"

> "我才不想你们，"悟空说，"你让师父念紧箍咒整我。我真该掏出铁棒狠狠敲你一顿。"

  八戒勉强挤出一个笑容。

> "我开玩笑的啦，悟空。我知道你其实是在保护师父。"

> "这一点也不好笑，"悟空说，"那紧箍咒真的很疼的。"

## ④

  八戒哭了起来。

> "求你回去吧。师父有危险，是大难。一个妖怪把他变成了老虎。悟净也被抓了。"

  悟空耸了耸肩。

> "你就跟妖怪说你是我的朋友——齐天大圣。他吓都吓死了，还怎么对付你们？"

> "哦，我跟他说起过你，"八戒撒了个谎。

> "真的？"悟空凑过来，"他怎么说？"

  八戒咬了咬嘴唇。

> "他哈哈大笑，说你是只胆小如鼠的小猴子。"

## ⑤

  悟空眼中怒火熊熊燃烧。

> "他会后悔说这话的。走吧，八戒！"

  此时，妖怪正坐在宴会厅里，仍旧伪装成英俊小伙子的模样。他正和国王、王后一起用餐。一个仆人走进来递给年轻人一封信。

> "抱歉，陛下，我有事得先走了。"

  他跑出了宴会厅。柱子后面，刚才的那个"仆人"目送他离去，只见光芒一闪，仆人变回了八戒。八戒暗暗窃喜。

> "妖怪看到我要大吃一惊了。"

## ⑥

  另一边，年轻人跑出宫门，变回了妖怪的模样。他腾空而起，飞回了自己的塔。他冲进门，一脸慌张，但看到百花公主后松了一口气。

> "哦，我的心肝！"他叫道，"吓死我了。我还以为再也见不到你了。"

> "你怎么会这样想？"公主问道。

  妖怪叹了口气。

> "我收到一封信，说有一只猴子在这里，企图毁坏我的塔。"

## ⑦

> "哦，那只猴子确实来过，"公主说。

  妖怪环顾四周。

> "可塔没有被毁呀。他来干什么？"

  公主犹豫了一下。

> "你听了不会高兴的。他把你抓来的紫阳真人放走了。"

  妖怪顿时大怒。

> "他怎敢如此！"

> "猴子还干了另外一件事呢，"公主说。

> "什么？"妖怪问道。

## ⑧

  只听见一声闪光，悟空突然出现在妖怪面前。猴子微微一笑。

> "我还把公主也救走了。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Thirty-Seven: Missing from Heaven

## ①

> "Who are you?" the monster asked the monkey. "What are you doing here?"

> "I am Sun Wukong, King of the Fruit and Flower Mountain," said the monkey. "I'm helping the Tang Monk reach the Western Paradise. Five hundred years ago, I caused a lot of trouble in heaven. Now I'm here to cause a lot of trouble for you."

> "I remember you," said the monster.

  Wukong pulled out his iron bar and swung it. *Whoosh!* The monster vanished.

## ②

  Wukong leaped into the air. He looked in every direction but didn't see the monster anywhere.

> "That monster said he remembered me," thought Wukong. "He must be from heaven. I'll go up there now to see if any spirits are missing."

  Wukong soared higher and higher until he reached the Southern Gate of Heaven.

> "Greetings, Wukong!" said the guard.

> "There's a monster on Earth causing trouble for the Tang Monk," said Wukong. "I think the monster is a spirit who escaped from heaven. Is anyone missing?"

## ③

  The guard sent a messenger to check. A moment later, the messenger returned with a guard.

> "You found the Wood Wolf Star," said the guard.

> "Who?" asked Wukong.

> "The Wood Wolf Star is a wolf spirit who lives in heaven," said the guard. "He escaped thirteen days ago and I've been looking all over for him."

  Wukong rubbed his chin.

> "That makes sense. The monster kidnapped a princess thirteen years ago on Earth. Thirteen years on Earth is equal to thirteen days in heaven."

## ④

  The guard nodded.

> "Yes. Let's go. I'll help you catch the Wood Wolf Star."

  Wukong went down to Earth with the guard. From the sky, the guard called down.

> "Wolf Star! Come up here at once!"

  Wukong saw a small splash in a river below. The monster leaped out. The monster turned into a wolf and flew up to the god. The wolf looked nervous.

## ⑤

> "You will be punished," said the god. He turned and led the wolf back up to heaven.

  Wukong flew to the Precious Image Kingdom and went into the palace. A big celebration was taking place. The king and queen were both hugging their daughter, Princess Hundred Flowers. The princess saw Wukong and smiled.

> "Father, Mother, this is Sun Wukong. He's a monkey spirit who rescued me and Sha Wu Jing earlier."

  The king and queen bowed.

> "We can never thank you enough," said the queen. "You and your friends have made us very happy."

## ⑥

> "It was nothing at all," said Wukong with a laugh. "We save people from monsters and demons almost every day."

  He looked around.

> "Where's the Tang Monk?"

  The king looked at the ground.

> "Didn't your friends tell you? He's really a tiger."

> "That's it," said Wukong. "That monster turned him into a tiger. That's all. Where is he?"

  The king and queen led Wukong out of the hall. They went down a flight of stairs and arrived at the palace dungeon. A large tiger sat in a cage.

## ⑦

> "Don't worry, Master," said Wukong. "I'll change you back into yourself."

  Wukong recited a spell. Bright light surrounded the cage for a moment. The Tang Monk was back. Wukong grabbed the bars and twisted them apart.

> "Thank you, Wukong!" cried the monk. He took the monkey's hands in his own. "I never should have told you to leave. Will you continue to journey with us?"

  Wukong smiled.

> "Of course, Master. We will reach the Western Paradise together."

---

# 🇨🇳 第三十七章：天宫失踪


## ①

> "你是谁？"妖怪问道，"你来这里干什么？"

> "我是花果山大王孙悟空，"猴子说，"我是护送唐僧前往西天取经的。五百年前，我在天庭大闹了一场。现在轮到你尝尝我的厉害了。"

> "我记得你，"妖怪说道。

  悟空掏出铁棒，抡了一下。呼！妖怪消失了。

## ②

  悟空跃入空中，四下张望，却到处都找不到妖怪的踪影。

> "那妖怪说记得我，"悟空想，"他一定来自天庭。我上去看看有没有哪路神仙不见了。"

  悟空越飞越高，一直飞到了南天门外。

> "悟空，你好！"守卫说。

> "地球上有个妖怪正在找唐僧的麻烦，"悟空说，"我猜他是从天庭逃走的精灵。你们有没有谁丢了？"

## ③

  守卫派了一名信使去查看。不一会儿，信使带着一位天神回来了。

> "就是木狼星，"天神说。

> "谁？"悟空问。

> "木狼星是天庭的一只狼精，"天神说，"他十三天前逃走了，我一直在到处找他。"

  悟空摸了摸下巴。

> "这就对了。妖怪十三年前在人间掳走了一位公主。人间十三年就是天庭十三天。"

## ④

  天神点了点头。

> "不错。走吧，我来帮你捉拿木狼星。"

  悟空跟随天神下到了人间。天神在空中向下喊叫。

> "狼星！立刻上来！"

  悟空看见下方小河里溅起一阵水花。妖怪一跃而出，变成了一只狼，飞到了天神身边。狼一脸慌张。

## ⑤

> "你将会受到惩罚，"天神说。他转身带着狼回到了天庭。

  悟空飞回宝象国，进入了宫殿。宫殿里正在举行盛大的庆祝活动，国王和王后都拥抱着他们的女儿百花公主。公主看到悟空，露出了微笑。

> "父王、母后，这位是孙悟空，他是一位猴仙，之前救出了我和沙悟净。"

  国王和王后鞠躬致谢。

> "我们感激不尽，"王后说，"你和你的朋友们让我们太高兴了。"

## ⑥

> "这算不了什么，"悟空大笑着说，"我们每天都得从妖怪手中救人呢。"

  他四下看了看。

> "唐僧呢？"

  国王低下了头。

> "你的伙伴没告诉你吗？他变成了一只老虎。"

> "哼，我就知道，"悟空说，"是那个妖怪把他变成老虎的。他在哪里？"

  国王和王后带着悟空出大殿，走下台阶，来到了地牢。一只大老虎被关在笼子里。

## ⑦

> "别担心，师父，"悟空说，"我马上就变回来。"

  悟空念起了咒语。明亮的光芒把笼子笼罩了一会儿。唐僧就恢复了人形。悟空抓住铁栏，用力一掰，把牢笼扯开了。

> "谢谢你，悟空！"唐僧叫道。他把猴子的手紧紧握住，"我真不该赶你走。你还愿意跟我们一起取经吗？"

  悟空笑了。

> "当然愿意，师父。我们一起到达西天。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Thirty-Eight: Bajie Tries to Sleep

## ①

  Time passed and it was soon spring. The air grew warm, flowers bloomed, and birds swooped from tree to tree. The road Wukong and the others were traveling on began to go up a mountain. Wukong stopped the group.

> "Bajie, go ahead and search the mountain. There might be a demon up there and I don't want Master to get hurt. Move, pig!"

> "You make me do all the hard work," grumbled the pig.

  He headed up the mountain road.

## ②

> "I'm going to follow the pig," Wukong turned to the Tang Monk and Wu Jing. "I want to make sure he really searches the mountain."

  The monkey turned invisible and followed Bajie up the road. The pig walked for a few minutes. When he was sure his companions wouldn't hear him, he turned around.

> "You dummies," said Bajie. "You make me do all the hard work. Well, guess what? I'm not going to search this mountain. I'm going to take a nap instead. And when I come back, I'll lie and say I searched the mountain."

  Bajie found a big log. He laid down behind it and fell fast asleep.

## ③

> "This pig is so lazy!" thought Wukong. "How could you manage him?"

  The monkey turned himself into a woodpecker and pecked the log. Bajie rolled over and mumbled. Wukong pecked again. The pig sat up.

> "Quit tapping, you annoying woodpecker! I'm trying to sleep."

  He fell asleep again. Wukong landed on Bajie's head. *Tap, tap, tap, tap, tap.*

> "Ouch!" cried Bajie, jumping to his feet. "Who..." The woodpecker flew away. Bajie rubbed his head. "I can't even take a nap. I guess I'll go back down."

## ④

  When Bajie found his companions, he lied.

> "I searched the entire mountain," he said. "It's safe."

> "Did you see any demons or monsters?" asked Wukong.

  Bajie shook his head.

> "How about woodpeckers?" asked the monkey. "Did you see any of them?"

  The pig looked surprised.

> "What? How did you...?"

> "That was me, Bajie!" shouted Wukong. "You took a nap. You didn't search the mountain at all."

## ⑤

  Bajie hung his head.

> "You should be ashamed of yourself, Bajie," said Wu Jing.

  The Tang Monk frowned.

> "Please go back and search the mountain, Bajie."

  The pig headed back up the road. He had walked for a while when he saw a fox.

> "I know that's you, Wukong!" he shouted. He swung his rake. The fox trotted away.

  A robin flew past Bajie's head.

> "Get away from me, Wukong!" yelped the pig, as he waved the rake at the bird.

  Bajie tripped and fell.

## ⑥

> "Wukong!" shouted the pig. "I know you're here. You're invisible and you just tripped me."

  He got back up and stood still for a moment. When he didn't see or hear Wukong, he continued walking. Every time Bajie saw an animal, he waved his rake and yelped.

  The road became very steep. The pig soon came to a cave. In front of the cave was a demon. Bajie held out his rake.

> "Tell me who you are!" he demanded.

> "My name is Golden Horn," said the demon. "Who are you?"

## ⑦

> "I am Zhu Bajie," said the pig. "I'm traveling to the Western Paradise with the Tang Monk."

> "Oh, the Tang Monk." A smile curled along the demon's lips. "I have heard that anyone who eats the Tang Monk will live forever."

---

# 🇨🇳 第三十八章：八戒想睡觉


## ①

  时光飞逝，转眼到了春天。天气变暖了，百花盛开，鸟儿在树枝间飞来飞去。悟空一行人走的路开始向山上延伸。悟空让大伙儿停了下来。

> "八戒，你去前面搜一下这座山。上面可能有妖怪，我可不想师父出什么事。快去吧，猪头！"

> "干吗总是让我干苦活？"八戒嘟囔着。

  他沿着山路往上走去。

## ②

> "我要跟着这头猪，"悟空对唐僧和悟净说，"我得确保他真上山搜索了。"

  猴子隐了身，跟着八戒上了山。八戒走了几分钟，确认同伴们听不到他说话了，就转了身。

> "一群笨蛋，"八戒说，"老是让我干苦活。你们猜怎么着？我才不去搜这座山呢。我要睡一觉去。等我回去，就说整座山都搜遍了。"

  八戒找到一根大圆木，躺在后面呼呼大睡起来。

## ③

> "这猪也太懒了吧！"悟空心想，"拿他真没办法。"

  猴子变成了一只啄木鸟，去啄那根木头。八戒翻了个身，嘟囔了几句。悟空又啄了一下。八戒坐了起来。

> "别啄了，你这只讨厌的啄木鸟！我正要睡觉呢。"

  他又躺下睡着了。悟空落在八戒的头顶上。笃、笃、笃、笃、笃。

> "哎呦！"八戒跳了起来，"谁......"啄木鸟飞走了。八戒揉着脑袋说，"连个觉都睡不成。唉，我还是下山回去吧。"

## ④

  八戒找到同伴们，撒了个谎。

> "整座山我都搜过了，"他说，"安全得很。"

> "有没有看到什么妖怪魔鬼？"悟空问。

  八戒摇了摇头。

> "有没有看到啄木鸟？"猴子又问，"看到过吗？"

  八戒一脸惊讶。

> "什么？你怎么......？"

> "那就是我，八戒！"悟空大喊道，"你睡了一觉。你压根儿就没搜山。"

## ⑤

  八戒耷拉着脑袋。

> "八戒，你自己应该感到惭愧，"悟净说。

  唐僧皱起了眉头。

> "请重新回去搜一下山吧，八戒。"

  八戒又沿着山路往上走。走了一会儿，他看到一只狐狸。

> "我知道是你，悟空！"他大叫一声，挥起钉耙砸去。狐狸一溜烟跑了。

  一只知更鸟从八戒头上飞过。

> "滚开，悟空！"八戒一边朝鸟挥舞钉耙一边喊。

  八戒一不留神，绊倒在地。

## ⑥

> "悟空！"八戒大喊，"我知道你在这里。你隐身了，刚才绊倒的就是你！"

  他爬起来，站了一会儿。既没看到悟空，也没听到悟空的动静，于是他继续往前走。一路上，八戒每看到一只动物，就挥着钉耙大叫。

  路变得越来越陡。八戒不久就到了一个洞口，洞前站着一个妖怪。八戒举起钉耙。

> "报上你的名号！"他大声喝道。

> "我叫金角大王，"妖怪说，"你又是谁？"

## ⑦

> "我是猪八戒，"八戒说，"我跟唐僧一起去西天取经。"

> "哦，唐僧。"妖怪的嘴角浮起一丝微笑，"我听说吃了唐僧肉就能长生不老。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Thirty-Nine: The Injured Monk

## ①

  Bajie swung his rake at the demon Golden Horn.

> "You'll never harm the Tang Monk!" shouted the pig. "My rake is very powerful."

  Bajie rushed toward Golden Horn. But the demon was strong. Bajie was knocked out. When he woke up, he was tied up in a dark cave.

## ②

> "Bajie is taking a long time to search the mountain," said the Tang Monk. "I hope he's okay."

> "I'm not sure," said Wukong. "He probably went back to sleep. I should have followed him again."

> "Let's keep walking," said Wu Jing. "We'll find Bajie along the way."

> "We must stay alert though," said Wukong. "We still don't know if there are any demons on this mountain."

  The group headed up the mountain.

## ③

  Soon they heard a voice.

> "Help me!" cried a man.

> "Someone is in trouble," said the Tang Monk. He and his companions hurried ahead and found an old monk lying near the road.

> "Goodness!" cried the old monk. "You must help me!"

  The Tang Monk got down from his horse.

> "Of course we will help you. Please stand up."

## ④

> "I can't," said the old man. "My leg is injured. It hurts terribly." He started to cry. "We'll never get back home."

> "Please don't cry," said the Tang Monk. "We will help you. How did your leg get hurt?"

> "A tiger attacked me," said the old monk.

  Wukong looked suspiciously at the man.

> "He isn't really a monk," he thought. "And I'm sure he wants to harm Master. But I can't tell Master that. He won't believe me."

## ⑤

> "Wukong," said the Tang Monk. "Please carry this poor monk down the mountain."

  Wukong walked over and picked up the old monk.

> "Ouch!" cried the monk.

> "Be careful, Wukong," said the Tang Monk. "His leg is hurt badly."

  The group continued along the road. Wukong carried the injured monk. He walked slowly, letting the Tang Monk and Wu Jing go ahead.

## ⑥

> "I know you're really a demon," the monkey whispered. "And I know you want to eat the Tang Monk."

> "I don't know what you're talking about," said the monk. "I'm just a simple monk who was attacked by a tiger."

  Wukong laughed.

> "Do you know who I am? I am Sun Wukong. Heaven's entire army couldn't defeat me. You're going to wish you'd never tried to harm the Tang Monk."

## ⑦

  As Wukong talked, he felt a heavy weight pressing down on him. He glanced up and realized an entire mountain was balanced on top of his head. The monkey laughed again.

> "So you're going to use magic tricks to trap me under a mountain? Well, let me tell you, Buddha himself once trapped me under a mountain, and I was able to lift it."

  Wukong felt more weight. Now he had two mountains on top of him. He walked more slowly.

> "This still isn't enough weight to stop me," he said. "Now that the Tang Monk isn't around, I should clobber you with my iron bar."

## ⑧

  Suddenly, the old monk vanished. A third mountain appeared on top of the first two. Wukong's knees buckled and all three mountains crashed down on top of him. The monkey was trapped.

  The old monk appeared again. There was a flash of light as he changed back into his demon form. Golden Horn laughed with delight.

> "Wukong was the most powerful of these travelers. It will be easy to defeat Wu Jing. Tonight I will dine on the Tang Monk."

---

# 🇨🇳 第三十九章：受伤的高僧


## ①

  八戒抡起钉耙朝金角大王砸去。

> "你休想伤害师父！"八戒大喊道，"我的钉耙可不是吃素的。"

  八戒朝金角冲过去。可是妖怪力大无比，八戒被打得昏了过去。等他醒来时，已经被绑在一个黑暗的山洞里。

## ②

> "八戒搜山搜了这么久，"唐僧说，"真希望他没事。"

> "不好说，"悟空道，"他八成又跑去睡觉了。我真该再跟上去盯紧他。"

> "咱们继续赶路吧，"悟净说，"路上也许能找到八戒。"

> "不过我们得提高警惕，"悟空说，"还不确定这座山上有没有妖怪。"

  一行人继续向山上走去。

## ③

  不一会儿，他们听到了一个声音。

> "救命啊！"一个男人在喊叫。

> "有人遇难了，"唐僧说。他和徒弟们赶紧朝前走，发现一个老和尚躺在路边。

> "善人啊！"老和尚叫道，"求求你们救救我！"

  唐僧下了马。

> "我们当然会帮你。请站起来吧。"

## ④

> "我站不起来，"老头说，"我的腿受伤了，疼得要命。"他哭了起来，"我们再也回不了家了。"

> "请别哭了，"唐僧说，"我们会帮你的。你的腿是怎么伤的？"

> "一只老虎攻击了我，"老和尚说。

  悟空狐疑地打量着那个人。

> "他才不是什么真正的和尚，"悟空想，"而且我敢肯定他是要害师父的。可是我不能告诉师父，他不会信的。"

## ⑤

> "悟空，"唐僧说，"请背着这位可怜的师傅下山。"

  悟空走过去，把老和尚背了起来。

> "哎呦！"老和尚叫了一声。

> "轻一点，悟空，"唐僧说，"他的腿伤得很重。"

  一行人继续沿着山路走。悟空背着受伤的和尚，故意走得很慢，让唐僧和悟净走在前面。

## ⑥

> "我知道你其实是个妖怪，"猴子低声说，"我也知道你想吃唐僧。"

> "我不明白你在说什么，"和尚说，"我只是个被老虎袭击的普通和尚罢了。"

  悟空笑了。

> "你知道我是谁吗？我是孙悟空。天兵天将都打不过我。你敢害我师父，就等着后悔吧。"

## ⑦

  悟空正说着，忽然觉得一股沉重的力量压了下来。他抬头一看——发现一整座大山压在了自己头上。猴子又笑了。

> "想用妖术把我压在山下？我告诉你，如来佛祖当年把我压在五行山下，我都能把它扛起来。"

  悟空觉得更重了——现在他头顶上有两座山了。他的脚步慢了下来。

> "这点分量还不足以拦住我，"他说，"等师父走远了，我就用铁棒收拾你。"

## ⑧

  突然，老和尚消失了。第三座山出现在前两座之上。悟空双腿一软，三座山轰然压了下来。猴子被彻底困住了。

  老和尚再次现身。一道闪光之后，他又变回了妖怪的本来面目。金角大王得意地大笑。

> "悟空是这些行者中最厉害的，剩下的悟净就不足为虑了。今晚，我就拿唐僧当晚餐！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty: The Magic Gold

## ①

  Bajie was in the cave when the door opened. Two small demons entered, dragging Wu Jing and the Tang Monk.

> "What happened?" cried Bajie after the demons left.

> "A demon attacked us," said Wu Jing. "I tried to fight him but he was too powerful."

> "I'm worried," said the Tang Monk. "We don't know what happened to Wukong."

## ②

  In another room inside the cave, Golden Horn talked to some smaller demons. They all laughed when Golden Horn told them that Wukong was trapped under three mountains.

> "Let's celebrate!" said one demon.

> "Not yet," said Golden Horn. "I'm afraid some Wukong might escape."

  He handed a gourd to one of the demons.

> "Take this magic gourd to the monkey. Say his name and he will be sucked into the gourd. In an hour, he will turn into liquid."

## ③

  Elsewhere, Wukong pushed as hard as he could. But the mountains were too heavy.

> "How will I ever get out of this?" thought the monkey.

  He was about to push again when the mountains rose into the air. Wukong jumped to his feet and looked around. A spirit stood nearby.

> "Wukong, I am the spirit of these mountains. Please forgive me. I tried to stop that demon from taking my mountains, but he was too powerful. I'm afraid some demons would be able to escape."

  The spirit bowed and then vanished with the mountains.

## ④

> "I'm lucky that spirit arrived," said Wukong. "Now I must find my companions. I wonder where that demon lives."

  He spotted a small demon coming down the road. The demon was carrying a gourd. Wukong ducked behind a rock before the demon saw him.

> "Another demon," thought the monkey. "He probably knows the one who trapped me under the mountains."

  Wukong made himself look like a demon and stepped back onto the road.

## ⑤

> "Hello!" he called. "Where are you going?"

> "My master sent me to capture Sun Wukong," said the demon.

> "Ha ha!" Wukong laughed. "I know that monkey and I don't like him at all. I'll help you capture him."

> "Thank you," said the demon. "But I can catch him myself quite easily."

> "Oh really?" asked Wukong. "How will you catch him?"

  The demon showed Wukong his gourd.

> "This gourd is magical. If it holds a demon or a spirit, I just have to say, 'Sun Wukong!' and he'll be sucked into it. After an hour, he'll turn into liquid."

## ⑥

  "Huh!" Wukong laughed. "I have a better gourd."

  He quickly plucked a hair and turned it into a gourd. He showed the gourd to the demon.

> "It can hold all of heaven."

  The demon looked interested.

> "I wish I had your gourd."

> "Well," said Wukong. "I might be willing to trade gourds with you."

  The demon gave Wukong a suspicious look.

> "How do I know you're telling the truth? Prove that your gourd can hold all of heaven. Then we'll trade."

## ⑦

> "I'll prove it to you," said Wukong.

  The monkey recited a quick spell and left his body standing on the road. He flew fast up to heaven.

> "I must make it look like heaven got sucked into this gourd," he thought. "I'll ask the guard to close the gate and dim the stars. Then it will look like heaven is gone."

  Greetings, Wukong. Said the guard at the Southern Gate of Heaven.

> "I need to pretend that heaven has been sucked into a gourd," said Wukong. "When I say the word, close the gate and dim the stars."

  The guard frowned.

> "I can't do that."

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十章：金箍棒


## ①

  八戒在山洞里待着，忽然门开了。两个小妖怪拖进来了悟净和唐僧。

> "怎么回事？"妖怪走后八戒叫了起来。

> "一个妖怪来攻击我们，"悟净说，"我试图跟他打，可他太厉害了。"

> "我担心的是，"唐僧说，"我们不知道悟空到底怎么样了。"

## ②

  在山洞的另一间屋子里，金角大王正在跟手下的小妖怪说话。当金角把悟空被三座大山压住的事告诉大家时，他们都哄笑起来。

> "咱们庆祝一下吧！"一个小妖怪说。

> "还不行，"金角大王说，"万一悟空跑了呢。"

  他把一个葫芦递给一个小妖怪。

> "拿着这个宝葫芦去找那只猴子。只要叫他的名字，他就会被吸进葫芦里。过上一个小时，他就会化成水。"

## ③

  另一边，悟空正拼命地推，可是山实在太重了。

> "我怎样才能逃出去呢？"猴子心想。

  他正准备再用力，忽然三座山被搬了起来。悟空一跃而起，四下张望。一位山神站在旁边。

> "悟空，我是这山神。实在抱歉。那个妖怪抢我的山，我拼命想拦住他，可他法力太高强了。那些妖怪恐怕是要作恶了。"

  山神鞠了一躬，然后带着山消失了。

## ④

> "幸亏山神来了，"悟空说，"现在我得去找同伴们。不知道那妖怪住在哪里。"

  他看到一个小妖怪沿着山路走来，手中拿着一个葫芦。悟空赶紧躲到石头后面，不让小妖怪发现。

> "又是妖怪，"猴子想，"他八成认识把我压在下面的那个。"

  悟空变成了一个妖怪，回到路上。

## ⑤

> "你好！"他招呼道，"去哪呀？"

> "我大王派我去捉拿孙悟空，"小妖怪说。

> "哈哈！"悟空大笑，"那只猴子我认识，我可不待见他。不如我帮你去抓他吧。"

> "谢谢你了，"小妖怪说，"不过我自己就能轻松抓住他。"

> "哦？真的吗？"悟空问，"怎么抓？"

  小妖怪把葫芦拿给悟空看。

> "这个葫芦是法宝。只要对着妖怪或神仙叫他的名字，比如'孙悟空！'他就会被吸进去。过上一个小时，他就化成水了。"

## ⑥

  "哼！"悟空笑了，"我有一个更好的葫芦。"

  他拔下一根毫毛，瞬间变成了一个大葫芦。他把葫芦拿给小妖怪看。

> "这个葫芦能把整个天庭都装进去。"

  小妖怪来了兴趣。

> "我真想拥有你的葫芦。"

> "要不，"悟空说，"咱们交换葫芦怎么样？"

  小妖怪一脸怀疑。

> "我怎么知道你说的是真话？证明一下你的葫芦能装下天庭，咱们再交换。"

## ⑦

> "我就证明给你看，"悟空说。

  猴子念了个咒语，留下肉身站在路上，元神飞上了天庭。

> "我得让天庭看起来像是被葫芦吸进去了，"他想，"我让守门的天官关上南天门，再把星星都遮住，看起来就像天庭消失了。"

  他飞到南天门。

> "你好啊，悟空，"南天门的天官说。

> "我需要假装天庭被葫芦吸进去了，"悟空说，"听我号令，把南天门关上，再把星星都熄了。"

  天官皱起了眉头。

> "这可不行。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-One: A Trade

## ①

  Wukong was angry at the guard at the southern gate of heaven.

> "Why can't you close the gate and dim the stars?"

  The guard looked nervous.

> "I could do that only if I have permission from the Jade Emperor."

> "I'm trying to save the Tang monk!" shouted Wukong. "But a demon is planning to eat him!"

> "I'm sorry," said the guard. "But I can't help you!"

  Wukong's eyes became wide and angry. He pulled the iron bar out of his ear.

## ②

  A messenger ran into the cloud palace and bowed.

> "Sun Wukong is at the southern gate of heaven, Your Majesty. He's going to destroy heaven if we don't do what he says."

  The Jade Emperor slammed his fist down.

> "That rotten monkey! What does he want?"

> "He wants us to close the gate and dim the stars," said the messenger.

> "Why?" asked the Emperor.

> "He wants to pretend heaven got sucked into a gourd," said the messenger.

  The Jade Emperor looked confused.

> "Why does he want to do that?"

> "He didn't say," said the messenger. "He just said he's trying to save the Tang monk."

  The Jade Emperor sighed.

> "You have my permission to close the gate and dim the stars. I don't want any more trouble from that monkey."

## ③

  The messenger returned to the gate.

> "We will close the gate and dim the stars," he said.

> "Good," said Wukong. He put the iron bar back in his ear.

  The sky went dark. Wukong had returned to his body, which was still in disguise as a demon.

> "Now I will call to heaven," said the monkey to the demon. "The whole place will get sucked into this gourd." He held up the gourd. "Heaven!"

  Right away the sky went dark.

> "Amazing!" cried the demon.

> "All of heaven is now in that gourd," said Wukong. "All the stars, planets, spirits, and gods are in here. Even the cloud palaces."

> "With the Jade Emperor too?"

## ④

> "Now I will let heaven back out." He held up the gourd. "Heaven, return!"

  The sky lit up again.

> "It works!" said the demon.

> "Let's trade gourds." He handed his gourd to Wukong. Wukong gave the fake gourd to the demon. Then he made the real gourd tiny and hid it in his robe.

> "I'll try to capture heaven now," said the demon. He held up the gourd. "Heaven!"

  Nothing happened.

> "Heaven!" said the demon again. "Heaven! Heaven!"

  He looked at the gourd.

> "Lord! This gourd isn't working! What's wrong with it?"

  Wukong laughed and made the fake gourd disappear. Then he made himself invisible.

> "I was tricked!" cried the demon. "I must tell Golden Horn!"

## ⑤

  The demon ran off and Wukong followed. Soon the road went up a mountain. The demon ran into a cave. Wukong made himself visible and stormed into the cave.

  Looking around at the group of demons, he pulled out his iron bar.

> "Return my friends at once!" he shouted. "Or I'll clobber all of you!"

  The small demons cried out. They ran in every direction, tripping over one another.

  Wukong swung his iron bar at Golden Horn. The demon stepped out of the way and pulled a golden rope from his sleeve. He swung the rope and it stretched toward Wukong.

  The monkey tried to get out of the way, but the rope snapped at him. It looped around his waist. The more Wukong tried to wriggle free, the tighter the rope got.

> "Ah!"

  Golden Horn laughed.

> "You'll never escape the golden rope. Tonight I will dine on the Tang monk!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十一章：交易


## ①

  悟空对南天门的守卫很生气。

> "你为什么不能关上天门、遮住星光？"

  守卫看起来很紧张。

> "那得玉皇大帝允许才行呀。"

> "我要去救唐和尚！"悟空大喊道，"有个妖怪要吃掉他！"

> "对不起，"守卫说道，"我帮不了你！"

  悟空气得双眼圆睁。他从耳朵里掏出了铁棒。

## ②

  一名使者跑进云宫跪下禀报。

> "陛下，孙悟空正在南天门，他说如果我们不听他的，他就要毁灭天宫。"

  玉皇大帝一掌拍了下去。

> "可恶的猴子！他要干什么？"

> "他要我们关上天门、遮住星光，"使者回答。

> "为什么？"玉帝问。

> "他想假装天宫被吸进葫芦里了，"使者说。

  玉皇大帝一脸困惑。

> "他干嘛要这么做？"

> "他没说，"使者回答，"他只说是要去救唐和尚。"

  玉皇大帝叹了口气。

> "好吧，准许他关上天门、遮住星光。我可不想再被那只猴子折腾了。"

## ③

  使者回到南天门。

> "我们答应关上天门、遮住星光，"他说。

> "好的，"悟空说。他把铁棒放回耳朵里。

  天空暗了下来。悟空回到了自己的身体，他那时仍装成小妖的模樣。

> "现在我要呼唤天宫了，"悟空对小妖说，"整个天宫都会被吸进这个葫芦。"他举起葫芦大喊："天宫！"

  天空一下就黑了。

> "太厉害了！"小妖惊叫道。

> "整个天宫都装进葫芦里了，"悟空说，"所有的星星、行星、仙人和神明都在这里面，连云宫也在。"

> "玉皇大帝也在吗？"

## ④

> "现在我把天宫放出来。"他举起葫芦喊道："天宫，回来！"

  天空又亮了。

> "真的灵验！"小妖称赞道。

> "我们换葫芦吧。"小妖把葫芦递给了悟空。悟空把假葫芦给了他，然后将真葫芦变小藏进袍子里。

> "现在我来试试吸天宫，"小妖说。他举起葫芦喊道："天宫！"

  什么都没发生。

> "天宫！"小妖又喊，"天宫！天宫！"

  他看了看葫芦。

> "天哪！这葫芦不灵了！怎么回事？"

  悟空大笑一声，让假葫芦消失了，然后隐了身。

> "我上当了！"小妖大哭，"我得去报告金角大王！"

## ⑤

  小妖拔腿就跑，悟空跟在后面。不一会儿路通到了一座山上，小妖跑进了一个洞府。悟空恢复了真身，大摇大摆地闯了进去。

  他环顾四周的群妖，抽出铁棒。

> "马上放了我朋友！"他大喝道，"不然把你们统统打死！"

  小妖们吓得尖叫起来，到处乱跑，互相绊倒。

  悟空挥棒朝金角打去。金角侧身躲开，从袖中取出一条金绳一甩，金绳伸展开来朝悟空飞去。

  悟空想躲开，但金绳已缠上他的腰身。他越是挣扎，绳子勒得越紧。

> "哎哟！"

  金角哈哈大笑。

> "你休想逃出金绳的缠绕！今晚我就吃唐和尚！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Two: Sun Kong Wu

## ①

  Wukong struggled to free himself from the golden rope. The gourd fell from his robe.

> "My magic gourd!" said Golden Horn, picking it up.

  He dragged Wukong to a dark room in the cave and locked him in.

  Right away, Wukong made himself tiny and escaped. He flew down a tunnel and squeezed through the cave's main door. Once he was outside, he returned to his normal size. He banged on the cave door.

> "Open up right now!"

  The door flew open and Golden Horn appeared.

## ②

> "Sun Wukong!" shouted the demon. "How did you escape?"

> "I'm not Sun Wukong," the monkey lied.

> "What? Do you look just like him?" said Golden Horn.

> "Yes, I do," said Wukong. "Sun Wukong is my twin brother. My name is Sun Wu Kong."

> "Why are you here, Sun Wu Kong?" asked Golden Horn.

> "I know you captured my brother," said Wukong. "Set him free."

  Golden Horn laughed.

> "I'm not going to do that."

> "Oh, that's too bad," said Wukong, pretending to feel bad. "I was hoping to solve this problem without violence." He took the iron bar out of his ear.

## ③

  Golden Horn had been holding the gourd behind his back the whole time. He quickly held it up and shouted.

> "Sun Wu Kong, shoo!"

  Wukong was sucked into the gourd. Golden Horn put a cap on the gourd and went back into his cave.

  Inside the gourd, Wukong stamped his foot.

> "How will I get out of here? I know I won't turn into liquid because I'm going to live forever. But I still have to save my friends."

  He tapped his chin.

> "I have an idea."

  He plucked a hair and made it look almost exactly like himself. There was just one difference. The fake Wukong had no legs. Next, Wukong made a hair look like a puddle. He placed the fake Wukong on the puddle. Now it looked as if the fake Wukong's legs had turned into liquid.

## ④

  Then the monkey made himself very, very tiny. Wukong went to the opening of the gourd and shouted.

> "Oh no! My legs turned into liquid!"

  The gourd shook as Golden Horn removed the cap. The tiny Wukong leaped out unseen. Golden Horn peered into the gourd and saw the fake Wukong in the puddle.

> "Ah! The monkey's legs did turn into liquid. Soon this entire body will be liquid. Ha! Ha!" Golden Horn laughed again and closed the gourd.

  He put the gourd down and started eating.

  The real Wukong returned to his normal size and then made himself look like a demon. He walked over to Golden Horn.

> "Hello, sir," said Wukong. "Are you enjoying your lunch?"

> "Yes," said Golden Horn.

## ⑤

  Wukong picked up the gourd.

> "Is Sun Wu Kong still in here?"

> "Yes," said Golden Horn. "He will turn completely into liquid soon. Stop asking all your questions. I'm trying to eat my lunch."

  Golden Horn tilted his head to take a drink. Wukong slipped the gourd into his robe. He quickly made a fake gourd with one of his hairs. He put it on the table and then ran outside.

  Wukong changed back into himself and then banged on the cave door again.

  Golden Horn threw the door open.

> "My name is Kong Sun Wu!" said Wukong. "You captured my nephew. Return him at once!"

  Golden Horn held up the fake gourd.

> "Kong Sun Wu!"

> "Cried Wukong, interrupting the demon. I have a gourd that looks just like that."

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十二章：真假悟空


## ①

  悟空挣扎着想要挣脱金绳。这时葫芦从他袍子里掉了出来。

> "我的宝葫芦！"金角说着捡了起来。

  他把悟空拖进洞里一间黑屋子，锁上了门。

  但悟空立刻将自己变小，逃了出去。他顺着一条通道飞了出去，从洞府大门挤了出去。到了外面，他恢复正常大小，用力拍打着洞门。

> "快开门！"

  洞门打开了，金角出现在面前。

## ②

> "孙悟空！"妖怪大喊，"你怎么逃出来的？"

> "我不是孙悟空，"悟空撒了个谎。

> "什么？你怎么跟他长得一模一样？"金角说道。

> "是啊，"悟空说，"孙悟空是我的孪生兄弟。我叫孙空行。"

> "你来这里干什么，孙空行？"金角问。

> "我知道你抓了我哥哥，"悟空说，"快放了他。"

  金角哈哈大笑。

> "我才不放呢。"

> "唉，太可惜了，"悟空假装难过地说，"我本想不动武就解决此事。"他说完从耳朵里掏出了铁棒。

## ③

  金角一直把葫芦藏在身后，此刻连忙举起，大喊一声。

> "孙空行，收！"

  悟空被吸进了葫芦。金角盖好盖子，回到洞里去了。

  在葫芦里面，悟空急得直跺脚。

> "我怎么出去呢？我知道自己不会化成液体，因为我是长生不老的。可我还得去救朋友们啊。"

  他想了想。

> "我有办法了。"

  他拔下一根毫毛，变得跟自己几乎一模一样，唯一不同的是，假悟空没有腿。然后悟空又用一根毫毛变成一滩水。他把假悟空放在水滩上，看起来就好像假悟空的腿已经化成液体了一样。

## ④

  然后悟空把自己变得非常非常小。他走到葫芦口大声喊。

> "不好了！我的腿化成液体啦！"

  金角揭开盖子，葫芦口透进了光。小小的悟空趁机跳了出去，没有被发现。金角往里看去，看见假悟空站在水滩中。

> "哈哈！这猴子的腿真的化成液体了。很快全身都会化掉！哈哈！"金角大笑着盖回葫芦，把葫芦放下，开始吃饭。

  真正的悟空恢复正常大小，然后变成了一个妖怪的模样。他走到金角跟前。

> "大王好，"悟空说，"您午饭吃得可好？"

> "不错，"金角说。

## ⑤

  悟空拿起葫芦。

> "孙空行还在里面吗？"

> "在呢，"金角说，"他很快就要全部化成液体了。别再问我问题了，我要吃饭。"

  金角歪过头去喝水。悟空趁机把葫芦塞进袍子里，又用一根毫毛变出一个假葫芦放在桌上，然后跑到了外面。

  悟空恢复了自己的模样，又去敲打洞门。

  金角一把将门拉开。

> "我叫空悟孙！"悟空说，"你抓了我侄子，快放了他！"

  金角举起假葫芦。

> "空悟孙！"

  悟空打断妖怪的话，大喊道："我跟你长得一模一样的葫芦！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Three: A Visit from Guanyin

## ①

  Golden Horn stared at Wukong.

> "I doubt you have a gourd like mine."

> "I do," said Wukong. He held up the real gourd.

  The demon looked carefully at the gourd.

> "That looks like my gourd. But my gourd is magical."

> "My gourd is magical too," said Wukong.

  The demon rubbed his chin.

> "What can your gourd do?"

> "It can hold a demon," said Wukong. "All I have to do is say a demon's name. The demon will get sucked in and then turn into liquid."

  Golden Horn raised his eyebrows.

> "My gourd can do that too."

> "Let's see whose gourd works better. I'll go first," said Wukong. "I forgot your name."

> "Kong Sun Wukong!" said the demon.

> "Oh yes, now I remember," said Wukong.

  Golden Horn held up his gourd.

> "Kong Sun Wukong!"

  Nothing happened. Golden Horn looked at his gourd.

> "Why isn't my gourd working?"

## ②

> "Let me try mine," said Wukong. "Golden Horn!"

  Instantly the demon was sucked into the gourd. Wukong laughed.

> "Golden Horn will soon be turned into liquid."

  He closed the gourd and ran into the cave. Several demons were inside. The monkey waved his gourd at them.

> "Bajie! Wujing! Get out of here before I clobber you all!" he shouted.

  The demons screamed and ran out of the cave.

  After a quick search of the cave, Wukong freed his companions.

> "We thought you were trapped under a mountain," said the Tang monk.

> "I was freed a couple of hours ago," said Wukong. He untied the monk.

> "A couple of hours ago?" asked Bajie. "What were you doing for all that time? We were scared to death in here!"

  Wukong shrugged.

> "I couldn't free you right away. I had to get rid of the demon first."

  The monkey untied Bajie and Wujing.

## ③

  They all went outside.

> "It's still early in the afternoon," said Wujing. "Let's start walking now."

> "Yes," said the Tang monk. "I want to be as far from this mountain as I can by nighttime."

  The travelers hurried west along the road. They hadn't gone far when an old man approached them.

> "Give me back my gourd!" said the old man.

  Wukong stepped forward.

> "What gourd? I don't have a gourd."

> "I know you have my gourd!" said the man.

> "I don't know what you're talking about," said the monkey.

  There was a flash of light. Then Laozi the sage stood before the travelers. He looked angry.

> "Give me my gourd, Wukong!" bellowed the sage.

## ④

  Wukong smiled.

> "Aha! Laozi! I was just joking around. I knew it was you. Here's your gourd."

  Wukong took the gourd out of his robe and handed it to the sage.

> "Why did that demon have your gourd?" asked the monkey.

> "Golden Horn works for me," said Laozi. "I sent him here to cause trouble for you. I wanted to make sure you are all serious about reaching the western paradise. You fought well, Wukong."

  Wukong scratched his head.

> "Golden Horn is probably all liquified by now."

> "No," said Laozi. "The gourd won't harm him. Goodbye."

  The sage vanished. The group continued west.

## ⑤

  As night fell, they arrived at a monastery. After a small dinner with the monastery's monks, everyone went to bed.

  The Tang monk was almost asleep when he heard a moaning sound from outside. The monk sat up, trembling with fear.

  Slowly his door creaked open. A man stood in the doorway, dripping wet. He looked at the monk and held out his hands.

> "Please help me."

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十三章：观音来访


## ①

  金角大王盯着悟空。

> "我才不信你也有像我这样的葫芦。"

> "我有，"悟空掏出真葫芦举了起来。

  妖怪仔细端详着葫芦。

> "那看起来跟我的葫芦很像。但是我的葫芦是有法力的。"

> "我的葫芦也有法力，"悟空说。

  妖怪摸着下巴。

> "你的葫芦能干什么？"

> "它能装妖怪，"悟空说，"只要我叫出妖怪的名字，他就会自动被吸进去，然后化成液体。"

  金角大王挑了挑眉。

> "我的葫芦也能做到。"

> "那就看看谁的葫芦更灵吧。我先来，"悟空说，"嗯，我忘了你的名字了。"

> "行者孙！"妖怪喊道。

> "哦对，我想起来了，"悟空说。

  金角大王举起他的葫芦。

> "行者孙！"

  什么也没发生。金角大王看了看自己的葫芦。

> "我的葫芦怎么不灵了？"

## ②

> "看我的，"悟空说，"金角大王！"

  眨眼间，妖怪被吸进了葫芦里。悟空大笑。

> "金角大王马上就化成液体了。"

  他盖好葫芦，冲进洞府。里面还有几个小妖。悟空举起葫芦朝他们一扬。

> "八戒！悟净！快跑！不然我统统收拾你们！"他大喊。

  小妖们尖叫着跑出了山洞。

  悟空在洞里快速搜索了一下，解救了同伴。

> "我们以为你被压在山下了呢，"唐僧说。

> "我几个小时前就已经脱身了，"悟空替师父松了绑。

> "几个小时前？"八戒问，"那这么久你在干什么？我们在这里怕得要死！"

  悟空耸了耸肩。

> "我没法马上救你们，得先把妖怪解决了才行。"

  悟空又替八戒和悟净松了绑。

## ③

  大家走到洞外。

> "现在还是下午，天色还早，"悟净说，"我们赶紧赶路吧。"

> "对，"唐僧说，"天黑之前，走得离这座山越远越好。"

  一行人沿路向西赶去。走了没多久，一个老人迎面走来。

> "把我的葫芦还给我！"老人说。

  悟空走上前。

> "什么葫芦？我哪有葫芦。"

> "我知道你拿了我的葫芦！"老人说。

> "我不知道你在说什么，"悟空说。

  突然一道强光闪过，太上老仙出现在旅行者面前，表情十分愤怒。

> "悟空，还我的葫芦！"老仙大声喝道。

## ④

  悟空笑了。

> "哈哈！太上老仙！我就是开个玩笑嘛。我早知道是您。葫芦给您。"

  悟空从袍子里掏出葫芦递给了老仙。

> "那个妖怪怎么会有您的葫芦呢？"悟空问。

> "金角大王是我的人，"太上老仙说，"是我派他来故意刁难你们的。我要看看你们是不是真心诚意要去西天取经。悟空，你打得不错。"

  悟空挠了挠头。

> "金角大王恐怕已经化成液体了吧。"

> "不会的，"太上老仙说，"那葫芦伤不了他。后会有期。"

  仙人消失了。一行人继续向西行。

## ⑤

  天黑的时候，他们来到一座寺院。和寺里的和尚简单吃过晚饭之后，大家都去睡了。

  唐僧快睡着的时候，忽然听到外面有呻吟声。他坐起身来，害怕得发抖。

  门吱呀一声慢慢地开了。一个浑身滴水的男人站在门口，他看着唐僧伸出了双手。

> "求求您，救救我吧。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Four: The King's Ghost

## ①

  The man walked into the Tang monk's room.

> "Who are you?" asked the Tang monk nervously.

> "I'm the King of the Black Rooster Kingdom," said the man. "My kingdom suffered a horrible drought five years ago. Crops wouldn't grow while my people were starving. One day a Taoist arrived in the kingdom. He said he had great powers and could pray for rain."

> "Did the Taoist's prayers bring rain?" asked the Tang monk.

  The king nodded.

> "It rained for days and our crops began to grow."

> "Wonderful!" said the Tang monk with a smile. But then his smile faded. "I'm confused. Why do you need my help?"

## ②

  The king took a deep breath.

> "After the Taoist's prayers brought the rain, we became close friends. One day we were walking when I noticed a strange light coming from my well. I went to the well and looked in. Suddenly I felt someone push me in. It was the Taoist. He had made himself look like me with magic so he could trick me. I fell deep into the water and he sealed the well."

  Tears came to the king's eyes.

> "My body is still down there. I'm just a ghost."

> "That's horrible!" said the Tang monk. "Your guards punished the Taoist, right?"

  The king shook his head.

> "The Taoist made himself look like me and now everyone thinks he's the real king. I've been in the land of the dead ever since. Tonight a spirit brought me to see you. He said you can help me."

## ③

> "How can I help you?" asked the monk. "I'm just a monk."

> "Yes, but you're traveling with Sun Wukong!" said the king. "Sun Wukong is very powerful. He can destroy the Taoist!"

  The Tang monk hesitated.

> "Wukong can't charge into the palace and attack the Taoist. People will think the monk is evil, attacking a king for no reason."

> "My son, the prince, can bring all of you into the palace," said the king. "Then Sun Wukong can fight the Taoist in private."

> "Where can we find the prince?" asked the monk.

> "He will be out hunting tomorrow," said the king. "Tell him everything I told you."

> "But he won't believe us," said the monk. "He thinks the Taoist is his father."

> "Show him this." The king held up a jade coin. "This is the one royal treasure I still have. When my son sees it, he'll know you're telling the truth."

## ④

  Suddenly the king looked at the hour.

> "The spirit is calling me. Let us go!"

  The king vanished. The Tang monk called to his companions, who rushed into the room. The monk told them everything that the king had said.

> "He showed me a jade coin," said the monk. He looked around. "I don't know where it is now, though. It was just a dream."

> "No, it wasn't a dream," said the monk, still looking around.

  He went outside and the others followed.

> "There it is!"

  A jade coin lay on the ground by the door.

## ⑤

  The next morning the prince went out hunting. He saw a white rabbit and shot an arrow. He missed and the rabbit ran. The prince chased the rabbit as it ran into a monastery.

  Inside the prince saw a monk, a pig, and a bearded spirit. Then the rabbit turned into a monkey.

> "What's going on here?" cried the prince.

  The monk stepped forward.

> "Don't be scared, Prince. We must tell you something."

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十四章：国王的鬼魂


## ①

  一个男人走进了唐僧的房间。

> "你是谁？"唐僧紧张地问。

> "我是乌鸡国的国王，"那男人说，"五年前，我的国家遭受了一场可怕的旱灾，庄稼长不出来，百姓们饿着肚子。有一天，一位道士来到了我国。他说自己法力高强，能祈来雨水。"

> "那道士祈来雨了吗？"唐僧问。

  国王点了点头。

> "连下了好几天雨，庄稼又开始生长了。"

> "太好了！"唐僧笑着说。但随后他的笑容消失了，"我不明白，您需要我帮什么忙？"

## ②

  国王深吸一口气。

> "那场雨下过之后，我们成了好朋友。有一天，我们一起散步，我发现井里闪出奇怪的光。我走到井旁往里看，突然有人推了我一把——正是那个道士。他用魔法变成了我的模样来骗我。我掉进了井水深处，他把井封住了。"

  国王眼眶里涌出了泪水。

> "我的身体还在井底，我现在只是一个鬼魂。"

> "太可怕了！"唐僧说，"您的卫兵一定惩罚了那个道士吧？"

  国王摇了摇头。

> "道士变成我的模样，如今所有的人都以为他是真正的国王。我一直困在阴间。今晚是一个鬼魂带我来看你的，他说你能帮上忙。"

## ③

> "可是我能帮什么忙呢？"唐僧说，"我不过一个出家人。"

> "但你身边有孙悟空啊！"国王说，"孙悟空法力高强，他能打败那个道士！"

  唐僧犹豫了。

> "悟空不能冲进王宫去打道士。否则百姓会以为我们和尚是坏人，无缘无故攻击国王。"

> "我儿子，王子殿下，可以把你们都带进王宫，"国王说，"到时候私下让孙悟空去对付那个道士。"

> "我们到哪里去找王子呢？"唐僧问。

> "他明天要出去打猎，"国王说，"你们把事情的经过都告诉他。"

> "可他不会相信我们的，"唐僧说，"他以为道士就是他父亲。"

> "把这个给他看。"国王掏出一枚玉币，"这是仅存的一件王室宝物。我儿子看到它，就知道你们说的是真话。"

## ④

  忽然国王看了看时辰。

> "鬼使在召唤我了。我该走了！"

  国王消失了。唐僧呼唤同伴们，他们赶紧跑进了房间。唐僧把国王的话全都告诉了他们。

> "给我看了一枚玉币，"唐僧说。他环顾四周，"不过现在不知道去哪儿了。也许只是个梦吧。"

> "不，不是梦，"唐僧说着，还在四处寻找。

  他走出门外，其他人跟了上去。

> "在那里！"

  一枚玉币躺在门边的地上。

## ⑤

  第二天一早，王子出去打猎。他看到一只白兔，射了一箭，但没有射中，兔子跑了。王子追了过去，兔子跑进了一座寺院。

  王子在寺院里看到一个和尚、一头猪和一个长着胡子的鬼魂。然后兔子变成了一只猴子。

> "这是怎么回事？"王子惊叫道。

  唐僧走上前来。

> "别怕，殿下。我们要告诉您一件事。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Five: The Treasure in the Realm

## ①

  The Tang monk introduced himself to the prince and then waved toward the others.

> "These are my companions. We're going to the western paradise to get scriptures from Buddha."

> "What's going on?" asked the prince. "Why did the monkey lead me here?"

  The man ruling the Black Rooster Kingdom is not really the king," said the monk. He told the prince everything. When the Tang monk's story was finished, the prince was furious.

> "You're lying. I will have you arrested for making up such a story."

  The Tang monk reached into his robe. He pulled out the jade coin.

> "Your father told me to show you this."

## ②

  The prince gasped.

> "That coin belongs to my father. It's a royal treasure." He began to cry. "Your story must be true. My poor father."

  The Tang monk introduced himself to the prince and then waved toward the others.

> "These are my companions. We're going to the western paradise to get scriptures from Buddha."

> "What's going on?" asked the prince. "Why did the monkey lead me here?"

  "The man ruling the Black Rooster Kingdom is not really the king," said the monk. He told the prince everything. When the Tang monk's story was finished, the prince was furious.

> "You're lying. I will have you arrested for making up such a story."

  The Tang monk reached into his robe. He pulled out the jade coin.

> "Your father told me to show you this."

  The prince gasped.

> "That coin belongs to my father. It's a royal treasure." He began to cry. "Your story must be true. My poor father."

## ③

> "All this time, people thought that evil Taoist was him."

> "Don't worry," said Wukong. "We'll get rid of that fake king."

  Late that night, Wukong lay awake.

> "The Taoist will deny everything," he thought. "We need proof that he killed the real king."

  He poked Bajie who was fast asleep.

> "Bajie, wake up."

  The pig rolled over.

> "Let me alone sleep."

> "We need to do something," said Wukong.

> "Not now."

> "I know where there's treasure."

  Someone to lie." Bajie's eyes popped open.

> "Where is the treasure?"

> "Follow me."

## ④

  Wukong went outside and flew to the palace. In a small courtyard, Wukong rushed toward a well.

> "The treasure is in this well," said the monkey, pulling the lid off.

  Bajie peered down into the darkness.

> "Is this the well the king was pushed into?"

> "Oh, I'm not sure," said Wukong, pretending to not know. "The treasure is definitely down there, though."

> "How will we get it out?" asked the pig.

  Wukong pushed Bajie and the pig splashed into the water.

> "You're walking, monkey!" shouted Bajie.

  The monkey laughed.

> "Find the treasure and I'll let you back up."

  Angry, Bajie dived down deeper and deeper until he arrived at a palace.

> "Greetings," said a dragon. "I'm the well dragon king."

> "My name is Zhu Bajie," said the pig. "I'm here for a treasure."

> "I don't have any treasure for you," said the dragon. He looked up. "You came from the well. Are you from the Black Rooster Kingdom?"

> "Not exactly," said Bajie. "My friends and I are helping the king of the Black Rooster Kingdom."

> "Really?" The dragon raised his eyebrows. "I have something for you. Follow me."

## ⑤

  The well dragon king led Bajie into a room. The pig gasped. The body of a man lay on a table.

> "This is the Black Rooster King's body," said the dragon. "Please take it back with you."

  Bajie was furious that Wukong had tricked him. He lifted the king's body and headed back to the well.

> "I will get revenge later," he said to himself.

  The next morning the Tang monk looked at the king's body.

> "I wish we could bring him back to life."

> "Wukong can bring him back to life!" said Bajie suddenly.

> "What?" cried the monkey.

  The Tang monk smiled.

> "That's wonderful, Wukong. Please bring him back to life right away."

> "I don't know how to do that," said the monkey.

> "Don't believe him, master," said Bajie. "He can bring the king back to life. He just doesn't want to."

> "That's not true," protested Wukong.

> "He's lying, master," said Bajie. "Use the tight headband spell."

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十五章：王国的宝藏


## ①

  唐僧向王子介绍了自己，然后挥手示意其他人过来。

> "这些是我的徒弟们。我们要去西天拜佛求经。"

> "到底是怎么回事？"王子问，"猴子为什么把我带到这里来？"

> "现在统治乌鸡国的根本不是真正的国王，"唐僧说。他把所有的事情都告诉了王子。唐僧讲完之后，王子大怒。

> "你们胡说八道！我要把你们抓起来，你们竟敢编这种故事！"

  唐僧把手伸进袍子里，掏出了那枚玉币。

> "你父王让我把这个给你看。"

## ②

  王子倒吸一口气。

> "这枚玉币是我父王的。它是王室的宝物。"他开始哭泣，"你们的说法一定是真的。我可怜的父王。"

  唐僧再次向王子介绍了自己，然后向同伴们挥手示意。

> "这些是我徒弟们，我们去西天拜佛求经。"

> "到底怎么了？"王子问，"猴精为什么带我到这里来？"

> "统治乌鸡国的那个人不是真正的国王，"唐僧说。他把事情的经过全部告诉了王子。听完之后，王子勃然大怒。

> "你们在撒谎！我要把你们抓起来，编出这种谎话来！"

  唐僧从袍中取出了玉币。

> "这是你父王让我给你的。"

  王子大吃一惊。

> "那是父王的玉币，是王室的宝物！"他大哭起来，"你们说的肯定是真的。我可怜的父王！"

## ③

> "这么久以来，人们都以为那个邪恶的道士就是国王。"

> "别担心，"悟空说，"我们会除掉那个假国王的。"

  深夜，悟空躺在床上睡不着。

> "道士肯定会否认一切，"他想，"我们需要证据证明他杀害了真正的国王。"

  他推了推睡得很熟的八戒。

> "八戒，醒醒。"

  猪翻了个身。

> "别吵我，睡觉。"

> "有件事要做，"悟空说。

> "现在不行。"

> "我知道有个地方藏着宝贝。"

  八戒一下子睡意全无。

> "宝贝在哪儿？"

> "跟我走。"

## ④

  悟空走出门外，飞到了王宫。在一个小院子里，悟空走到一口井前。

> "宝贝就在这井里，"悟空说着掀开了井盖。

  八戒朝黑漆漆的井底张望。

> "这是不是国王被推进的那口井？"

> "嗯，不太确定，"悟空假装不知道，"不过宝贝肯定在下面。"

> "怎么弄上来呢？"猪八戒问。

  悟空一把推过去，猪八戒"哗啦"一声掉进水里。

> "你个该死的猴子！"八戒大喊。

  悟空大笑。

> "找到宝贝我就拉你上来。"

  八戒气得往井底游去，越潜越深，最后来到了一座宫殿。

> "你好，"一条龙说，"我是井龙王。"

> "我叫猪八戒，"八戒说，"我是来找宝贝的。"

> "我没什么宝贝给你，"龙王说。他往上看了看，"你是从井里来的。你是乌鸡国的人吗？"

> "不完全是，"八戒说，"我和朋友在帮乌鸡国国王。"

> "真的吗？"龙王挑了挑眉，"我有样东西给你，跟我来。"

## ⑤

  井龙王带八戒走进一间屋子。猪八戒大吃一惊，一个人的尸体躺在桌上。

> "这是乌鸡国国王的遗体，"龙王说，"请将它带回去吧。"

  八戒对悟空骗他的事十分生气。他背起国王的遗体往井上走去。

> "这笔账我以后找你算，"他自言自语道。

  第二天一早，唐僧看到了国王的遗体。

> "真希望我们能让国王活过来。"

> "悟空能让国王复活！"八戒突然说。

> "什么？"悟空惊声道。

  唐僧笑了。

> "太好了悟空。快让国王复活吧。"

> "我不会，"悟空说。

> "别信他，师父，"八戒说，"他能救活国王，只是不愿意罢了。"

> "不是这样的，"悟空辩解道。

> "他在撒谎，师父，"八戒说，"念紧箍咒！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Six: 1,000 Pills

## ①

  The Tang monk glared at Wukong.

> "Bajie says you can bring the king back to life," said the monk. "Please do so now."

  Wukong shot a look at Bajie, who was trying not to laugh.

> "Master, use the tight headband spell," said the pig. "Don't cry, Wukong."

  Laozi the sage has pills that can make people live forever. Maybe he makes pills that can bring people back to life.

## ②

  Laozi the sage was busy working on a potion. Steam rose from the bubbling cauldron. Suddenly, Wukong burst into the room.

> "Hello, Laozi!"

  Laozi the sage groaned.

> "What are you doing here, Wukong? You're supposed to be helping the Tang monk reach the western paradise."

  Wukong walked around the room, looking at all the bottles and equipment.

> "I'm still helping the Tang monk," he said. "We're helping a king right now, though." He poked a blue bottle filled with liquid.

  Laozi looked up from his potion.

> "Don't touch anything. Just tell me why you're here."

> "I need pills that will bring someone back to life," said Wukong. "Give me one thousand of them."

## ③

  Laozi the sage stopped what he was doing and walked over to Wukong.

> "How dare you tell me to give you one thousand pills!" he said. "Get out of here right now!"

  The monkey laughed.

> "I'm kidding. I don't really need one thousand pills. Just give me one hundred."

  "Not a chance." Laozi squeezed his hands into fists.

> "I'm not giving you any pills. Now get out of here."

  Wukong scratched his head, pretending to think.

> "Now that I think about it, I don't need one hundred pills. Just give me ten."

> "You are rude and disrespectful."

> "You're rude and disrespectful. Get out of here."

> "I really just need one pill," said Wukong. "Give me that."

> "Get out of here!" shouted Laozi.

  Wukong sighed and then left.

## ④

  Laozi went back to his potion and stirred, but then he stopped.

> "That monkey would definitely come back and cause trouble," he said to himself. "I should just give him a pill."

  The sage opened a jar and took out a pill. He went outside and found Wukong waiting for him.

> "Hello again," said the monkey. "I was just trying to decide what sort of trouble I could cause for you."

  Laozi flinched, shoving the pill toward Wukong.

> "Take this and leave."

## ⑤

  Wukong returned to the monastery. Everyone watched as the monkey put the pill in the king's mouth.

  The pill sparkled around the king. And then his eyes popped open. The king sat up and looked at Wukong.

> "You saved me," the king said. "I'm alive again."

  He turned and saw the prince standing nearby.

> "My son."

> "Father," said the prince. He took his father's hands and bowed his head. "I've missed you."

> "It's time for you to return to your palace."

  The prince led everyone to the palace. They walked past guards and went into the throne room. The prince kneeled down before the Taoist.

> "Greetings, son," said the Taoist. "Who are these people?"

  The prince stood up.

> "This is the Tang monk. He is going to the western paradise to get scriptures from Buddha. These three are his companions."

  The Taoist looked at a person standing near them. The person was wearing a hood.

> "Who was that man wearing the hood?"

  The man pulled the hood back and showed his face. The Taoist gasped.

> "The King!"

  Wukong pulled out his iron bar and leapt toward the Taoist. The Taoist snapped his fingers and vanished.

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十六章：千粒仙丹


## ①

  唐僧瞪着悟空。

> "八戒说你能让国王复活，"唐僧说，"现在就让他活过来吧。"

  悟空瞥了八戒一眼，八戒拼命忍住笑。

> "师父，念紧箍咒，"八戒说。"别耍赖了，悟空。"

  太上老仙有长生不老的仙丹，说不定他也有能让人复活的仙丹。

## ②

  太上老仙正忙着炼药，丹炉里咕嘟咕嘟冒着热气。忽然，悟空闯了进来。

> "你好啊，老仙！"

  太上老仙叹了口气。

> "悟空，你来干什么？你不是应该护送唐僧去西天取经吗？"

  悟空在屋里走来走去，看着所有的瓶子和器具。

> "我还在保唐僧呢，"他说，"不过我们现在正在帮一位国王。"他戳了戳一只装满蓝色液体的瓶子。

  老仙从药炉前抬起头。

> "什么都别碰。快说是来干什么的。"

> "我需要能让人复活的仙丹，"悟空说，"给我一千颗。"

## ③

  太上老仙放下手里的活，走到悟空面前。

> "你竟敢让我给你一千颗仙丹！"他大声喝道，"马上给我滚出去！"

  悟空笑了。

> "开个玩笑嘛。我真不需要一千颗，给我一百颗就行了。"

> "没门儿。"老仙双手攥紧。

> "我一颗都不会给你，现在就滚！"

  悟空挠了挠头，假装想了想。

> "我想了一下，一百颗也多了。给我十颗吧。"

> "你这猴子又粗鲁又放肆。"

> "你才又粗鲁又放肆呢。快让我走。"

> "我真的只要一颗就行了，"悟空说，"给我一颗吧。"

> "滚出去！"老仙大喊道。

  悟空叹了口气，然后走了出去。

## ④

  老仙回去继续搅药，但接着又停了下来。

> "那猴子肯定会回来捣乱，"他自言自语道，"还不如给他一颗。"

  老仙打开一个罐子，取出一颗仙丹。他走到外面，发现悟空正在等他。

> "又见面了，"悟空说，"我正在琢磨能给你惹出什么麻烦来。"

  老仙吓了一跳，赶紧把仙丹塞给悟空。

> "拿着，快走吧。"

## ⑤

  悟空回到寺院。众目睽睽之下，悟空把仙丹放进国王嘴里。

  仙丹在国王体内发出金光，随后他的眼睛睁开了。国王坐起来看着悟空。

> "你救了我，"国王说，"我又活过来了。"

  他转过身，看见王子站在旁边。

> "我的儿子。"

> "父王，"王子说，他握住父亲的双手，低下了头，"我好想您。"

> "是时候回王宫了。"

  王子带着众人回到了王宫。他们穿过守卫，走进大殿。王子向道士跪下。

> "孩儿，拜见父王，"道士说，"这些人是谁？"

  王子站起来。

> "这是唐僧，他要去西天拜佛求经。这三位是他的徒弟。"

  道士看了看旁边站着的一个戴兜帽的人。

> "那个戴兜帽的人是谁？"

  那人掀开兜帽，露出了真面目。道士大惊失色。

> "是国王！"

  悟空抽出铁棒，朝道士扑去。道士打了个响指，凭空消失了。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Seven: Two Tang Monks

## ①

  The Taoist had vanished. Wukong ran outside and shot into the air. He looked in every direction.

> "Where did the Taoist go?" asked the monkey.

  Then he heard a shout from inside the palace.

> "There are two Tang monks!" cried Bajie.

  Wukong flew back inside. Two Tang monks stood side by side.

> "We can't tell them apart," said Wujing. "They look exactly alike."

> "Which one of you is the real Tang monk?" asked Wukong.

> "I am," said one.

  The other monk glared at the first one.

> "No, I am!"

  The first monk looked at Wukong.

> "Don't believe him, Wukong. I am the real Tang monk."

> "Don't believe him!" said the other monk. "I am the real Tang monk!"

## ②

  Angry, Wukong pulled out his iron bar.

> "Which one of you is the real Tang monk!"

  Both Tang monks fell to their knees, shaking with fear.

> "Don't hit me!" they both cried.

  The monkey sighed. He turned to Bajie and Wujing.

> "What can we do?"

> "I have an idea," said Bajie, smiling. "But you won't like it."

> "What is it?" asked Wukong.

> "The two Tang monks should recite the Tight Headband Spell," said the pig. "Only the Tang monk, Guanyin and Buddha know the spell. We'll know right away which Tang monk is fake."

  "You just want to see me in pain," said Wukong. Then he sighed. "But it is a good idea."

## ③

  Bajie and Wujing stood near the monks.

> "Master, recite the Tight Headband Spell," said Wukong.

  Both monks began speaking. And Wukong fell to the floor.

> "It hurts!" he cried.

  Bajie watched the Tang monks carefully. One of them was reciting the spell. But the other one wasn't.

> "This is a fake Tang monk!" shouted the pig, pointing. "He's just mumbling nonsense!"

  The real monk stopped reciting the spell. Bajie and Wujing tried to grab the fake monk, but the monk changed into a green lion and ran out of the throne room.

> "Get him!" shouted Wukong.

## ④

  He and his companions chased the lion.

  Outside, the lion leaped into the air. Wukong and the others shot after him. Clouds swirled and soon they had the lion surrounded.

  Wukong pulled out his iron bar and raised it to strike. Just then a deep voice called out.

> "Do not hit him, Sun Wukong."

  Everyone looked up.

> "It's the Bodhisattva Manjushri," said Wukong.

> "This green lion is my pet," said the Bodhisattva. "The king of the Black Rooster Kingdom was cruel to someone many years ago, so my lion came to earth to punish him. The king's punishment is over now."

  The Bodhisattva and the lion disappeared above the clouds.

## ⑤

  That night the king of the Black Rooster Kingdom hosted a feast. During the feast he turned to the Tang monk.

> "Thank you for your help. I hope you will reach the western paradise very soon."

  Weeks passed and the travelers continued west. One day Wukong saw a mysterious red cloud over the mountains ahead.

> "Something is wrong," he said quietly.

> "What's wrong?" asked the Tang monk.

  The red cloud disappeared. Wukong shook his head.

> "Nothing, Master. I thought I saw a red cloud."

  They walked some more. Wukong saw the red cloud again. He held up his hand for the others to stop.

  The red cloud disappeared once again, and Wukong started to walk again. But then the red cloud reappeared.

> "Saw it again," said the Tang monk.

> "Wukong, should we keep going or not?"

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十七章：两个唐僧


## ①

  道士消失了。悟空跑到外面，飞入空中，朝四面八方张望。

> "那道士去哪儿了？"悟空问。

  忽然他听到宫里传来一声喊叫。

> "有两个唐僧！"八戒大叫。

  悟空飞回宫内。两个唐僧并排站在了一起。

> "我们分不清他们啊，"悟净说，"他们长得一模一样。"

> "你们两个究竟谁是真正的唐僧？"悟空问。

> "我是，"一个说道。

  另一个瞪了第一个一眼。

> "不，我才是！"

  第一个唐僧看向悟空。

> "别信他，悟空，我才是真的唐僧。"

> "别信他！"另一个唐僧说，"我才是真正的唐僧！"

## ②

  悟空勃然大怒，抽出了铁棒。

> "到底谁是真唐僧！"

  两个唐僧都扑通跪在地上，吓得直抖。

> "别打我！"两人同时喊道。

  悟空叹了口气，转向八戒和悟净。

> "咱们怎么办？"

> "我有个主意，"八戒笑着说，"不过你不一定乐意听。"

> "什么主意？"悟空问。

> "让两个唐僧都念紧箍咒，"八戒说，"只有唐僧、观音菩萨和佛祖才会念紧箍咒。谁不会念，谁就是假的。"

> "你就是想看我被念咒头疼吧，"悟空说，然后叹了口气，"不过还真是个好主意。"

## ③

  八戒和悟净站在两个唐僧旁边。

> "师父，念紧箍咒吧，"悟空说。

  两个唐僧都开始念念有词悟空疼得摔倒在地。

> "好疼啊！"悟空大叫。

  八戒仔细端详两个唐僧。其中一个确实在念咒，可另一个根本就没念。

> "这个唐僧是假的！"八戒指着他大喊，"他只是在胡言乱语！"

  真唐僧停住了口。八戒和悟净上前去抓假唐僧，可那唐僧变成了一头青狮子，跑出了大殿。

> "抓住他！"悟空大喊。

## ④

  悟空和同伴们追了出去。

  到了外面，青狮子一跃而起。悟空等人也腾空追去。白云翻滚，很快他们就把狮子团团围住。

  悟空抽出铁棒，正要打下去，忽然一个低沉的声音传来。

> "不要打他，悟空！"

  众人抬头一看。

> "是文殊菩萨，"悟空说。

> "这头青狮是我的坐骑，"文殊菩萨说，"几年前，乌鸡国国王对一个神仙不敬，所以我的狮子下凡来惩罚他。现在国王的惩罚已经结束了。"

  文殊菩萨和青狮子一起，消失在云层之上。

## ⑤

  当晚，乌鸡国国王设宴款待众人。席间，他对唐僧说。

> "感谢你们的帮助。希望你们早日踏上西天取经的路途。"

  几个星期过去了，一行人继续向西行。一天，悟空看到前方山头飘着一团神秘的红云。

> "情况不妙，"他小声说。

> "怎么了？"唐僧问。

  红云消失了。悟空摇了摇头。

> "没什么，师父。我以为看到了一团红云。"

  他们继续往前走，悟空又看到了那团红云。他举起手，示意大家停下来。

  红云又消失了，悟空继续往前走。可红云再次出现了。

> "悟空，又出现了，"唐僧不安地问道。

> "悟空，我们到底走还是不走？"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Eight: The Scared Boy

## ①

  Sun Wukong stared at the mountains. A red cloud was appearing over those mountains.

> "He said, there must be a demon ahead. The road leads right into those mountains."

  Said the Tang monk nervously.

> "Sun Wukong, we must be careful."

  He pulled out his iron bar and held it up. Wujing held up his spear, and Bajie held up his rake. The group walked cautiously.

  A red demon sat on a mountain peak, watching the travelers approach.

> "The Tang monk has finally arrived in my mountain," the demon said to himself. "I've heard that even just one bite of him will make me live forever."

  The demon looked at the travelers again.

> "Uh-oh. The monk's companions have their weapons out. They probably saw my red cloud. I'll have to trick them with a disguise."

## ②

  The demon made himself look like a scared little boy. Then he went down to the road, sat alongside it, and waited.

  Soon the travelers approached. The Tang monk saw the boy and got down from his horse.

> "Master, that's a demon," warned Wukong.

  The Tang monk scowled at the monkey.

> "He's just a scared little boy." He turned back to the boy. "What's wrong?"

> "My family was attacked by robbers," said the boy. "Please help me."

> "I know what you are," growled Wukong. "You're a demon. I will not let you eat the Tang monk."

  The boy looked horrified.

> "Wukong, stop scaring the child. You're scaring him!"

> "Ah! Master, you're being a fool again," cried the monkey. "You always fall for a demon's tricks and you never believe me."

> "Be quiet, Wukong," said the Tang monk. "Or I'll recite the Tight Headband Spell."

  Wukong glared angrily at the boy. But he didn't say another word.

## ③

  The Tang monk helped the boy to stand up.

> "Can you walk?" asked the monk.

  The boy shook his head.

> "My leg is injured."

  The Tang monk waved Wukong over.

> "Please carry the boy. And don't be mean to him."

  The group continued west with Wukong carrying the boy on his back. The monkey walked slowly, and soon his companions were far ahead.

> "You tricked the Tang monk," said Wukong to the boy. "But you haven't tricked me. I know you're a demon."

> "I don't know what you're talking about," said the boy.

## ④

  A powerful wind blew up, bending trees and almost knocking over Wukong.

  The monkey laughed.

> "I know that you're making this wind blow. Use all the magic you want. You won't be able to blow me away. I once defeated heaven's entire army."

  The road now ran along the edge of a cliff. Wukong looked down.

> "I should throw you over the edge of this cliff," he said. "Then I'll just tell the Tang monk you ran away."

  The monkey tried to grab the boy from his back. But at that moment the boy disappeared.

  Wukong laughed.

> "He must have gotten scared."

  The wind suddenly grew stronger and dust filled the air. Wukong heard screams and rushed ahead to find his friends.

## ⑤

> "Master!" cried the monkey, trying to see through the dust. "Where are you?"

  When the wind stopped, he saw Bajie and Wujing lying by the road.

> "That was some wind," said the pig, getting up. "It knocked us over," said Wujing.

  Wukong looked frantically around.

> "Where's Master?"

> "Oh no!" cried Bajie. "That boy was a demon. He kidnapped Master!"

  Wukong shook his head.

> "Let's all go home. The journey is over."

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十八章：受惊的男孩


## ①

  悟空凝视着前方的山峦。一团红云正在山头上空出现。

> "前方肯定有妖怪，"悟空说，"这条路正好通进那些山里。"

  唐僧紧张地说："悟空，我们得小心。"

  悟空掏出铁棒举在手中。悟净举起长枪，八戒举起钉耙。一行人小心翼翼地向前走去。

  一个红色的小妖怪坐在山顶上，注视着渐渐走近的师徒们。

> "唐僧终于来到我的地盘了，"小妖怪自言自语，"听说只要吃上一口他的肉就能长生不老。"

  妖怪又看了看随行的众人。

> "坏了。这和尚的徒弟都拿着兵器。他们八成看到我的红云了。得变个装来骗他们。"

## ②

  妖怪变成了一个受惊的小男孩。然后他沿路坐在路边等着。

  不一会儿，师徒们走近了。唐僧看见小男孩，从马上下来。

> "师父，那是妖怪，"悟空警惕地说。

  唐僧瞪了悟空一眼。

> "他只是个受了惊吓的小娃娃。"他转身对男孩说，"你怎么了？"

> "我家里人遇上强盗了，"小男孩说，"请你们帮帮我。"

> "我知道你是什么，"悟空低声喝道，"你是妖怪休想吃掉唐和尚。"

  小男孩装出一副害怕的样子。

> "悟空，别吓唬孩子。你吓着他了！"唐僧说。

> "哎！师父，您又犯糊涂了，"悟空大叫，"您老是上妖怪的当，就是不信我。"

> "闭嘴，悟空，"唐僧说，"不然我就念紧箍咒。"

  悟空狠狠瞪了小男孩一眼，没再说话。

## ③

  唐僧扶小男孩站了起来。

> "你能走路吗？"唐僧问。

  小男孩摇了摇头。

> "我的腿受伤了。"

  唐僧朝悟空招了招手。

> "你背这孩子吧。别再对他不客气了。"

  一行人继续向西走，悟空背着小男孩。悟空故意走得慢，渐渐地把同伴们远远甩在了后面。

> "你骗了我师父，"悟空对小男孩说，"可你骗不了我。我知道你是妖怪。"

> "我不知道你在说什么，"小男孩说。

## ④

  忽然狂风大作，树木被吹得东倒西歪，悟空也差点被吹倒。

  悟空哈哈大笑。

> "我知道这风是你搞的鬼。你用尽法力也刮不走我。当年我可是大闹过天宫，天兵天将都被我打败了。"

  这时道路沿着一处悬崖延伸。悟空往下看。

> "我干脆把你扔下悬崖，"他说，"就跟师父说你跑了。"

  悟空伸手想从背上把那男孩拽下来。可就在那一刻，男孩消失了。

  悟空笑了。

> "看来他是被吓跑了。"

  忽然风更大了，飞沙走石遮天蔽日。悟空听到呼救声，赶紧跑去找同伴。

## ⑤

> "师父！"悟空在沙尘中大喊，"您在哪儿？"

  风停之后，他看见八戒和悟净倒在路上。

> "好大的风啊，"八戒爬起来说。"把我们刮倒了，"悟净说。

  悟空焦急地四处张望。

> "师父呢？"

> "不好！"八戒惊叫道，"那男孩就是妖怪，他把师父抓走了！"

  悟空摇了摇头。

> "咱们都回家吧。这趟取经之路结束了。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Forty-Nine: Red Boy

## ①

  "Wukong is right," said Bajie. "We should all go home and forget about reaching the Western Paradise. I'll return to my cave and take a nice long nap." Bajie started to walk away.

> "Are you crazy?" cried Wukong.

  "We can't go home," said Wujing.

## ②

> "I know that," said the monkey. "I wasn't serious about going home. But I'm angry with Master. How many times have I warned him about demons? He never believes me. If he had listened to me earlier, he wouldn't have been kidnapped."

  Wukong sighed. "We need to figure out where the demon took him. I'll summon a local spirit."

  The monkey closed his eyes and muttered some words. A soft breeze blew and then a spirit appeared.

> "Hello, Sun Wukong," said the spirit. "I am the spirit of this mountain."

## ③

> "Our master was kidnapped by a demon," said Wukong. "We think the demon lives near here, but we don't know where."

> "I can tell you," said the spirit. He looked nervous. "Your master was probably kidnapped by Red Boy, a very nasty demon. His cave is near the peak of that mountain." The spirit pointed to a nearby mountain. "You shouldn't go there, though," the spirit continued. "Red Boy is very powerful. His father is the Bull Demon King, one of the most horrible demons ever."

## ④

  A smile spread across Wukong's face and he began to laugh.

> "Ha ha ha ha! That is good news!"

  Everyone looked at the monkey in surprise.

> "Why is that good news?" asked Wujing.

> "The Bull Demon King is an old friend of mine," said Wukong. "Before I caused trouble in Heaven, I was friends with a group of demon kings. The Bull Demon King was one of them. When I tell Red Boy who I am, he'll release the Tang Monk right away."

## ⑤

  The three travelers said goodbye to the spirit and headed up the mountain. They came to a cave near the peak. The door was closed.

> "Open up, Red Boy!" Wukong shouted. "I need to speak with you."

  The door blew open and Red Boy stepped out.

> "Who are you?" demanded Red Boy. "What do you want?"

> "You kidnapped our master, the Tang Monk," said the monkey. "Please return him to us."

## ⑥

  Red Boy snorted.

> "I'm not going to return the Tang Monk to you. I'm going to eat him and live forever. Now go away before I get very angry."

  Wukong laughed.

> "My dear boy, you don't realize who you're talking to. I am Sun Wukong, the Monkey King. Your father and I are old friends."

> "I don't care who you are," said Red Boy. "Now all of you get off my mountain!"

## ⑦

  Wukong pretended to be disappointed.

> "I was hoping we could solve this problem nicely."

  He removed the iron bar from his ear. Red Boy laughed.

> "Do you think I'm scared of your little weapon?"

> "This iron bar is a treasure from Heaven," said Wukong. "It was used to measure the oceans and rivers. It is very powerful and can do whatever I tell it to do." The monkey puffed out his chest. "Return the Tang Monk at once, or I'll destroy your entire mountain!"

## ⑧

> "I also have a powerful weapon," said Red Boy. "I'll show it to you."

  The demon punched himself in the nose. Smoke poured from his nostrils and fire from his mouth. A moment later, flames covered the entire mountainside.

---

# 🇨🇳 第四十九章：红孩儿


## ①

  "悟空说得对，"八戒说，"我们都该回家，别再去西天了。我要回洞里去睡个长觉。"八戒转身就走。

> "你疯了吗？"悟空喊道。

  "我们不能回家，"悟净说。

## ②

> "我知道，"猴子说，"我可不是真说要回家。可是我对师父很生气。我警告过他多少次有妖怪？他就是不听。要是他早听我的，就不会被妖怪抓走了。"

  悟空叹了口气："我们得查查妖怪把师父带到哪里去了。我来召唤一个当地的土地神。"

  猴子闭上眼睛念了几句咒语。一阵微风吹过，一个神灵出现了。

> "你好，孙悟空，"神灵说，"我是这座山的山神。"

## ③

> "我们的师父被妖怪抓走了，"悟空说，"我们觉得妖怪就住在附近，但不知道具体在哪里。"

> "我可以告诉你，"神灵说。他看上去很紧张，"抓走你师父的很可能是红孩儿，一个非常凶恶的妖怪。他的洞就在这座山的山顶附近。"神灵指着附近的一座山说："不过你们不该去那里，"神灵继续说，"红孩儿法力高强，他的父亲是牛魔王，是最可怕的妖怪之一。"

## ④

  悟空脸上露出笑容，哈哈大笑起来。

> "哈哈哈！这可是好消息！"

  大家惊讶地看着猴子。

> "为什么是好消息？"悟净问。

> "牛魔王是我的老朋友，"悟空说，"我大闹天宫之前，跟一群妖王结成了兄弟。牛魔王就是其中之一。我告诉红孩儿我是谁，他会立刻把唐僧放了的。"

## ⑤

  三位行者告别了神灵，向山上走去。他们来到山顶附近的一个洞前，洞门关着。

> "快开门，红孩儿！"悟空叫道，"我有话要跟你说。"

  洞门猛然打开，红孩儿走了出来。

> "你是谁？"他质问道，"你想干什么？"

> "你抓走了我们的师父唐僧，"猴子说，"请把他交还给我们。"

## ⑥

  红孩儿哼了一声。

> "我不会把唐僧还给你们。我要吃了他，好长生不老。现在快滚，别惹我发火。"

  悟空笑了起来。

> "小伙子，你还不明白自己在跟谁说话。我是孙悟空齐天大圣，你爹跟我可是老交情。"

> "我才不管你是谁，"红孩儿说，"赶紧滚出我的山！"

## ⑦

  悟空装作很失望的样子。

> "我本来还想跟你好好商量呢。"

  他从耳朵里掏出了金箍棒。红孩儿大笑起来。

> "你以为我会怕你那根小棍子？"

> "这根金箍棒可是天上的宝贝，"悟空说，"当年大禹治水用来测量江河湖海的神针。它法力无边，我说什么它就做什么。"猴子挺起胸膛，"立刻把唐僧交出来，不然我把你的整座山都砸个稀巴烂！"

## ⑧

> "我也有一件厉害的兵器，"红孩儿说，"让你见识见识。"

  妖怪朝自己鼻子上捶了一拳，浓烟从鼻孔里冒出来，火焰从嘴里喷出来。不一会儿，整座山坡都被火焰吞没了。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty: Magic Fire

## ①

  Wukong and his companions ran back down the mountain, escaping the fire.

> "Red Boy's fire is powerful," said the monkey. "We were nearly roasted."

> "Yes," said Bajie.

  Wujing looked up at the mountain peak.

> "The fire is dying down now."

> "Yes," said Wukong, looking at the last few wisps of smoke. "But he'll use it again if we go back up there."

> "We'd need water," said Wujing. "Then if he makes fire again, we can just put it out."

## ②

  Wukong nodded.

  "You two wait here. I know who can help us."

  The monkey shot into the air and flew away. When he returned, the Dragon King of the Eastern Sea was with him. Wukong introduced the Dragon King to Bajie and Wujing.

> "I can summon rain clouds," said the Dragon King. "Go back up the mountain and get Red Boy to come out. As soon as he makes his fire, I'll create a huge rainstorm."

  The Dragon King flew up into the sky. Wukong and the others returned to the cave.

## ③

  "Open up, Red Boy!" The monkey pounded on the cave door.

  The door flew open and Red Boy ran outside.

> "Release the Tang Monk right now!" shouted Wukong.

> "Never!" shouted the demon.

  He made a fist and punched himself in the nose. Smoking fire poured from his face again.

> "Dragon King!" called the monkey.

  Thunder rumbled as dark clouds filled the sky. Rain poured down. The fire however didn't go out. Instead of shrinking, the fire grew bigger. The smoke became thick, choking and unable to breathe.

## ④

  Wukong covered his face. He saw Bajie and Wujing running away. The monkey tried to get to the cave door, but the smoke was too thick. He tripped on a rock and tumbled down the side of the mountain.

  *Splash!* Wukong landed in a river and floated downstream. Finally, he washed up on the riverbank, coughing and wheezing. Bajie and Wujing rushed over to the monkey.

> "Wukong, are you alright?" asked Wujing.

> "I think so," said the monkey. He coughed again. "That fire is no ordinary fire. The water made it worse."

> "You're right," said the pig. "It must be magic fire."

## ⑤

> "What will we do now? Red Boy still has the Tang Monk in his cave."

> "I'll go to Guanyin for help," said Wukong, standing up.

> "You rest," said Bajie. "You breathed in a lot of smoke."

  "Bajie, go straight to Guanyin," said the monkey, coughing again. "No naps."

## ⑥

  Meanwhile, Red Boy was sitting on his mountain peak.

  "My fire was too powerful for Sun Wukong and his friends," he said to himself. "They must be dead now." The demon patted his belly. "And that is good because I am hungry. I'll go inside now and start cooking the Tang Monk."

  The demon stood up to leave when he spotted something in the sky.

  "It's the pig," he said. "I wonder what."

  Red Boy thought for a minute. "The pig must be going to Guanyin. Putuo Luojia is in the South Sea. He must be going to ask her for help. I'll stop him."

## ⑦

  The demon recited a quick spell and light sparkled around him. Now Red Boy looked exactly like Guanyin.

  Bajie soared through the sky on his cloud. He saw Guanyin coming toward him.

> "Bajie!" called the fake Guanyin with a smile. "This is a surprise. I was just about to go see you."

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十章：三昧真火


## ①

  悟空和同伴们逃下了山，躲避火焰。

> "红孩儿的火真厉害，"猴子说，"我们差点被烤熟了。"

> "是啊，"八戒说。

  悟净抬头望向山顶。

> "火现在已经小了。"

> "不错，"悟空望着最后几缕烟雾说，"可是如果我们再上去，他还会放火的。"

> "我们需要水，"悟净说，"这样他再放火的时候，我们就可以把火扑灭。"

## ②

  悟空点了点头。"你们两个在这里等着，我知道谁能帮忙。"

  猴子腾空而起，飞走了。等他回来时，东海龙王跟他在一起。悟空把龙王介绍给了八戒和悟净。

> "我能召唤雨云，"龙王说，"你们回到山上去，把红孩儿引出来。他一放火，我就下大雨。"

  龙王飞上了天空。悟空和其他人回到了洞口。

## ③

  "快开门，红孩儿！"猴子用力敲打着洞门。

  洞门猛然打开，红孩儿冲了出来。

> "立刻把唐僧放出来！"悟空大喊道。

> "休想！"妖怪大叫。

  他攥紧拳头朝自己鼻子捶了一拳，浓烟烈火再次从脸上冒出来。

> "龙王！"悟空喊道。

  雷声隆隆，乌云密布，大雨倾盆而下。然而火焰并没有熄灭，反而越烧越旺。浓烟滚滚，呛得人喘不过气来。

## ④

  悟空捂住脸，他看见八戒和悟净正在逃跑。猴子想跑到洞口，但烟太浓了。他被一块石头绊倒，顺着山坡滚了下去。

  *哗啦！*悟空掉进了一条河里，顺流漂下。最后他冲上了河岸，不停地咳嗽喘息。八戒和悟净冲到猴子身边。

> "悟空，你没事吧？"悟净问。

> "应该没事，"猴子说，他又咳嗽了一声，"那火不是普通的火，水反而让它更厉害了。"

> "你说得对，"八戒说，"那一定是三昧真火。"

## ⑤

> "现在怎么办？红孩儿还把师父关在洞里呢。"

> "我去找观音菩萨帮忙，"悟空站起身来说。

> "你先歇着，"八戒说，"你吸了那么多烟。"

  "八戒，你直接去找观音菩萨，"猴子又咳了一声，"别半路偷懒。"

## ⑥

  与此同时，红孩儿正坐在山顶上。

  "我的火把孙悟空和他的同伴们打得落花流水，"他自言自语道，"他们肯定已经死了。"妖怪拍了拍肚子，"那正好我肚子饿了，我现在就进去开始烹唐僧。"

  妖怪起身要走，忽然看到天上有动静。

  "是那头猪，"他说，"不知道他去干什么。"

  红孩儿想了一会儿："那猪一定是去观音那儿。普陀洛迦山在南面，他肯定是去请观音帮忙。我得拦住他。"

## ⑦

  妖怪念了一段咒语，周身发出光亮。此刻红孩儿变得跟观音菩萨一模一样。

  八戒驾着云在空中飞行，看见观音迎面走来。

> "八戒！"假观音笑着喊道，"真是巧了，我正想去找你呢。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-One: Guanyin Becomes Angry

## ①

  Bajie didn't know Guanyin was really Red Boy in disguise.

> "The Tang Monk is in trouble," said the pig to the fake Guanyin. "A demon named Red Boy is planning to eat him. Can you help us?"

> "Of course," said the fake Guanyin. "I know Red Boy. He's very nice. I doubt he'll harm the Tang Monk. Let's go to Red Boy's cave and talk to him."

## ②

  Bajie and the fake Guanyin flew to Red Boy's cave. Bajie went in first. Red Boy returned to his normal appearance and then sneaked up behind Bajie. He threw a sack over the pig.

> "Hey, what's going on?" shouted Bajie.

> "You fool!" The demon laughed. "I'm Red Boy, and now you're trapped."

  The demon locked Bajie in a room.

## ③

> "Why isn't Bajie back yet?" asked Wujing.

  Wukong groaned.

> "He probably stopped to take a nap. That pig is so lazy."

  Wujing nodded.

> "Yes, he's very lazy. What should we do now?"

> "I'm going to sneak into Red Boy's cave," said Wukong. "I want to make sure the Tang Monk is still alive. Then I'll go to Guanyin myself."

## ④

  The monkey turned himself into a bee and flew up the mountain. He slipped through the cave door and flew down a long tunnel. Soon he heard the Tang Monk crying.

  *Master is scared,* thought Wukong. *But at least he's still alive.*

  The monkey went further and heard a shout. It was Bajie.

> "You filthy demon! How dare you make yourself look like Guanyin and trick me!"

  *Bajie didn't take a nap after all,* thought Wukong. *I must go to the real Guanyin right away.*

## ⑤

  The monkey flew out of the cave and told Wujing what he just learned. Then he jumped onto a cloud and headed south. He found Guanyin in her pagoda.

> "Wukong, why are you here?" asked Guanyin.

> "We have a problem, Bodhisattva," said the monkey. "The Tang Monk was caught by a demon named Red Boy. The demon breathes magic fire that water can't put out. Bajie was on his way here to ask for your help, but the demon made himself look like you and tricked the pig."

## ⑥

  Guanyin's face burned with anger.

> "How dare that demon make himself look like me!"

  The Bodhisattva grabbed a vase and stormed outside. She threw the vase down into the ocean, where it sank beneath the waves.

  Wukong gasped.

> "That vase was a Buddhist treasure. Why did you throw it away?"

  Guanyin didn't answer. A minute later, the water rumbled. The vase appeared on the back of a giant turtle. The turtle came onto the shore and bowed his head.

## ⑦

> "Go down and get the vase," said Guanyin.

  The monkey ran down the mountain and tried to pick up the vase. Wukong gasped and used all of his strength. But no matter how hard he tried, he couldn't lift the vase at all.

> "Bodhisattva!" he called. "It's just a small vase, but I can't lift it."

## ⑧

  Guanyin came down the mountain.

> "That vase just traveled around the world through all the oceans and rivers. It now holds an ocean's worth of water. Magic water. The water will put out Red Boy's fire."

  Guanyin picked up the vase with one hand. She held up her other hand and several swords appeared. She waved them and they turned into a large lotus seat.

> "I have what I need now," said Guanyin.

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十一章：观音的愤怒


## ①

  八戒不知道观音竟然是红孩儿假扮的。

> "唐僧有难了，"八戒对假观音说，"一个叫红孩儿的妖怪要吃他。你能帮帮我们吗？"

> "当然可以，"假观音说，"我认识红孩儿，他很善良，我不相信他会伤害唐僧。我们去他的洞里跟他谈谈吧。"

## ②

  八戒和假观音飞到了红孩儿的洞前。八戒先进了洞。红孩儿恢复了原形，悄悄从八戒身后靠近，把一个口袋套在了猪头上。

> "哎，怎么回事？"八戒大喊道。

> "你这个蠢货！"妖怪大笑起来，"我是红孩儿，你现在跑不了啦！"

  妖怪把八戒关进了一个房间。

## ③

> "八戒怎么还不回来？"悟净问。

  悟空哼了一声。

> "他准是半路停下睡觉去了。这头猪太懒了。"

  悟净点了点头。

> "是啊，他确实很懒。现在怎么办呢？"

> "我要偷偷潜入红孩儿的洞里，"悟空说，"我要确认师父还活着，然后我自己去找观音。"

## ④

  猴子变成了一只蜜蜂飞上山，从洞门缝隙钻了进去，沿着长长的通道飞去。不一会儿他就听到了唐僧的哭声。

  *师父吓坏了，*悟空想，*不过还好他还活着。*

  猴子继续往里飞，听到了一声喊叫，是八戒。

> "你这个脏妖怪！竟敢变成观音来骗我！"

  *八戒并没有偷懒睡觉，*悟空想，*我必须马上赶去找真正的观音。*

## ⑤

  猴子飞出洞外，把情况告诉了悟净，然后跳到一朵云上向南飞去。他在宝塔里找到了观音菩萨。

> "悟空，你怎么来了？"观音问。

> "菩萨，我们遇到麻烦了，"猴子说，"唐僧被一个叫红孩儿的妖怪抓了，那妖怪会喷三昧真火，水也灭不了。八戒本来要去请菩萨帮忙，结果被那妖怪变成菩萨给骗了。"

## ⑥

  观音气得脸色通红。

> "那妖怪竟敢假扮我！"

  菩萨抓起一只净瓶冲出外面，把瓶子扔进了大海，沉入波涛之中。

  悟空大吃一惊。

> "那净瓶可是佛门宝贝啊，菩萨为什么把它扔了？"

  观音没有回答。过了一会儿，水面翻涌起来，瓶子驮在一只大龟背上出现了。大龟爬上岸，低下头。

## ⑦

> "下去把瓶子拿上来，"观音说。

  猴子跑下山去试着捡起净瓶。悟空使出全力，不论怎么使劲，瓶子纹丝不动。

> "菩萨！"他喊道，"就这么一个小瓶子，我怎么拿不起来？"

## ⑧

  观音下了山。

> "那瓶子周游了全世界的海洋和江河，现在装了整整一海洋的水，那是神奇的甘露，能灭掉红孩儿的三昧真火。"

  观音一手拿起净瓶，另一只手一伸，几把宝剑出现。她一挥，宝剑变成了一座巨大的莲花台。

> "我需要的一切都已准备好了，"观音说。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Two: An Ocean from a Vase

## ①

  Wukong and Guanyin stood on the lotus platform above Red Boy's mountain.

> "Let's attack Red Boy now!" said the monkey.

> "Wait, Wukong," said Guanyin, holding up a hand. "There's a lot of water in this vase. Enough for an ocean. I don't want any animals harmed when I pour it out."

  She recited a quick spell. A moment later, the local spirit arrived.

> "What is your order?" said the spirit. "What can I do for you?"

> "I'm going to pour magic water around Red Boy's mountain," said Guanyin. "Please make sure all the animals are far away from the mountain."

## ②

> "Yes, my lady!" said the spirit.

  The spirit flew down to Earth. Wukong watched the ground below. First, he saw some small animals scurry out from under bushes. Birds flew from branches. Then tigers, bears, and other large animals stampeded down the mountainside. Soon there was not a single animal anywhere near the mountain.

> "Now I can pour the water out," said Guanyin.

  She took the vase and rolling waves of water poured out. The waves washed down the side of the mountain. The water level rose higher and higher, forming an ocean. Only the top of the mountain was above water.

## ③

> "Wukong, go down there and get the demon to come out," said Guanyin. "Fight him, but don't defeat him. Instead, lead him up here to me."

  Wukong jumped down to the mountain. He pulled out his iron bar and swung it. The door to the cave exploded. Red Boy ran out of the cave looking furious.

> "You smashed my front door!" he shouted.

> "That's right," said the monkey. "And I'll smash you if you don't release my master."

## ④

  Red Boy laughed and then punched himself in the nose. Nothing happened.

> "Why didn't my fire magic work?" asked the demon.

  Then he noticed the ocean surrounding his mountain. Wukong laughed.

> "Ha ha ha ha ha! That is magic water brought here by the Bodhisattva Guanyin. You can't make fire anywhere near it!"

> "Ah!" Red Boy stabbed at Wukong with his lance.

  Clang! The monkey blocked the lance with his iron bar.

  Red Boy grunted and stabbed again. Wukong swung his iron bar, nearly knocking the lance from Red Boy's hands.

## ⑤

  The two fought until Wukong pretended to be scared. He leaped into the air. Red Boy followed.

  Up into the sky they flew. Red Boy kept jabbing his lance at Wukong. The monkey blocked it with his iron bar.

  Wukong hurried toward Guanyin on the lotus platform. He flew fast and ducked behind her. When Red Boy saw the Bodhisattva, he stopped.
