> "What are you doing here, Bodhisattva?" he demanded.

  Guanyin stared back at the demon, but she didn't say a word.

## ⑥

> "I asked why you're here!" shouted Red Boy.

  Again Guanyin didn't answer.

> "Did Wukong call after you to come here?" shouted the demon. "Why don't you speak?"

  Guanyin continued to stare silently at Red Boy.

  The demon became furious. He raised his lance and struck toward Guanyin.

  The Bodhisattva vanished.

## ⑦

  Red Boy laughed. He looked at the empty lotus platform.

> "Wukong is a fool! He couldn't defeat my fire magic, so he asked Guanyin for help. Then what did she do? She ran away as soon as I raised my weapon. Now this lotus throne is mine!"

  Red Boy sat down on the platform. Instantly the platform turned into swords, which surrounded the demon. Sharp points stuck to him on all sides.

> "Oh no!" cried Red Boy.

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十二章：瓶中大海


## ①

  悟空和观音站在莲花台上，俯瞰红孩儿的山头。

> "现在就去攻打红孩儿吧！"猴子说。

> "等等，悟空，"观音举起手来，"这瓶子里有很多水，足足装得下一个海洋。我不希望倒水的时候伤到任何动物。"

  她念了一段咒语。不一会儿，当地的土地神来了。

> "请问有何吩咐？"神灵说，"我能为您做什么？"

> "我要在红孩儿的山的周围倒下甘露，"观音说，"请确保所有动物都离开这座山。"

## ②

> "遵命，菩萨！"神灵说。

  神灵飞下凡间。悟空注视着下方。首先他看到一些小动物从灌木丛中逃了出来。鸟儿从树枝上飞走。接着老虎、熊和其他大型动物也从山坡上奔逃而下。不一会儿，这座山附近一只动物也没有了。

> "现在我可以倒水了，"观音说。

  她拿起净瓶，滚滚波涛倾泻而出。巨浪顺着山坡奔涌而下，水位越来越高，汇成了一片汪洋。只有山顶还露出水面。

## ③

> "悟空，你下去把那妖怪引出来，"观音说，"跟他打，但别打败他。把他引到我这里来。"

  悟空跳下山去，掏出金箍棒一棒挥下，洞门轰然爆炸。红孩儿怒气冲冲地从洞里跑了出来。

> "你砸碎了我的大门！"他大喊道。

> "没错，"猴子说，"你要是不放出我师父，我就把你一块儿砸了！"

## ④

  红孩儿大笑起来，然后朝鼻子捶了一拳。什么也没发生。

> "我的三昧真火怎么不灵了？"妖怪问道。

  然后他注意到山四周变成了汪洋大海。悟空大笑起来。

> "哈哈哈！这是观音菩萨带来的甘露，你在这儿可放不了火！"

> "啊！"红孩儿挺枪朝悟空刺去。

  铛！猴子用金箍棒挡住了枪。

  红孩儿哼了一声，又是一枪。悟空挥动金箍棒，差点把枪从红孩儿手里打落。

## ⑤

  两人打了一阵，悟空装作害怕，纵身跃上了天空。红孩儿追了上去。

  他们飞上天空，红孩儿不停地用枪刺杀悟空，猴子用金箍棒一一挡住。

  悟空飞回莲花台上观音菩萨身边，飞快躲到了她身后。红孩儿看到菩萨，停下了手。

> "你怎么在这儿，菩萨？"他质问道。

  观音盯着妖怪，一言不发。

## ⑥

> "我问你在这儿干什么！"红孩儿大喊道。

  观音还是没回答。

> "是悟空请你来的吗？"妖怪大喊道，"你怎么不说话？"

  观音继续默默注视着红孩儿。

  妖怪勃然大怒，举起长枪向观音刺去。

  菩萨消失了。

## ⑦

  红孩儿大笑起来，他看着空荡荡的莲花台。

> "悟空真是个蠢货！他打不过我的火，就去请观音帮忙。结果呢？我一举兵器她就跑了。这莲花台归我了！"

  红孩儿坐到了莲花台上。刹那间，莲花台变成了宝剑，从四面八方将妖怪围住。锋利的剑尖刺入他的身体。

> "不好了！"红孩儿大叫道。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Three: The Man in the Canoe

## ①

  From behind Guanyin, Wukong peered at Red Boy. The demon was trapped by the swords, all pointed at his face.

> "Get these swords away from me!" cried the demon.

> "You must become a Buddhist," said Guanyin. "Then I'll release you."

> "I promise!" cried Red Boy. "I'll do whatever you say!"

  Guanyin recited a spell and the swords vanished.

## ②

  Red Boy's eyes flashed with anger.

> "Bodhisattva, watch out!" cried Wukong.

  Red Boy charged toward Guanyin. Wukong jumped in front of him. The monkey was about to strike the demon when Guanyin held up five metal bands. She threw them at Red Boy. Instantly they clamped around his head, wrists, and ankles.

## ③

> "Evil demon!" said Guanyin. "How dare you try to attack me!"

  Unable to move, Red Boy glared at Guanyin. Wukong raised his iron bar to strike him.

> "No, Wukong," said Guanyin. "Don't hurt the demon. I will take him back to Mount Putuo Luojia to be my student."

> "Yes, Bodhisattva," said the monkey.

## ④

  Guanyin took the vase down to Earth. She recited a spell and all the water flowed back into the vase.

  She then led Red Boy towards the south. Wukong went into Red Boy's cave and freed the Tang Monk. Then he found Bajie and freed him. The three of them went down the mountain and found Wujing.

  The group continued west.

## ⑤

  They traveled for weeks and then months. One day they came to a wide river.

> "I can't believe we have to cross another one," muttered Bajie.

> "There are many rivers between here and the west," said Wukong. "We'll have to cross them all."

> "How will we cross this one?" asked the Tang Monk.

  A small canoe came into view. A man paddled it toward the travelers. As the man paddled, he stared at the Tang Monk.

## ⑥

> "Greetings!" called the man as he came closer. "Do you all need a ride across the river?"

> "Yes," said the Tang Monk. "We were just wondering how we would get across. We're going to the west to get scriptures from Buddha."

> "You must be the Tang Monk," said the man brightly. "I've heard you would pass through this area eventually."

> "Really?" asked the Tang Monk.

> "Yes," said the man with a smile. "You're famous!" He glanced down at his canoe. "I would be happy to take you all across. But as you can see, my canoe is not very big. I can take only two passengers at a time."

## ⑦

  As the man talked, Wukong watched him carefully. Something about the man didn't look quite right. The monkey was about to say something when Bajie stepped forward.

> "The Tang Monk and I will go first," said the pig.

  Wukong hesitated.

> "Master, I don't think this is a good idea."

  The Tang Monk frowned.

> "You never trust people, Wukong. This kind man is willing to help us cross the river."

  The monkey bit his lip as the monk and Bajie climbed into the canoe. They sat down and the man paddled away from shore.

## ⑧

  Wukong watched the canoe glide across the river. When it was about halfway across, Wukong noticed something.

> "Am I imagining things or is the canoe sinking?" asked the monkey.

  Wujing looked.

> "You're not imagining things," he said. "It is sinking."

  The two of them watched as the canoe slipped under the surface of the water. Wukong stamped his foot.

> "That man kidnapped Master and Bajie! I knew he looked suspicious."

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十三章：独木舟上的人


## ①

  悟空从观音身后窥看红孩儿。妖怪被宝剑困住，每一把剑都指向他的面部。

> "快把这些剑拿走！"妖怪哭喊道。

> "你必须皈依佛门，"观音说，"然后我就放了你。"

> "我发誓！"红孩儿大喊道，"我一定听你的话！"

  观音念了一段咒语，宝剑消失了。

## ②

  红孩儿眼中闪现怒火。

> "菩萨小心！"悟空大喊道。

  红孩儿向观音冲去。悟空跳到了他面前。猴子正要打那妖怪时，观音举起了五个金箍，扔向红孩儿。金箍立刻套在了他的头上、手腕上和脚踝上。

## ③

> "恶毒的妖怪！"观音说，"你竟敢袭击我！"

  红孩儿动弹不得，只能瞪着观音。悟空举起金箍棒要打他。

> "别，悟空，"观音说，"别伤着他。我带他回普陀洛迦山做我的弟子。"

> "遵命，菩萨，"猴子说。

## ④

  观音拿着净瓶来到地面。她念了一段咒语，所有的水都流回了瓶中。然后她带着红孩儿向南走去。悟空走进红孩儿的洞，救出了唐僧，接着又找到八戒，也救了他出来。三人下了山，找到了悟净。

  一行人继续向西前行。

## ⑤

  他们走了几个星期，又走了几个月。一天，他们来到一条宽阔的大河前。

> "真不敢相信又要过河，"八戒嘟囔道。

> "从这里到西天，要过的河多着呢，"悟空说，"全都得过。"

> "这条河怎么过啊？"唐僧问。

  一条小独木舟出现在视野中，一个人划着船向行者们驶来，一边划船一边盯着唐僧看。

## ⑥

> "你们好！"那人靠近了喊道，"你们需要渡河吗？"

> "需要，"唐僧说，"我们正发愁怎么过去呢。我们要去西天拜佛求经。"

> "你一定是唐僧吧，"那人高兴地说，"我听说你们早晚会路过这里。"

> "是吗？"唐僧问。

> "是啊，"那人笑着说，"您可有名了！"他低头看了看自己的小船，"我很乐意载你们过去。不过你们也看到了，我的船不大，一次只能带两个人。"

## ⑦

  那人说话的时候，悟空仔细地打量着他，总觉得这人有些地方不太对劲。猴子正要开口，八戒走上前来。

> "我和师父先过去，"八戒说。

  悟空犹豫了一下。

> "师父，我觉得这不太好吧。"

  唐僧皱起了眉头。

> "你总是不信任别人，悟空。这位好心人愿意帮我们过河。"

  猴子咬了咬嘴唇，看着唐僧和八戒上了船。那两人坐下后，那人划船离开了岸边。

## ⑧

  悟空看着小船在河上前行。大约走到河中央的时候，悟空发现了异常。

> "是我眼花了还是船在下沉？"猴子问。

  悟净看了看。

> "你没眼花，"他说，"船确实在下沉。"

  两人眼睁睁看着小船沉入了水底。悟空跺了跺脚。

> "那人绑架了师父和八戒！我就说他可疑！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Four: The River God

## ①

> "I should have stopped Master from getting in that canoe," said Wukong. "But whenever I warn him about someone, he doesn't believe me."

  Wujing nodded and the water spirit dived into the river. He soon came to a palace. A sign on the gate read, "Palace of the Black River God." Wujing tapped on the door with his spear.

> "Open up!"

  The door opened and a lizard demon peeked out.

## ②

> "What do you want?" asked the lizard.

> "I'm looking for my companions," said Wujing. "One is a monk and the other is a pig. They were kidnapped by a man pretending to be the river god."

> "They were kidnapped by me," said the lizard.

> "What?" said Wujing. "Yes."

  The lizard smiled. "I planned to eat the Tang Monk and he'll live forever."

  Wujing struck the lizard with his spear. The lizard spun around, blocking his spear with his tail. The blow nearly knocked Wujing over. Right away the lizard was on top of him.

## ③

> "Got me!" shouted Wujing.

  He shoved the lizard. The lizard attacked again. Wujing swung his spear and then swam upward. He splashed out of the river and landed next to Wukong.

> "There's a lizard demon in the river," said Wujing, breathing heavily. "He's very powerful."

  Wukong was about to respond when he noticed someone nearby. The man from the canoe was walking toward them. The monkey pulled out his iron bar.

> "Out there! You kidnapped my friends!"

## ④

  The man fell to his knees, shaking.

> "It wasn't me!" he cried. "It was a lizard demon! I am the Black River God, and this is my river. But that lizard demon pretended he was me."

  Wukong put the iron bar back in his ear.

> "I believe you," he said. "Do you know who the lizard is?"

> "I don't," said the river god. He looked even more frightened now.

> "What? His uncle is the mighty Dragon King of the Eastern Sea?"

  Wukong laughed.

> "Ha ha! That dragon is a friend of mine. He's also a bit scared of me. I'll go have a talk with him."

## ⑤

  A moment later, the monkey was at the Dragon King's palace.

> "Hello again, Wukong," said the Dragon, smiling. "What can I do for you?"

> "Why did you let your nephew take over the Black River?" demanded the monkey.

  The Dragon's smile faded.

> "What are you talking about?"

> "Your nephew, a lizard demon, took over the Black River," said Wukong. "And now he's planning to eat the Tang Monk."

> "Oh dear," said the Dragon. "I had no idea. I'll take care of it."

## ⑥

  Wukong and the Dragon flew back to the Black River. The Dragon came shouting.

> "Nephew, come out of that river at once!"

  The lizard crept from the river.

> "Uncle! It's nice of you to visit."

> "I'm not here to visit," yelped the Dragon. "I'm here to take you to the Jade Emperor. You will be punished."

## ⑦

  The lizard gulped, his head hung low. He followed his uncle up into the sky. With a splash, the river god appeared from the water. The Tang Monk and Bajie were with him.

> "Thank you, Wukong," said the river god.

> "You're welcome," said the monkey. "But we still need to cross your river."

## ⑧

> "That's easy," said the river god.

  He held up his hand. Instantly the river stopped flowing. The water formed walls. The travelers walked across the muddy riverbed and continued west.

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十四章：河神


## ①

> "我本不该让师父上那条船的，"悟空说，"可每次我提醒他当心别人，他就是不信。"

  悟净点了点头，水神纵身跃入河中。他很快就来到了一座宫殿前，门上写着"黑水河河神之府"。悟净用长枪敲了敲门。

> "快开门！"

  门开了，一个鼍龙妖怪探出头来。

## ②

> "你要干什么？"妖怪问。

> "我在找我的同伴，"悟净说，"一个是和尚，一个是猪。他们被一个假扮河神的人抓走了。"

> "是我抓的，"妖怪说。

> "什么？"悟净说。

  妖怪笑了起来："我计划吃掉唐僧，就能长生不老。"

  悟净一枪刺向妖怪。妖怪转了个身，用尾巴挡住了长枪。这一击差点把悟净打翻，转眼间妖怪就骑在了他身上。

## ③

> "放开我！"悟净大喊道。

  他用力推开妖怪。妖怪再次进攻。悟净挥枪挡了一下，然后向上游去。他冲出水面，落在了悟空身旁。

> "河里有个妖怪，"悟净喘着粗气说，"他法力很强。"

  悟空正要说话，发现附近有个人在朝他们走来，正是那个船夫。猴子掏出了金箍棒。

> "原来是你！你抓了我的朋友！"

## ④

  那人扑通跪在地上，浑身发抖。

> "不是我！"他哭喊道，"是河里有个妖怪！我才是黑水河河神，这是我的河。那妖怪假扮成了我。"

  悟空把金箍棒放回耳朵里。

> "我相信你，"他说，"你知道那妖怪是什么来头吗？"

> "我不知道，"河神说。他看上去更害怕了，"不过他的舅舅好像是东海龙王。"

  悟空大笑起来。

> "哈哈！那龙王可是我的朋友，他也有点怕我。我去跟他理论。"

## ⑤

  不一会儿，猴子就到了龙王的宫殿。

> "又见面了，悟空，"龙王笑着说，"有什么事吗？"

> "你为什么让你外甥霸占黑水河？"猴子厉声问道。

  龙王的笑容消失了。

> "你在说什么？"

> "你外甥，一个鼍龙妖怪，霸占了黑水河，"悟空说，"他现在还要吃唐僧呢。"

> "哎呀，"龙王说，"我完全不知道。我来处理这件事。"

## ⑥

  悟空和龙王飞回黑水河，龙王大声喊道：

> "外甥，马上从河里给我出来！"

  鼍龙从河里爬了出来。

> "舅舅！您能来看我真好。"

> "我不是来看你的，"龙王喝道，"我是来抓你去见玉皇大帝的，你要受罚！"

## ⑦

  鼍龙咽了口唾沫，低下了头，跟着舅舅飞上了天空。哗啦一声，河神从水里出来了，唐僧和八戒跟他在一起。

> "谢谢你啊，悟空，"河神说。

> "不客气，"猴子说，"不过我们还是要过你的河。"

## ⑧

> "这好办，"河神说。

  他举起手来，河水立刻停止了流动，水流变成了两堵水墙。行者们从河床走了过去，继续向西前行。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Five: The Monks and the Carts

## ①

> "Everybody, wake up!" called Wukong.

  The travelers had camped for a night in the woods. The Tang Monk woke up and stretched. Wujing opened his eyes and yawned. Bajie moaned.

> "It's so early. Let me sleep just a few more hours."

> "Bajie, don't be lazy," said the Tang Monk. "It's time to get up. Please start making breakfast."

  The pig got to his feet.

> "All we do is work," he said. "Cook food, carry bags, walk, walk, walk."

## ②

> "We're on a noble mission," said Wujing. "Because of our difficult journey, the Tang Empire will have the true scriptures. You should be happy to do all this work."

  After a quick breakfast, the group started walking. They went through a valley and over some hills. Later that afternoon, they heard yelling.

> "It sounds like some people are in trouble," said the Tang Monk.

  Wujing nodded.

> "Yes. I wonder what's going on."

> "You all wait here," said Wukong. "I'll go and investigate."

## ③

  The monkey leaped into the air and looked around. He saw a group of Buddhist monks pushing a cart up a steep hill. The cart was loaded with big stones. The monks looked miserable. Their robes were dirty and ripped.

  Two Taoist priests stood nearby, dressed in fine clothes.

> "Work faster!" yelled one of the priests.

  The Buddhists looked frightened. They struggled to move the cart faster.

  *Why are those monks pushing that cart?* thought Wukong. *And why are they scared of the Taoists?*

## ④

  The monkey waited for the Taoists to leave. Then he made himself look like a Buddhist monk.

> "Hello," said Wukong, walking toward the group of monks. "Why are you pushing this cart?"

  The monks stopped pushing the cart and turned toward Wukong. They looked surprised.

> "You must be new here," one monk said. "You should leave before you're discovered."

> "Why?" asked Wukong.

## ⑤

> "Taoists are in charge here," said another monk.

  Wukong shrugged.

> "People from different religions can still get along."

> "Not in this kingdom," said the first monk. "Buddhists are treated horribly here. The Taoists make us do hard work."

> "Why do the Taoists treat you so badly?" asked Wukong.

> "Years ago this kingdom had a drought," said the monk. "Crops died and people starved. Buddhist monks prayed to Buddha for rain, but no rain came."

## ⑥

> "One day a powerful Taoist arrived," said the other monk. "He's called the Tiger Immortal. He recited prayers and right away rain fell. Since then, Taoists have been in charge. They destroyed all the Buddhist monasteries and statues."

> "That's terrible," said Wukong. "Those Taoists can't get away with this."

## ⑦

> "The Taoists won't treat us this way forever," said a third monk. "The spirit of the planet Venus visited us in a dream one night. He said that one day someone would come along to save us."

> "Really?" Wukong raised an eyebrow. "Who is going to save you?"

> "A fierce monkey spirit," said the monk. "His name is Sun Wukong. He is so powerful that Heaven's entire army couldn't defeat him."

## ⑧

  Wukong smiled.

> "I've heard of Sun Wukong. And it's true that he's very powerful. Did Venus tell you what he looks like?"

> "Oh yes."

> "So you recognize him if you see him?" asked Wukong, trying not to laugh.

> "Certainly," said the monk. "Why do you ask?"

  Light sparkled around Wukong. A moment later, he was a monkey again.

> "Sun Wukong!" cried the monks.

  They all fell to their knees and bowed.

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十五章：推车僧侣


## ①

> "大家快起来！"悟空喊道。

  旅行者们在林子里扎营过了一夜。唐僧醒了过来，伸了个懒腰。悟净睁开眼睛打了个大哈欠。八戒哼哼唧唧的。

> "天还早着呢，让我再睡一会儿。"

> "八戒，别偷懒了，"唐僧说，"该起床了，去做早饭吧。"

  八戒爬起身来。

> "我们整天就知道干活，"他说，"做饭、挑行李、走啊走啊。"

## ②

> "我们肩负着神圣的使命，"悟净说，"正是因为这段艰难的旅程，大唐才能得到真经。你应该乐于做这些事。"

  匆匆吃过早饭后，一行人又上路了。他们穿过山谷，翻过山丘。到了下午晚些时候，他们听到了叫喊声。

> "好像是有人遇到了麻烦，"唐僧说。

  悟净点了点头。

> "是啊，不知道出了什么事。"

> "你们都在这里等着，"悟空说，"我去看看。"

## ③

  猴子腾空而起，四下张望。他看到一群和尚正在推着一辆车上陡峭的山坡，车上装满了大石头，和尚们的样子很凄惨，衣服又脏又破。

  两个道士站在旁边，穿着华丽的衣裳。

> "快一点！"其中一个道士大声喊道。

  和尚们满脸恐惧，艰难地推着车前行。

  *这些和尚为什么要推车？*悟空想道，*他们为什么怕道士？*

## ④

  猴子等到道士走开了，就把自己变成了一个和尚的模样。

> "你们好，"悟空走到一群和尚面前说，"你们为什么推着这辆车？"

  和尚们停下手中的活，转身看着悟空，一脸惊讶。

> "你一定是新来的，"一个和尚说，"快走吧，免得被发现。"

> "为什么？"悟空问。

## ⑤

> "这里是道士说了算，"另一个和尚说。

  悟空耸了耸肩。

> "不同信仰的人还是可以和平相处的嘛。"

> "在这个国家可不行，"第一个和尚说，"和尚们在这里被虐待得惨极了。道士们逼我们做苦力。"

> "道士们为什么对你们这么坏？"悟空问。

> "几年前这里闹过大旱，"和尚说，"庄稼全死了，人们都挨饿。和尚们向佛祖祈雨，可是一滴雨也没下。"

## ⑥

> "后来来了一个法力高强的道士，"另一个和尚说，"他叫虎力大仙。他念了咒，立刻就下雨了。从那以后就是道士说了算。他们把和尚们的寺庙和佛像全都毁掉了。"

> "太可恶了，"悟空说，"那些道士不能这么横行霸道。"

## ⑦

> "道士们不会永远这样对我们了，"第三个和尚说，"太白金星托梦给我们，说总有一天会有人来救我们。"

> "真的？"悟空挑了挑眉毛，"谁来救你们？"

> "一个法力高强的猴精，"和尚说，"他叫孙悟空。他的本事大到天兵天将都打不过他。"

## ⑧

  悟空微微一笑。

> "我听说过孙悟空。他确实很厉害。太白金星跟你们说了他长什么模样吗？"

> "当然说了。"

> "所以你们见到他就认得出来？"悟空强忍着笑问。

> "那当然，"和尚说，"你问这个干什么？"

  金光一闪，悟空恢复了猴子的模样。

> "孙悟空！"和尚们惊呼一声。

  他们纷纷跪倒在地。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Six: The Tiger Immortal

## ①

  Wukong led the monks to his companions. The monks told the Tang Monk everything that they had told Wukong.

> "That's terrible," said the Tang Monk. "We must help you."

> "Yes!" the monkey agreed. "I'll deal with the Tiger Immortal in the morning."

  The monks knew of an empty building nearby. They led the travelers there and everyone went to sleep for the night.

## ②

  The next morning, Wukong woke up early. Someone was pounding on the door of the building. A voice boomed.

> "I am the Tiger Immortal!"

  The Tang Monk's eyes widened with fear. He and all the other monks trembled.

  Wukong, Wujing, and Bajie drew their weapons.

> "No worry, everyone," said Wukong with a smile. "I'll deal with this villain."

  The monkey went outside.

## ③

> "Who are you?" demanded the Tiger Immortal.

> "I am Sun Wukong," said the monkey. "And you should be ashamed of yourself. Just because you're a little powerful, you think you can treat the Buddhist monks badly."

> "A little powerful?" The Tiger Immortal looked offended. "I am very powerful."

  Wukong laughed.

> "You're not as powerful as I am. Did you know that the Jade Emperor is afraid of me? I defeated his entire army."

## ④

  The Tiger Immortal puffed out his chest.

> "I can summon rain," he said. "I doubt you can do that."

  Wukong snored.

> "I can summon rain. It's easy."

  "Well then, let's have a contest," said Wukong. "Whoever summons more rain is the winner."

  "If you win," said the Tiger Immortal, "I'll let you and all the monks go free. But if I win, you must stay here and be my slaves."

> "You're on," said Wukong. "I accept your challenge."

## ⑤

  The Tiger Immortal led everyone into town. In the center of town was a Daoist altar. A stone tablet, incense sticks, and papers with magic writing were on the altar. A crowd of people arrived to see what was going on.

> "I will go first," announced the Tiger Immortal.

  He walked toward the altar.

## ⑥

  The Tang Monk shook his head.

> "This is terrible," he muttered.

  Bajie glanced at him.

> "Don't worry, Master. We'll win this contest."

> "But what if he doesn't win?" asked the monk. "We'll all be stuck here, forced to work for the Tiger Immortal. If that happens, we'll never reach the Western Paradise. The true scriptures will never get to the Tang Empire."

  The monk buried his face in his hands.

> "Bajie is right, Master," said Wujing. "We have nothing to worry about."

  Wukong stood by them smiling. From the altar, the Tiger Immortal called out.

> "I will now pray to Heaven for rain!"

## ⑦

  The Tiger Immortal lit the incense and then sat down. He closed his eyes and began to recite a spell. Next, he lit one of the papers on fire. When that one went out, he lit another paper. Soon all of the papers were gone.

  The Tiger Immortal lifted the stone tablet and then slammed it down. There was a gasp from the crowd.

  Wukong looked up at the sky, which was becoming dark. Wind blew and dark clouds moved in. Thunder rumbled.

  The Tang Monk trembled.

> "Oh no, it's working. It's going to rain."

## ⑧

  Wukong chuckled.

> "You all stay here. I'll probably be right back."

  The monkey recited a quick spell and then left his body. Up in the sky, he found the Old Woman of the Wind fanning the clouds. The Dragon King of the Eastern Sea was approaching.

> "Stop what you're doing!" Wukong called out. "Don't make any rain."

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十六章：虎仙


## ①

  悟空带着和尚们来到同伴身边。那些和尚把告诉悟空的事又都对唐僧说了一遍。

> "太残忍了，"唐僧说，"我们一定要帮你们。"

> "没错！"猴子说，"明天一早我就去对付虎力大仙。"

  和尚们知道附近有一处空房子，就带行者们去了那里。大家都睡了一夜。

## ②

  第二天一早，悟空早早地就醒了，有人正在用力拍打房门。一个洪亮的声音传来。

> "我是虎力大仙！"

  唐僧吓得睁大了眼睛，他和其他和尚全都浑身发抖。

  悟空、悟净和八戒都拔出了兵器。

> "大家别担心，"悟空笑着说，"我来对付这个恶人。"

  猴子走到了外面。

## ③

> "你是谁？"虎力大仙问道。

> "我是孙悟空，"猴子说，"你应该为自己感到可耻。就因为你有点法力，就可以这样虐待和尚吗？"

> "有点法力？"虎力大仙面露怒色，"我可是法力高强的！"

  悟空笑了起来。

> "你可没有我厉害。你知道玉皇大帝都怕我吗？我打败过他的全部天兵天将。"

## ④

  虎力大仙挺起胸膛。

> "我能呼风唤雨。"

  悟空哼了一声。

> "我恐怕你未必做得到。"

> "我能呼风唤雨，"虎力大仙说，"这很简单。"

  悟空说："那好，我们来比一比。谁唤来的雨多谁就赢。"

  "你要是赢了，"虎力大仙说，"我就让所有和尚都自由。不过要是我赢了，你们就得留下来做我的奴才。"

  "一言为定，"悟空说，"我接受你的挑战。"

## ⑤

  虎力大仙带着所有人进了城。城中央有一座道教祭坛，祭坛上放着石碑、香和写有符咒的纸。一大群人赶来看热闹。

> "我先来！"虎力大仙宣布道。

  他走向祭坛。

## ⑥

  唐僧摇了摇头。

> "这可怎么办，"他嘟囔道。

  八戒看了看他。

> "师父别担心，我们会赢的。"

> "可他要是输了呢？"一个和尚问，"那我们就全都被困在这里，给虎力大仙当苦力。那样的话，我们就再也到不了西天，经书也永远送不回大唐。"

  和尚把脸埋在手里。

> "八戒说得对，师父，"悟净说，"我们不用担心的。"

  悟空站在一旁微笑着。祭坛上，虎力大仙大声喊道：

> "我现在就向天祈雨！"

## ⑦

  虎力大仙点了香，坐下来闭上眼睛，开始念咒。然后他点燃了一张符纸，烧完之后又点燃另一张。不一会儿，符纸全都烧完了。

  虎力大仙拿起石碑，用力拍了下去。人群中传来一阵惊呼。

  悟空抬头望向天空，天色渐渐暗了下来。风吹过来，乌云聚集。雷声隆隆。

  唐僧吓得发抖。

> "不好了，他真的在唤雨。"

## ⑧

  悟空微微一笑。

> "你们在这里等着，我一会儿就回来。"

  猴子念了一段咒语，灵魂出窍飞上天空。在天上他找到了风婆婆在扇风鼓云。东海龙王正朝这边飞来。

> "停下手来！"悟空大喊道，"一滴雨也不许下！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Seven: A Guessing Game

## ①

  "Don't make any rain yet," Wukong repeated. "But we must!" said the old woman of the wind. "Someone on Earth just prayed for it!"

  "And the Jade Emperor heard the prayers," added the Dragon King of the Eastern Sea.

  "The person who recited the prayers is Bad," said Wukong. "He's the tiger immortal, and he plans to make the Tang Monk a slave."

  The Dragon King looked concerned. "That's terrible. We all want the Tang Monk to reach the Western Paradise."

  "But we must obey the Jade Emperor's orders," said the woman.

  "Yes, wait a moment," said the monkey. "I'll go back down to the ground now. When I raise my iron bar, you can make it rain."

  The woman and the Dragon King agreed to wait a moment.

## ②

  Wukong returned to his body. The stiffened tiger immortal shook with anger.

> "Why didn't my spell of water work?" he cried.

  Bajie laughed at him. "Some rain! You couldn't even summon one drop."

> "Don't try again!" said the tiger immortal.

  "No, you won't," said Wukong. "You had a chance to summon rain, and you obviously can't. Now it's my turn."

## ③

  The monkey raised his iron bar into the air. Instantly clouds moved back in, and thunder boomed. Rain began to pour down. The crowd cheered.

  The Tang Monk sighed. "Wonderful. Now all the Buddhist monks will be free. And we can continue our journey."

## ④

  The tiger immortal stomped over to Wukong.

> "I want another contest."

  Wukong laughed. "Why would you want another contest? You'll lose again."

  The tiger immortal ignored the monkey's question. "I challenge the Tang Monk to a guessing game."

  The Tang Monk's mouth fell open. "But..."

  "We accept your challenge," said the monkey with a smile.

  "Good!" said the tiger immortal. "I will be right back." He walked away.

## ⑤

> "Wukong, why did you agree to this contest?" asked the Tang Monk.

  "I will win. Don't worry, Master," said the monkey. "I'll help you."

  The tiger immortal soon came back with a small box.

> "If you can guess what's in this box, I will let you all go free."

  As the Tang Monk stared at the box, Wukong plucked a hair. Using his magic, he made the hair look like himself. Then he made himself tiny and squeezed through a crack in the box. Inside the box was a ripe peach. Quickly, he ate the peach, leaving only the pit. A moment later, he was standing next to the Tang Monk again.

## ⑥

  Wukong leaned toward the monk and whispered:

> "It's a peach pit."

> "Are you sure?" whispered the monk. "How do you know?"

> "Stop talking to each other!" said the tiger immortal. "What's in the box?"

> "I think it's a peach pit," said the monk nervously.

  "You're wrong, monk," said the tiger immortal. "It's not just a peach pit. It's a whole peach. I'll show you."

## ⑦

  The tiger immortal opened the box and showed it to everyone.

> "See?"

  The Tang Monk smiled. "I was right. It is a peach pit."

  "What?" cried the tiger immortal. He looked in the box and gasped. "Who ate the peach?"

  Wukong laughed.

> "Wukong, with the Tang Monk, guessed correctly. I guess we can leave now," said Wujing.

  "Yes, but we should eat some dinner first," said Bajie. "All this talk about peaches has made me hungry."

  Wukong looked at the tiger immortal. "You will set the Buddhist monks free now, right?"

## ⑧

  The tiger immortal glared at the monkey.

> "I challenge you to another contest!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十七章：猜谜游戏


## ①

  "先别下雨，"悟空重复道。"但我们必须下！"风婆婆说。"地上有人祈雨了！"

  "玉帝听到了祈祷，"东海龙王补充道。

  "祈雨的是虎力大仙，"悟空说。"他是只虎精，他想让唐僧做他的奴隶。"

  龙王看起来很担心。"太可怕了。我们都希望唐僧能到达西天。"

  "但我们必须遵从玉帝的命令，"风婆婆说。

  "好，等一下，"悟空说。"我现在回到地面去。等我举起金箍棒，你们就下雨。"

  风婆婆和龙王同意等一等。

## ②

  悟空回到了自己的身体里。僵住的虎力大仙气得发抖。

> "我的求雨法术怎么不灵了？"他叫道。

  八戒嘲笑他。"还下雨呢！你连一滴雨都求不来。"

> "别再试了！"虎力大仙说。

  "不，该你了，"悟空说。"你有机会求雨，可你明显不行。现在轮到我。"

## ③

  悟空将金箍棒举向空中。顿时乌云密布，雷声轰鸣，大雨倾盆而下。人群欢呼起来。

  唐僧叹了口气。"太好了。现在所有佛教僧侣都自由了，我们可以继续赶路了。"

## ④

  虎力大仙气冲冲地走到悟空面前。

> "我要再比一场。"

  悟空笑了。"你为什么还要比？你又会输的。"

  虎力大仙不理会悟空的话。"我挑战唐僧，比猜物！"

  唐僧张大了嘴。"可是……"

  "我们接受你的挑战，"悟空笑着说。

  "好！"虎力大仙说。"我马上回来。"他走开了。

## ⑤

> "悟空，你为什么答应这个比赛？"唐僧问。

  "我们会赢的。别担心，师父，"悟空说。"我会帮你的。"

  虎力大仙很快带着一个小匣子回来了。

> "如果你们能猜出这匣子里装的是什么，我就放你们走。"

  唐僧盯着匣子，悟空拔了一根毫毛，用毫毛变了个自己，然后把自己变小，从匣子的裂缝钻了进去。匣子里是一颗熟透的桃子。悟空迅速把桃子吃了，只剩桃核。一会儿，他又回到了唐僧身边。

## ⑥

  悟空凑近唐僧低声说：

> "是桃核。"

> "你确定吗？"唐僧低声问。"你怎么知道的？"

> "别互相说话了！"虎力大仙说。"匣子里是什么？"

> "我觉得是桃核，"唐僧紧张地说。

  "你猜错了，和尚，"虎力大仙说。"不只是桃核，是一整个桃子。我给你们看。"

## ⑦

  虎力大仙打开匣子给大家看。

> "看到了吧？"

  唐僧笑了。"我猜对了，就是桃核。"

  "什么？"虎力大仙叫道。他看了看匣子，大吃一惊。"谁把桃子吃了？"

  悟空哈哈大笑。

> "悟空和唐僧猜对了。我想我们现在可以走了吧，"悟净说。

  "可以，但我们应该先吃晚饭，"八戒说。"说了这么多桃子，我都饿了。"

  悟空看着虎力大仙。"你现在就释放那些佛教僧侣，对吧？"

## ⑧

  虎力大仙怒视着悟空。

> "我再挑战你们比一场！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Eight: The Meditation Contest

## ①

  To the West, chapter fifty-eight: the Meditation Contest.

> "I challenge you to a Meditation Contest," said the tiger immortal. "Whoever can meditate the longest without moving is the winner."

  Wukong pondered. *I used to meditate a lot,* he thought. *But I haven't done it lately. I'm terrible at sitting still.*

  The Tang Monk stepped forward. "I accept your challenge."

> "Master, are you sure?" asked Wujing.

  The Tang Monk nodded. "I've spent many years meditating. This contest will be easy for me."

  The tiger immortal grinned. "This won't be an ordinary meditation contest. We will float in the air and meditate. Can you do that?"

  Now the Tang Monk looked nervous.

## ②

  But before the monk could answer, Wukong clapped him on the back.

> "Of course the Tang Monk can float in the air and meditate," he replied.

  Then he whispered into the monk's ear: "Don't worry, Master. You just meditate. I'll handle everything else."

> "What are you babbling about?" snapped the tiger immortal. "Let's start the contest!"

## ③

  The tiger immortal and the Tang Monk went in front of the crowd. They sat down with their legs crossed and their palms facing up. They closed their eyes and started meditating. After a moment the tiger immortal slowly floated up into the air.

> "Ah," said Bajie. "Master can't do that. He'll lose the contest."

  "Don't worry," said Wukong. "He just needs some help from me."

## ④

  Wukong recited a spell and then blew toward the Tang Monk. The monk lifted off the ground. His eyes remained closed. Soon he was floating next to the tiger immortal.

> "I think Master will win this contest," said Wujing.

  "I'm pretty good at meditating too," said Bajie. "I could have competed in this contest."

  "Wukong's smart. It would take a lot of magic to lift you, Bajie."

  "The pig's mortified."

## ⑤

> "Master's space is twitching!" said Wujing suddenly.

  "I'll check," said Bajie. "I wonder what's wrong."

> "Maybe he has a flea," said Wujing. "This isn't good. If the monk moves at all, he will lose the contest."

  Wukong looked up at the Tang Monk. "I think he has an itch," said the monkey. "Wait here."

  Wukong became invisible and flew up to the monk. A flea was crawling on the monk's head.

  *Hmm,* thought Wukong. *Why would a flea land on the Tang Monk? He has no hair.* The monkey bit his lip. *The tiger immortal must have used magic to put this flea here. That rotten cheater.*

  Wukong brushed the flea away and scratched the Tang Monk's head. The monk's face stopped twitching.

## ⑥

  *Now I'll teach the tiger immortal a lesson,* thought Wukong.

  The monkey plucked one of his hairs and turned it into a centipede. He dropped the centipede onto the tiger immortal's head. The tiger immortal's ear twitched as the centipede crawled over it. Then the centipede crawled along his mouth. The tiger immortal's lip curled slightly. His eyes wrinkled.

  Next the centipede crawled onto the tiger immortal's nose. The tiger immortal sniffed. And then—

> "Ow!" cried the tiger immortal. "Something bit me!"

  He lost his concentration and fell, hitting the ground with a puff of smoke. When the smoke cleared, a dead tiger lay on the ground. The crowd gasped.

## ⑦

  Wukong and the Tang Monk came back down. The crowd was silent. Daoists and Buddhists all stared at one another. The monkey cleared his throat.

> "The tiger immortal was just an evil tiger spirit. Now that he's gone, I want you Daoists to treat the Buddhists kindly. Everybody should live together peacefully."

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十八章：打坐比试


## ①

  西游记第五十八集：打坐比赛。

> "我挑战和你们比打坐，"虎力大仙说。"谁打坐不动的时间最长，谁就赢。"

  悟空想了起来。*我以前经常打坐，*他想。*但最近没坐了。我最不擅长安静地坐着了。*

  唐僧走上前。"我接受你的挑战。"

> "师父，您确定吗？"悟净问。

  唐僧点了点头。"我打坐多年，这个比赛对我来说轻而易举。"

  虎力大仙咧嘴一笑。"这可不是普通的打坐比赛。我们要在空中悬浮着打坐。你们能做到吗？"

  这下唐僧看起来紧张了。

## ②

  但没等唐僧回答，悟空拍了拍他的肩膀。

> "唐僧当然能在空中悬浮打坐，"他回答说。

  然后他在唐僧耳边低语："别担心，师父。您只管打坐，其余的交给我。"

> "你们在嘀咕什么？"虎力大仙厉声说。"开始比赛吧！"

## ③

  虎力大仙和唐僧走到人群前面。他们盘腿坐下，掌心向上，闭上眼睛开始打坐。过了一会儿，虎力大仙缓缓飘向了空中。

> "啊，"八戒说。"师父可做不到这个。他会输掉比赛的。"

  "别担心，"悟空说。"他需要我帮点忙。"

## ④

  悟空念了个咒语，然后朝唐僧吹了一口气。唐僧离开地面飘了起来，眼睛依然闭着。很快他就和虎力大仙一样悬浮在空中了。

> "我觉得师父能赢这场比赛，"悟净说。

  "我打坐也挺厉害的，"八戒说。"我也可以参加这场比赛。"

  "悟空聪明得很。八戒，要浮起来你可得费不少法力。"

  八戒满脸窘态。

## ⑤

> "师父的脸在抽动！"悟净突然说。

  "我去看看，"八戒说。"不知道怎么回事。"

> "也许他长了跳蚤，"悟净说。"这可不好。只要师父动一下，他就输了。"

  悟空抬头看着唐僧。"我想他有点痒，"悟空说。"等一下。"

  悟空隐身飞到唐僧身边。一只跳蚤正爬在唐僧的光头上。

  *嗯？*悟空想。*跳蚤怎么会落在唐僧头上？他又没有头发。*悟空咬了咬嘴唇。*一定是虎力大仙用法术把跳蚤放在这的。这个卑鄙的家伙。*

  悟空赶走跳蚤，给唐僧挠了挠头。唐僧的脸不抽动了。

## ⑥

  *现在该教训教训虎力大仙了，*悟空心想。

  他拔下一根毫毛，变成了一条蜈蚣，放到虎力大仙的头上。蜈蚣爬过他的耳朵，他又爬到了他的嘴边。虎力大仙的嘴唇微微扭动，眼睛也眨了眨。

  接着蜈蚣又爬上了他的鼻子。虎力大仙吸了吸鼻子。然后——

> "哎哟！"虎力大仙叫道。"什么东西咬我！"

  他失去了注意力，从空中跌落下来，"砰"的一声摔在地上，化作一团烟雾。烟雾散去后，地上一只死老虎。人群倒吸一口凉气。

## ⑦

  悟空和唐僧降了下来。人群一片寂静。道士和佛教徒面面相觑。悟空清了清嗓子。

> "虎力大仙不过是一只邪恶的虎精。现在他不在了，我希望你们道士善待佛教徒。大家应该和平共处。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Fifty-Nine: Scared Villagers

## ①

> "Can we please stop and rest?" moaned Bajie one day.

  The group had spent the morning walking down a long mountain trail.

> "My knees are weak," cried the pig.

  "We'll rest in a little while, Bajie," said the Tang Monk.

  As they walked, the travelers started to hear the sound of rushing water. It grew louder and louder.

> "We're approaching a river," said Wujing.

  The trail went around a hill. A moment later, the travelers saw the river.

> "How will we cross this river?" said the Tang Monk. "It's so wide, I can't see the other side."

  Wukong leaped into the air and looked around. "There's a small village nearby," he said. "Maybe someone there has a boat."

## ②

  The group walked to the village. The street was deserted. A few villagers peeked out of windows and from behind doors. They looked scared.

  A man was getting water from a well.

> "Hello?" said Wujing.

  Startled, the man dropped his bucket down the well and spun around. "Who are you?"

  The Tang Monk stepped forward. "I'm from the Tang Empire. We're traveling to the Western Paradise to get scriptures from Buddha."

## ③

  The man relaxed a bit.

  "We need a boat to get across the river," said Bajie.

> "I don't have a boat," said the man. "But someone in the village might. Please come with me. I'll make some tea. My name is Chen."

  The travelers followed Chen to his home. Inside they sat down as Chen boiled water for tea.

> "Why does everyone in this village seem so scared?" asked the Tang Monk.

  Chen sighed and sat down. He started to cry.

> "Dear man," said the Tang Monk. "What's wrong? Did I upset you?"

> "No," said Chen through his tears. "It's just that life is very bad in this village."

## ④

  "A few years ago, a terrible demon arrived. He's always treated us badly, but now things are worse. He demanded that we give him a child. If we don't, he'll destroy our entire village. Tomorrow morning, I must hand over my son."

  Chen burst into tears all over again.

  Wukong giggled and then laughed.

  The Tang Monk glared at the monkey.

> "Wukong! Why are you laughing?"

  Bajie shook his head. "He's cruel, Master. You should recite the Tight-Fillet Spell," he said.

  "No need for that," said Wukong, still laughing.

## ⑤

  He turned to Chen. "I'm not laughing at you, sir. I'm laughing because today is the luckiest day of your life."

  Chen raised his eyebrows. "Oh, am I lucky?"

> "You've probably never heard of me," said Wukong. "But I am Sun Wukong, the Monkey King. I once defeated the Jade Emperor's entire army. And tomorrow I will save your son's life."

> "Are you a spirit?" asked Chen.

  "Yes, a very powerful spirit," said Wukong. "Bring your son out here. I need to look at him."

  Chen left the room for a moment. When he came back, a small boy was with him.

> "This is my son," said Chen.

  Wukong walked around the boy, examining him closely. Finally, the monkey folded his arms and said:

> "I have a plan."

## ⑥

  The next morning the boy climbed onto a small platform. Several villagers carried the platform to the edge of the river. They placed the platform on the ground and then backed away. For a moment everything was quiet. The boy sat alone on the platform.

  Suddenly a dark cloud approached. A fierce-looking demon emerged from the cloud. It had shark teeth.

  The boy smiled at the demon.

> "Hello?"

---

# 🇨🇳 第五十九章：受惊的村民


## ①

> "我们能停下来休息一会儿吗？"八戒抱怨道。

  一行人一上午都在沿着一条长长的山路走着。

> "我的腿都软了，"八戒叫道。

  "过一会儿就休息，八戒，"唐僧说。

  他们走了一会儿，开始听到哗哗的水声。声音越来越大。

> "快到一条河了，"悟净说。

  小路绕过一座小山。不久，一行人看到了那条河。

> "我们怎么过河呀？"唐僧说。"河太宽了，我都看不到对岸。"

  悟空腾空而起，看了看四周。"附近有个小村庄，"他说。"也许那里有人有船。"

## ②

  一行人走到村里。街上空无一人。几个村民从窗户和门后偷偷张望，看起来很害怕。

  一个男人正在井边打水。

> "你好？"悟净打招呼。

  男人吓了一跳，水桶掉进了井里，转身问道："你们是谁？"

  唐僧走上前。"我来自大唐。我们要去西天拜佛求经。"

## ③

  男人放松了一些。

  "我们需要一条船过河，"八戒说。

> "我没有船，"男人说。"但村里也许有人有。请跟我来，我给你们沏茶。我叫陈澄。"

  一行人跟着陈澄回到家。他们坐下来，陈澄烧水泡了茶。

> "为什么这个村里的人看起来都这么害怕？"唐僧问。

  陈澄叹了口气，坐下来。他哭了起来。

> "好人啊，"唐僧说。"怎么了？我惹你不高兴了吗？"

> "不是，"陈澄流着泪说。"只是我们村的日子太苦了。"

## ④

  "几年前来了一个可怕的妖怪。他一直欺负我们，但现在更糟糕了。他逼我们给他送一个孩子。如果不送，他就会毁掉我们整个村子。明天早上，我必须把我儿子交给他。"

  陈澄又放声大哭起来。

  悟空偷偷笑了起来，随即哈哈大笑。

  唐僧怒视着悟空。

> "悟空！你笑什么？"

  八戒摇了摇头。"他太坏了，师父。您该念念紧箍咒了。"

  "不用念，"悟空还在笑。

## ⑤

  他对陈澄说："我不是在笑话您。我笑是因为今天是您最幸运的日子。"

  陈澄挑起眉毛。"哦，是吗？"

> "您可能没听说过我，"悟空说。"但我就是齐天大圣孙悟空。我当年打败过玉帝的整支天兵天将。明天我就能救您儿子的命。"

> "您是神仙吗？"陈澄问。

  "是的，一个非常厉害的神仙，"悟空说。"把您儿子带出来吧，我得看看他。"

  陈澄离开房间一会儿。回来的时候，身边跟着一个小男孩。

> "这是我儿子，"陈澄说。

  悟空绕着男孩走了一圈，仔细查看。最后，悟空抱起双臂说：

> "我有个计划。"

## ⑥

  第二天早上，男孩爬上了一个小平台。几个村民把平台抬到了河边。他们把平台放在地上，然后退开。四周安静了片刻。男孩独自坐在平台上。

  突然一朵乌云逼近。一个面目狰狞的妖怪从云中现身，长着鲨鱼般的牙齿。

  男孩对着妖怪笑了笑。

> "你好？"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty: Snow

## ①

  The demon eyed the smiling boy suspiciously.

> "Are you scared of me?" asked the demon.

> "No," said the boy. "Should I be?"

> "Well, yes," said the demon. "I plan to eat you. Doesn't that sound terrible?"

  The boy shrugged. "Not really."

  The demon hesitated for a moment and then moved closer. Suddenly the boy changed into Wukong. The monkey pulled out his iron bar and swung. The demon jumped back and Wukong missed.

## ②

> "Who are you?" demanded the demon.

> "I am Sun Wukong," said the monkey. "And you should be ashamed of yourself. What kind of monster eats children?"

  "Sun Wukong," said the demon. "I thought you were trapped under a mountain. What are you doing here?"

> "My punishment is over," said the monkey. "I'm traveling to the Western Paradise with the Tang Monk."

  The demon hesitated a little, then turned. Wukong lunged. The demon spun around and disappeared.

## ③

  The monkey returned to Chen's home and told everyone what had happened.

> "Because of you, I still have my son," said Chen. "Thank you."

> "You're welcome," said Wukong. "But I believe the demon now wants to capture the Tang Monk. So in the morning we must find a boat and leave."

  Meanwhile the demon was deep under the water.

  "I must capture the Tang Monk and eat him," he said to himself. "It won't be easy with that monkey around. I'll need some magic."

## ④

  Late that night, a cold wind blew. A snowflake drifted to the ground. Then another one fell, and another.

  Bajie couldn't sleep.

  "It's freezing in here," he said to himself. He looked at Wukong and Wujing. Both of them were sleeping soundly.

  "Those two look very comfortable. That blanket must be warmer than mine."

## ⑤

  In the morning, Wukong woke up shivering.

  "That was terrible. I'm so cold," he said to himself. He looked down at his body. "No wonder I was cold. What happened to my blanket?"

  Wujing woke up. "Why is it so cold? And where did my blanket go?"

  They looked at Bajie. The pig was tucked cozy under three blankets. Even his head was covered.

  Wukong gave him a kick. "Wake up, pig!"

## ⑥

  Bajie rolled over, giggling under the blanket.

  Wujing frowned.

  Wukong scratched his head. "Why is it so cold anyway? It's spring!" He looked out the window and gasped. "It snowed last night."

  They woke the Tang Monk, Chen, and everyone went outside. A thick blanket of snow covered the entire village.

> "It would be dangerous to cross the river in this weather," said Chen. "You should stay here until the snow melts."

## ⑦

  A villager ran over. "The river is frozen solid," he said.

  "That's wonderful news," the Tang Monk smiled. "Maybe we can walk across it."

  The travelers thanked Chen and said goodbye. Soon they were standing at the edge of the frozen river.

> "I wonder if it's safe to walk on," said Wujing.

  "I'll test it with my rake," said Bajie.

  The pig walked onto the ice and raised his rake. *Bam!* He brought the rake down hard, but the ice didn't crack.

> "It's solid," he said.

## ⑧

  The travelers stepped onto the ice and started walking. After a few hours, the river bank was no longer in sight.

  Suddenly there was a rumbling sound. And the ice shook.

> "What caused that?" asked the monk.

> "I don't know," said Wujing. "But we should be—"

  *Crack.*

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十章：大雪


## ①

  妖怪狐疑地打量着这个微笑的男孩。

> "你怕我吗？"妖怪问。

> "不怕，"男孩说。"我应该怕吗？"

> "当然应该，"妖怪说。"我打算吃了你。听着不可怕吗？"

  男孩耸了耸肩。"没什么可怕的。"

  妖怪犹豫了一下，然后凑近了些。突然男孩变成了悟空。悟空掏出金箍棒就抡了过去。妖怪跳开了，悟空扑了个空。

## ②

> "你是谁？"妖怪问道。

> "我是孙悟空，"悟空说。"你真该感到羞耻。什么妖怪连小孩子都吃？"

  "孙悟空，"妖怪说。"我以为你被压在山下呢。你来这里干什么？"

> "我的惩罚已经结束了，"悟空说。"我和唐僧正在去西天的路上。"

  妖怪犹豫了一下，然后转身要跑。悟空扑了过去。妖怪转了个身就不见了。

## ③

  悟空回到陈家，把经过告诉了大家。

> "多亏了你，我还留住了儿子，"陈澄说。"谢谢你。"

> "不客气，"悟空说。"但我相信那妖怪现在想来抓唐僧。所以明天一早我们得找条船赶紧离开。"

  与此同时，妖怪潜到了水底深处。

  "我必须抓住唐僧吃了他，"他自言自语。"有那只猴子在可不容易。我得用些法术。"

## ④

  深夜，一阵寒风吹来。一片雪花飘落到地上。然后又落了一片，又一片。

  八戒睡不着。

  "太冷了，"他自言自语。他看了看悟空和悟净，两人都睡得很香。

  "这两人看起来真舒服。他们的毯子一定比我的暖和。"

## ⑤

  第二天早上，悟空冻得发抖，醒了过来。

  "太冷了，"他自言自语。他低头看了看自己。"难怪我冷。我的毯子哪去了？"

  悟净也醒了。"怎么这么冷？我的毯子呢？"

  他们看了看八戒。这猪裹着三条毯子，舒舒服服地躺着，连头都盖住了。

  悟空踢了他一脚。"醒醒，猪八戒！"

## ⑥

  八戒翻了个身，在毯子底下偷笑。

  悟净皱了皱眉。

  悟空挠了挠头。"怎么这么冷？明明是春天！"他朝窗外一看，倒吸一口气。"昨天下雪了。"

  他们叫醒唐僧、陈澄和所有人。大家走到外面。厚厚的积雪覆盖了整个村庄。

> "这种天气过河太危险了，"陈澄说。"你们应该等雪化了再走。"

## ⑦

  一个村民跑了过来。"河已经冻得结结实实了，"他说。

  "太好了，"唐僧笑了。"也许我们可以走过去。"

  一行人谢过陈澄，告别出发。他们很快站在结冰的河边。

> "不知道走上去安不安全，"悟净说。

  "我用钉耙试试，"八戒说。

  八戒走上冰面，举起钉耙。"嘭！"他使劲砸了下去，冰面纹丝不动。

> "冰很结实，"他说。

## ⑧

  一行人踏上冰面开始行走。几个小时后，河岸已经从视野中消失了。

  突然传来一阵轰隆声，冰面晃动起来。

> "那是什么声音？"唐僧问。

> "不知道，"悟净说。"但我们应该——"

  *咔嚓。*

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-One: The Demon Under the Ice

## ①

  Wukong leaped into the air. His three companions and the horse fell into the water with a splash. Bajie climbed back out, coughing. Wujing came up next, pulling the horse behind him.

> "Where's the Tang Monk?" cried Wukong.

  Below the ice, the Tang Monk struggled as the demon carried him deep underwater. The demon laughed.

> "You all fell for my trick. I froze the river and waited for you to cross it. Once you were above me, I cracked the ice open. As soon as his friends leave, I will eat him and live forever."

## ②

  They arrived at a palace. A sign over the door read: *Residence of the River Turtle*.

  The demon went inside and locked the monk in a stone box.

  Up on the ice, Wukong paced back and forth.

> "The ice didn't crack by accident," said the monkey. "I'm sure it was the demon. The demon probably caused this strange cold weather too. He made us freeze! I can't believe we fell for his trick. We must save the Tang Monk."

## ③

  Wukong stopped pacing and looked at his companions.

> "My powers aren't very strong underwater. You two must go down there and entice the demon to come back up."

  Wu Jing and Bajie nodded and dived into the river. They soon spotted a palace. Wujing read the sign over the door.

> "Residence of the River Turtle. I wonder if the demon is in here."

  Bajie knocked on the door. *Whop! Whop!* He shouted.

## ④

  The door opened and the demon stepped out. He was holding a large hammer.

> "What do you want?" he asked.

> "Did you kidnap our master?" asked Wujing.

> "Yes," said the demon. "I plan to eat him. Now go away."

  The demon tried to close the door, but Wujing stopped it with his spear. The demon moved toward him. Bajie's rake came crashing down.

  *Cling!*

  The demon blocked the rake with his hammer. The three fighters clashed.

## ⑤

  After a few minutes, Bajie pretended to be scared. He swam upward and Wujing soon followed.

> "Go after them!" called the demon, swimming toward the surface.

  The demon jumped out of the water and onto the ice. Wukong was waiting for him. The monkey swung his iron bar. The demon dodged. The bar hit the ice. The demon swung his hammer.

  *Bam!* More cracks formed in the ice. *Cling! Boom! Clash!*

  The spirit fought on the broken ice. The demon hit Bajie's legs.

> "Ow!" cried the pig.

  He slid across the ice and slammed into Wujing. The pig slipped and fell.

  The demon laughed and dived back under the ice.

## ⑥

  Bajie and Wujing stood back up.

> "The demon escaped," said the pig.

  "We must stop him before he eats the Tang Monk," said Wukong. "Go back down there and try to lead him up here again."

  Wujing and Bajie dived into the river. When they reached the palace, they found a huge pile of rocks blocking the door. Bajie struck the rocks with his rake. The rake bounced off. The rocks didn't move at all. Wujing stabbed at the rocks with his spear. Again, the rocks didn't move.

> "What kind of rocks are these?" cried the pig.

> "Maybe they're held in place with magic," said Wujing.

## ⑦

  They returned to the surface of the river and told Wukong about the rocks.

  The monkey sighed. "We need Guanyin's help."

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十一章：冰下妖怪


## ①

  悟空腾空而起。他的三个同伴和马匹扑通一声掉进了水里。八戒咳嗽着爬了出来。悟净紧随其后，拖着马。

> "唐僧呢？"悟空叫道。

  冰层下面，唐僧拼命挣扎，而妖怪正把他往水底深处拖。妖怪大笑起来。

> "你们都中了我的计。我冻住了河流，等你们走在上面，然后弄破冰面。等你们的朋友们一走，我就吃了他，永远不死。"

## ②

  他们来到了一座宫殿。门上挂着一块牌子："河鼋之宅"。

  妖怪走进宫里，把唐僧锁在了一个石匣里。

  冰面上，悟空来回踱步。

> "冰面裂开不是意外，"悟空说。"肯定是妖怪干的。这场怪寒大概也是他搞的。他让我们挨冻！真不敢相信我们上了他的当。我们必须去救唐僧。"

## ③

  悟空停下脚步，看着同伴们。

> "我的法力在水下不太强。你们俩得下去把那妖怪引上来。"

  悟净和八戒点了点头，潜入了河里。很快他们看到了一座宫殿。悟净念了念门上的牌子。

> "河鼋之宅。不知道妖怪在不在里面。"

  八戒敲了敲门。*咚咚咚！*他喊着。

## ④

  门开了，妖怪走了出来，手里拿着一把大锤子。

> "你们想干什么？"他问。

> "是不是你绑架了我们师父？"悟净问。

> "是，"妖怪说。"我打算吃他。现在快滚。"

  妖怪想关门，但悟净用矛挡住了门。妖怪向他逼近。八戒的钉耙猛砸下来。

  *叮！*

  妖怪用锤子挡住了钉耙。三个战士打作一团。

## ⑤

  打了一会儿，八戒假装害怕了，向水面游去，悟净也跟着游了上去。

> "追他们！"妖怪喊着，向水面游去。

  妖怪跃出水面，跳上了冰面。悟空正等着他。悟空抡起金箍棒。妖怪躲开了，棒子砸在冰上。妖怪挥起锤子。

  *啪！*冰面又裂开了几道口子。*叮！轰！哐！*

  妖怪在碎冰上厮杀，踢了八戒的腿一下。

> "哎哟！"八戒叫了起来。

  八戒在冰上滑了一大截，撞到了悟净。八戒摔倒了。

  妖怪大笑着跳回了水下。

## ⑥

  八戒和悟净重新站了起来。

> "妖怪跑了，"八戒说。

  "我们必须阻止他，不然他就要吃了唐僧，"悟空说。"再下去一趟，试着把他引上来。"

  悟净和八戒再次潜入河里。他们到宫殿前，发现一大堆石头堵住了门。八戒用钉耙猛砸石头，钉耙弹了回来，石头纹丝不动。悟净用矛猛刺石头，还是动不了。

> "这是什么石头？"八戒叫道。

> "大概是用法术固定的，"悟净说。

## ⑦

  他们回到水面，把石头的事告诉了悟空。

  悟空叹了口气。"我们需要观音来帮忙了。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Two: The Goldfish in the Basket

## ①

  Wukong landed on Mount Potalaka. A young man was meditating in the garden.

> "Where's Guanyin?" asked the monkey.

> "She's making a basket," said the man. He glanced at the monkey. "It's good to see you again, Wukong."

  Wukong was puzzled. "How do you know my name? Don't you recognize me?"

  Wukong stared for a moment and then gasped.

> "You're Red Boy! You look like a kind spirit now."

> "Yes," said Red Boy. "I'm not an evil demon anymore. And I have you to thank for that. You brought Guanyin into my life. She is teaching me all about Buddhism and now I'm very happy."

> "You're welcome," said Wukong. "You and I have a lot in common. We were both evil, causing all sorts of problems. Now we're both Buddhists."

## ②

  Guanyin came over holding a basket.

> "Hello, Wukong," said the Bodhisattva. "I knew you would come here today. I've been working on this basket all morning."

  A look of confusion spread across the monkey's face. "That's a nice basket, Bodhisattva. But what is it for?"

> "This basket has magical powers," said Guanyin. "I will catch the demon with it. Let's go."

## ③

  Wukong returned to the river with Guanyin. The Bodhisattva used a rope to lower the basket into the river. She recited a spell and then waited. After a moment she pulled the basket out of the water. Wukong looked in the basket. A small goldfish was flopping around in it.

  The monkey laughed. "I guess you need to try again, Bodhisattva. That's not the demon."

> "This is my goldfish," said Guanyin. "It usually lives in my lotus pond. The pond is near my garden where I teach my students. After years of listening to my lessons, the fish became a spirit. It escaped to Earth a few days ago. I had been wondering where it was."

> "A few days ago," repeated Wukong. "That means it's been on Earth for a few years."

> "Correct," said Guanyin. "The Tang Monk is safe now. You may go free him and continue your journey to the Western Paradise."

## ④

  Guanyin flew off and Wukong swam down to the palace. Now that the goldfish was gone, so was its magic. The monkey smashed the rocks with his iron bar and went inside.

> "Master, I'm here!" he cried.

  He got the monk out of the box and carried him out of the river.

  By now all the villagers had heard that Wukong had rescued Chen's son. When the travelers returned, the villagers cheered.

> "Please stay in our village!" said a man.

> "Yes," said an old woman. "Stay for as long as you like!"

> "Thank you," said the Tang Monk. "But we can stay only one more night to rest. In the morning we must leave. We still have far to travel."

## ⑤

  The villagers held a feast for the travelers that evening. By the time everyone went to sleep, it was late.

  The next morning the travelers woke to the sound of chopping.

> "What's going on?" asked the Tang Monk.

  They went to the river and found a very busy scene. Several men were chopping down trees. Other people carried tools.

> "We're building a boat for you!" said a smiling man.

> "Thank you," said the monk.

  He and his companions sat down by the water to wait. Suddenly there was a rumble and waves splashed onto the shore. Everyone stared in fear as a large creature rose from the waves.

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十二章：篮中金鱼


## ①

  悟空来到了普陀山。一个年轻人正在花园里打坐。

> "观音菩萨在哪？"悟空问。

> "她在编竹篮，"年轻人说。他看了看悟空。"悟空，又见到你真好。"

  悟空很困惑。"你怎么知道我的名字？你不认识我了吗？"

  悟空仔细看了看，随即吃了一惊。

> "你是红孩儿！你现在看起来像个善神了。"

> "是的，"红孩儿说。"我不再是妖怪了。这得感谢你。是你把观音请来的。她教我佛法，我现在很快乐。"

> "不客气，"悟空说。"你和我有很多相似之处。我们以前都是恶的，惹了不少麻烦。现在我们都成了佛门弟子。"

## ②

  观音拿着一个竹篮走了过来。

> "你好，悟空，"菩萨说。"我就知道你今天会来。我整个上午都在编这个篮子。"

  悟空一脸困惑。"篮子挺好看，菩萨。但它是用来做什么的？"

> "这个竹篮有法力，"观音说。"我要用它来收服妖怪。走吧。"

## ③

  悟空和观音回到了河边。菩萨用绳子把竹篮放进了河里。她念了一段咒语，然后等着。过了片刻，她把竹篮拉出水面。悟空朝篮子里一看，一条小金鱼在里面扑腾。

  悟空笑了。"菩萨，我想你得重新试试。那可不是妖怪。"

> "这是我的金鱼，"观音说。"它平常住在我莲花池里。池子在我花园旁边，我在那教书。多年来它听我讲课，修成了精。几天前它逃到了人间。我还一直找不到它呢。"

> "几天前？"悟空重复道。"那它在人间已经有好几年了。"

> "没错，"观音说。"现在唐僧安全了。你们可以去救他出来，继续西行取经。"

## ④

  观音飞走了，悟空游到水底的宫殿。金鱼一走，魔法也消失了。悟空一棒砸碎了堵住门的石头，走了进去。

> "师父，我来救你了！"他喊道。

  他把唐僧从石匣里救了出来，扛着他游出了河。

  此时全村人都听说悟空救了陈家的儿子。一行人回到村里时，村民们欢呼起来。

> "请留在我们村里吧！"一个男人说。

> "对呀，"一位老奶奶说。"想待多久就待多久！"

> "谢谢你们，"唐僧说。"但我们只能再住一晚休息。明天一早必须出发，前路还很远。"

## ⑤

  当天晚上村民们为旅行者举办了宴席。等所有人都去睡觉时，已经很晚了。

  第二天早上，旅行者们被叮叮当当的声音吵醒了。

> "发生什么事了？"唐僧问。

  他们走到河边，发现了一幅忙碌的景象。几个男人在砍树，其他人在搬运工具。

> "我们在给你们造船呢！"一个笑着的男人说。

> "谢谢你们，"唐僧说。

  他和同伴们在水边坐下来等着。突然一阵轰隆声响起，波浪拍到了岸上。一个巨大的生物从水中升起，大家恐惧地盯着它看。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Three: A Question for Buddha

## ①

  A steep riverbank lay ahead. The Tang Monk jumped to a stop as the villagers hid behind trees. Wukong, Wujing, and Bajie pulled out their weapons.

  A large shell rose from the water.

> "It's a giant turtle," said Bajie.

## ②

  The turtle bowed its head toward Wukong.

> "A bad demon had taken over my house and the river. Thank you for getting rid of him."

  The turtle then looked at the villagers.

> "You don't need to make a boat. I can take the travelers across the river."

## ③

> "That's wonderful," said the Tang Monk.

> "I'm from the Tang Empire and I know who you are," interrupted the turtle. "You're traveling to the Western Paradise to get scriptures from Buddha. I knew you would cross my river eventually. Climb onto my shell."

  Wukong eyed the turtle suspiciously.

> "How do we know we can trust you?"

## ④

> "Demons all along the way are waiting for my master to pass by," added Bajie. "They all want to eat him."

> "I promise I won't hurt the Tang Monk," said the turtle. "I want to help him reach the Western Paradise."

  After a little more hesitation, the travelers stepped onto the turtle's shell. The turtle began to paddle.

## ⑤

  The villagers came out from behind the trees and waved.

> "Goodbye," called a woman. "Please visit us on your way home," shouted someone else.

> "We will, I promise," called the monk.

  Soon the turtle was far from shore. Bajie fell asleep.

## ⑥

  The turtle glanced back at the Tang Monk.

> "Excuse me, but can you do me a favor?"

> "Of course," said the monk. "What do you need me to do?"

> "I have been a good Buddhist for over a thousand years," said the turtle. "But sadly I'm still just a turtle. Can you ask Buddha when I will be reborn as a human?"

  The Tang Monk nodded.

> "I will ask him."

## ⑦

  A few hours later, the turtle reached the other side of the river. The travelers stepped onto dry land.

> "Thank you," said the Tang Monk.

> "You're welcome," said the turtle. "Please don't forget to ask Buddha about me."

  The turtle disappeared under the water. The Tang Monk climbed onto the horse and the group continued on the road.

## ⑧

  As usual, Bajie soon started complaining.

> "I'm tired of walking already. I wish we could ride that turtle the whole way to the west."

> "Stop complaining," said Wukong. "Be happy that the road is flat here."

  They walked for another couple of hours. The road started to go up a mountain, getting steeper and steeper.

## ⑨

> "The road isn't flat anymore," the pig moaned.

  A cold wind whipped past them. Wujing shivered.

> "Look," said the Tang Monk, pointing.

  Higher up the mountain was a large monastery.

> "Maybe we can rest there," said the monk.

## ⑩

  Wukong looked at the monastery. A dark mist hung over it. The monkey shook his head.

> "That's a bad place. We're not going there."

> "It looks fine to me," said the monk.

> "I can see things that humans can't see," said Wukong. "And I see a dark mist hanging over that monastery. A demon could be in there."

## ⑪

  There was a sudden growling sound. Wukong looked around to see what had caused it. Bajie patted his stomach.

> "Sorry. I'm a bit hungry."

> "We're all tired and hungry," said the Tang Monk. "We should just go to that monastery."

> "No," said Wukong sharply. "Stay here. I will find food for us."

  He looked at the monk and warned him again.

> "Do not go to that monastery."

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十三章：问佛


## ①

  前方是一段陡峭的河岸。唐僧停下脚步，村民们纷纷躲到树后。悟空、悟净和八戒都拔出了兵器。

  一个巨大的龟壳从水中升起。

> "是一只大海龟。"八戒说。

## ②

  海龟朝悟空低下了头。

> "之前有个恶霸占了我的家和这条河，谢谢你们把他除掉了。"

  海龟又看了看村民们。

> "你们不需要造船了，我可以送行者们过河。"

## ③

> "太好了，"唐僧说。

> "我来自大唐，我知道您是谁，"海龟插话道，"您正在前往西天，向佛祖求取真经。我早就知道您早晚会过我的这条河。请爬上我的龟壳吧。"

  悟空怀疑地打量着海龟。

> "我们怎么知道可以相信你？"

## ④

> "一路上有那么多妖怪等着师父经过，"八戒补充道，"他们都想吃掉他。"

> "我保证不会伤害唐僧，"海龟说，"我想帮他到达西天。"

  一行人犹豫了一会儿，最终踏上了海龟的龟壳。海龟开始划水前行。

## ⑤

  村民们从树后走出来，朝他们挥手告别。

> "再见了，"一个女子喊道，"回来的时候请来看我们啊，"另一个人也喊道。

> "一定会的，我保证，"唐僧喊道。

  不一会儿，海龟已经离岸很远了。八戒睡着了。

## ⑥

  海龟回头望向唐僧。

> "请问，能帮我一个忙吗？"

> "当然可以，"唐僧说，"你需要我做什么？"

> "我已经做了一千多年的好佛教徒了，"海龟说，"可惜我还是只能做一只乌龟。你能帮我问问佛祖，我什么时候才能转世为人吗？"

  唐僧点了点头。

> "我会帮你问的。"

## ⑦

  几个小时后，海龟到达了河对岸。行者们踏上了陆地。

> "谢谢你，"唐僧说。

> "不客气，"海龟说，"请别忘了帮我问佛祖那件事。"

  海龟消失在水中。唐僧翻身上马，一行人继续赶路。

## ⑧

  不出所料，八戒又开始抱怨了。

> "走路太累了，真希望能骑那只海龟一路到西天。"

> "别抱怨了，"悟空说，"这段路平坦，你应该高兴才对。"

  又走了几个钟头，道路开始往山上走，越来越陡。

## ⑨

> "路不平坦了，"八戒哼哼道。

  一阵冷风吹过他们，悟净打了个寒颤。

> "看，"唐僧指着前方说。

  高处有一座大寺院。

> "也许我们可以在那里歇一歇，"唐僧说。

## ⑩

  悟空看着那座寺院，上面笼罩着一团黑雾。猴子摇了摇头。

> "那是个不好的地方，我们不能去。"

> "我看没什么问题啊，"唐僧说。

> "我能看到凡人间看不到的东西，"悟空说，"我看到那座寺院上空飘着一团黑雾，里面可能有妖怪。"

## ⑪

  突然传来一声咕噜声。悟空四下张望，想看看是什么发出的声音。八戒拍了拍肚子。

> "不好意思，我有点饿了。"

> "我们又累又饿，"唐僧说，"我们还是去那座寺院吧。"

> "不行，"悟空断然说道，"你们待在这里，我去给大家找吃的。"

  他看着唐僧，再次警告道。

> "千万不要去那座寺院。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Four: Magnificent Silk Vests

## ①

> "I hope that monkey finds a lot of food," said Bajie. "I'm hungry."

  The Tang Monk shivered and hugged himself.

> "I'm so cold," he said.

  He looked up at the monastery again and then back at his companions.

> "Do you two believe there are demons up there?"

  Wujing stroked his chin.

> "I'm not sure. Wukong believed it though."

## ②

> "Kai," Bajie snorted. "Wukong is too careful. He's always worried that we'll bump into a demon."

  His stomach grumbled.

> "Oh, I'm starving."

  Wujing looked at the monastery again.

> "That place looks perfectly safe to me."

## ③

  Bajie nodded.

> "It looks warm too. Maybe the monks there will take us in."

> "It would be nice to get out of this cold," said the Tang Monk.

> "That settles it," said the pig. "Who cares what that monkey thinks? What does he know? Let's go up there, get warm, and eat some food."

  The Tang Monk climbed back onto the horse and the three travelers headed toward the monastery.

## ④

  When they got there, no people were around.

> "This place is deserted," said Wujing.

  Bajie knocked on the door but no one answered.

> "Hello!" the pig called. "Is anybody in there?"

  Again, there was no answer.

## ⑤

  Bajie looked at his companions.

> "Maybe the monks didn't hear me."

  His eyes lit up.

> "Maybe they're all in the kitchen cooking food. With noodles boiling and vegetables sizzling, a kitchen can be quite noisy."

  The pig's stomach growled again.

> "I'll go in and find out."

  He opened the door and stepped inside. The monastery was dark and silent.

## ⑥

> "I don't hear anyone cooking," Bajie said to himself. "Maybe there isn't anyone here."

  He walked down a long hallway past several dark rooms. He called again. Then he saw a room that was lit up. He went inside.

  Bright sunlight was streaming through a window and onto a table. On the table were three silk vests.

## ⑦

> "Those vests look magnificent," said the pig.

  He shivered.

> "They also look warm."

  He looked around. He grabbed the vests and hurried back outside.

> "Nobody's in there," he said to the monk and Wujing. "When I found these vests."

  Wujing grabbed a vest.

> "Great. I'm freezing."

## ⑧

  Bajie handed a vest to the Tang Monk.

> "Here you go, Master."

  The monk frowned.

> "I won't wear that. You stole it."

> "I didn't steal it," said Bajie. "I borrowed it."

  The monk glared at him.

> "You must return those vests right away."

## ⑨

> "We can return the vests before we leave," offered Wujing. "Right, Bajie."

> "Oh, I'm sure," said the pig. "We can do that."

> "You two are terrible," said the Tang Monk. "We'll never get the true scriptures from Buddha if you steal."

## ⑩

  Bajie shrugged.

> "Master, you don't have to wear one of the vests. But I'm cold."

  He put his arm through the armhole. Wujing did the same. Bajie put his other arm through. Wujing began buttoning his vest.

  Suddenly they both cried out.

> "It's tight," cried Bajie. "I can't breathe."

> "I can't breathe," cried Wujing.

  They both fell to the ground trying desperately to take the vests off.

## ⑪

> "This vest won't come off," cried the pig.

> "Who stole my vests?" a voice shouted.

  A demon with one big horn rushed over. He looked at Bajie and Wujing and then turned to the Tang Monk.

> "Who are you?" demanded the demon.

## ⑫

> "I'm from the Tang Empire," said the monk, shaking with fear. "I'm traveling to the west for..."

  The demon clapped his hands together.

> "You're the Tang Monk!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十四章：华美丝袍


## ①

> "希望那只猴子能找到很多吃的，"八戒说，"我都饿了。"

  唐僧打了个寒战，抱紧了自己。

> "我好冷啊，"他说。

  他又抬头看了看山上的寺院，然后把目光转回同伴身上。

> "你们俩真的觉得上面有妖怪吗？"

  悟净摸了摸下巴。

> "不好说，不过悟空是这么认为的。"

## ②

> "切，"八戒哼了一声，"悟空也太小心了，他总是担心我们会碰到妖怪。"

  他的肚子咕噜噜叫了起来。

> "哎呀，我快饿扁了。"

  悟净又看了看那座寺院。

> "我看那里挺安全的。"

## ③

  八戒点了点头。

> "看着也挺暖和的，说不定那里的僧人会收留我们。"

> "能离开这冰天雪地就好了，"唐僧说。

> "就这么定了，"八戒说，"管那只猴子怎么想呢？他懂什么？咱们上去暖和暖和，吃点东西。"

  唐僧翻上马背，三个行者朝寺院走去。

## ④

  到了那里才发现，一个人也没有。

> "这地方空荡荡的，"悟净说。

  八戒敲了敲门，没人回应。

> "有人吗？"八戒喊道，"里面有人吗？"

  还是没有回答。

## ⑤

  八戒看了看同伴们。

> "可能是和尚们没听见。"

  他眼睛一亮。

> "说不定他们都在厨房做饭呢。面条在锅里滚着，蔬菜在锅里滋滋响，厨房里应该很热闹。"

  八戒的肚子又咕噜噜叫了。

> "我进去看看。"

  他推开门走了进去。寺院里又黑又安静。

## ⑥

> "我好像没听到有人在做饭，"八戒自言自语道，"也许这里根本没人。"

  他沿着一条长廊走着，经过了好几间黑漆漆的房间。他又喊了一声，然后看到一间亮着灯的房间。他走了进去。

  明亮的阳光透过窗户照在一张桌子上。桌子上放着三件丝绸背心。

## ⑦

> "这些背心看起来真漂亮，"八戒说。

  他冷得发抖。

> "看起来也很暖和。"

  他四下看了看，抓起背心就跑出门外。

> "里面没有人，"他对唐僧和悟净说，"我找到了这些背心。"

  悟净抓起一件背心。

> "太好了，我快冻僵了。"

## ⑧

  八戒递给唐僧一件背心。

> "师父，给您。"

  唐僧皱了皱眉头。

> "我不穿，这是你偷来的。"

> "我没有偷，"八戒说，"我只是借来用用。"

  唐僧瞪着他。

> "你必须马上把背心还回去。"

## ⑨

> "我们走之前再还回去就是了，"悟净提议道，"对吧，八戒？"

> "当然啦，"八戒说，"我们肯定会还的。"

> "你们俩太不像话了，"唐僧说，"如果偷东西，我们永远也取不到佛祖的真经。"

## ⑩

  八戒耸了耸肩。

> "师父，您可以不穿背心，可是我好冷啊。"

  他把胳膊伸进了袖口。悟净也照做了。八戒把另一只胳膊也伸了进去。悟净开始扣背心的扣子。

  突然两个人都叫了起来。

> "好紧啊，"八戒叫道，"我喘不过气了。"

> "我也透不过气了，"悟净也叫道。

  两个人都倒在地上，拼命想脱掉背心。

## ⑪

> "这件背心脱不下来了，"八戒叫道。

> "谁偷了我的背心？"一个声音大吼道。

  一个长着一根大角的妖怪冲了过来。他看了看八戒和悟净，然后转向唐僧。

> "你们是什么人？"妖怪质问道。

## ⑫

> "我来自大唐，"唐僧浑身发抖说，"我前往西天去……"

  妖怪拍了一下手。

> "你就是唐僧！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Five: The Metal Ring

## ①

  The demon tied up the Tang Monk in a dark room. Then the demon dragged in Bajie and Wujing. They were still trapped in the vests. The demons dumped them in a corner and approached the monk.

> "I've been hoping you would pass my mountain," the demon said with an evil smile.

> "Please let us go," said the Tang Monk. "We're trying to reach the Western Paradise."

## ②

> "I know where you're going," said the demon. "I also know that I'll live forever if I eat you."

> "Who are you?" demanded Wujing from the corner.

  The demon turned to face him.

> "I am One-Horned Buffalo."

> "Not friendly at all," said Bajie. "He's very powerful. And when he learns that you kidnapped us, he'll destroy your entire mountain."

## ③

  One-Horned Buffalo scrunched up his face.

> "Who is your friend?"

> "His name is Sun Wukong," said Bajie.

  The demon's smirk disappeared.

> "Is he the Sun Wukong who caused trouble in Heaven?"

  The demon sounded nervous.

## ④

> "Yes, he is," said Wujing.

> "Heaven's entire army couldn't defeat him," Bajie added. "Even the Jade Emperor is afraid of him."

  One-Horned Buffalo stood taller.

> "Well, I'm not afraid of him."

## ⑤

  The demon walked out of the room. Once he was away from the others, though, he grew worried again.

> "That monkey is powerful," he said to himself. "I'm going to need my special weapon to defeat him."

  He lifted his sleeve, revealing a metal ring around his arm.

## ⑥

  Carrying food, Wukong returned to where he left his friends. When he didn't see them, he looked up toward the monastery. The building was gone. In its place was a dark cave.

  Wukong shook his head.

> "That monastery was an illusion. A demon must have made it to trick people."

  He stamped his foot.

> "They never believe me when I warn them about demons."

  He put down the food and rushed to the cave.

## ⑦

> "Open up!" shouted the monkey. "If you don't, I'll turn this entire mountain into a pile of rubble!"

  The door flung open, and One-Horned Buffalo stepped out.

> "Why are you yelling?" demanded the demon. "It's rude."

> "Release my friends," yelled Wukong.

> "No." One-Horned Buffalo folded his arms. "I'm not going to release your friends. They're criminals. They stole my valuable silk vests."

## ⑧

> "That's a lie," said Wukong. "The Tang Monk is a good and honest man. He would never steal. I can't believe you would even suggest it."

> "Oh." The monkey scratched his head. "Well, then I believe you. But that doesn't matter."

## ⑨

  Wukong pulled out his iron bar and swung it at the demon. One-Horned Buffalo dodged the bar, which smashed into the mountainside. Rocks exploded and tumbled down the mountain slope.

  The demon glared at Wukong.

> "I remember you. The Jade Emperor may fear you, but I don't."

## ⑩

  He rushed at Wukong and the monkey swung his iron bar again. The demon blocked it with his arm.

> "Man, ow," cried One-Horned Buffalo, rubbing his arm.

  He fell to his knees and turned his back to the monkey.

## ⑪

> "My iron bar is not an ordinary weapon," said Wukong. "It's extremely heavy."

  He noticed the demon reaching up his sleeve.

> "What are you doing?"

  One-Horned Buffalo spun around, holding up the metal ring.

## ⑫

  Instantly, Wukong felt himself being pulled toward the ring. Using all of his strength, the monkey reached into the air. But the bar was wrenched from his hands. It flew into the metal ring and vanished.

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十五章：金钢琢


## ①

  妖怪把唐僧绑在一间暗室里，然后拖进了八戒和悟净——他们还被困在丝织背心里呢。妖怪把他们扔在角落里，然后走向唐僧。

> "我一直盼着你们经过我的山，"妖怪邪恶地笑着说。

> "请放了我们吧，"唐僧说，"我们是要去西天的。"

## ②

> "我知道你们要去哪儿，"妖怪说，"我也知道如果吃了你，我就能长生不老。"

> "你是什么人？"悟净在角落里质问道。

  妖怪转身面向他。

> "我是独角牛魔王。"

> "这家伙一点不友善，"八戒说，"他可是很厉害的。等他知道了你绑架了我们，他一定会把整座山都踏平。"

## ③

  独角牛魔王皱了皱眉头。

> "你的朋友是谁？"

> "他叫孙悟空，"八戒说。

  妖怪的得意笑容消失了。

> "他就是那个在天宫闹过事的孙悟空？"

  妖怪的语气变得有些紧张了。

## ④

> "没错，就是他，"悟净说。

> "天宫的千军万马都打不过他，"八戒补充道，"连玉皇大帝都怕他。"

  独角牛魔王挺直了腰杆。

> "哼，我才不怕他呢。"

## ⑤

  妖怪走出了房间。可一离开其他人，他的担忧又重新浮现。

> "那只猴子确实厉害，"他自言自语道，"我非得用上我的特殊兵器才能打败他。"

  他抬起袖子，露出了手臂上的一个金属圈。

## ⑥

  悟空带着食物回到他放下同伴的地方。当他发现同伴不见了，便抬头朝寺院的方向望去。那栋建筑已经不见了，取而代之的是一座黑暗的山洞。

  悟空摇了摇头。

> "那座寺院是个幻象，一定是妖怪变出来的，用来骗人。"

  他跺了跺脚。

> "每次我提醒他们有妖怪，他们偏偏不信。"

  他放下食物，朝山洞冲去。

## ⑦

> "开门！"猴子大喊道，"再不开门，我就把整座山夷为平地！"

  门猛地开了，独角牛魔王走了出来。

> "你嚷嚷什么？"妖怪质问道，"太没礼貌了。"

> "放出我的朋友！"悟空大喊。

> "不行。"独角牛魔王双手交叉在胸前，"我不会放你的朋友的。他们是罪犯，偷了我珍贵的丝绸背心。"

## ⑧

> "胡说八道，"悟空说，"唐僧是个善良正直的人，他绝不会偷东西，我不相信你会这么认为。"

> "哦。"猴子挠了挠头，"好吧，我相信你。但这也不重要了。"

## ⑨

  悟空掏出金箍棒朝妖怪挥去。独角牛魔王闪身一躲，金箍棒重重地砸进了山壁里，石块爆炸般向山坡上翻滚而去。

  妖怪瞪着悟空。

> "我记得你。玉皇大帝可能怕你，但我不怕。"

## ⑩

  他朝悟空扑去，猴子再次挥出金箍棒。妖怪用胳膊挡住了金箍棒。

> "哎哟，"独角牛魔王捂着胳膊叫了一声。

  他跪倒在地，背对着猴子。

## ⑪

> "我的金箍棒可不是普通的兵器，"悟空说，"它重极了。"

  他注意到妖怪把手伸进了袖子里。

> "你在干什么？"

  独角牛魔王猛地转过身来，举起了那个金属圈。

## ⑫

  刹那间，悟空感觉自己正被金属圈吸过去。猴子用尽全身力气挣扎着，手臂向空中乱抓。但金箍棒还是脱手而去，飞进了金属圈里，消失不见。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Six: Help from Heaven

## ①

  One-Horned Buffalo went back into his cave and slammed the door shut.

> "He stole my iron bar," cried Wukong. "What am I going to do?"

  He thought for a moment.

> "That demon said he remembered me. He also mentioned the Jade Emperor. Maybe that demon escaped from Heaven."

## ②

  The monkey shot into the sky and soon arrived at the Southern Gate of Heaven. He told the guard everything that had happened.

  The guard sent a messenger to see if any spirits were missing from Heaven. The messenger returned quickly with a warrior. The warrior held a large sword.

## ③

> "The Emperor sent me," said the warrior. "Nobody is missing from Heaven. But I will arrest One-Horned Buffalo for you."

  Wukong returned to earth with the warrior. The warrior banged on the cave door.

> "Open up, One-Horned Buffalo!"

## ④

  The demon came outside and eyed the warrior.

> "What do you want?"

  The warrior puffed out his chest.

> "I'm here to arrest you."

  One-Horned Buffalo sneered.

> "Go away."

> "How dare you tell me to go away?" said the warrior. "The Jade Emperor sent me." He pointed his sword at the demon. "If you don't come with me, I'll have you."

## ⑤

  One-Horned Buffalo held up the metal ring and *whoosh* -- the warrior's sword flew into it.

  The warrior's face fell as he looked at his empty hand. The demon laughed and went back into the cave.

## ⑥

> "That metal ring is powerful," said the warrior to Wukong. "We need more help."

  They returned to Heaven and bowed before the Jade Emperor.

> "I'm sorry, Your Majesty," said the warrior. "But the demon stole my sword. I need more help."

  The Jade Emperor turned to his general.

> "Send the Fire God to earth with us, too."

## ⑦

  The Fire God joined Wukong and the warrior. The god held a large, flaming spear.

> "I'll arrest the demon for you," said the god.

  The three of them went down to earth and landed on the mountain. The Fire God stood in front of the cave door. He held up his fire spear and shouted:

> "Come out, One-Horned Buffalo. You are under arrest."

## ⑧

  The cave door opened and the demon stepped outside.

> "Who are you?"

> "I'm the Fire God, sent by the Jade Emperor," said the god.

  One-Horned Buffalo scoffed.

> "I'm not afraid of you."

  The Fire God threw the flaming spear at the demon. But once again the demon held up the metal ring, and the spear was gone. The demon returned to his cave.

## ⑨

  Wukong shook his head.

> "This is bad."

  The three of them returned to Heaven and bowed before the Jade Emperor.

> "Your Majesty," said the Fire God. "One-Horned Buffalo is very powerful. I wasn't able to arrest him. We need more help."

  The Jade Emperor sighed and turned to his general.

> "Send the Thunder God within this time."

## ⑩

  Back down on earth, Wukong watched as the Thunder God approached the cave door.

> "Be careful," warned the warrior.

> "Yes," said the Fire God. "The demon's metal ring is very dangerous."

> "Ha ha ha," the Thunder God laughed. "Don't worry about me."

## ⑪

  He turned to the cave door and boomed:

> "One-Horned Buffalo, you are under arrest."

  The cave door opened and One-Horned Buffalo stepped outside.

  The Thunder God instantly hurled his thunderbolts at the demon. One-Horned Buffalo held up the metal ring and *whoosh* -- the thunderbolts were gone.

## ⑫

  The demon looked around at everyone and laughed.

> "Thank you for all the weapons."

  He went back into his cave and slammed the door shut again.

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十六章：天兵相助


## ①

  独角牛魔王回到洞里，用力关上了门。

> "他偷走了我的金箍棒，"悟空哭喊道，"我该怎么办？"

  他想了一会儿。

> "那个妖怪说他记得我，还提到了玉皇大帝。也许那个妖怪是从天上逃下来的。"

## ②

  猴子飞上了天空，很快就到了南天门。他把发生的一切告诉了守卫。

  守卫派了一名使者去查看天上有没有少什么灵官。使者很快带着一名天将回来了。天将手中握着一把大剑。

## ③

> "是玉帝派我来的，"天将说，"天上没有缺少什么灵官，不过我愿意帮你们去捉独角牛魔王。"

  悟空和天将回到了地上。天将用力拍打洞门。

> "开门，独角牛魔王！"

## ④

  妖怪走了出来，打量了一番天将。

> "你们想干什么？"

  天将挺起胸膛。

> "我来捉拿你。"

  独角牛魔王冷笑了一声。

> "滚吧。"

> "竟敢叫我滚？"天将说，"是玉皇大帝派我来的。"他用剑指着妖怪，"你不跟我走的话，我可就不客气了。"

## ⑤

  独角牛魔王举起金属圈，"嗖"的一声，天将的剑飞进了圈里。

  天将看着自己空空的手，面如土色。妖怪大笑着走回洞中。

## ⑥

> "那个金属圈法力高强，"天将对悟空说，"我们需要更多的帮手。"

  他们回到了天庭，跪拜在玉帝面前。

> "陛下，臣惭愧，"天将说，"妖怪偷走了臣的剑，臣需要更多的帮手。"

  玉帝转身对将军下令。

> "派火神下凡帮忙。"

## ⑦

  火神加入了悟空和天将的队伍。火神手中握着一柄烈焰长矛。

> "我去帮你们捉拿妖怪，"火神说。

  三人下到凡间，落在山上。火神站在洞门前，举起火矛大喊道。

> "独角牛魔王，滚出来！你被捕了。"

## ⑧

  洞门开了，妖怪走了出来。

> "你是什么人？"

> "我是玉皇大帝派来的火神，"火神说。

  独角牛魔王轻蔑地哼了一声。

> "我才不怕你呢。"

  火神将烈焰长矛朝妖怪掷去。但妖怪又一次举起金属圈，长矛瞬间消失了。妖怪回到了洞里。

## ⑨

  悟空摇了摇头。

> "这可不妙。"

  三人又回到了天庭，跪拜在玉帝面前。

> "陛下，"火神说，"独角牛魔王太厉害了，臣没能捉拿他，需要更多帮手。"

  玉帝叹了叹气，对将军说。

> "这次派雷神去吧。"

## ⑩

  又回到了凡间，悟空看着雷神走向洞门。

> "小心点，"天将提醒道。

> "是啊，"火神也说，"那个妖怪的金属圈很危险。"

> "哈哈哈，"雷神大笑着，"不用担心我。"

## ⑪

  他转过来对着洞门大喊道。

> "独角牛魔王，你被捕了！"

  洞门开了，独角牛魔王走了出来。

  雷神立刻将雷电朝妖怪掷去。独角牛魔王举起金属圈，"嗖"的一声，雷电消失了。

## ⑫

  妖怪看着众人，哈哈大笑。

> "谢谢你们送的所有兵器。"

  他又走回洞里，再次重重关上了门。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Seven: The Master of Faith

## ①

> "What are we going to do now?" cried Wukong. "One-Horned Buffalo stole all our weapons."

  The warrior rubbed his chin. He looked very serious.

> "We can't go back to the Jade Emperor. He'll be angry if he finds out we couldn't arrest the demon."

## ②

> "You're right," said the Fire God. "We need a different plan. It's getting dark out, almost nighttime. Maybe one of us can sneak into the cave and steal that metal ring."

## ③

  The Thunder God smiled.

> "I know who's perfect for that job."

  The others all looked at the god.

> "One of us is a master thief," the Thunder God continued. "He once stole all the peaches from the Royal Peach Garden."

  Now everyone looked at Wukong.

## ④

  The monkey pretended to laugh.

> "Ha ha ha. Yes, it's true. I used to steal things, but I know now that stealing is wrong. However, I will steal that metal ring because I need to save the Tang Monk. You all wait here."

## ⑤

  The monkey turned himself into a tiny bug and flew into the cave. He went down a long dark tunnel followed by another tunnel. Then he heard One-Horned Buffalo.

  Wukong flew toward the voice. The demon was sitting on the edge of a bed, talking to himself. The metal ring was still on his arm.

## ⑥

> "Ah, it's time for bed," said the demon with a yawn. "I hope I can eat the Tang Monk tomorrow. I couldn't eat him today because of that annoying monkey and his friends from Heaven."

  The demon lay down and was soon asleep.

## ⑦

  Wukong flew over and landed on the demon's arm.

> "I'll bite his arm," thought the monkey. "He'll get itchy and have to take off the metal ring."

  Wukong bit the demon's arm again and again.

  The demon rolled over and mumbled in his sleep. He scratched his arm.

  Wukong bit him some more. The demon scratched and scratched, but he didn't take off the metal ring.

## ⑧

> "This isn't working," thought Wukong.

  He was about to leave the room when he spotted something in the corner. He gasped. It was the weapons!

  Quietly, he changed back into himself. He made his iron bar small and put it in his ear. Then he grabbed the flaming spear, the thunderbolt, and the sword.

## ⑨

  Outside the cave, the others were waiting.

  The warrior made a fist.

> "I hope Wukong steals that metal ring. I'm so angry at that demon."

> "Shh," said the Fire God. "I can't believe he stole my fire spear."

## ⑩

  The Thunder God held up a hand.

> "The door is opening."

  The three of them held their breath. When they saw Wukong peek out, they were relieved.

> "Did you get the ring?" asked the Thunder God.

> "No, but look."

  The monkey held up the weapons.

## ⑪

> "Well done, Wukong," said the Fire God.

  The Thunder God cracked the monkey on the back.

> "Thank you, Wukong."

  The warrior held up his sword.

> "We're all armed. We can easily defeat the demon now."

> "You're right," said Wukong. He looked around. "Is everyone ready?"

> "Yes," said the warrior.

> "Yes," said the Fire God.

> "Yes," said the Thunder God.

## ⑫

  The monkey banged on the cave door.

> "Wake up, One-Horned Buffalo! Get out here right now or we'll destroy your entire mountain."

  The demon stepped outside yawning. Then he saw the weapons.

> "How dare you steal from me!"

  He held up the metal ring. Before anyone could react, the weapons were sucked into it, once again.

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十七章：偷天换日


## ①

> "我们现在怎么办？"悟空叫道，"独角牛魔王偷走了我们所有的兵器。"

  天将摸着下巴，表情十分严肃。

> "我们不能回去见玉帝了。让他知道我们没能捉住妖怪，他定会发怒。"

## ②

> "说得对，"火神说，"我们需要换个计划。天色渐渐暗下来了，马上就是晚上了。也许我们中间有哪个人能溜进山洞，把那个金属圈偷出来。"

## ③

  雷神微微一笑。

> "我知道谁最适合干这个差事。"

  大家都看向了雷神。

> "我们中间有一个神偷，"雷神继续说，"他曾把蟠桃园里的仙桃全都偷了。"

  众人齐刷刷地看向悟空。

## ④

  猴子装出一副大笑的样子。

> "哈哈哈，没错，我从前确实偷过东西，不过现在我知道偷东西是不对的。不过，为了救唐僧，我愿意去偷那个金属圈。你们都在这里等着。"

## ⑤

  猴子变成了一只小虫子，飞进了山洞。他穿过一条漫长的黑暗地道，接着又穿过另一条。然后他听到了独角牛魔王的声音。

  悟空朝声音的方向飞去。妖怪正坐在床边自言自语，金属圈仍然戴在他胳膊上。

## ⑥

> "啊，该睡觉了，"妖怪打着哈欠说，"希望明天能吃上唐僧肉。今天没吃成，都是那只讨厌的猴子和他那帮天庭的朋友碍事。"

  妖怪躺下来，很快就睡着了。

## ⑦

  悟空飞过去落在妖怪的胳膊上。

> "我就咬他的胳膊，"猴子心想，"他一定会觉得痒，不得不把金属圈取下来。"

  悟空咬了咬妖怪的胳膊，一口又一口。

  妖怪翻了个身，在睡梦中嘟囔着。他抓了抓胳膊。

  悟空又咬了几口。妖怪挠了又挠，可就是没有取下那个金属圈。

## ⑧

> "这招不管用，"悟空心想。

  他正准备离开房间，突然看到了角落里有什么东西。他倒吸一口凉气，是那些兵器！

  他悄悄地变回了自己原来的模样。把金箍棒变小放进耳朵里，然后一把抓起烈焰长矛、雷电之剑和宝剑。

## ⑨

  洞外，其他人在等着。

  天将握紧了拳头。

> "希望悟空能把那个金属圈偷出来，我对那个妖怪真是气极了。"

> "嘘，"火神说，"真不敢相信他偷走了我的火矛。"

## ⑩

  雷神举起一只手。

> "门开了。"

  三人都屏住了呼吸，看见悟空探出头来，都松了口气。

> "你拿到金属圈了吗？"雷神问。

> "没有，不过你们看。"

  猴子举起了那些兵器。

## ⑪

> "干得好，悟空，"火神说。

  雷神拍了一下猴子的后背。

> "谢谢你啊，悟空。"

  天将举起了自己的宝剑。

> "我们都有兵器了，现在可以轻松打败那个妖怪了。"

> "没错，"悟空说。他环顾四周，"大家都准备好了吗？"

> "准备好了，"天将说。

> "准备好了，"火神说。

> "准备好了，"雷神说。

## ⑫

  猴子用力敲打着洞门。

> "独角牛魔王，快滚出来！再不出来我们就毁了整座山。"

  妖怪打着哈欠走了出来。然后他看到了那些兵器。

> "竟敢偷我的东西！"

  他举起金属圈。大家还没来得及做出反应，所有的兵器再一次被吸进了圈里。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Eight: The Woman in the Crowd

## ①

  Wukong stood at the cave door, shocked.

> "I don't believe it. One-Horned Buffalo stole our weapons again!"

> "What will we do now?" asked the Fire God.

> "This demon's powers are stronger than any I've seen before," said Wukong. "I know one person who can definitely defeat him. Buddha. I'll be back soon."

## ②

  The monkey leaped onto a cloud and soared toward the west. He arrived at the Thunder Clap Monastery. A guard at the gate stopped him.

> "I need to ask Buddha for help," Wukong told the guard. "It's about the Tang Monk's journey."

  The guard waved the monkey through.

## ③

  Wukong entered the monastery and bowed before Buddha.

> "Blessed Buddha," said the monkey. "I need..."

  Buddha held up a hand.

> "I know why you're here, Wukong. I also know who the demon is. You must go to Laozi for help."

> "Oh, okay," said the monkey, a bit surprised. "Thank you."

## ④

  Wukong flew toward Heaven.

> "Laozi doesn't like me much," thought the monkey. "He won't be happy to see me."

  When Wukong arrived at Laozi's house, the sage frowned.

> "What do you want, Wukong?" asked Laozi.

> "Buddha told me to come here," said Wukong. "The Tang Monk was captured by a demon called One-Horned Buffalo."

## ⑤

> "Oh dear," said Laozi.

> "Do you know him?" asked the monkey.

  Laozi nodded.

> "He's my green buffalo. I didn't realize he escaped."

> "Well, he did," said Wukong, getting annoyed. "And he's planning to eat the Tang Monk. Your buffalo also has a metal ring. Every time we try to fight him, the ring sucks in our weapons."

## ⑥

  Laozi held up his hands.

> "Okay, okay. I can capture the buffalo. Don't worry."

  The sage went into another room. When he came back, he was holding a fan.

> "Let's go."

## ⑦

  Wukong and Laozi returned to the mountain.

> "Buffalo!" shouted Laozi. "Get out here right now."

  The door flew open, and One-Horned Buffalo stepped outside. His face fell when he saw Laozi.

  Laozi raised the fan and brought it down fast. A fierce wind nearly knocked over One-Horned Buffalo.

## ⑧

  The demon pulled off the metal ring and flung it at Laozi. The sage caught it and brought the fan down once more.

  The wind knocked over the demon, and he turned into a large green buffalo. The buffalo stood up and snorted.

  Laozi tucked the fan and the ring into his robe. Then he climbed onto the buffalo and rode up into the sky.

## ⑨

  Wukong went into the cave, and the warrior and two gods followed. They soon found their weapons.

> "The gods and I will return to Heaven now," said the warrior. "Good luck with your journey, Wukong."

> "Thank you," said the monkey.

## ⑩

  Wukong found his companions deep in the cave.

> "What took you so long?" cried Bajie.

> "I was busy fighting demons," said Wukong, untying the Tang Monk.

> "Thank you, Wukong," said the monk.

> "You're welcome," said the monkey. "But next time I tell you to stay away from a place, please listen."

## ⑪

  A few weeks later, the travelers arrived at a busy city. The streets were filled with people selling vegetables, spices, and other goods. An old woman was stirring a large pot of soup. Other food sizzled over fires.

  Bajie breathed deep.

> "Ah! That smells wonderful!"

## ⑫

  Suddenly a young woman rushed out of the crowd.

> "The Tang Monk!" she cried.

  She threw her arms around the monk. A fierce wind swirled, and a second later, they were both gone.

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十八章：金兜山


## ①

  悟空站在洞门口，震惊不已。

> "真不敢相信，独角牛魔王又偷走了我们的兵器！"

> "我们现在怎么办？"火神问道。

> "这个妖怪的法力比我见过的任何妖怪都要强，"悟空说，"我知道有一个人一定能打败他——佛祖。我很快就回来。"

## ②

  猴子翻上云头，向西飞去。他赶到了雷音寺。门口的守卫拦住了他。

> "我需要请佛祖帮忙，"悟空对守卫说，"是关于唐僧取经的事。"

  守卫挥了挥手，放猴子进去了。

## ③

  悟空走进寺内，向佛祖行礼。

> "佛祖在上，"猴子说，"我需要……"

  佛祖举起一只手。

> "悟空，我知道你为什么来。我也知道那个妖怪是谁。你必须去找老君求助。"

> "哦，好的，"猴子有些吃惊，"谢谢佛祖。"

## ④

  悟空朝天上飞去。

> "老君本来就不喜欢我，"猴子想，"他看到我肯定不会高兴。"

  悟空到了老君的住处，老者皱起了眉头。

> "悟空，你有什么事？"老君问。

> "佛祖让我来找您的，"悟空说，"唐僧被一个叫独角牛魔王的妖怪抓走了。"

## ⑤

> "哎呀，"老君叹了口气。

> "您认识他吗？"猴子问。

  老君点了点头。

> "他是我的青牛精，没想到他逃跑了。"

> "他确实跑了，"悟空有些恼火，"而且他打算吃掉唐僧。您的青牛精手上还有一个金属圈，每次我们跟他打，那个圈就把我们的兵器吸走。"

## ⑥

  老君举起双手。

> "好了好了，我去收服那头牛。别担心。"

  老者走进另一个房间，出来的时候手里拿着一把扇子。

> "我们走吧。"

## ⑦

  悟空和老君回到了那座山。

> "孽畜！"老君大喊道，"快给我滚出来。"

  门猛地开了，独角牛魔王走了出来。当他看到老君时，脸色大变。

  老君举起扇子用力一扇，一阵狂风险些把独角牛魔王吹翻。

## ⑧

  妖怪扯下金属圈朝老君扔去。老者接住圈子后又扇了一扇子。

  狂风把妖怪吹倒在地，他现出了原形——一头巨大的青牛。青牛站起来，打了个响鼻。

  老君把扇子和金属圈收进袍子里，骑上青牛飞天而去。

## ⑨

  悟空走进洞里，天将和两位天神跟在后面。他们很快就找到了自己的兵器。

> "我和天神们现在就回天庭了，"天将说，"悟空，祝你取经一路顺利。"

> "谢谢你，"猴子说。

## ⑩

  悟空在洞深处找到了他的同伴们。

> "你怎么这么久才来？"八戒叫道。

> "我一直在收拾妖怪呢，"悟空一边给唐僧松绑一边说。

> "谢谢你，悟空，"唐僧说。

> "不客气，"猴子说，"不过下次我让你们离某个地方远一点的时候，请一定听我的。"

## ⑪

  几个星期后，一行人到了一座热闹的城市。街上挤满了卖蔬菜、香料和各种货物的人。一位老太太正在搅动一大锅汤。其他食物也在火上滋滋作响。

  八戒深吸了一口气。

> "啊，真香啊！"

## ⑫

  突然一个年轻女子从人群中冲了出来。

> "唐僧！"她哭喊道。

  她一把抱住了唐僧。一阵狂风卷起，眨眼之间，他们两人都不见了踪影。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Sixty-Nine: The Stabbing Pain

## ①

  That woman was a demon! cried Wukong, and she kidnapped the Tang monk! He leaped into the air, and Bajie and Wujing followed.

## ②

  In the distance, the monkey saw dark clouds speeding toward a mountain.

> "That must be her," said Wukong.

> "Quickly!" said Wujing. "We must catch her!"

## ③

  They raced after the cloud, which disappeared when it reached the mountain. They soon arrived and found a cave with its door closed. Wukong pounded on the cave door.

> "Open up!" he yelled.

## ④

  The door flew open, and the woman came out.

> "Who are you?" demanded the woman. "Why are you pounding on my door?"

> "Release our master!" shouted Wukong, ignoring her questions.

  The woman laughed.

> "Don't tell me what to do."

  The monkey attacked. The woman spun around fast, blocking his iron bar and striking back with fury.

> "You shouldn't have come here," she shouted as she fought. "Even the Jade Emperor is afraid of me."

## ⑤

  Bajie tried to hit her with his rake, but missed. The woman was now spinning faster and faster.

> "She's faster than a tornado!" cried the pig.

  Wukong leaped at the woman. Suddenly he felt a stabbing pain.

> "Ah ha ha!" cried the monkey, grabbing his head. "It hurts! It hurts!"

  He ran down the mountain. Bajie and Wujing stared after Wukong in shock. The woman went back into her cave.

## ⑥

> "What happened to Wukong?" asked the pig. "Nothing hurts him except for the tight headband spell."

> "I don't know," said Wujing, scratching his head.

## ⑦

  They went down the mountain and found the monkey crouching by a stream. He was still holding his head.

> "Are you alright?" asked Wujing.

> "That woman stabbed me in the head," moaned Wukong. "The pain is horrible."

  Bajie snorted.

> "You're always bragging about how tough you are. Now you're crying about getting stabbed in the head. Pathetic!"

  Shouted the monkey angrily.

## ⑧

  Wujing moved closer.

> "Let me see where she stabbed you."

  Wukong lowered his hands. There was no injury.

> "Ha ha ha!" Bajie laughed. "Gosh, he's fine! He just wants us to feel bad for him."

## ⑨

  The monkey glared at the pig.

> "I'm telling you, it hurts!"

  He took a deep breath.

> "The pain is going away now, though. Let's go back up there and fight her again."

## ⑩

  The three companions returned to the cave.

> "Wukong, you stand back," said Bajie, laughing. "I don't want you getting hurt again."

  Wukong clenched his teeth. The pig hit the door with his rake. Smash! The door exploded. The woman ran outside.

> "You smashed my door!" she shouted.

> "Release our master!" shouted the pig.
