  The woman spun around faster and faster.

## ⑪

  Bajie and Wujing tried to strike her with their weapons, but the woman was too fast. Wukong raised his iron bar, waiting for a good moment to strike. Suddenly Bajie cried out.

## ⑫

  He covered his nose and ran back down the mountain. The woman spun toward Wukong and Wujing, and they turned and ran back down as well. Bajie was huddled on the ground, tears streaming from his eyes.

> "It hurt so badly!"

  Wukong laughed.

> "No laughing, Bajie!" cried Bajie. "She stabbed my nose!"

> "You deserved it," said the monkey. "You didn't believe me when I got hurt."

## ⑬

> "Stop arguing," said Wujing. "We still have to save the Tang monk."

> "You're right," said Wukong. "Let's go back up there."

  A voice called out.

> "Wait."

  It was Guanyin. She was walking towards the group.

> "Beware of that scorpion spirit."

---

# 🇨🇳 第六十九章：刺骨之痛

## ①

  "那女人是个妖怪！"悟空大叫道，"她把唐僧掳走了！"

  他纵身一跃跳到空中，八戒和悟净紧随其后。

## ②

  远远地，悟空看见一团乌云正向一座山疾飞而去。

> "一定是她，"悟空说。

> "快！"悟净喊道，"我们得追上她！"

## ③

  三人追着那团云，云到了山前便消失了。他们很快赶到山前，发现了一个洞穴，洞门紧闭。悟空用力捶打洞门。

> "开门！"他大喊道。

## ④

  门猛地打开，那女人走了出来。

> "你们是谁？"那女人厉声问道，"为什么砸我的门？"

> "放了我们师父！"悟空不理会她的问题，大声喝道。

  那女人哈哈大笑。

> "轮不到你来命令我。"

  猴子挥棒攻击。那女人迅速转身，挡开铁棒反打回来，怒不可遏。

> "你们不该来这里！"她一边打一边喊。"就连玉帝都怕我！"

## ⑤

  八戒举起钉耙打她，却扑了个空。那女人旋转得越来越快。

> "她比龙卷风还快！"八戒惊叫道。

  悟空纵身扑向那女人，突然感到一阵刺骨的疼痛。

> "哈哈哈！"悟空抱着头叫道，"好疼！好疼！"

  他转身跑下了山。八戒和悟净望着悟空的背影，愣住了。那女人退回了洞中。

## ⑥

> "悟空怎么了？"八戒问道，"除了紧箍咒，没有什么能伤害他啊。"

> "我也不知道。"悟净挠了挠头说。

## ⑦

  他们下了山，发现悟空蹲在一条小溪边，双手还抱着头。

> "你没事吧？"悟净问。

> "那女人用兵器刺了我的头，"悟空痛苦地说，"太疼了，疼得厉害！"

  八戒哼了一声。

> "你老是吹嘘自己有多厉害。现在被刺了头倒哭起来了，真没用！"

  悟空怒吼了一声。

## ⑧

  悟净走近了些。

> "让我看看她刺了你哪里。"

  悟空放下双手，头上并没有任何伤口。

> "哈哈哈！"八戒大笑起来，"他好好的！只是想让我们同情他。"

## ⑨

  悟空瞪了八戒一眼。

> "我告诉你们，真的很疼！"

  他深吸了一口气。

> "不过现在疼得不那么厉害了。我们回去再跟她打一场。"

## ⑩

  三人回到了洞穴前。

> "悟空，你站远点，"八戒得意地说，"我可不想你又受伤。"

  悟空咬紧牙关。八戒用钉耙猛砸洞门，"轰"的一声，门被炸开了。那女人跑了出来。

> "你们砸了我的门！"她大喊道。

> "放了我们师父！"八戒喝道。

  那女人又飞快地旋转起来。

## ⑪

  八戒和悟净举起兵器进攻，但那女人实在太快了。悟空高举金箍棒，等待出击的好时机。突然，八戒惨叫了一声。

## ⑫

  他捂着鼻子往山下跑。那女人转身冲向悟空和悟净，两人也转身往山下逃去。八戒蜷缩在地上，眼泪从脸上流下来。

> "疼死了！"

  悟空大笑起来。

> "不许笑！"八戒哭喊道，"她刺了我的鼻子！"

> "活该，"悟空说，"谁叫你刚才不信我。"

## ⑬

> "别吵了，"悟净说，"我们还得去救唐僧呢。"

> "你说得对，"悟空说，"我们再去一次。"

  一个声音从远处传来。

> "等等。"

  是观音菩萨，她正朝他们走来。

> "当心那个蝎子精，她很危险。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy: The Star Lord

## ①

  Guanyin shook her head.

> "You cannot go back to that cave," said Guanyin.

> "But we must go back," said Wukong. "That woman kidnapped the Tang monk."

> "That woman is a scorpion spirit. She is very dangerous."

## ②

> "She sure is!" cried Bajie. "What did she stab us with, anyway?"

> "It was her stinger that stabbed you," said Guanyin.

  Wukong thought about the pain he'd felt.

> "I won't go near her."

## ③

> "Even Buddha is afraid of her," said Guanyin. "He was teaching his students one day and saw that scorpion creeping toward him. He tried to move it away, but it stung him. The pain was horrible. He told his guards to capture the scorpion, but it escaped to Earth."

## ④

  Wukong paced anxiously.

> "What are we going to do, then?"

> "We must save the Tang monk. Go to Heaven and ask the Star Lord for help," said Guanyin.

  Guanyin disappeared in a flash of light.

## ⑤

  A little while later, Wukong stood at the southern gate of Heaven.

> "Greetings, Wukong," said the guard.

> "I must speak with the Star Lord," said the monkey.

  The guard told Wukong the way to the Star Lord's palace. A few minutes later, the monkey knocked on the palace door.

## ⑥

> "Wukong," said the Star Lord. "What can I do for you?"

> "I need your help," said Wukong. "I'm traveling to the Western Paradise with the Tang monk, but he was captured by a demon. Guanyin said you can help me."

  The Star Lord looked confused.

> "I don't know why you need my help. I've heard you're quite strong. What kind of demon is it?"

## ⑦

> "It's a scorpion spirit," said the monkey.

> "Ah," said the Star Lord. "I understand now. Lead the way. We must hurry."

## ⑧

  Wukong led the Star Lord out of Heaven and down to Earth. They landed on the mountain where Bajie was still rubbing his nose.

> "The Star Lord is here to help us," said Wukong.

  The Star Lord looked at Bajie's nose.

> "I can heal that for you."

  Bajie walked over to the Star Lord, who then blew on the pig's nose. The injury healed instantly.

## ⑨

> "Thank you," said the pig, smiling.

> "I was stabbed too," said Wukong. "But the stinger didn't leave a mark on me." He grinned at Bajie. "I'm much more powerful than the pig."

  Bajie frowned.

## ⑩

> "I have special magic that I'll use to defeat the Scorpion," said the Star Lord. "You just need to get her to come outside."

  Everyone went up to the cave. Bajie and Wujing hid behind some rocks. Wukong stood in front of the cave entrance and shouted.

> "Come out, demon! Release my master!"

  Then he ran as fast as he could away from the cave.

## ⑪

  The woman rushed out of the cave, spinning wildly. Suddenly the Star Lord turned into an enormous rooster. The rooster crowed, and the sound echoed through the mountains. The woman screamed and held her hands over her ears. The rooster crowed again, and the woman disappeared in a puff of smoke. In her place was a dead scorpion.

## ⑫

  Wukong ran into the cave. He found the Tang monk sitting at a table. The monk's eyes lit up.

> "Wukong! Thank you for saving me!"

  The monkey smiled.

> "As long as I'm protecting you, no demon will ever harm you."

## ⑬

  The Tang monk shook his head.

> "That woman didn't want to harm me. She wanted to marry me."

  The monk sighed.

> "But I told her that I'm a Buddhist monk and I will never marry. My only goal is to reach the Western Paradise."

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十章：昴日星官

## ①

  观音摇了摇头。

> "你们不能再回那个洞去了，"观音说。

> "可是我们必须回去，"悟空说，"那女人掳走了唐僧。"

> "那女人是蝎子精，非常危险。"

## ②

> "她确实危险！"八戒叫道，"她到底用什么刺我们的？"

> "是她的尾刺刺了你们，"观音说。

  悟空想起那阵疼痛，心有余悸。

> "我再也不靠近她了。"

## ③

> "连佛祖都怕她，"观音说，"有一天佛祖正在讲经，看见这只蝎子悄悄向他爬来。他想把她赶走，却被她的尾刺蛰了一下。那疼痛难以忍受。他叫护法金刚把她捉住，但她却逃到了人间。"

## ④

  悟空焦急地来回踱步。

> "那我们怎么办？我们得救唐僧啊。"

> "去天上请昴日星官帮忙。"观音说。

  观音说完便在一道金光中消失了。

## ⑤

  过了一会儿，悟空来到了南天门外。

> "大圣，你好。"守卫说。

> "我要见昴日星官。"悟空说。

  守卫给悟空指了去昴日星官宫殿的路。几分钟后，悟空敲响了宫殿的门。

## ⑥

> "悟空，"昴日星官说，"你有什么事？"

> "我需要你的帮助，"悟空说，"我和唐僧正在去西天取经的路上，但他被一个妖怪抓走了。观音菩萨说你能帮我。"

  昴日星官一脸困惑。

> "我不明白你为什么需要我的帮助。听说你很厉害，是什么妖怪？"

## ⑦

> "是一只蝎子精。"悟空说。

> "噢，我明白了，"昴日星官说，"带路吧，我们得赶快。"

## ⑧

  悟空领着昴日星官离开天庭来到人间。他们降落在山上，八戒正在那里揉鼻子。

> "昴日星官来帮我们了。"悟空说。

  昴日星官看了看八戒的鼻子。

> "我来帮你治好。"

  八戒走到昴日星官面前，星官朝他的鼻子吹了一口气，伤口瞬间就愈合了。

## ⑨

> "谢谢！"八戒笑着说。

> "我也被刺了，"悟空说，"不过尾刺没在我身上留下痕迹。"他朝八戒咧嘴一笑，"我可比这猪强多了。"

  八戒皱了皱眉。

## ⑩

> "我有一套特别的法术可以降服蝎子精，"昴日星官说，"你们只需要把她引出洞来。"

  大家一起上了山。八戒和悟净躲在石头后面，悟空站在洞口大喊。

> "蝎子精！快出来见我师父！"

  然后他飞快逃离洞口。

## ⑪

  那女人冲出洞来，疯狂地旋转着。突然之间，昴日星官变成了一只巨大的公鸡。公鸡高声啼鸣，声音在山间回荡。那女人惨叫一声，双手捂住耳朵。公鸡又啼叫了一声，那女人在"砰"的一声中化作了一团青烟。原地留下一只死了的蝎子。

## ⑫

  悟空跑进洞里，发现唐僧正坐在桌旁。唐僧眼睛一亮。

> "悟空，谢谢你救我！"

  悟空笑道。

> "只要有我保护你，没有任何妖怪能伤害你。"

## ⑬

  唐僧摇了摇头。

> "那女人并非想害我，她想跟我成亲。"

  唐僧叹了口气。

> "但我告诉她我是出家人，绝不会娶亲。我唯一的目标就是到达西天取经。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-One: The Unexpected Danger

## ①

> "I'm hungry," Bajie moaned. His stomach rumbled loudly. "Can we stop walking?"

> "We'll stop for lunch soon," said the Tang monk. "The weather is nice and the road is smooth. I want to keep moving. I'm eager to reach the Western Paradise."

  Wukong laughed.

> "Master, I don't know why you're still going there. You should have married that scorpion spirit instead."

## ②

  The Tang monk frowned.

> "That's not funny, Wukong."

> "I agree with Wukong," said Bajie. "I wouldn't mind marrying her."

  Wukong raised an eyebrow.

> "I doubt she would have married you."

> "Why not?" Bajie puffed out his chest. "I'm very handsome."

  Everybody laughed, including Bajie.

## ③

  They had continued for another hour when the pig complained again.

> "My legs are tired," he said.

> "We'll stop at the next village," said the Tang monk.

  Bajie sighed.

> "I hope we reach the next village soon."

> "I know how we can get there soon," said Wukong with a laugh. The monkey smacked the horse with his stick, and the horse charged forward.

## ④

> "Wukong!" cried the Tang monk, hanging on tightly.

  When the horse finally stopped running, the monk was far ahead of his companions. A group of nasty-looking men stood in front of him.

> "Give us all your money!" said a man with an axe.

  The Tang monk shook with fear. Wukong was already running over.

## ⑤

> "Don't you dare harm my master!" shouted the monkey.

> "Oh, you!" said a man. "Who are you?"

> "My name is Sun Wukong. Give us all your money."

> "I don't have much money," said the monkey. "You'd better give yours to me."

  The man's face turned red.

## ⑥

> "I'm not going to give you money!"

> "Let's make a bet then," said Wukong. He pulled out his iron bar, which quickly grew to the height of a person. The men looked nervous. The monkey stuck the bar into the ground. "If you can pick this up, we'll give you all of our money."

## ⑦

> "Careful," said the man with an axe. "I'm sure I can pick that bar up."

> "Go ahead and try," said Wukong.

  The man put down his axe. He grasped the bar with his hands and tried to lift it.

> "It's heavier than it looks," said the man. He tried to lift the bar again. Sweat poured down his red face. But the bar didn't budge.

## ⑧

> "Now it's my turn," said Wukong. He lifted the bar over his head and twirled it around. His eyes flashed with anger. He got ready to strike the man.

> "Wukong, don't!" shouted the Tang monk.

  The man took a step back. Suddenly the bar dropped from Wukong's hands.

## ⑨

  Crying out, the monkey held his head. He fell to his knees as the Tang monk quietly recited the tight headband spell. The robbers glanced at one another and then ran away.

  When the monk stopped reciting the spell, Wukong was furious.

> "Why did you do that?" he cried. "They were going to rob you!"

## ⑩

> "You must not hurt people," commanded the monk.

> "I destroy demons all the time," said the monkey.

> "It's fine to hurt demons. But you must not hurt people," the monk said. "You're still evil, Wukong. I can't bring you to the Western Paradise. You must leave."

> "But you need me, Master!" Wukong insisted.

## ⑪

> "I refuse. Please go," said the Tang monk. "Or I'll recite the tight headband spell until your head explodes."

  Wukong could see that the monk wasn't going to change his mind. With tears in his eyes, the monkey leaped into the air and was gone.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十一章：意外之险

## ①

> "我饿了，"八戒嚷嚷着，肚子咕咕直叫，"我们能歇会儿吗？"

> "很快就停下来吃午饭，"唐僧说，"天气这么好，道路也平坦，我想继续赶路。我急着要到西天去。"

  悟空听了说：

> "师父，我真不明白你为什么还非要去西天。你当初还不如娶了那个蝎子精呢。"

## ②

  唐僧皱起眉头。

> "悟空，这一点也不好笑。"

> "我同意悟空的话，"八戒说，"我倒是很乐意娶她呢。"

  悟空挑了挑眉毛。

> "恐怕人家还未必看得上你呢。"

> "为什么？"八戒挺起胸膛，"我可英俊得很。"

  大家都笑了，八戒也跟着笑了起来。

## ③

  他们又走了一个时辰，八戒又抱怨起来。

> "我的腿好酸。"

> "我们在下一个村子歇脚。"唐僧说。

  八戒叹了口气。

> "但愿快点到下一个村子。"

> "我知道怎么才能快点到，"悟空笑着说，他拍了白龙马一巴掌，马猛然向前飞奔。

## ④

> "悟空！"唐僧惊叫着死死抓住缰绳。

  等马终于停下来时，唐僧已经远远走到了同伴们的前面。一群凶神恶煞的汉子挡在他面前。

> "把身上的钱都交出来！"一个拿斧头的人说。

  唐僧吓得浑身发抖。悟空已经飞奔过来。

## ⑤

> "你们竟敢伤害我师父！"悟空大喊道。

> "哼，你又是谁？"一个人说。

> "我叫孙悟空。把你们的钱都交出来。"

> "我没多少钱，"悟空说，"你们最好把你们的钱给我。"

  那人涨红了脸。

## ⑥

> "我才不会给你钱！"

> "那我们来打个赌，"悟空说。他掏出金箍棒，迎风一晃，变得有一人高。那些汉子面露惧色。悟空将金箍棒立在地上："如果你们谁能举起这根棒子，我们就把所有钱给你们。"

## ⑦

> "小心，"拿斧头的人说，"我肯定能举起这根棒。"

> "那就来试试吧。"悟空说。

  那人放下斧头，双手抓住金箍棒使劲往上抬。

> "比看起来重多了，"那人说，他又试着抬了一次，汗水从涨红的脸上淌下来，可金箍棒纹丝不动。

## ⑧

> "现在轮到我了，"悟空说着把金箍棒举过头顶，舞了起来，眼中闪出怒火，准备打那人。

> "悟空，住手！"唐僧大喊道。

  那人连连后退。忽然悟空手一松，金箍棒从手中掉落。

## ⑨

  他双手抱头，扑通跪倒在地——原来唐僧正在默念紧箍咒。那些强盗互相看了一眼，转身逃跑了。

  唐僧停下咒语，悟空愤怒地质问。

> "你为什么要这样做？他们可是要抢你啊！"

## ⑩

> "你绝不能伤害人。"唐僧命令道。

> "我打的都是妖怪。"悟空说。

> "打妖怪可以，但你绝不能伤害人，"唐僧说，"悟空，你还是太凶恶了。我不能带你去西天了，你必须离开。"

> "可是师父，你需要我呀！"悟空坚持道。

## ⑪

> "不行，走吧，"唐僧说，"不然我就一直念紧箍咒，念到你脑袋炸开为止。"

  悟空看出唐僧心意已决，眼中含泪，纵身一跃，消失在空中。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Two: A Surprise at the Fruit and Flower Mountain

## ①

  Wukong went straight to Mount Potalaka. The Bodhisattva Guanyin was in her garden.

> "Fala Wukong. How was the journey going?"

  Wukong threw up his hands.

> "The Tang monk is crazy."

> "Why?" asked the Bodhisattva.

> "He told me to leave," said the monkey. "He was mad because I was going to hurt some robbers."

## ②

  Guanyin frowned.

> "It's wrong to hurt people, Wukong. You know that."

> "I hurt demons all the time," said Wukong.

> "That's different," said Guanyin. "Demons are evil, and you're doing a good thing when you get rid of them. But you must not hurt people."

## ③

  The monkey sat down and put his head in his hands.

> "Dear Bodhisattva, you're right."

  He started to cry.

> "This is terrible. Now I'll never reach the Western Paradise with the Tang monk. I wanted to earn forgiveness."

> "Don't cry, Wukong," said Guanyin. "You will still help the Tang monk reach the Western Paradise. He will seek your help soon. In the meantime, you may stay here with me."

## ④

  Bajie dropped the bags.

> "Let's rest here," he said. "I'm starving."

  The Tang monk climbed down from his horse and stretched. The horse drank from a stream while Bajie looked in a bag.

> "No food," said the pig.

> "We'll have to beg for food somewhere," said Wujing. He looked at the monk. "Master, you wait here while Bajie and I find a village."

## ⑤

  The monk sat down in the grass next to the road and closed his eyes. He had nearly dozed off when he heard a voice.

> "Master!"

  It was Wukong. The Tang monk glared at the monkey.

> "Wukong! Why are you here?"

  The monkey fell to his knees.

> "I'm begging you, please let me join you again!"

## ⑥

> "No," said the monk. "You're still evil, Wukong. You can't go to the Western Paradise with me. Now leave, before I recite the tight headband spell."

  The monkey was furious. He pulled out his iron bar, which quickly grew. Before the monk could recite the spell, Wukong struck him and knocked him out. Quickly the monkey grabbed the bags and then vanished.

## ⑦

  Wujing and Bajie soon returned. They found the Tang monk sitting by the road, rubbing his head.

> "Master!" cried Wujing. "What happened? Where are the bags?"

  Bajie looked around.

> "Did Wukong return?"

  Said the Tang monk.

> "He begged me to let him join us again. I said no, and then he attacked me."

## ⑧

> "That's terrible," said Wujing. "That rotten monkey!"

  Bajie stamped his foot.

> "We can't let him get away with this. He probably went home to the Fruit and Flower Mountain. I'll go there and deal with him," said Wujing.

  Bajie gave Wujing directions to the Fruit and Flower Mountain.

## ⑨

  When Wujing arrived, he found Wukong near the waterfall.

> "Wukong!" shouted Wujing. "Why did you attack Master?"

  The monkey looked at Wujing blankly.

> "Who are you?"

  Wujing raised an eyebrow.

> "What are you talking about? You know who I am."

## ⑩

> "No, I don't," said Wukong.

> "I'm Sha Wujing. We were traveling to the west together."

> "I'm going to the west but not with you," said Wukong. He pointed to a group of figures. "I'm going with them."

  Wujing looked over. A monk who looked exactly like the Tang monk sat on a horse. A pig stood next to the horse.

## ⑪

> "Bajie?" said Wujing.

  Just then he saw a purple figure walk over to the horse. Wujing gasped in shock.

> "Wujing?"

  The purple figure was an exact copy of himself.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十二章：花果山惊变

## ①

  悟空直奔普陀山。观音菩萨正在花园里。

> "悟净，这一路怎么样？"

  悟空举起双手，无奈地说：

> "唐僧疯了。"

> "怎么回事？"菩萨问。

> "他让我走人，"猴子说，"就因为我要收拾几个强盗，他生气了。"

## ②

  观音皱起眉头。

> "悟空，伤害人是不对的，这你知道。"

> "我杀的可是妖怪啊。"悟空说。

> "那不一样，"观音说，"妖怪作恶，你除掉它们是做好事。但你绝不能伤害人。"

## ③

  猴子坐下来，双手抱头。

> "菩萨，您说得对。"

  他哭了起来。

> "这下糟了，我再也到不了西天了，也再也不能陪唐僧取经了。我想求得原谅的。"

> "别哭了，悟空，"观音说，"你还是会帮助唐僧到达西天的，他很快就会来请你帮忙。在此期间，你就住在我这里吧。"

## ④

  八戒放下了行李袋。

> "我们歇一会儿吧，"他说，"我饿坏了。"

  唐僧从马上下来，伸了伸懒腰。白龙马喝着溪中的水，八戒翻找着行囊。

> "没吃的了，"八戒说。

> "我们得去找个村子化点斋饭，"悟净看了看唐僧说，"师父，您在这里等着，我和八戒去找村子。"

## ⑤

  唐僧在路边的草地上坐了下来，闭上眼睛。他正要打盹，忽然听到一个声音。

> "师父！"

  是悟空。唐僧瞪着猴子。

> "悟空！你怎么来了？"

  猴子扑通跪倒在地。

> "求求师父，重新让我跟你们走吧！"

## ⑥

> "不行，"唐僧说，"悟空，你恶性难改。你不能跟我去西天了。快走吧，否则我就念紧箍咒了。"

  悟空怒火中烧。他掏出金箍棒，迎风一晃便变长了。趁唐僧还没来得及念咒，悟空一棒打去，将唐僧打晕在地，然后一把抢走行囊，消失得无影无踪。

## ⑦

  悟净和八戒很快回来了。他们看到唐僧坐在路边揉着头。

> "师父！"悟净惊叫道，"出什么事了？行李呢？"

  八戒环顾四周。

> "悟空回来了？"

  唐僧说：

> "他求我收留他，我拒绝了，他就打晕了我。"

## ⑧

> "太过分了，"悟净说，"这遭瘟的猴子！"

  八戒跺了跺脚。

> "不能让他这么跑了。他多半回老家花果山去了。我去花果山收拾他，"悟净说。

  八戒给悟净指了去花果山的路。

## ⑨

  悟净来到花果山，看见悟空站在瀑布前。

> "悟空！"悟净大喊，"你为什么要打师父？"

  猴子茫然地看着悟净。

> "你是谁？"

  悟净挑了挑眉毛。

> "你说什么？你认识我的。"

## ⑩

> "不，不认识。"悟空说。

> "我是沙悟净，我们一起去西天取经的。"

> "我是要去西天，但不是跟你一起，"悟空指着远处的一队人说，"我是跟他们走。"

  悟净放眼望去，一个和唐僧长得一模一样的和尚骑着马，旁边还站着一头猪。

## ⑪

> "八戒？"悟净惊诧道。

  就在这时，一个紫色的身影朝马走去。悟净倒吸一口凉气。

> "悟净？"

  那紫色的身影竟然是自己的翻版。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Three: Two Wukongs

## ①

  Wujing watched as the fake Wujing fed the horse some hay. The purple spirit spoke.

> "I don't know how you made fake versions of Wukong, Bajie, and the Tang monk, but you won't get the true scriptures without the real Wukong."

  Wukong folded his arms.

> "Oh yes I will."

  Wujing leaped into the air and flew south.

> "I'll tell the Bodhisattva what Wukong is doing," he thought. "She can stop him."

## ②

  When Wujing arrived at Mount Potalaka, he was even more shocked. Wukong was meditating in the Bodhisattva's garden.

> "Wukong!" cried Wujing. "How did you get here so fast?"

> "What are you talking about?" asked the monkey.

## ③

  Guanyin came out of her pagoda.

> "Wujing, what are you doing here?"

  The purple spirit bowed.

> "Bodhisattva, I must speak with you. Wukong has made fake versions of me, Bajie, and the Tang monk. He's planning to make the journey without us."

> "What?" shouted Wukong.

## ④

  Wujing glanced at the monkey.

> "I just saw him on the Fruit and Flower Mountain. I don't know how he got here before me."

> "You're lying!" yelled Wukong.

  Guanyin smiled.

> "You're mistaken, Wujing. Wukong has been here the whole time."

  Wujing was surprised.

> "He has?"

  Guanyin nodded.

## ⑤

  Wukong made a fist.

> "Someone is pretending to be me, and he's living on my mountain. I'm going there right now. I'm going to destroy him."

> "I'll go with you," said Wujing.

  Wukong and Wujing soon arrived on the Fruit and Flower Mountain. The monkey's eyes burned with anger when he saw the fake Wukong.

> "Who are you?" demanded Wukong.

> "Who are you?" asked the fake Wukong.

## ⑥

> "I am Sun Wukong, King of the Fruit and Flower Mountain!"

> "No," said the other monkey. "I am Sun Wukong."

  The fake Wukong pulled out his iron bar and swung. The other Wukong blocked the bar and swung back.

> "Wujing, help me!" cried one Wukong.

  Wujing raised his spear and was about to enter the fight.

## ⑦

  The other Wukong shouted.

> "No! Wujing, help me!"

  Wujing looked from one Wukong to the other.

> "Who is the real Wukong?"

> "I am!" shouted one Wukong as he struck at the other.

> "No!" shouted the other Wukong, blocking the first one's attack. "I am!"

> "Don't listen to him!" cried one monkey.

> "Don't listen to him!" cried the other.

## ⑧

  Wujing stamped his foot.

> "Stop fighting!" he shouted.

  Instantly both monkeys stopped fighting. They looked at the purple spirit.

> "I don't know which one of you is the real Wukong! Go to Mount Potalaka. Guanyin will be able to tell who is who. I will return to the Tang monk to tell him what's going on."

## ⑨

  The two Wukongs glared at each other.

> "That's a good idea," said one of them. "Guanyin will easily see that I am the real Wukong."

> "It is a good idea," the other agreed. "Guanyin will easily see that I am the real Wukong."

  Soon the two Wukongs stood before Guanyin. She looked carefully at each one.

> "I can't tell which one of you is the real Wukong," she said.

## ⑩

  One Wukong took a deep breath.

> "Use the tight headband spell. The spell will work only on my headband -- the real headband."

> "Yes," said the other one. "Use the tight headband spell. The spell will only work with my headband -- the real headband."

  Guanyin recited the tight headband spell. Both monkeys fell to the ground, howling in pain.

> "Stop the spell!" they cried.

  Guanyin stopped reciting, and the two monkeys stood back up.

## ⑪

> "I still don't know which of you is the real Wukong," the Bodhisattva said. "You should both go to Heaven. The real Wukong used to live there. Maybe the Jade Emperor can tell who is who."

> "Good idea," said one Wukong. He pointed at the other. "The Jade Emperor will see that this monkey is a fake."

> "I'm not a fake!" cried the other monkey. "You are!"

  He tried to strike the other Wukong, but that one dodged the blow and swung back.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十三章：真假悟空

## ①

  悟净眼睁睁看着那个假悟净在给马喂草。紫色的身影对他说：

> "我不知道你怎么变出了悟空、八戒和唐僧的假身，但没有真的悟空，你们取不到真经。"

  悟空抱起双臂。

> "哦，我偏要。"

  悟净纵身一跃，向南飞去。

> "我要去告诉菩萨悟空在做什么，"他想，"她能制止他。"

## ②

  悟净来到普陀山，眼前的景象让他更加震惊。悟空竟然坐在菩萨的花园里打坐。

> "悟空！"悟净惊叫道，"你怎么这么快就来了？"

> "你说什么呢？"猴子问道。

## ③

  观音从宝塔里走出来。

> "悟净，你怎么来了？"

  紫色的身影向菩萨行礼。

> "菩萨，我必须跟您说一件事。悟空变出了我、八戒和唐僧的假身，他要甩开我们自己去取经。"

> "什么？"悟空大喝一声。

## ④

  悟净瞥了猴子一眼。

> "我明明在花果山看到他的，不知道他怎么赶在我之前到这里了。"

> "你撒谎！"悟空大喊。

  观音微微一笑。

> "悟净，你弄错了。悟空一直在这里。"

  悟净大吃一惊。

> "他一直在这里？"

  观音点了点头。

## ⑤

  悟空紧握拳头。

> "有人假冒我，还占了我的花果山。我现在就要回去收拾他。"

> "我跟你一起去。"悟净说。

  悟空和悟净很快来到了花果山。看到那个假悟空时，悟空怒目圆睁。

> "你是谁？"悟空厉声喝道。

> "你是谁？"假悟空反问。

## ⑥

> "我是孙悟空，花果山美猴王！"

> "不对，"另一个猴子说，"我才是孙悟空。"

  假悟空掏出铁棒就打。真悟空举棒格挡，又反击回来。

> "悟净，快来帮我！"一个悟空喊道。

  悟净举起降妖杖，正要加入战斗。

## ⑦

  另一个悟空大叫道：

> "不！悟净，帮我！"

  悟净左看看右看看，分不清谁是真的。

> "到底谁才是真的悟空？"

> "我！"一个悟空边打边喊。

> "不对！"另一个悟空挡住攻击，"我才是！别听他的！"一个猴子叫道。

> "别听他的！"另一个也喊道。

## ⑧

  悟净一顿脚。

> "别打了！"他大喊道。

  两个猴子立刻停手，齐刷刷看向悟净。

> "我不知道你们谁是真的！去普陀山找观音菩萨吧，她一定分辨得出来。我回去禀报师父。"

## ⑨

  两个悟空怒目相视。

> "好主意，"其中一个说，"观音菩萨一眼就能看出我才是真的悟空。"

> "好主意，"另一个也表示同意，"观音菩萨一看就知道我才是真的。"

  两个悟空很快来到观音面前。菩萨仔细端详了两人。

> "我也分不出你们谁是真的。"

## ⑩

  一个悟空深吸一口气。

> "念紧箍咒吧。紧箍咒只对真的金箍起作用。"

> "对，念紧箍咒，"另一个也说，"咒只对真的金箍有效。"

  观音念起紧箍咒，两个猴子同时倒地，痛得直叫。

> "别念了！"他们齐声叫道。

  观音停下咒语，两个猴子又站了起来。

## ⑪

> "我还是分辨不出谁是真的，"菩萨说，"你们去天庭吧。玉帝或许能分辨出来。"

> "好主意，"一个悟空说，指着另一个，"玉帝一看就知道这个猴子是假的。"

> "我不是假的！"另一个猴子叫道，"你才是！"

  他挥棒打向另一个悟空，对方闪身躲过，又反击回来。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Four: Curious Ears

## ①

  The two monkeys were still fighting when they arrived at the southern gate of Heaven. The Heavenly guard narrowed his eyes.

> "Wukong? Is that you?"

> "Yes, it's me," said both of the Wukongs.

> "I must speak with the Jade Emperor," said one monkey. He pointed at the other. "He's a fake Wukong."

> "I'm not a fake Wukong," said the other monkey. "I'm the real one."

## ②

> "I must speak with the Jade Emperor," said the second monkey.

  The guard allowed both Wukongs to enter Heaven.

  Crash! Bang! The two Wukong fought all over Heaven. The monkeys knocked over statues and trees. Still fighting, they stormed into the Cloud Palace. When the Jade Emperor saw them, he was furious.

> "What's going on?" he boomed.

## ③

> "Your Majesty," said one of the Wukongs. "Please punish this monkey. He's pretending to be me."

> "Punish him!" cried the other. "He's pretending to be me!"

> "Stand still, both of you," said the Jade Emperor. "Let me get a good look at you."

  The two Wukongs stood still as the Jade Emperor looked carefully at them. Finally, the Emperor shrugged.

> "You look exactly alike. I can't tell who is who."

## ④

  One of the Wukongs swung at the other with his iron bar.

> "I'm the real Wukong!"

> "No." The other Wukong blocked the bar and swung back. "I'm the real Wukong!"

> "Both of you leave at once!" thundered the Jade Emperor. "One Wukong is bad enough. I don't want two of you around. Go fight somewhere else!"

  The two monkeys kept fighting as they headed out of the palace.

## ⑤

  The spirit of the planet Venus followed them.

> "Wukong," said the spirit.

  Both monkeys stopped to look at him.

> "Go to the Land of Darkness," said Venus. "Maybe the judge of the dead can tell you apart."

## ⑥

  Soon the two Wukongs were standing before the judge of the dead. The judge shook his head.

> "You look exactly alike!"

> "Check the directory," said one of the Wukongs. "Maybe it will have some information about the fake Sun Wukong."

> "Yes!" said the other Wukong. "Check the directory!"

  The judge nodded and opened the giant book, reading carefully. He turned the pages, studying them. Finally, he closed it.

## ⑦

> "There's no fake Sun Wukong in the directory," said the judge. "I'm sorry, but I have no idea which one of you is the real Wukong."

  A spirit was sitting at a nearby desk.

> "I believe my pet beast, Di Ting (Curious Ears), can help," said the spirit.

  He took a step back, and a small beast crept out from under the desk.

> "Curious Ears can tell the true from the false," said the spirit.

  The beast stared hard at the two Wukongs. Finally, it spoke.

> "I know who the fake Sun Wukong is."

## ⑧

  The two Wukongs stared at Curious Ears.

> "I'm the real Wukong!" shouted one monkey.

> "No, it's me!" shouted the other.

> "I know which of you is the fake Sun Wukong," said Curious Ears. "But I won't say who it is. The fake Sun Wukong has all the same powers as the real one. If I point him out, he'll get angry. He could destroy the entire palace!"

## ⑨

> "It's true," said one Wukong. "I could destroy this whole palace if I wanted to."

> "Do you mean I could destroy it?" said the other Wukong.

> "No!" yelled the other. "I could!"

  The two Wukongs began swinging their iron bars at each other.

> "Please, stop!" cried the judge of the dead. "You'll destroy the whole palace!"

  The monkeys stopped.

## ⑩

> "But I can help you," said Curious Ears. "The Buddha will be able to see which of you is the real Wukong, and he's powerful enough to destroy the fake one."

> "Of course!" cried one Wukong. "Let's go see Buddha."

> "Oh, um, sure," said the other Wukong. He looked worried.

## ⑪

> "You're nervous," said the first Wukong. "That's because you know Buddha is going to see who you really are."

> "No!" shouted the other Wukong. He swung his iron bar furiously.

> "Get out!" cried the judge of the dead. "Take your battle somewhere else."

> "Go to the Western Paradise," said Venus.

  The two Wukongs left the Land of Darkness. Clouds swirled and thundered as the two mighty spirits battled across the sky.

## ⑫

  They soon arrived in the Western Paradise. A guard rushed out of the Thunderclap Monastery.

> "Stop fighting immediately!" he called up to them. "Tell me who you are."

  The two Wukongs landed in front of the guard. The guard looked surprised.

> "Wukong! There are two of you."

> "Yes," said one of the Wukongs. "I must speak with Buddha right away."

  The other Wukong scratched his head.

> "If Buddha is busy, we can just come back another time."

  The first Wukong shot a look at the other.

> "No, we can't."

## ⑬

> "You may enter," said the guard. "But you must behave yourselves while inside."

  As the first Wukong started to enter the monastery, the other one backed away.

> "You are coming with me!" said the first Wukong.

  He grabbed the other monkey by the arm and dragged him into the monastery. In front of Buddha, the first Wukong bowed. The other Wukong hesitated a moment and then bowed also.

## ⑭

  Greetings, Buddha. Said the first Wukong. I must ask for your help.

> "I know why you're here, Wukong," said Buddha. He looked at the other monkey. "And I know that you are a fake."

  The other Wukong gasped and then vanished. Buddha held a bowl up in the air and then placed it upside down on a table.

> "I've trapped the fake Wukong under this bowl," said Buddha.

  When Buddha lifted the bowl, a tiny monkey spirit lay on the table.

## ⑮

  Wukong leaned closer to see.

> "He was a monkey who became an evil spirit," said Buddha. "He wanted to be you because you're so powerful."

  Wukong laughed.

> "Many spirits want to be me."

  The monkey thanked Buddha and then flew back to Mount Potalaka.

## ⑯

  Guanyin decided it was time for Wukong to rejoin his companions on the journey. She and the monkey found the Tang monk and the others along the road to the west. The Bodhisattva told the Tang monk that it wasn't Wukong who attacked him.

> "You must keep Wukong with you," explained Guanyin.

> "Yes, Bodhisattva," said the Tang monk, bowing.

## ⑰

> "Thank you, Bodhisattva," said Wukong. "I'll make sure the Tang monk reaches the Western Paradise."

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十四章：谛听辨真假

## ①

  两个悟空一路打到南天门外。天将眯起眼睛。

> "悟空？是你吗？"

> "是我是我。"两个悟空齐声说。

> "我要见玉帝，"一个猴子说，指着另一个，"他是个冒牌货。"

> "我才是真的，"另一个猴子说。"我才是真悟空。"

## ②

> "我也要见玉帝。"第二个悟空说。

  天将放两个悟空进了天庭。

  哗啦！乒乒乓乓！两个悟空在天庭到处打，推翻了雕像和树木。打着打着，他们闯进了灵霄宝殿。玉帝看到他们，勃然大怒。

> "怎么回事？"他厉声喝道。

## ③

> "陛下，"一个悟空说，"请惩罚这个猴子，他假冒我。"

> "惩罚他！"另一个叫道，"他才是假冒的！"

> "你们两个都别动，"玉帝说，"让我好好看看。"

  两个悟空站定，玉帝仔细端详。最后，玉帝耸了耸肩。

> "你们长得一模一样，我分辨不出来。"

## ④

  一个悟空挥棒打向另一个。

> "我才是真悟空！"

> "不对！"另一个挡住金箍棒反击，"我才是真悟空！"

> "你们两个都给我滚出去！"玉帝雷霆大怒，"一个悟空就够烦的了，我才不要两个。你们去别处打！"

  两个猴子一边打一边出了殿。

## ⑤

  太白金星跟在后面。

> "悟空，"太白金星说。

  两个猴子停下来看他。

> "去地府看看吧，"金星说，"也许阎王能分辨你们。"

## ⑥

  很快两个悟空站在了阎王面前。阎王摇了摇头。

> "你们长得一模一样！"

> "查生死簿，"一个悟空说，"里面可能有关于假孙悟空的信息。"

> "对！查生死簿！"另一个也说。

  阎王点了点头，打开生死簿，仔细地翻看着，最后合上了书。

## ⑦

> "生死簿上没有假孙悟空的记录，"阎王说，"抱歉，我实在分不清你们谁是真的。"

  旁边案上坐着一位天神。

> "我相信我的神兽谛听可以帮忙，"那神仙说。

  他退了一步，一只小兽从桌下爬了出来。

> "谛听能辨别真假，"神仙说。

  神兽仔细盯着两个悟空看了半天。终于开口了。

> "我知道谁是假孙悟空。"

## ⑧

  两个悟空盯着谛听。

> "我才是真悟空！"一个猴子大叫。

> "不，是我！"另一个也喊。

> "我知道谁是假孙悟空，"谛听说，"可我不敢说。假孙悟空跟真的本事一样大，我要是当面指出来，他会发怒，说不定把我的地府全毁了！"

## ⑨

> "没错，"一个悟空说，"我要想拆了这地府易如反掌。"

> "你说谁能拆？"另一个悟空说。

> "我！"另一个大喊。

  两个悟空又挥棒打了起来。

> "别打了，求你们！"阎王大喊道，"会把地府全毁的！"

  两个猴子停下手。

## ⑩

> "不过我可以帮你们，"谛听说，"如来佛祖能分辨你们谁是真悟空，而且法力高强，足以降服假的。"

> "当然！"一个悟空叫道，"我们找佛祖去！"

> "行、好吧，"另一个悟空说，脸上露出一丝担忧。

## ⑪

> "你心虚了，"第一个悟空说，"因为你知道到了佛祖面前你就原形毕露了。"

> "才不是！"另一个悟空大喊，挥棒就打。

> "滚出去！"阎王大怒，"你们去别处打！"

  两个悟空离开了地府，两团云雾翻腾，电闪雷鸣，两个神通广大的妖精在空中激战。

## ⑫

  他们很快到了西天。一个守卫从雷音寺冲出来。

> "立刻住手！"他朝上大喊，"报上名来。"

  两个悟空落在守卫面前。守卫大吃一惊。

> "悟空！怎么有两个你？"

> "是的，"一个悟空说，"我要立刻见佛祖。"

  另一个悟空挠了挠头。

> "佛祖要是忙的话，我们改天再来也行。"

  第一个悟空瞪了他一眼。

> "不行，今天必须见。"

## ⑬

> "你们可以进去，"守卫说，"但在里面不许动手。"

  第一个悟空正要进寺，另一个想溜。

> "你跟我一起进去！"第一个悟空一把抓住他的胳膊，拖着进了雷音寺。在佛祖面前，第一个悟空行礼。另一个犹豫了一下，也施了礼。

## ⑭

> "佛祖在上，"第一个悟空说，"我来求您帮忙。"

> "悟空，我知道你为什么来，"佛祖说，目光转向另一个猴子，"我也知道，你是个假货。"

  另一个悟空倒吸一口凉气，随即消失了。佛祖举起一个钵盂，然后倒扣在桌上。

> "我把假悟空扣在这个钵下面了，"佛祖说。

  佛祖揭开钵盂，桌上一只小猴妖趴在那里。

## ⑮

  悟空凑近来看。

> "他是一只修炼成精的猴子，"佛祖说，"因为你法力高强，他想取而代之。"

  悟空大笑。

> "想取代我的妖精还真不少。"

  悟空谢过佛祖，飞回了普陀山。

## ⑯

  观音觉得是时候让悟空回到取经队伍中了。她和猴子在西行路上找到了唐僧和众人。菩萨告诉唐僧，之前打他的那个并非真悟空。

> "你千万要留住悟空，"观音吩咐道。

> "是，菩萨。"唐僧恭敬地行礼。

## ⑰

> "谢谢菩萨，"悟空说，"我发誓一定保师父到达西天。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Five: Battle of the Wukongs

## ①

  Curious Ears spoke. The two Wukongs stared at it.

> "I know which of you is the fake Sun Wukong," said Curious Ears. "But I won't say who it is."

## ②

> "The fake Sun Wukong has all the same powers as the real one. If I point him out, he'll get angry. He could destroy the entire palace!"

> "It's true," said one Wukong. "I could destroy this whole palace if I wanted to."

> "Do you mean I could destroy it?" said the other Wukong.

> "No!" yelled the other. "I could!"

## ③

  The two Wukongs began swinging their iron bars at each other.

> "Please, stop!" cried the judge of the dead. "You'll destroy the whole palace!"

  The monkeys stopped.

> "But I can help you," said Curious Ears. "The Buddha will be able to see which of you is the real Wukong. And he's powerful enough to destroy the fake one."

## ④

> "Of course!" cried one Wukong. "Let's go see Buddha."

> "Oh, um, sure," said the other Wukong. He looked worried.

> "You're nervous," said the first Wukong. "That's because you know Buddha is going to see who you really are."

> "No!" shouted the other Wukong. He swung his iron bar furiously.

> "Get out!" cried the judge of the dead. "Take your battle somewhere else."

## ⑤

  The two Wukongs left the Land of Darkness. Clouds swirled and thundered as the two mighty spirits battled across the sky. They soon arrived in the Western Paradise. A guard rushed out of the Thunderclap Monastery.

> "Stop fighting immediately!" he called up to them. "Tell me who you are."

## ⑥

  The two Wukongs landed in front of the guard. The guard looked surprised.

> "Wukong! There are two of you."

> "Yes," said one of the Wukongs. "I must speak with Buddha right away."

  The other Wukong scratched his head.

> "If Buddha is busy, we can just come back another time."

  The first Wukong shot a look at the other.

> "No, we can't."

> "You may enter," said the guard. "But you must behave yourselves while inside."

## ⑦

  As the first Wukong started to enter the monastery, the other one backed away.

> "You are coming with me!" said the first Wukong.

  He grabbed the other monkey by the arm and dragged him into the monastery. In front of Buddha, the first Wukong bowed. The other Wukong hesitated a moment and then bowed also.

## ⑧

> "Greetings, Buddha," said the first Wukong. "I must ask for your help."

> "I know why you're here, Wukong," said Buddha. He looked at the other monkey. "And I know that you are a fake."

  The other Wukong gasped and then vanished.

## ⑨

  Buddha held a bowl up in the air and then placed it upside down on a table.

> "I've trapped the fake Wukong under this bowl," said Buddha.

  When Buddha lifted the bowl, a tiny monkey spirit lay on the table.

## ⑩

  Wukong leaned closer to see.

> "He was a monkey who became an evil spirit," said Buddha. "He wanted to be you because you're so powerful."

  Wukong laughed.

> "Many spirits want to be me."

## ⑪

  The monkey thanked Buddha and then flew back to Mount Potalaka. Guanyin decided it was time for Wukong to rejoin his companions on the journey. She and the monkey found the Tang monk and the others along the road to the west. The Bodhisattva told the Tang monk that it wasn't Wukong who attacked him.

> "You must keep Wukong with you," explained Guanyin.

> "Yes, Bodhisattva," said the Tang monk, bowing.

## ⑫

> "Thank you, Bodhisattva," said Wukong. "I'll make sure the Tang monk reaches the Western Paradise."

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十五章：真假猴王大决战

## ①

  谛听开口了。两个悟空盯着它。

> "我知道谁是假孙悟空，"谛听说，"可我不敢说。"

## ②

> "假孙悟空跟真的本事一样大。我要是当面指出来，他会发怒，说不定把整个宫殿都毁了！"

> "说得对，"一个悟空说，"我要想拆了这宫殿易如反掌。"

> "你说谁能拆？"另一个悟空说。

> "我！"另一个大喊。

## ③

  两个悟空又挥起铁棒打了起来。

> "别打了，求你们！"阎王大喊道，"会把整个地府全毁的！"

  猴子们停下手。

> "不过我可以帮你们，"谛听说，"佛祖能分辨你们谁是真悟空，而且他法力无边，足以降服假的。"

## ④

> "当然！"一个悟空叫道，"我们找佛祖去！"

> "行、好吧，"另一个悟空说，脸上露出一丝担忧。

> "你心虚了，"第一个悟空说，"因为你知道到了佛祖面前你就原形毕露了。"

> "才不是！"另一个悟空大喊，挥棒就打。

> "滚出去！"阎王大怒，"你们去别处打！"

## ⑤

  两个悟空离开了地府。两团云雾翻腾，电闪雷鸣，两个神通广大的妖精在空中激战，很快到了西天。一个守卫从雷音寺冲出来。

> "立刻住手！"他朝上大喊，"报上名来。"

## ⑥

  两个悟空落在守卫面前。守卫大吃一惊。

> "悟空！怎么有两个你？"

> "是的，"一个悟空说，"我要立刻见佛祖。"

  另一个悟空挠了挠头。

> "佛祖要是忙的话，我们改天再来也行。"

  第一个悟空瞪了他一眼。

> "不行，今天必须见。"

> "你们可以进去，"守卫说，"但在里面不许动手。"

## ⑦

  第一个悟空正要进寺，另一个想逃。

> "你跟我一起进去！"第一个悟空一把抓住他的胳膊，拖着进了雷音寺。在佛祖面前，第一个悟空行礼。另一个犹豫了一下，也施了礼。

## ⑧

> "佛祖在上，"第一个悟空说，"我来求您帮忙。"

> "悟空，我知道你为什么来，"佛祖说，目光转向另一个猴子，"我也知道你是个假货。"

  另一个悟空倒吸一口凉气，随即消失了。

## ⑨

  佛祖举起一个钵盂，然后倒扣在桌上。

> "我把假悟空扣在这个钵下面了，"佛祖说。

  佛祖揭开钵盂，桌上一只小猴妖趴在那里。

## ⑩

  悟空凑近来看。

> "他是一只修炼成精的猴子，"佛祖说，"因为你法力高强，他想取而代之。"

  悟空大笑。

> "想取代我的妖精还真不少。"

## ⑪

  悟空谢过佛祖，飞回了普陀山。观音觉得是时候让悟空回到取经队伍中了。她和猴子在西行路上找到了唐僧和众人。菩萨告诉唐僧，之前打他的那个并非真悟空。

> "你千万要留住悟空，"观音吩咐道。

> "是，菩萨。"唐僧恭敬地行礼。

## ⑫

> "谢谢菩萨，"悟空说，"我发誓一定保师父到达西天。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Six: The Iron Immortal

## ①

  Wukong was once again traveling west with the Tang monk.

> "Master," said Wukong. "While I was at Mount Potalaka, I thought a lot. I realize now that it's wrong to harm people. I won't ever do it again."

> "I'm glad, Wukong," said the Tang monk.

  Bajie moaned.

## ②

> "Can we please slow down?"

  Wukong laughed.

> "Not much has changed. Bajie still complains all the time."

  Wujing said with a frown, "It is hot. Maybe we should take a break."

> "Yes," said the Tang monk. "But I don't understand why it's so hot. It's not summer."

## ③

  The travelers soon reached a village. An old man offered to take them in for the night. Later that evening they were all eating dinner.

> "Isn't it always so hot here?" asked Bajie.

  The man nodded.

> "The Mountain of Flames is near here. It's always burning."

> "Well, I'll be happy when we continue on our journey," said the pig. "Then we can get away from this heat."

## ④

> "Where are you going?" asked the man.

> "We're going to the Western Paradise," said the Tang monk.

  The man frowned.

> "You can't travel west from here."

  Everyone stopped eating and looked at the old man.

> "Why not?" asked the Tang monk.

## ⑤

> "The Mountain of Flames is to the west," said the man. "It's impossible to pass."

> "We'll go around it," said the Tang monk.

  The old man shook his head.

> "All the land around the mountain is covered in flames. The land stretches to the north and the south. It's impossible to go around."

> "Then we must wait for a strong rainstorm," said Bajie. "That will put out the flames."

## ⑥

> "No," said the man. "The flames are magical. There's just one spirit who can put them out."

> "Oh?" asked Wukong.

> "She's called the Iron Immortal," said the man. "She has a special fan that can put out the flames. It's made from a plantain leaf."

  Wukong stood up.

> "Where does the Iron Immortal live? I'll ask her to put out the flames."

## ⑦

> "He won't listen to you!" said the man. "She is very powerful."

  Wukong folded his arms in front of his chest.

> "I am as powerful as a god. Just tell me where she lives."

  The old man told Wukong where the Iron Immortal lived. The monkey leaped into the air. The man gasped.

> "He's a spirit!"

## ⑧

  Wukong was soon on the Iron Immortal's mountain. He found a cave door and knocked.

> "Open up!" he demanded.

  The door flew open and a tall woman appeared. She held a large fan.

> "Who are you?" she asked.

> "I am Sun Wukong. I need to borrow your fan."

## ⑨

> "Sun Wukong? Oh!" cried the Iron Immortal. "You are my worst enemy!"

  Wukong was confused.

> "I am? Why?"

  The Iron Immortal glared at the monkey.

> "My husband is the Bull Demon King, who used to be your friend. And our son is Red Boy. Because of you, Red Boy is a prisoner of the Bodhisattva Guanyin."

## ⑩

  Wukong laughed.

> "Red Boy isn't a prisoner. He is Guanyin's student. He isn't evil anymore."

  The Iron Immortal shrieked.

> "That's even worse!"

  Wukong sighed.

> "Can I please just borrow your fan for a little while?"

> "No," said the woman.

## ⑪

> "Well then, can I speak with the Bull Demon King?" asked the monkey.

> "He's at a banquet," said the Iron Immortal. "Now, leave!"

  Wukong grew angry.

> "I'm not leaving until I borrow your fan!"

> "Mush!" The Iron Immortal waved the fan.

  A furious wind blew, and Wukong was gone.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十六章：铁扇仙

## ①

  悟空又和唐僧一起踏上西行的路。

> "师父，"悟空说，"我在普陀山待了这段时间想了很多。我现在明白了伤害人是不对的，我再也不会那样做了。"

> "悟空，你能这样想我就放心了。"唐僧说。

  八戒在一旁哼哼唧唧。

## ②

> "我们能走慢点吗？"

  悟空笑了。

> "真是一点都没变，八戒还是整天抱怨。"

  悟净皱了皱眉说：

> "实在太热了。我们歇一歇吧。"

> "好，"唐僧说，"可我真不明白为什么这么热，现在又不是夏天。"

## ③

  一行人来到一座村庄，一位老人留他们过夜。傍晚时分，大家围在一起吃晚饭。

> "这里一直这么热吗？"八戒问。

  老人点了点头。

> "附近有座火焰山，山上一直在燃烧。"

> "那我们继续赶路就好了，"八戒说，"就能离开这个鬼地方了。"

## ④

> "你们要去哪里？"老人问。

> "我们要去西天取经。"唐僧说。

  老人皱起了眉头。

> "你们从这里是过不了火焰山的。"

  大家都停下来吃饭，望着老人。

> "为什么？"唐僧问。

## ⑤

> "火焰山就在西边，"老人说，"根本过不去。"

> "我们可以绕过去。"唐僧说。

  老人摇了摇头。

> "火焰山四面都是火，南北也一样。根本绕不过去。"

> "那等一场大雨，"八戒说，"雨就能把火浇灭。"

## ⑥

> "不行，"老人说，"那火是魔火，浇不灭的。只有一个神仙能灭那火。"

> "哦？"悟空问。

> "她叫铁扇仙，"老人说，"她有一把神奇的芭蕉扇，能熄灭火焰山的火。"

  悟空站起身来。

> "她住在哪里？我去请她灭火。"

## ⑦

> "你请不动她的！"老人说，"她法力高强。"

  悟空双手抱在胸前。

> "我和神仙一样厉害。你只管告诉我她在哪里就行。"

  老人告诉了悟空铁扇仙的住处。悟空纵身一跃飞上天空。老人倒吸一口气。

> "原来是个神仙！"

## ⑧

  悟空很快到了铁扇仙的山上。发现一个洞口，他上前敲门。

> "快开门！"他喝道。

  门猛地开了，一个高个女人出现了，手里拿着一把大扇子。

> "你是谁？"她问。

> "我是孙悟空，来借你的芭蕉扇一用。"

## ⑨

> "孙悟空？哎呀！"铁扇仙惊叫起来，"你是我的死对头！"

  悟空糊涂了。

> "我是？为什么？"

  铁扇仙怒视着猴子。

> "我丈夫是牛魔王，以前是你的朋友。我儿子是红孩儿。因为你的缘故，红孩儿被观音菩萨收走了。"

## ⑩

  悟空大笑。

> "红孩儿不是被关押，他是观音菩萨的弟子，已经改邪归正了。"

  铁扇仙尖声叫道：

> "那更糟！"

  悟空叹了口气。

> "那你能不能把扇子借我用一用？"

> "不行！"女人断然拒绝。

## ⑪

> "那我跟牛魔王说行不行？"悟空问。

> "他去赴宴了，"铁扇仙说，"快走！"

  悟空恼了。

> "借不到扇子我绝不走！"

> "休想！"铁扇仙一扇扇子。

  一阵狂风刮来，悟空被吹得无影无踪。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Seven: The Magic Fan

## ①

  For over a day, the wind from the fan carried Wukong. When he finally landed, he was far from the Iron Immortal's mountain. Wukong looked around and saw a mountain nearby. It looked familiar.

> "Mount Sumeru," said Wukong. "The Bodhisattva Lingji lives there. Maybe he can help me deal with the Iron Immortal. He was able to stop the Great King Yellow Wind's wind magic."

  The monkey went to Lingji's pagoda. The Bodhisattva was sitting in his garden.

## ②

> "Greetings, Wukong," said the Bodhisattva.

> "Hello, Lingji," said Wukong. "It's good to see you again. I was just about to have tea."

  Wukong and Lingji sat outside drinking tea. The monkey told the Bodhisattva everything that had happened with the Iron Immortal.

## ③

  The Bodhisattva handed a small stone to Wukong.

> "Keep this magic stone in your pocket. It will stop the wind from blowing you away."

> "Thank you, Bodhisattva," said the monkey.

> "Would you like to stay for lunch?" asked Lingji.

> "No, thank you," said Wukong. "I must get back to my companions. I need to get that fan from the Iron Immortal so we can continue west."

## ④

  Wukong returned to the Iron Immortal's cave door.

> "Open up!" he shouted. "I need your fan."

  The Iron Immortal came out and frowned.

> "I thought I got rid of you."

  She raised her fan.

> "I'll just have to wave harder this time."

  The woman waved the fan furiously. A terrible wind blew past Wukong, but the monkey didn't move.

## ⑤

  The Iron Immortal's eyes burned with anger.

> "The Bodhisattva Lingji gave me a magic stone. Your fan can't blow me away now."

  The monkey pulled out his iron bar.

> "Now give me that fan."

  The Iron Immortal turned and ran back into her cave. Before she could shut the door, Wukong turned into a cricket and slipped into the cave.

## ⑥

  Silently he followed the Iron Immortal along a tunnel. When the woman reached the room, she sat down. She tucked the fan into her robe.

> "Wukong is a horrible monkey," she said to herself. "He forced my poor baby Red Boy to become good. Then he demanded to borrow my precious fan."

## ⑦

  The Iron Immortal reached for a cup of water. As she took a drink, Wukong leaped into the cup.

  Inside the Iron Immortal's stomach, Wukong changed back into himself and pushed and kicked. The Iron Immortal fell to her knees.

> "What was in that water? I feel awful."

> "It was me," shouted Wukong. "I'm in your stomach now. And I won't stop punching and kicking until you give me that fan."

## ⑧

> "Please stop!" cried the Iron Immortal. "You can have the fan. Just don't hurt me anymore."

  Wukong leaped out of the woman's nose and returned to his normal size.

> "Give me the fan," he demanded.

## ⑨

  The Iron Immortal climbed back to her feet. She reached into her robe and pulled out a fan.

> "Here. Take it."

  Wukong found his companions in the village with the old man. The monkey explained how he tricked the Iron Immortal.

> "Wonderful," said the Tang monk. "Now we can continue our journey."

  They all thanked the old man and then headed west.

## ⑩

  They came to the top of the hill and saw the Mountain of Flames. Fire covered all the land around it.

> "Watch this," said Wukong.

  The monkey waved the fan hard. A strong wind blew toward the mountain.

  Wukong smiled. But in a moment, suddenly there was a roar and the flames grew bigger, filling the sky.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十七章：芭蕉扇

## ①

  铁扇仙的扇子把悟空吹了一整天。等他终于落地时，已经到了离铁扇仙的山很远的地方。悟空环顾四周，看到附近有一座熟悉的山。

> "须弥山，"悟空说，"灵吉菩萨住在这里。也许他能帮我收拾铁扇仙，当初他就是用定力降服了黄风怪的风魔大法的。"

  猴子来到灵吉的宝塔前。菩萨正坐在花园中。

## ②

> "悟空，你好。"菩萨说。

> "灵吉菩萨，又见面了。"悟空说，"好巧，我刚想找你有事。"

  悟空和灵吉坐在外面喝茶。猴子把在铁扇仙那里的遭遇全说了一遍。

## ③

  菩萨递给悟空一颗小石子。

> "把这颗定风丹放在口袋里，她的扇子就吹不动你了。"

> "谢谢菩萨！"悟空道谢。

> "留下来吃午饭吗？"灵吉问。

> "不了，我得回去找同伴。我得从铁扇仙那里拿到扇子，才能继续往西走。"

## ④

  悟空回到铁扇仙的洞门前。

> "开门！"他大喊，"我要借你的扇子！"

  铁扇仙走出来了，眉头紧皱。

> "我以为再也见不到你了。"

  她举起扇子。

> "这次我得用力扇了。"

  女人用力扇动，一阵狂风掠过悟空面前，可猴子纹丝不动。

## ⑤

  铁扇仙怒火中烧。

> "灵吉菩萨给了我定风丹。你的扇子再也不能把我吹跑了。"

  猴子掏出铁棒。

> "快把扇子交出来！"

  铁扇仙转身就往洞里逃，还没关上门悟空就变成一只蟋蟀溜了进去。

## ⑥

  他悄悄跟着铁扇仙穿过隧道到了房间。女人坐下后把扇子藏进了衣袍里。

> "这猴子真是该死，"她自言自语道，"先把我可怜的红孩儿变成了观音的弟子，现在又来抢我的宝贝芭蕉扇。"

## ⑦

  铁扇仙端起一杯水来喝。趁她喝水的当口，悟空跳进了杯中。

  在铁扇仙的肚子里，悟空现出原形，又推又踢。铁扇仙扑通跪倒在地。

> "我喝的是什么？难受死了！"

> "是我！"悟空在里面大喊，"我在你肚子里呢。你不把扇子给我，我就一直踢个不停。"

## ⑧

> "求求你住手吧！"铁扇仙哭喊道，"扇子给你，别再折磨我了！"

  悟空从女人鼻孔里飞了出来，恢复原形。

> "把扇子给我。"他命令道。

## ⑨

  铁扇仙颤巍巍地站起来，从衣袍里掏出了一把扇子。

> "拿去，拿去吧。"

  悟空回到村里找到了同伴们，跟大家说了自己如何智取铁扇仙。

> "太好了，"唐僧说，"这下我们可以继续赶路了。"

  他们谢过老人，向西出发。

## ⑩

  他们来到小山顶上，看到了火焰山。烈火覆盖了四周所有的土地。

> "看好了，"悟空说。

  猴子用力扇动芭蕉扇。一阵猛烈的风朝火焰山吹去。

  悟空得意地笑了。谁知突然一声巨响，火焰非但没有熄灭，反而越烧越大，直冲云霄。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Eight: Tricked Again and Again

## ①

  Wukong looked at the fan.

> "This fan doesn't work! The Iron Immortal must have tricked me!"

  The travelers made their way back to the village. The fire burned hotter.

> "What will we do?" asked the Tang monk. "We can't go through that fire."

  Bajie threw his hands up.

> "Let's just go home! We'll write a letter to Buddha explaining what happened."

> "Bajie, we can't do that," the Tang monk scolded.

## ②

  Wukong spoke up.

> "I used to be friends with the Iron Immortal's husband, the Bull Demon King. I have an idea."

  The Iron Immortal was in her cave when she heard a knock.

> "Oh no!" she said to herself. "That monkey is back."

  She walked quietly to the door and peeked outside. When she saw the Bull Demon King, she smiled and opened the door.

## ③

> "I'm glad you're back," said the Iron Immortal.

> "Sun Wukong was here," said the demon. "I used to be friends with him. It would be nice to see him again."

  His wife was confused.

> "What do you mean? You told me that you never really liked him."

> "Oh, really?" said the demon. "He was very rude."

  Said the woman.

> "He demanded I let him borrow my fan."

## ④

> "You didn't give it to him, did you?" asked the demon.

> "Of course not," said his wife. "I gave him a fake fan that looks just like the real one."

  The demon began pacing.

> "Wukong is very smart and very powerful. He'll realize you tricked him, and then he'll come back here. What should we do?" asked the Iron Immortal.

> "Give me the fan," said the demon. "I'll keep it safe."

## ⑤

  The Iron Immortal opened a chest and took out the fan. She handed it to her husband. Suddenly, light sparkled, and Wukong stood in front of her.

> "I tricked you!" the monkey laughed. He ran out of the cave.

  The Iron Immortal stamped her foot. She was still angry when her husband came home.

> "Hello, dear," said the Bull Demon King with a big smile.

  But then his smile faded.

> "What's wrong?"

> "Your friend Sun Wukong was here," she snapped.

## ⑥

> "He's not my friend," said the demon. "Even before he defeated Red Boy, I never really liked him."

> "Well, you'll like him even less now," said the Iron Immortal. "He stole my fan."

  The demon looked surprised.

> "My rival's wind magic is powerful. How did the monkey steal it?"

> "He tricked me into giving it to him," said his wife. "He made himself look like you!"

## ⑦

  The demon's face turned red.

> "How dare he do that?"

  He took a deep breath.

> "Don't worry. I will find that rotten monkey. I'll get your fan back."

  The Bull Demon King stomped out of the cave.

## ⑧

  Wukong walked along the road, carrying the plantain leaf fan. He was still laughing about how he tricked the Iron Immortal. Then he saw Bajie approaching.

> "Bajie!" cried Wukong. "What are you doing here?"

> "I was coming to help," said the pig.

> "Thanks, but I don't need help." Wukong held up the fan. "I tricked the Iron Immortal and got the real fan this time."

## ⑨

> "Good!" said Bajie. "I can carry it for you."

> "Thanks!" said Wukong as he handed the fan to Bajie.

  The monkey patted his friend on the shoulder.

> "Now let's get back to Master. We need to..."

  Suddenly there was a flash of light. A second later, the Bull Demon King stood next to Wukong. The demon laughed.

> "I tricked you, Wukong!"

  There was another flash, and the demon was gone.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十八章：再遭欺骗

## ①

  悟空看着手中的扇子。

> "这扇子没用！铁扇仙又骗了我！"

  一行人回到了村里。火焰烧得更旺了。

> "我们怎么办？"唐僧问道，"那火是过不去的。"

  八戒把手一摊。

> "干脆回家算了！我们给佛祖写封信说明情况。"

> "八戒，那怎么行？"唐僧训斥道。

## ②

  悟空开口了。

> "我以前跟铁扇仙的丈夫牛魔王是朋友。我有一个主意。"

  铁扇仙在洞里听到敲门声。

> "坏了！"她心里一惊，"这猴子又回来了。"

  她悄悄走到门口，从门缝往外看。看到牛魔王时她笑了，打开门。

## ③

> "你回来啦。"铁扇仙说。

> "孙悟空来过了，"牛魔王说，"我以前跟他可是好兄弟。能再见到他也挺好。"

  妻子感到困惑。

> "你说什么？你不是说你一直讨厌他吗？"

> "哦，是吗？"牛魔王说。

  女人说。

> "他来找我借芭蕉扇。"

## ④

> "你没借给他吧？"牛魔王问。

> "当然没有，"妻子说，"我给了他把假扇子，跟真的一模一样。"

  牛魔王开始来回踱步。

> "孙悟空又聪明又厉害。他会发现你骗了他，到时候还会回来找麻烦的。怎么办？"铁扇仙问。

> "把扇子给我，"牛魔王说，"我来保管。"

## ⑤

  铁扇仙打开箱子，取出了芭蕉扇，交给了丈夫。突然光芒一闪，悟空出现在她面前。

> "我又骗到你了！"猴子大笑一声，跑出了洞。

  铁扇仙气得直跺脚。这时她的丈夫回来了。

> "夫人。"牛魔王满面笑容。

  但他很快笑不出来了。

> "怎么了？"

> "你那个朋友孙悟空来过！"铁扇仙怒道。

## ⑥

> "他可不是我的朋友，"牛魔王说，"就算在红孩儿事件之前，我也没多喜欢他。"

> "哼，你现在更该恨他了，"铁扇仙说，"他抢走了我的芭蕉扇。"

  牛魔王吃了一惊。

> "孙悟空的风魔法很厉害，他怎么抢到扇子的？"

> "他骗我交出来的，"妻子说，"他变成了你的模样！"

## ⑦

  牛魔王气得满脸通红。

> "岂有此理！"

  他深吸了一口气。

> "别担心，我去找那该死的猴子。一定把扇子夺回来。"

  牛魔王大步走出山洞。

## ⑧

  悟空走在路上，手里拿着芭蕉扇，还笑自己智取铁扇仙的事。这时八戒迎面走来。

> "八戒！"悟空叫道，"你怎么来了？"

> "我来帮你呀。"八戒说。

> "谢了，不过不需要。"悟空举起扇子，"这次我骗了铁扇仙，拿到真的了。"

## ⑨

> "太好了！"八戒说，"我来帮你拿吧。"

> "好！"悟空把扇子交给了八戒。

  猴子拍了拍朋友的肩膀。

> "走吧，我们回去找师父。我们要……"

  突然一道闪光。眨眼之间，牛魔王出现在悟空面前。

  那妖怪大笑。

> "孙悟空，我又骗到你了！"

  又是一道闪光，妖怪消失了。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Seventy-Nine: The Mountain of Flames

## ①

  The mountain of flames. Wukong was furious.

> "The Bull Demon King tricked me!"

  The monkey rushed back to the cave and smashed the door. Crush! The Bull Demon King ran outside.

> "You villain!" he shouted. "You destroyed my door."

## ②

> "Give me that fan right now!" yelled Wukong. "Or I'll destroy the rest of your mountain!"

> "Never!" said the demon.

  Wukong charged toward the demon. Whoa! The demon turned into a crane and flew away.

## ③

  He's not the only one who can turn into other animals, thought the monkey.

  Wukong turned into a phoenix and shot after the crane. With his claws out, he swooped down at the crane.

  The crane dipped into the lower, and Wukong missed. When Wukong looked back, the crane was gone.

## ④

  Where did he go? thought Wukong.

  He looked down and saw an antelope grazing in a field.

  That's him!

  Wukong landed and turned into a tiger. He crept through the tall grass. When he got close to the antelope, he leaped.

## ⑤

  Light flashed, and the antelope turned into a huge white bull. The bull flew up into the sky, and Wukong followed.

  He had almost caught up to the bull when he heard a shout.

> "Step back, Wukong!"

  It was a soldier from heaven, sent by the Jade Emperor to help.

## ⑥

  More soldiers rushed toward the bull. With a snort, the bull spun around and flew the other way. But other soldiers appeared and blocked the bull's path.

  Wukong watched as soldiers surrounded the bull. They moved in closer, their swords and spears all pointed at the bull.

  The Bull Demon King returned to his demon form.

## ⑦

> "Please don't hurt the Iron Fan Princess," she cried, rushing toward the soldiers. "Don't harm my husband! He didn't mean to be evil."

  One soldier lowered his sword.

> "We won't harm you if you're truly sorry for being evil. But right now you're stopping the Tang Monk from continuing his journey."

> "Wukong will call for your fan."

  The Iron Fan Princess handed the fan to the soldier.

## ⑧

> "Here's the fan," she said. "We are truly sorry. My husband and I will be good Buddhists from now on. Just please don't hurt us!"

  The soldier looked at the Bull Demon King. The demon nodded.

> "We promise."

> "Very well," said the soldier. "You two may return to your cave. But you must avoid trouble from now on."

## ⑨

  The demon and his wife bowed and left. The soldier handed the fan to Wukong.

> "It's good that you'll be the one to put out the mountain flames, Wukong."

  Wukong was confused.

> "Why?"

> "You're the one who caused the fire," said the soldier. "It was when Laozi tried to burn you up in his pot. You leapt out of the pot, disturbing the fire in his workroom. The burning ember fell to earth that day. It started the fire on the mountain."

## ⑩

  Wukong looked at the fan.

> "I'll be happy to put out the fire."

  Wukong returned to the village. The Tang Monk and his companions were at the old man's house again. Once again they thanked the man and followed the road up the hill.

  At the top they looked at the mountain of flames. Wukong looked at the fan and waved it. Whoosh! Instantly the fire went out.

## ⑪

  The air cooled down, and Wukong saw the valley start to turn green. Leaves grew on trees and small flowers popped up here and there. Birds sang in the branches as other animals ran through the grass.

  Wukong smiled. He had done evil things a long time ago. Now he was fixing them.

---

# 🇨🇳 第七十九章：火焰山

## ①

  火焰山。悟空怒火中烧。

> "牛魔王骗了我！"

  猴子冲回洞中，砸碎了大门。轰隆！牛魔王从外面跑了出来。

> "你这恶棍！"他大叫道，"你毁了我的门！"

## ②

> "把扇子还给我！"悟空吼道，"不然我就把你的山全毁了！"

> "休想！"妖怪说。

  悟空向妖怪冲去。嚯！妖怪变成一只鹤飞走了。

## ③

  他会变身，我也会，猴子心想。

  悟空变成一只凤凰，朝着鹤飞去。他伸出利爪，向鹤猛扑过去。

  鹤俯冲而下，悟空扑了个空。当悟空回头时，鹤已经不见了。

## ④

  他去哪儿了？悟空心想。

  他低头看去，看到一只羚羊在田野里吃草。

  是他！

  悟空落到地上，变成一只老虎。他悄悄穿过高高的草丛。当他接近羚羊时，他纵身一跃。

## ⑤

  光芒一闪，羚羊变成了一头巨大的白牛。白牛飞上天空，悟空紧随其后。

  他差点就追上白牛，忽然听到一声喊。

> "退后，悟空！"

  是天兵，玉帝派他来助阵。

## ⑥

  更多天兵冲向白牛。白牛哼了一声，转身朝另一个方向飞去。但其他天兵出现，挡住了去路。

  悟空看着天兵包围了白牛。他们越靠越近，刀剑长矛全部指向白牛。

  牛魔王恢复了妖怪的真身。

## ⑦

> "请不要伤害我丈夫！"铁扇公主哭着冲向天兵。"他不是存心作恶的。"

  一个天兵放下了剑。

> "如果你们真心悔改，我们不会伤害你们。但现在你们阻断了唐僧西行的道路。"

> "悟空要借你的扇子。"

  铁扇公主把扇子交给了天兵。

## ⑧

> "扇子在这里，"她说，"我们真心知错了。我和丈夫从今以后一定做个好佛门弟子。请不要伤害我们！"

  天兵看着牛魔王。牛魔王点了点头。

> "我们发誓。"

> "很好，"天兵说，"你们可以回洞去了。但从今以后不得再惹事生非。"

## ⑨

  妖怪和妻子鞠躬离去。天兵把扇子交给了悟空。

> "你能来扑灭这山火，真是太好了，悟空。"

  悟空很困惑。

> "为什么这么说？"

> "火是你引起的，"天兵说，"当年太上老君把你扔进炼丹炉里烧你。你跳出丹炉时，弄翻了炉子里的火。燃烧的余烬掉落人间，点燃了这座山。"

## ⑩

  悟空看着手中的扇子。

> "我很乐意去灭火。"

  悟空回到村子。唐僧和同伴们正在老人家。他们再次谢过老人，沿着山路前行。

  到了山顶，他们望着火焰山。悟空看了一眼扇子，挥了一挥。呼！大火瞬间熄灭。

## ⑪

  空气凉爽下来，悟空看到山谷开始变得翠绿。树上长出绿叶，到处开着小花。鸟儿在枝头歌唱，动物在草地上奔跑。

  悟空微笑了。他很久以前做过恶事，现在他在弥补。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eighty: The Small Thunder-Clap Monastery

## ①

  One afternoon, Wukong and his companions were resting by a stream. They were eating peaches and berries.

> "We must be getting close to the Western Paradise," said the Tang Monk. "We've been traveling for years."

> "I feel like we've been traveling for thousands of years," said Bajie.

## ②

> "We still have a long way to go," said Wukong. "But don't worry. Eventually we'll arrive in the Western Paradise and climb up the Spirit Mountain."

  Buddha's home, the Thunderclap Monastery, he sits halfway up the mountain.

  The Tang Monk took a bite of his peach.

> "The Thunderclap Monastery must be wonderful to see."

## ③

> "The Monastery is spectacular," said the monkey. "Golden light shines from it."

  Bajie moaned.

> "So we're going to have to climb a mountain at the end of this journey? Just thinking about that makes me tired."

  Wujing stroked his chin.

> "I really hope the journey ends soon."

## ④

  The pig nodded.

> "You're tired of traveling, too?"

> "No," said Wujing with a serious look. "I'm just tired of hearing you complain."

  Everyone was quiet for a moment. Then Wujing's face broke into a smile, and everybody laughed. Even Bajie.

## ⑤

> "Very funny, Wujing," said Bajie.

  The Tang Monk stood up.

> "We should go. I'd like to find a village or a monastery before dark."

  A couple of hours later, they were traveling up a mountain road. The road curved around a bend. Ahead, they could see a small monastery.

## ⑥

  The Tang Monk gasped.

> "Is that the Thunderclap Monastery?"

  "Look at that," said Bajie. "Golden light is shining from it."

> "It's all along the mountain," Wujing added.

  Wukong laughed.

## ⑦

> "It's not the Thunderclap Monastery. We're not even in the Western Paradise yet."

  The monk appeared puzzled for a moment, and then frowned.

> "We must be careful. I see dark clouds over the monastery."

  The travelers continued walking along the road. Soon they were standing in front of the monastery. A sign over the door read: "Small Thunder-Clap Monastery."

## ⑧

> "Wow!" cried the Tang Monk. "This monastery must belong to Buddha."

  Wukong shook his head.

> "It doesn't belong to Buddha. Let's keep walking."

> "Hold on," said Bajie. "Golden light is shining from this monastery. It must be an important place."

## ⑨

> "It's not," said Wukong. "We should really—"

> "We're going in," the Tang Monk said. "This is a Buddhist monastery. We should visit."

  The monk opened the monastery's door and entered. Bajie and Wujing followed. Wukong sighed and went in after them.

## ⑩

  This place was definitely not what it seemed. The monkey pulled out his iron bar.

  The group entered the building's main hall. A large golden statue of Buddha sat before them.

> "Do you see that statue, Wukong?" said the Tang Monk. "This is a real Buddhist monastery."

## ⑪

  Suddenly a voice boomed.

> "Who dares to enter without bowing to Buddha?"

  The Tang Monk trembled with fear. Right away, he fell to his knees and bowed. Bajie and Wujing bowed. Wukong continued to stand, peering at the statue. It looked very suspicious.

## ⑫

> "Why don't you bow?" the voice asked.

  Wukong whispered to the Tang Monk.

> "Show some respect."

> "I will bow to—" shouted Wukong. "I can see that you're a fake!"

## ⑬

  Clang! Before the monkey could finish yelling, a large pair of cymbals fell from above. They slammed together, sealing Wukong inside.

> "Wukong!" cried the Tang Monk.

  Light flashed, and the statue turned into a demon with yellow eyebrows. The demon stood up and smiled.

  The Tang Monk!

---

# 🇨🇳 第八十章：小雷音寺

## ①

  一天下午，悟空和同伴们在小溪边休息。他们在吃桃子和浆果。

> "我们一定快到西天了，"唐僧说，"我们已经走了很多年了。"

> "我感觉我们走了好几千年了，"八戒说。

## ②

> "还有很长的路要走呢，"悟空说，"不过别担心。我们终究会到达西天，爬上灵山。"

  佛祖的居所——雷音寺，就在山的半山腰。

  唐僧咬了一口桃子。

> "雷音寺一定很壮观吧。"

## ③

> "那座寺院非常壮观，"猴子说，"金光闪闪。"

  八戒呻吟道。

> "所以到了旅途最后我们还要爬山？光是想想就累了。"

  悟净摸着下巴。

> "我真希望旅途早点结束。"

## ④

  猪八戒点了点头。

> "你也厌倦了赶路？"

> "不，"悟净一脸严肃地说，"我只是厌倦了听你抱怨。"

  大家沉默了一会儿。接着悟净的脸上露出了笑容，大家都笑了。连八戒也笑了。

## ⑤

> "真有意思，悟净，"八戒说。

  唐僧站了起来。

> "我们该出发了。我想在天黑前找个村庄或寺院。"

  几个小时后，他们在山路上行进着。道路转过一个弯道，前面出现了一座小寺院。

## ⑥

  唐僧倒吸一口凉气。

> "那就是雷音寺吗？"

  "你们看，"八戒说，"金光从那里射出来。"

> "整座山都是金色的，"悟净补充道。

  悟空笑了。

## ⑦

> "那不是雷音寺。我们还没到西天呢。"

  唐僧怔了一会儿，接着皱起了眉头。

> "我们要小心。我看到寺院上空有乌云。"

  旅行者们继续沿着道路往前走。很快他们就到了寺院门前。门上的牌匾写着"小雷音寺"。

## ⑧

> "哇！"唐僧叫道，"这座寺院一定是佛祖的。"

  悟空摇了摇头。

> "不属于佛祖。我们绕道走吧。"

> "等等，"八戒说，"这座寺院金光闪闪，一定是个重要的地方。"

## ⑨

> "不是的，"悟空说，"我们真的应该——"

> "我们要进去，"唐僧说，"这是座佛门寺院，我们理当拜访。"

  唐僧推开寺院的门走了进去。八戒和悟净跟在后面。悟空叹了口气，也跟了进去。

## ⑩

  这个地方绝不是表面看起来的那样。猴子掏出了铁棒。

  一行人走进大殿，一尊巨大的金色佛像端坐眼前。

> "悟空，你看到那尊佛像了吗？"唐僧说，"这是真正的佛门寺院。"

## ⑪

  忽然传来一声雷鸣般的喝问。

> "是谁敢见佛不拜？"

  唐僧吓得发抖，立刻跪地叩拜。八戒和悟净也拜了下去。悟空依然站着，审视着佛像。他心中生疑。

## ⑫

> "你为何不拜？"那声音问道。

  悟空低声对唐僧说。

> "小心有诈。"

> "我正要拜——"悟空大喊，"我发现你们是假的！"

## ⑬

  当啷！猴子还没喊完，一对巨大的铙从天而降。它们合在一起，将悟空困在里面。

> "悟空！"唐僧大叫。

  光芒一闪，佛像变成了一个黄眉妖怪。妖怪站起来，微微一笑。

  唐僧上当了！

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eighty-One: Help From a Dragon

## ①

  Bajie and Wujing swung their weapons at the demon.

  Ah! The demon laughed.

> "I'm much too powerful for you!"

  From inside the cymbals, Wukong heard the fight. He heard grunts and the sounds of weapons clashing.

> "No!" the Tang Monk cried.

## ②

  Then there was silence.

> "What happened out there?" shouted Wukong.

  There was no answer. The monkey punched and kicked the inside of the cymbals for hours. But the two cymbals would not come apart.

> "This is terrible," he said to himself. "How will I get out of here?"

## ③

  The monkey was about to strike the cymbals again when he heard a voice.

> "Wukong, are you in there?"

> "Who is that?" Wukong asked.

> "I'm the gold dragon," said the voice. "The Jade Emperor sent me to help you. I'll wedge my horn between the cymbals and pry them apart."

## ④

> "Please try," said Wukong.

  Slowly the dragon's horn slipped through. But the cymbals were still tightly clasped together. Wukong groaned.

> "I can't escape."

> "Maybe we could find another way to pry the cymbals apart," said the dragon.

## ⑤

> "Actually, I have a different idea," said the monkey.

  Wukong turned his iron bar into a drill. The monkey drilled a hole in the dragon's horn. Then he made himself tiny and climbed into the hole.

> "Pull your horn out now!" said Wukong.

## ⑥

  The dragon pulled and pulled and finally got his horn out. The monkey jumped out of the hole and returned to his normal size.

> "Thank you," said Wukong. "Now we must free my friends!"

> "We have to be quiet," said the dragon. "The demon is sleeping."

  Wukong nodded.

## ⑦

  Then he turned toward the cymbals and raised his iron bar. The cymbals shattered.

> "You did that?" cried the dragon.

  Wukong shrugged.

> "I was angry."

  The demon stormed into the room.

> "Sun Wukong! How did you escape? Who are you?"

## ⑧

> "How do you know my name?" demanded Wukong.

> "My name is Yellow Brows," said the demon. "I've been waiting for you and the Tang Monk to pass by my mountain."

  Wukong narrowed his eyes.

> "Why?"

## ⑨

> "I'm a Buddhist," said the demon. "I plan to go to the Western Paradise and get the true scriptures myself."

> "You can't do that!" shouted Wukong.

  The monkey and the dragon charged toward the demon. The demon pulled a cloth from his robe and threw it. The cloth wrapped around Wukong and the dragon. And then it became very small.

## ⑩

  Soon they were tied up in a room. The Tang Monk, Bajie and Wujing were also in the room. Their bags were lying in a corner.

> "I'm sorry for not believing you, Wukong," said the Tang Monk. "You suspected this place was dangerous."

> "Don't worry about that, Master," said the monkey.

## ⑪

> "We must escape as soon as the demon goes back to sleep. He plans to get the true scriptures himself."

  The group waited for a while. Finally, Wukong made himself tiny and slipped out from his ropes. He untied his companions and the dragon.

> "Let's go," the monkey whispered. "Bajie, get the bags."

## ⑫

> "Everyone, be quiet," the dragon warned.

  They tiptoed toward the monastery door and were soon outside. Wukong looked at Bajie and frowned.

> "Where are the bags?"

  The pig moaned.

## ⑬

> "Ah, I forgot them."

> "Master's special robes are in one of those bags," Wukong sighed. "Wait here. I'll go back and get them."

  The monkey quietly hurried back to the room and grabbed the bags. But as he was leaving, he tripped and knocked over a statue.

## ⑭

  Then, from another room, Yellow Brows shouted.

> "What was that?"

---

# 🇨🇳 第八十一章：龙王相助

## ①

  八戒和悟净挥舞着武器向妖怪打去。

  哈！妖怪大笑。

> "你们根本不是我的对手！"

  在铙钹里面，悟空听到了打斗声。他听到喘息声和兵器碰撞的声音。

> "不！"唐僧喊道。

## ②

  随后一片寂静。

> "外面发生什么了？"悟空大喊。

  没有回应。猴子拼命捶打踹踢铙钹内壁好几个时辰，但那对铙钹纹丝不动。

> "太糟糕了，"他自言自语，"我怎么才能出去呢？"

## ③

  猴子正要再次猛击铙钹，忽然听到一个声音。

> "悟空，你在里面吗？"

> "你是谁？"悟空问。

> "我是金龙，"那声音说，"玉帝派我来帮你。我把角塞进铙钹缝里，把它们撬开。"

## ④

> "试试吧，"悟空说。

  慢慢地，龙角钻了进来。但铙钹仍然紧紧合拢。悟空呻吟了一声。

> "我出不去。"

> "也许我们还有别的办法把铙钹撬开，"龙说。

## ⑤

> "其实我有个别的主意，"猴子说。

  悟空把铁棒变成了一把钻。猴子在龙角上钻了一个洞。然后他变得极小，爬进了洞里。

> "现在把角抽出来！"悟空说。

## ⑥

  龙用力拉拽，终于把角抽了出来。猴子跳出洞口，恢复了正常大小。

> "谢谢你，"悟空说，"现在我们必须救出朋友们！"

> "我们要轻一点，"龙说，"妖怪睡着了。"

  悟空点了点头。

## ⑦

  然后他转向铙钹，举起了铁棒。铙钹 shattered了。

> "是你干的？"龙惊叫。

  悟空耸了耸肩。

> "我很生气。"

  妖怪冲进了房间。

> "孙悟空！你怎么逃出来的？你是谁？"

## ⑧

> "你怎么知道我的名字？"悟空质问道。

> "我叫黄眉，"妖怪说，"我一直在等你和唐僧路过我的山。"

  悟空眯起了眼睛。

> "为什么？"

## ⑨

> "我是佛门弟子，"妖怪说，"我打算自己去西天取经。"

> "你休想！"悟空大喊。

  猴子和龙向妖怪冲去。妖怪从袍子里掏出一块布扔了出去。布裹住了悟空和龙，然后变得极小。

## ⑩

  很快他们被绑在一间屋里。唐僧、八戒和悟净也在屋里。行李包扔在角落里。

> "对不起，悟空，我不该不相信你，"唐僧说，"你早就怀疑这地方不对劲。"

> "别放在心上，师父，"猴子说。

## ⑪

> "等妖怪睡着我们就必须逃出去。他打算自己去取经。"

  大家等了好一会儿。终于，悟空把自己变得极小，从绳索中溜了出来。他解开了同伴们和龙的绳子。

> "走吧，"猴子低声说，"八戒，拿上行李。"

## ⑫

> "大家别出声，"龙警告道。

  他们蹑手蹑脚走向寺院大门，很快到了外面。悟空看着八戒，皱起了眉头。

> "行李呢？"

  八戒哼哼了一声。

## ⑬

> "哎，我忘拿了。"

> "师父的锦襕袈裟就在其中一个包里，"悟空叹道，"你们等着，我回去拿。"

  猴子悄悄跑回房间，抓起行李包。但就在他离开的时候，他绊了一跤，碰倒了一尊雕像。

## ⑭

  然后，从另一个房间里传来黄眉的大喊。

> "那是什么声音？"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eighty-Two: The Magic Cloth

## ①

  "Oh no!" thought Wukong. "Yellow Brows is coming!"

  The monkey jumped back to his feet and ran fast out of the monastery. When he got outside, everyone was waiting for him.

> "Where are the bags?" asked Wujing.

  The monkey looked at his empty hands. He slapped his forehead.

## ②

> "I must have dropped them."

  He heard footsteps approaching from inside the monastery.

> "We can't worry about the bags now," whispered Wukong. "Yellow Brows is coming! We have to go quickly!"

  He helped the Tang Monk up onto the horse. The group hurried down the road.

## ③

> "Run faster, Bajie!" hissed Wujing.

  Bajie breathed heavily.

> "I... don't like running!"

  They hadn't gotten far before Yellow Brows flew over them.

## ④

> "You can't escape from me!" shouted the demon. "And you will not be going to the West. I am a true Buddhist, and I will be the one to get the true scriptures!"

  Wukong, Bajie and Wujing pulled out their weapons. The gold dragon bared its claws. Yellow Brows scoffed.

## ⑤

> "Do you really think you can fight me?"

  He reached into his robe and pulled out the cloth. Bajie lowered his rake and laughed.

> "Ha! We have powerful weapons, and all you have is a piece of cloth!"

> "That's not an ordinary cloth," warned the dragon.

  Yellow Brows threw the cloth towards the group.

## ⑥

> "Look out!" cried Wukong.

  The monkey leaped up to the side just before the cloth wrapped around his companions. Quickly, the demon grabbed the cloth with the group in it. He ran back into his monastery and slammed the door shut.

  Wukong sat down on a cloud to think.

## ⑦

  How could he rescue his companions?

  I can't ask the Jade Emperor for help, thought Wukong. He already sent the gold dragon, who was just captured again. Maybe I can ask someone else for help.

  As Wukong was wondering what to do, two spirits approached him. One was a turtle and the other was a serpent.

## ⑧

  The two spirits each carried a sword and a shield.

> "We're from Wu-Dang Mountain," said the turtle. "We've come to help you."

  The serpent nodded.

> "We heard the Tang Monk was captured by a demon called Yellow Brows."

> "Thank you for coming," said Wukong. He quickly told them what had happened.

## ⑨

> "Let's go to the monastery now," said the turtle. "Yellow Brows won't be able to fight all three of us."

> "We are much too powerful for him," added the serpent.

  Wukong led the two spirits down to the monastery.

## ⑩

> "Just be careful of his cloth," warned the monkey. "He'll try to capture us with it."

  Wukong banged on the monastery door.

> "Release my friends right now, Yellow Brows! If you don't, I'll knock down your monastery. Then I'll smash your entire mountain!"

  The door flew open. Yellow Brows stepped out and threw the cloth.

## ⑪

> "Look out!" cried Wukong.

  The monkey jumped out of the way, but the turtle and serpent weren't fast enough. The cloth wrapped around them. Laughing, the demon grabbed the bundle and went back into the monastery.

  Wukong flew back up into the sky. He sat on a cloud and moaned.

## ⑫

> "Now what will I do?"

  He was still thinking when he heard a voice.

> "Hello, Wukong."

  Wukong looked toward the voice and saw a man with a big belly. The man was smiling.

## ⑬

> "Do you know who I am?" asked the man.

  Wukong smiled.

> "You're the Buddha, Maitreya!"

> "Yes," said Maitreya. "And I've come to help you."

---

# 🇨🇳 第八十二章：魔布

## ①

  "坏了！"悟空心想，"黄眉来了！"

  猴子一跃而起，飞快逃出寺院。到了外面，大家都在等他。

> "行李呢？"悟净问。

  猴子看了看空空的双手，拍了拍额头。

## ②

> "我一定掉了。"

  他听到寺院内传来脚步声。

> "现在顾不上行李了，"悟空低声说，"黄眉来了！我们得赶快走！"

  他扶唐僧上了马，一行人匆匆上了路。

## ③

> "跑快点，八戒！"悟净催促道。

  八戒喘着粗气。

> "我……不喜欢跑步！"

  他们还没跑出多远，黄眉就从头顶飞了过来。

## ④

> "你们逃不出我的手掌心！"妖怪大叫，"你们也别想去西天了。我才是真正的佛门弟子，取经的非我莫属！"

  悟空、八戒和悟净掏出兵器。金龙亮出利爪。黄眉冷笑道。

## ⑤

> "你们真以为能打得过我？"

  他从袍子里掏出了那块布。八戒放下钉耙，哈哈大笑。

> "哈！我们有厉害的兵器，你只有一块破布！"

> "那可不是普通的布，"龙警告道。

  黄眉将布朝众人扔去。

## ⑥

> "小心！"悟空大叫。

  猴子向旁边一跃，布裹住了他的同伴。妖怪一把抓起布连带里面的人，跑回寺院，砰地关上了大门。

  悟空坐在云上思索对策。

## ⑦

  怎样才能救出同伴呢？

  我不能找玉帝帮忙，悟空心想。他已经派了金龙来，结果也被抓了。也许我可以找别人帮忙。

  悟空正在发愁，两个精灵朝他走来。一个是乌龟，一个是蛇精。

## ⑧

  两个精灵各持一面盾牌和一把剑。

> "我们来自武当山，"乌龟说，"我们来帮你。"

  蛇精点了点头。

> "我们听说唐僧被一个叫黄眉的妖怪抓了。"

> "谢谢你们前来相助，"悟空说，他迅速把事情经过告诉他们。

## ⑨

> "我们现在就去寺院吧，"乌龟说，"黄眉打不过我们三个。"

> "我们远比他厉害，"蛇精补充道。

  悟空领着两个精灵来到寺院。

## ⑩

> "小心他的布，"猴子提醒道，"他会用它来抓我们。"

  悟空猛敲寺院大门。

> "快放了我的朋友，黄眉！不然我就砸了你的寺院，再踏平你的整座山！"

  大门飞开。黄眉走出来，扔出了那块布。

## ⑪

> "小心！"悟空大叫。

  猴子闪身躲开，但乌龟和蛇精不够快。布把他们裹了起来。妖怪大笑着抓起包裹回到了寺院。

  悟空飞回天上。他坐在云上唉声叹气。

## ⑫

> "现在我该怎么办？"

  正在发愁时，他听到一个声音。

> "你好，悟空。"

  悟空循声望去，看见一个大肚子的男人，正微笑着。

## ⑬

> "你知道我是谁吗？"那人问。

  悟空笑了。

> "你是弥勒佛！"

> "不错，"弥勒佛说，"我来帮你。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eighty-Three: The Melon Field

## ①

> "Are you sure you can help?" Wukong asked the Buddha Maitreya. "Yellow Brows is powerful. He captured everyone with a magic cloth. He trapped me in a pair of cymbals."

> "I can defeat Yellow Brows," said Maitreya. "He used to be my student. The cloth and cymbals are precious Buddhist treasures that he stole from me."

> "Sorry, but I destroyed the cymbals," said Wukong.

## ②

  Maitreya smiled.

> "Don't worry about that. We must capture Yellow Brows. I'll tell you my plan."

  Wukong flew up to the monastery.

> "Yellow Brows!" he shouted. "Return my friends, or I'll smash your entire mountain!"

## ③

  The door flew open and Yellow Brows stepped out.

> "How dare you threaten me? Do you know how powerful I am?"

> "You're not powerful," said the monkey. "You're nothing, because you have that cloth. I bet you're too scared to fight me without it."

> "I'm not scared of you," said the demon.

## ④

  He went back inside and came back a moment later. He was holding a heavy wooden club.

  Wukong pulled out his iron bar as the demon rushed toward him. Wham! Their weapons smashed together again and again.

  As he fought the demon, Wukong took small steps backward. Slowly, he moved the fight away from the monastery. Soon they were fighting in the valley at the bottom of the mountain.

## ⑤

  Wukong took another swing at Yellow Brows and then pretended to be scared.

> "You are too powerful!" cried the monkey. "I can't fight you anymore!"

  He turned and ran away.

> "Hey! Get back here, child!" the demon ran after Wukong.

## ⑥

  The monkey ran through some woods and into a melon field. Yellow Brows chased him.

> "Where are you, Wukong?" he shouted.

  Then the demon noticed all the melons. He licked his lips.

  "Juicy," he said to himself.

  A farmer was working nearby. He had a big belly.

## ⑦

> "Hey, farmer," called Yellow Brows. "Give me one of your melons."

  The farmer put down his hoe and smiled. He walked over to the demon.

> "I'll find a nice ripe melon for you."

  The farmer searched the ground. Finally, he held up a ripe melon.

> "Here you go."

## ⑧

  Yellow Brows lifted the melon to take a bite. Suddenly, the melon shrank to the size of a berry. It leaped out of his hand and went right down his throat.

  Gold? The demon fell to his knees.

  "What was wrong with that melon?"

  Inside the demon, Wukong kicked and chopped.

## ⑨

  "Poof! Ho! Poof! Ho!" cried Yellow Brows.

  Then he noticed the farmer was gone. Instead, Maitreya stood over him. Maitreya glared at the demon.

> "Give me my magic cloth."

> "Yes, yes, Master."

  Yellow Brows pulled the cloth from his robe and handed it to Maitreya.

## ⑩

> "You may come out now, Wukong," said Maitreya.

  A tiny Wukong leaped from the demon's nose. Maitreya threw the cloth over Yellow Brows. It wrapped around the demon and became small. Maitreya put the bundle into a pocket.

  Wukong returned to his normal size. He and Maitreya went to the monastery.

## ⑪

  Maitreya recited a spell and the cymbals repaired themselves. He smiled at Wukong.

> "Good luck."

  Then he vanished.

  Wukong untied his companions and the other spirits. The dragon, the turtle and the serpent thanked the monkey and flew away.

## ⑫

> "Thank you, Wukong," said the Tang Monk. "I'm sorry for not believing you when you warned us about this place."

  Wukong laughed.

> "Maybe you'll believe me one of these days, Master."

  The travelers went outside and continued west.

---

# 🇨🇳 第八十三章：瓜田

## ①

> "你确定能帮上忙？"悟空问弥勒佛，"黄眉很厉害。他用一块魔布把所有人都抓住了，还用铙钹把我困住了。"

> "我能降服黄眉，"弥勒佛说，"他曾经是我的弟子。那块布和铙钹是他从我这里偷走的佛门宝物。"

> "对不起，我把铙钹砸坏了，"悟空说。

## ②

  弥勒佛微笑了。

> "别担心。我们必须抓住黄眉。我把计划告诉你。"

  悟空飞到寺院前。

> "黄眉！"他大叫，"还我朋友，不然我踏平你的山！"

## ③

  大门飞开，黄眉走了出来。

> "你敢威胁我？你知道我有多厉害吗？"

> "你没什么厉害的，"猴子说，"你全靠那块布。我敢说你没了布就不敢跟我打。"

> "我才不怕你，"妖怪说。

## ④

  他回身进屋，不一会儿拿着一根沉重的木棍出来。

  妖怪冲过来，悟空掏出铁棒迎战。当！两件兵器反复碰撞。

  悟空一边打一边慢慢后退。渐渐地，他把妖怪从寺院引到了山谷。不久他们在山脚下打了起来。

## ⑤

  悟空又朝黄眉打了一棒，然后装作害怕。

> "你太厉害了！"猴子叫苦，"我打不过你了！"

  他转身就跑。

> "站住！回来，小子！"妖怪追赶悟空。

## ⑥

  猴子穿过一片树林，跑进了一个瓜田。黄眉紧追不舍。

> "悟空你躲哪里去了？"他大喊。

  这时妖怪注意到了满地的瓜。他舔了舔嘴唇。

  "真甜啊，"他自言自语。

  旁边有个农夫在干活。他有个大肚子。

## ⑦

> "喂，农夫，"黄眉叫道，"给我一个瓜。"

  农夫放下锄头，微微一笑。他走到妖怪面前。

> "我给你找个熟的好瓜。"

  农夫在地里找了一会儿。终于，他举起一个熟透的瓜。

> "给你。"

## ⑧

  黄眉举起瓜正要咬。突然，瓜缩小到豆子那么大。它从他手里跳出来，直接钻进了他的喉咙。

  哎哟！妖怪跪倒在地。

  "这瓜怎么了？"

  在妖怪肚子里，悟空拳打脚踢。

## ⑨

  "哎哟！疼啊！"黄眉大叫。

  然后他发现农夫不见了。取而代之的是弥勒佛站在他面前。弥勒佛怒视着妖怪。

> "把我的魔布交出来。"

> "是，是，师父。"

  黄眉从袍子里掏出布，交给了弥勒佛。

## ⑩

> "悟空，你可以出来了，"弥勒佛说。

  一个小小的悟空从妖怪鼻子里跳了出来。弥勒佛把布往黄眉身上一扔，布裹住了妖怪，变得很小。弥勒佛把包裹放进口袋。

  悟空恢复了正常大小。他和弥勒佛回到了寺院。

## ⑪

  弥勒佛念了一句咒语，铙钹自动修复了。他朝悟空笑了笑。

> "祝你好运。"

  然后他消失了。

  悟空解开了同伴和其他精灵们。金龙、乌龟和蛇精谢过悟空，飞走了。

## ⑫

> "谢谢你，悟空，"唐僧说，"之前你不说这地方有危险，我不该不信你。"

  悟空笑了。

> "也许有一天你会相信我的，师父。"

  一行出了寺院，继续向西前行。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eighty-Four: The Sad King

## ①

> "I wish I had money," Bajie moaned. "All this food looks so good!"

  The travelers were walking through a city in the Scarlet Kingdom. The streets were lined with people selling food and other goods.

> "Stop thinking about food, Bajie," said Wujing. "What's going on over there?"

  He pointed to a crowd of people reading a sign on a wall.

## ②

  The travelers walked over to the crowd. The sign read: "The King of the Scarlet Kingdom is seeking help. Anyone who can defeat demons must report to the royal palace."

  The Tang Monk sighed.

> "I don't want to delay our journey. But you three can defeat demons. We must report to the palace."

> "Don't worry, Master," said Wukong. "I'm great at defeating demons. This won't take long."

## ③

> "I hope there's food at the palace," said Bajie. "I'm starving."

  The travelers arrived at the palace gates. They spoke with a guard who then led them into the court. The king sat on his throne, looking very sad.

> "Your Majesty," said the guard, "the Tang Monk is here to see you. He says his companions can defeat demons."

  The king looked up but didn't say anything.

## ④

  The guard whispered to the travelers.

> "His Majesty is very upset. If you can help him, please do."

  Wukong walked up to the king.

> "Greetings, Your Majesty. I am Sun Wukong, King of the Fruit and Flower Mountain. You need someone who can defeat demons. Well, here I am."

## ⑤

  Suddenly the king covered his face with his hands and burst out crying.

> "Oh, it's terrible," cried the king. "I have no hope anymore."

  Wukong scratched his head.

> "What's wrong?"

> "The Queen, my wife," cried the king. "I'll never see her again!"

## ⑥

  Wukong frowned.

> "Your Majesty, stop crying."

> "Wukong," hissed the Tang Monk. "Show some respect."

  Wukong calmed himself and looked at the king.

> "I realize you're upset, but if you want my help, you must stay calm and explain everything to me."

## ⑦

  The king sniffed and sat up straight. He pulled out a handkerchief and blew his nose.

> "I will tell you what happened. Three years ago, the Demon of Power attacked the kingdom. The demon kidnapped the Queen. I sent soldiers to fight the demon and bring back my love. But the demon was too powerful."

> "Where is the demon?" asked Wukong.

## ⑧

  The king got up and walked to a window. He pointed to a mountain in the distance.

> "The demon lives on that mountain."

  Wukong slapped the king on the back.

> "You can stop being sad now, Your Majesty. I will rescue the Queen. In the meantime, please take care of my companions. I think Bajie is hungry."

## ⑨

  Wukong landed on the demon's mountain. Several small demons were standing outside a cave entrance.

> "Return the Queen, or I'll destroy all of you!" shouted the monkey.

  The small demons cried and ran into the cave.

  Wukong heard another voice inside the cave.

## ⑩

> "What's going on?" it said.

> "Master!" cried one demon. "There's a monkey outside. We must return the Queen, or he'll destroy all of us!"

  A large demon with broad shoulders came out of the cave. She wore three bells.

> "I am the Demon of Power!" shouted the demon. "Get off of my mountain!"

## ⑪

  Wukong was furious.

> "Do you know who I am? I'm the Great—"

  Whoosh! A blast shot all over. Smoke filled the air and blinded poor Wukong. The monkey coughed as sand got in his eyes and nose.

> "This is awful," cried Wukong.

  He covered his face and leapt off the mountain.

---

# 🇨🇳 第八十四章：悲伤的国王

## ①

> "我要是有钱就好了，"八戒哼哼道，"这些食物看起来真好吃！"

  旅行者们正在朱紫国的城中行走。街道两旁都是卖食物和各种货物的人。

> "别光想着吃的了，八戒，"悟净说，"那边是怎么回事？"

  他指着墙边的一群人。

## ②

  一行人走上前去。告示上写着："朱紫国国王求助。能降妖者速来王宫。"

  唐僧叹了口气。

> "我不想耽误行程，但你们三个能降妖。我们必须去王宫看看。"

> "别担心，师父，"悟空说，"降妖是我的拿手好戏，花不了多少时间。"

## ③

> "希望王宫里有吃的，"八戒说，"我饿坏了。"

  一行人来到王宫门前。他们和卫兵说了几句话，卫兵领他们进了大殿。国王坐在王座上，神情十分悲伤。

> "陛下，"卫兵说，"唐僧求见。他说他的徒弟能降妖除魔。"

  国王抬起头，但没有说话。

## ④

  卫兵低声对旅行者们说。

> "陛下非常伤心。如果你们能帮上忙，请一定帮忙。"

  悟空走到国王面前。

> "陛下您好。我是花果山美猴王孙悟空。您需要有人降妖，我不期而至。"

## ⑤

  国王突然双手捂面，放声大哭。

> "太惨了，"国王哭着说，"我已经没有希望了。"

  悟空挠了挠头。

> "怎么了？"

> "王后，我的妻子，"国王哭着说，"我再也见不到她了！"

## ⑥

  悟空皱起了眉头。

> "陛下，别哭了。"

> "悟空，"唐僧低声喝道，"注意礼节。"

  悟空定了定神，看着国王。

> "我知道您难过，但如果要让我帮忙，您必须冷静下来，把事情的来龙去脉说清楚。"

## ⑦

  国王抽了抽鼻子，坐直了身子。他掏出手帕擦了擦鼻涕。

> "我告诉你怎么回事。三年前，赛太岁妖怪来犯，掳走了王后。我派士兵去救她，但妖怪太厉害了。"

> "妖怪住在哪里？"悟空问。

## ⑧

  国王起身走到窗前，指着远处的一座山。

> "妖怪就住在那座山上。"

  悟空拍了拍国王的后背。

> "陛下别难过了，我去把王后救回来。这期间请照看好我的同伴们。八戒肯定饿了。"

## ⑨

  悟空降落在妖怪的山上。几个小妖怪正站在洞口。

> "交出王后，不然我把你们全部消灭！"猴子大喊。

  小妖怪们吓得哭喊着跑进洞里。

  悟空听到里面传来另一个声音。

## ⑩

> "怎么回事？"那声音说。

> "大王！"一个小妖怪叫道，"外面来了个猴子。我们得把王后还给他，不然他要毁了我们的！"

  一个膀大腰圆的大妖怪从洞里走了出来。妖怪脖子上挂着三个铃铛。

> "我是赛太岁！"妖怪大叫，"滚出我的山！"

## ⑪

  悟空怒火中烧。

> "你知道我是谁吗？我是齐天大圣——"

  呼！一股黄沙扑面而来，烟雾弥漫，悟空睁不开眼睛。猴子咳嗽不止，沙土灌进他的眼睛和鼻子。

> "太可恶了！"悟空大喊。

  他捂住脸，跳下了山。

# Journey to the West · Chapter Eighty-Five: Magic Bells

## ①

  Outside the cave, Wukong shouted. He shouted all kinds of insults about the Demon of Power.

  Inside the cave, the guard woke up. He ran to the demon's bedroom.

> "Master! The monkey is back!" cried the guard.

> "It's the middle of the night," said the demon. "What does he want?"

## ②

> "He said we must return the Queen!" said the guard. "If we don't, he'll smash our entire mountain! He also yelled some terrible things about you!"

  Ah! The Demon of Power climbed out of bed and grabbed three bells.

> "I'll blow that monkey away with my fire, smoke, and sand again!"

  She tied the bells around her neck and went outside.

## ③

  The demon glared at Wukong.

> "Go away! I'm sleeping!"

> "Return the Queen!" shouted the monkey.

> "Never!" said the demon. She reached for the bells around her neck.

  Wukong pretended to be surprised.

> "Oh! I have bells just like those!"

## ④

  The demon squinted at the monkey.

> "I doubt your bells are like mine!"

> "Let me see them!"

  Wukong held up the bells. The demon peered at them for a moment.

> "Those bells do look like mine! But my bells are magic!"

> "So am I," said Wukong. "My bells can make fire, smoke, and sand!"

## ⑤

  The demon smiled.

> "That's interesting!"

  Wukong smiled.

> "My bells can do that too."

> "Really?" The Demon of Power looked surprised. "Let's compare bells to see whose work better."

> "Okay," said Wukong. "You go first."

## ⑥

> "Ah! I was planning to!" said the demon.

  He shook his bells. Nothing happened.

  He shook the bells again. Again, nothing happened.

> "That's strange," the demon mumbled. He looked closely at the bells. "These bells work fine yesterday!"

  Wukong tried not to laugh.

> "I'm sorry. Let's see if my bells work," he said.

## ⑦
