# Journey to the West · Chapter Ninety-Nine: The Monster's Cave

## ①

  "Who's down there now?" the monster yelled from inside the cave.

  Bajie fell to his knees and cried, tears streaming from his eyes.

> "I can't believe you actually believed that monster!" Wukong frowned at his companions.

  He sighed.

> "Wait here," said the monkey.

## ②

  The monkey turned into a moth and flew into the cave. He soon found the Tang monk tied up in a dark room. Wukong turned back into himself.

> "Wukong!" cried the Tang monk.

> "Shhh!" The monkey untied the monk. "We must be quiet!"

## ③

  Wukong recited a spell. A moment later, the sound of snoring drifted into the room.

> "My spell worked on the monsters and demons," said the monkey. "Let's go!"

  Wukong and the monk came out of the cave. Bajie and Wujing were thrilled.

> "Master! We thought you'd been captured!" said Bajie.

## ④

> "I knew he was fine," said Wukong. "Now I'm going to make sure these villains never bother anyone again."

  He pulled out his iron bar and willed it until it was the size of a very tall tree.

  *CRUSH!* With one swing, Wukong destroyed the entire cave. Rocks exploded and fell on top of one another. Wukong looked at the rubble and smiled.

## ⑤

  Weeks went by and the travelers arrived in a small town. Bajie's stomach growled loudly.

> "I guess we should look for food," laughed Wukong.

  They saw an old monk walking down a street.

> "Kind monk," said the Tang monk, "do you know where we can beg for some food? We are quite hungry."

## ⑥

  The old monk nodded.

> "Go to Squire Kou's house. The squire is about to feed ten thousand Buddhist monks. He will surely give you some food."

  He gave the Tang monk directions to the house.

> "Thank you," said the Tang monk.

## ⑦

  The travelers arrived at the Squire's estate and a servant let them in. The Squire's house was very large and fancy. Squire Kou came outside.

> "Greetings," he said with a smile. "Please come inside."

  The travelers sat with the Squire in a large room. A servant brought tea and snacks.

> "Thank you for inviting us in, Squire," said the Tang monk. "We heard that you made a vow to feed ten thousand monks."

## ⑧

> "Yes," said the Squire. "I've made plenty of money during my life, but I wanted to do good deeds as well. I hope to be reborn one day as a bodhisattva or even a Buddha."

> "Wow, Squire," said Bajie. "Today's your lucky day. I can easily eat as much food as ten thousand monks. So if you feed me, you'll definitely become a Buddha."

## ⑨

  Everybody laughed.

> "If it is my lucky day," said the Squire, "last night, I checked to see how many monks I've fed. So far, I've fed nine thousand nine hundred ninety-nine monks. I need to feed only four more in order to fulfill my vow."

  A smile spread across his face.

> "And there are four of you."

## ⑩

  That evening, Squire Kou held a feast. Everybody in the town was invited. The travelers sat with the Squire and his wife, Lady Kou. Bajie's eyes darted at all of the wonderful food on the table.

  Noodles, buns, mushrooms — he didn't know what to choose!

  As they ate, Squire Kou leaned toward the Tang monk.

> "So, where are you and your companions going?"

## ⑪

> "We're traveling to the Western Paradise," said the Tang monk. "We're going to fetch the true scriptures from Buddha."

  The Squire's eyes lit up.

> "You are special guests. I can't let you leave."

---

# 🇨🇳 第九十九章：魔怪之洞

## ①

  "里面是谁？"怪物在洞穴里大叫道。

  八戒跪在地上大哭起来，眼泪从眼眶中流出来。

> "我真不敢相信你们居然相信了那个怪物！"悟空对同伴们皱起了眉头。

  他叹了口气。

> "在这儿等着，"猴子说。

## ②

  猴子变成一只飞蛾飞进了洞穴。他很快发现唐僧被绑在一个黑暗的房间里。悟空现出了原形。

> "悟空！"唐僧叫道。

> "嘘——"猴子给唐僧松了绑，"我们一定要安静！"

## ③

  悟空念了一道咒语。过了一会儿，鼾声传进了房间。

> "我的法术让妖怪和妖魔都睡着了，"猴子说，"我们走吧！"

  悟空和唐僧走出了洞穴。八戒和悟净激动不已。

> "师父！我们还以为您被抓了！"八戒说。

## ④

> "我早就知道他没事的，"悟空说，"现在我要确保这些坏蛋再也不会骚扰任何人了。"

  他掏出铁棒一挥，铁棒变得像一棵非常高大的树一样粗。

  *轰隆！*悟空一棒扫平了整座洞穴。岩石爆裂塌方，互相压在一起。悟空看着废墟，微微笑了。

## ⑤

  几周过去了，一行旅人来到了一个小镇。八戒的肚子咕噜噜地大声叫了起来。

> "我想我们该去找点吃的了，"悟空笑着說。

  他们看到一位老和尚正沿街走来。

> "善良的师父，"唐僧说，"您知道我们去哪里可以讨到一些食物吗？我们非常饿。"

## ⑥

  老和尚点了点头。

> "去寇员外家吧。员外正要款待一万个僧人。他一定会给你们食物的。"

  他为唐僧指了去员外家的路。

> "谢谢您，"唐僧说。

## ⑦

  一行旅人来到了寇员外的府邸，一个仆人让他们进去了。员外的宅院十分宽敞华丽。寇员外走了出来。

> "欢迎欢迎，"他笑着说，"请进来坐。"

  旅人和员外一起坐在大厅里。一个仆人端上了茶和点心。

> "感谢员外邀请我们，"唐僧说，"听说您发愿要款待一万个僧人。"

## ⑧

> "是的，"员外说，"我这辈子赚了不少钱，但我也想做善事。我希望有一天能转世做菩萨，甚至成佛。"

> "哎呀，员外，"八戒说，"今天是您的幸运日啊。我一顿就能吃下一万个僧人的饭量。您请了我，保准您能成佛。"

## ⑨

  大家都笑了。

> "如果今天真是我的幸运日，"员外说，"昨晚我查了一下已经款待了多少僧人。到现在为止，我已经款待了九千九百九十九个僧人。我只要再请四个就能圆愿了。"

  他脸上露出了笑容。

> "而你们正好是四个。"

## ⑩

  那天晚上，寇员外设宴席款待，镇上的人都来赴宴。旅人和员外及员外的妻子寇夫人一起用餐。八戒的眼睛盯着桌上所有佳肴，馋得不得了。

  面条、包子、蘑菇——他都不知道该选什么好！

  吃着吃着，寇员外凑近唐僧。

> "请问你们要去哪里？"

## ⑪

> "我们要去西天，"唐僧说，"我们要去佛祖那里取真经。"

  员外的双眼明亮了起来。

> "你们是我的贵客，我可不能让你们走。"

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred: A Terrible Robbery

## ①

  For over a month, the travelers stayed at Squire Kou's house. Every time they tried to leave, the Squire begged them to stay longer. Finally, one morning during breakfast, the Tang monk insisted on leaving.

> "We'll never fetch the true scriptures if we stay here."

## ②

> "Please, don't leave!" said Squire Kou. "You are very important monks. Having you as guests is a good deed."

> "I'd like to stay here," said Bajie. He took a bite of a peach. "No — Master's right," said Bajie. "We must continue our journey."

## ③

  Lady Kou grew angry.

> "You monks are ungrateful. We have fed you and taken care of you. Yet you can't wait to leave."

> "We are very grateful," said the Tang monk. "But we cannot stay any longer."

## ④

  After breakfast, Wujing got the horse from Squire Kou's stable. Bajie gathered the bags. The Tang monk bade Squire and Lady Kou farewell, and the travelers headed west.

> "They are ungrateful," muttered Lady Kou.

## ⑤

  The next morning, Lady Kou ran into the town's courthouse. Tears filled her eyes.

> "I must speak with the judge," she cried.

  The judge rushed to her.

> "Lady Kou, what's wrong?"

## ⑥

> "Robbers broke into our house last night," said Lady Kou breathlessly. "They stole many valuable items and two of our horses. Squire Kou tried to stop them, but the robbers — they killed my husband."

  Lady Kou burst into tears. The judge gasped.

> "Oh no! Did you see the robbers?"

## ⑦

  Lady Kou sniffed.

> "Yes. And I know who they are."

> "Who are they?" asked the judge.

  Lady Kou gritted her teeth.

> "The Tang monk and his companions."

## ⑧

  The judge turned to a soldier.

> "Gather some soldiers and arrest the Tang monk and his companions."

> "I'm glad we're headed west again," said the Tang monk as the travelers walked. "I'm eager to reach the Western Paradise."

  Wujing nodded.

> "We were delayed at Squire Kou's house for too long."

  Bajie snorted.

> "We should have stayed longer."

## ⑨

  Suddenly a group of men stepped onto the road. They carried swords and axes. Their horses carried several large bundles.

> "Give us your money!" shouted one of them.

  Wujing pulled out his iron bar.

> "Wujing," said the Tang monk. "Remember, you must not harm people."

> "I'm just going to talk to them, Master," Wujing smiled.

## ⑩

  He turned to the man who had shouted.

> "We have no money."

> "No money, huh?" said the man. "Then we're going to beat up all of you."

  Wujing laughed.

> "You don't realize who I am. I'm Sha Wujing, who served the Curtain-Lifting General in heaven."

> "We don't care who you are," said the man. "We're dangerous robbers. Last night we robbed a very wealthy squire."

## ⑪

  The Tang monk raised his eyebrows.

> "The squire..."

  Wukong quickly recited a spell, which froze the robbers. Wujing rushed to the horses and opened one of the bundles. Inside were dishes, jewels, and other valuable items.

## ⑫

> "These items belong to Squire Kou," Wujing gasped. "So do the horses."

  The Tang monk bit his lip.

> "Squire Kou is a good man. We must return his belongings."

  Everyone agreed. Wukong recited another spell and the robbers became unfrozen. The monkey grew large, and fire burned in his eyes.

## ⑬

> "Get out of here!" he thundered. "And never steal again!"

  The robbers screamed and ran away. The travelers headed back toward town with the Squire's horses. Soon they saw a group of soldiers on horseback.

> "Those soldiers are riding toward us," said Wujing.

> "I wonder what they want," said the Tang monk.

## ⑭

  One of the soldiers pointed a sword at the travelers.

> "Stop, thieves! You're all under arrest."

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百章：可怕的劫案

## ①

  一行人在寇员外家住了一个多月。每次他们想走，员外都苦苦挽留。一天早上吃早饭的时候，唐僧坚决说要走。

> "再待下去，我们就永远取不到真经了。"

## ②

> "求求你们，别走！"寇员外说，"你们是不凡的僧人。留你们做客也是做善事。"

> "我倒想留在这里，"八戒咬了一口桃子。"不过——师父说得对，"八戒说，"我们得继续赶路了。"

## ③

  寇夫人恼了起来。

> "你们这些僧人真是忘恩负义。我们管你们吃管你们住，你们却急着想走。"

> "我们非常感激，"唐僧说，"但我们不能再待下去了。"

## ④

  吃完早饭，悟净到马厩牵马。八戒收拾包裹。唐僧辞别了寇员外和寇夫人，一行往西出发。

> "他们真是忘恩负义，"寇夫人嘟囔着。

## ⑤

  第二天一早，寇夫人跑到了镇上的公堂。她眼中含着泪。

> "我要见大人！"她哭喊着。

  县官急忙迎出来。

> "寇夫人，怎么了？"

## ⑥

> "昨晚有强盗闯进了我们家，"寇夫人气喘吁吁地说，"他们偷了许多贵重财物和两匹马。寇员外想拦他们，可那些强盗——他们把我丈夫杀了。"

  寇夫人放声大哭。县官倒抽一口冷气。

> "天哪！你看清那些强盗了吗？"

## ⑦

  寇夫人擦了擦眼泪。

> "看清楚了，我知道他们是谁。"

> "他们是谁？"县官问道。

  寇夫人咬了咬牙。

> "就是那个唐僧和他的徒弟们。"

## ⑧

  县官转身对一个士兵下令。

> "带人立刻去抓捕唐僧和他的徒弟们！"

> "这次我们又往西走了，真高兴，"唐僧一行人走在路上说，"我迫不及待想到西天了。"

  悟净点了点头。

> "我们在寇员外家耽误太久了。"

  八戒哼了一声。

> "真该再多住几天。"

## ⑨

  突然，一伙人拦住了去路。他们手持刀斧，马背上驮着几个大包裹。

> "把钱交出来！"其中一个人大叫着。

  悟净抽出了降妖宝杖。

> "悟净，"唐僧说，"记住，万万不可伤人。"

> "我只是和他们说说话，师父，"悟净微微一笑。

## ⑩

  他转向那个大叫的人。

> "我们没有钱。"

> "没钱，是吧？"那汉子说，"那我们就要把你们统统打一顿。"

  悟净哈哈大笑。

> "你们不知道我的厉害。我曾在天庭做卷帘大将。"

> "不管你是谁，"那汉子说，"我们是厉害的强盗。昨晚我们抢了一个非常有钱的员外。"

## ⑪

  唐僧挑了挑眉毛。

> "员外家……"

  悟空立刻念了一道定身法，把强盗们定住了。悟净冲到马旁，打开一个包裹，里面是器皿、珠宝等各种贵重物品。

## ⑫

> "这些东西都是寇员外家的，"悟净惊呼道，"马也是他的。"

  唐僧咬了咬嘴唇。

> "寇员外是个好人。我们必须把东西还给他。"

  大家一致同意。悟空又念了一道解咒，强盗们恢复了自由。猴子现出法天象地，眼中冒火。

## ⑬

> "快滚！"他喝斥道，"今后再不可做强盗！"

  强盗们惨叫一声，落荒而逃。一行旅人牵着员外的马返回镇上。不久他们看见一队骑马的士兵。

> "那些士兵正朝我们过来，"悟净说。

> "不知他们要做什么，"唐僧说。

## ⑭

  一个士兵用剑指着旅人们。

> "站住，盗贼！你们全被捕了！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and One: Arrested

## ①

> "This is ridiculous," said the Tang monk. "Why are we under arrest?"

  Soldiers were bringing the travelers back to the town.

> "You robbed Squire Kou's house last night," said one of the soldiers.

> "What?" cried Bajie. "We would never rob somebody. Especially not the Squire. He was kind to us."

## ②

> "You had all the stolen items," replied the soldier. "You also had the two horses that were stolen from his stable."

> "We got everything from the real robbers," said the Tang monk. "We were going to return it all to Squire Kou."

  The soldier laughed.

> "Oh, you got everything from the real robbers. Tell me — where are the real robbers now?"

## ③

> "I let them go," said Wukong.

  The soldier laughed again.

> "Oh, that was very kind of you."

  Wukong could tell that the soldier didn't believe him. By now they had reached the town. A crowd of people had gathered to watch. The soldiers brought the travelers into the courthouse.

## ④

  The judge frowned at the monk and the others.

  *Clang!* The lock shut on the cell door.

> "This is a mistake," the Tang monk pleaded. "We can't go to jail. We're making an important journey to visit Buddha."

## ⑤

  The judge shook his head.

> "Buddha doesn't allow killers in the Western Paradise."

> "Killers?" said Wujing. "What are you talking about?"

> "You killed Squire Kou," said the judge.

  The Tang monk's face went pale.

> "The Squire is dead?"

## ⑥

  The judge narrowed his eyes at the monk. The travelers were shoved into a jail cell and the door was slammed shut.

> "This is terrible," the monk started to cry.

> "Lady Kou framed us," said Wujing. "But why?"

> "I'll find out tonight," promised Wukong.

## ⑦

  The Tang monk looked grateful.

> "We must prove our innocence."

  That night Wukong turned into a bee and flew out of the jail to Squire Kou's house. He found Lady Kou mourning over a coffin. The monkey changed back into himself and hid behind a curtain.

  Imitating the Squire's voice, he said:

## ⑧

> "My lady, it's me — your husband."

  Lady Kou's eyes went wide.

> "Is it really you?"

> "Yes," said Wukong.

> "Why did you tell the judge that the Tang monk and his companions killed me?"

## ⑨

  Lady Kou hesitated.

> "I was angry with them. You wanted them to stay here, but they insisted on leaving. That was an insult to us."

> "You have done a terrible thing!" thundered Wukong.

  The walls of the house shook and Lady Kou trembled.

## ⑩

  The monkey continued.

> "Tomorrow you must tell the judge that the Tang monk and his companions are innocent. If you don't, I will haunt you for the rest of your life."

  Tears poured from the woman's eyes.

> "I will talk to the judge tomorrow. I promise. Please don't haunt me."

## ⑪

  Wukong flew back to the courthouse. He saw the judge sitting at a desk reading some papers. Wukong flew over the roof, then he turned into an enormous spirit body and lowered one foot.

  When the judge saw the giant foot, he gasped. The papers fell from his hands.

## ⑫

  Wukong's voice boomed.

> "I am the wandering spirit, and I will send you to see Buddha! Lady Kou lied to you. The Tang monk did not kill Squire Kou. He is on an important journey. If you don't free him and his companions, I will lower my other foot. Then I will stomp all over this town until there is nothing more."

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零一章：被捕

## ①

> "这太荒唐了，"唐僧说，"为什么要把我们抓起来？"

  士兵们押着旅人返回镇上。

> "你们昨晚抢劫了寇员外的家，"一个士兵说。

> "什么？"八戒大叫，"我们才不会抢劫。更不会抢劫寇员外。他对我们那么好。"

## ②

> "赃物全在你们手上，"士兵回答说，"从他们家偷的两匹马也在你们手上。"

> "这些东西是从真正的强盗那里得来的，"唐僧说，"我们正准备把东西全部还给寇员外。"

  士兵大笑。

> "哦，从真正的强盗那里得来的。那我倒要问——真正的强盗现在在哪里？"

## ③

> "我放了他们。"悟空说。

  士兵又笑了。

> "哦，你可真够仁慈的呀。"

  悟空看得出士兵根本不信他们。到了镇上，街上已经围满了看热闹的人。士兵把旅人押进了公堂。

## ④

  县官一脸怒色地瞪着唐僧等人。

  锁链锁上了牢房的门。

> "这真是一场误会，"唐僧恳求说，"我们不能坐牢啊。我们正在赶路去拜见佛祖。"

## ⑤

  县官摇了摇头。

> "佛祖可不容许杀人犯进入西天。"

> "杀人犯？"悟净说，"你在说什么？"

> "你们杀了寇员外，"县官说。

  唐僧脸色苍白。

> "员外死了？"

## ⑥

  县官瞪视着唐僧，旅人被推进了牢房，牢门"砰"的一声关上了。

> "这太糟了，"唐僧哭了起来。

> "是寇夫人诬陷了我们，"悟净说，"可她为什么要这样做？"

> "我今晚就去查明真相。"悟空说。

## ⑦

  唐僧感激地看着悟空。

> "我们必须证明自己的清白。"

  到了夜里，悟空变成一只蜜蜂飞出牢房，飞到了寇员外家。他看见寇夫人正对着一口棺材哭泣。猴子又变回原形，躲在帘子后面。

  他模仿着员外的声音说：

## ⑧

> "夫人，是我——你的丈夫。"

  寇夫人大惊失色。

> "真的是你吗？"

> "是我，"悟空说。

> "你为什么去公堂对大人说唐僧师徒杀了我？"

## ⑨

  寇夫人犹豫了。

> "我对他们生气。你想留他们多住几天，他们却偏要走。这不是不给我们面子吗？"

> "你做了一件大恶事！"悟空声如雷霆。

  房屋四壁摇晃，寇夫人吓得浑身发抖。

## ⑩

  猴子继续说道。

> "明天你必须到县官面前说唐僧师徒是清白的。如果你不去，我下半辈子都会缠着你。"

  泪水从寇夫人眼中滚滚流出。

> "我明天就去向县官禀明真相。我保证。求求你别来缠我。"

## ⑪

  悟空飞回县衙。他看见县官正坐在桌子前看文书。悟空从屋顶上飞过，然后变为一个巨大的灵体形象，把一只大脚伸到了屋顶上。

  县官看到那只大脚，倒抽了一口冷气。手中的文书撒落一地。

## ⑫

  悟空声音如雷。

> "我是游荡的英魂，我要带你去见佛祖！是寇夫人对你说了谎。唐僧并未杀害寇员外，他正在去西天取经的路上。如果你不立刻释放唐僧师徒，我就把另一只脚也踩下来。我会踏平这座城镇，不留一物！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Two: The Prisoners Are Released

## ①

  Lady Kou ran into the courthouse early the next morning. With tears in her eyes, she told the judge that she had lied the day before.

> "The Tang monk and his companions are innocent," Lady Kou sniffed. "Please release them."

  The judge nodded.

> "I was going to release the prisoners this morning."

  He explained how the wandering spirit had visited him the night before.

## ②

  Lady Kou gasped.

> "My husband visited me last night!"

> "We must release the prisoners at once."

  They hurried to the Tang monk's cell. A guard swung open the cell door.

> "I'm glad to be out of there," said Wujing.

> "Me too," said Bajie with a yawn. "The beds were very uncomfortable."

## ③

  Lady Kou bowed to the Tang monk.

> "I framed you for killing my husband. It was a terrible thing to do. Please forgive me."

  The Tang monk put his hand on Wukong's shoulder.

> "Don't yell, Wukong."

  He looked at Lady Kou.

> "We forgive you. The Squire was a kind man. His death is a terrible tragedy."

## ④

  Wukong rubbed his chin.

> "I can probably bring him back to life."

  Lady Kou and the judge were shocked.

> "Can you really do that?" asked Lady Kou.

## ⑤

  The Tang monk smiled.

> "Yes, he can. Wukong brought the King of the Black Rooster Kingdom back to life."

  He turned to the monkey.

> "The sage Laozi helped you that time. Will you ask him for help again?"

> "No," said Wukong. "Laozi doesn't really like me. I'll go to the Land of Darkness and talk to the judge of the dead instead."

## ⑥

  When Wukong entered the palace of darkness, the judge of the dead frowned.

> "Why are you here, Wukong? You already made yourself immortal by crossing out your name in the directory."

  Wukong laughed.

> "I wondered if you would remember that. I'm looking for Squire Kou's name."

> "Squire Kou!" The judge opened the directory and flipped through some pages.

## ⑦

> "Ah, yes. He died two days ago. You know — he works for the Bodhisattva Ksitigarbha in the Jade Palace. It's here in the Land of Darkness."

  Wukong went to the Jade Palace.

> "Greetings, Sun Wukong," said the Bodhisattva.

> "Greetings, Bodhisattva." The monkey bowed.

## ⑧

> "Two nights ago, a friend of mine — Squire Kou — was killed up there on Earth. I would like to bring him back."

  The Bodhisattva raised an eyebrow.

> "You want him to return to life?"

> "Yes," said Wukong. "I'm helping the Tang monk reach the Western Paradise to fetch the true scriptures. The Squire was very kind to us."

## ⑨

  The Bodhisattva smiled.

> "Very well. The Squire may return to Earth until it's time for him to come back here."

  The Bodhisattva brought Wukong to an office. Squire Kou was sitting behind a large desk smiling as he studied some documents. His eyes sparked with light when he saw Wukong.

## ⑩

> "It's good to see you, Wukong," said the Squire. "What are you doing here?"

> "I have good news," said the monkey. "Your life isn't over yet. I'm taking you back to Earth."

  The Squire looked confused. He glanced at the Bodhisattva. The Bodhisattva nodded.

> "You may return to Earth. When your life is over, you will return to your job here."

## ⑪

  The Squire came out from behind his desk and bowed.

> "Thank you, Bodhisattva. I am happy here, but I would love to see my wife and friends again."

  Wukong moved closer to the Squire.

> "You'll be home soon, Squire."

  The monkey recited a spell and the Squire vanished.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零二章：释囚

## ①

  第二天一早，寇夫人跑到公堂上，含着泪水告诉县官她昨天撒了谎。

> "唐僧和他的徒弟们是清白的，"寇夫人抽噎着，"请您放了他们。"

  县官点了点头。

> "我本来就打算今天一早释放他们。"

  他告诉寇夫人，昨晚一位游荡的鬼魂曾拜访过他。

## ②

  寇夫人大惊。

> "我丈夫昨晚来托梦给我了！"

> "我们必须立刻释放囚犯。"

  他们急忙赶到唐僧的牢房前。一个狱卒打开牢门。

> "终于能出来了，"悟净说。

> "是啊，"八戒打了个哈欠，"床太不舒服了。"

## ③

  寇夫人向唐僧鞠躬。

> "我诬告您杀了我丈夫。这是我做的一件大恶事。请您原谅我。"

  唐僧把手放在悟空肩上。

> "悟空，别冲动。"

  他看着寇夫人。

> "我们原谅你。员外是个好心人。他的死是一场大悲剧。"

## ④

  悟空摸了摸下巴。

> "我大概能让他起死回生。"

  寇夫人和县官都大吃一惊。

> "你真的能做到吗？"寇夫人问道。

## ⑤

  唐僧微笑了。

> "能做到的。悟空曾把乌鸡国的国王救活过。"

  他转向猴子。

> "那次是太上老君帮了你。这次你再去请他帮忙好吗？"

> "不必了，"悟空说，"太上老君不太喜欢我。我还是去地府跟阎王谈吧。"

## ⑥

  悟空来到阴司的幽冥殿，阎王皱起了眉头。

> "悟空，你来做什么？你不是早就从生死簿上勾了名字，成了不死之身吗？"

  悟空笑了。

> "我猜你还记得那件事。我来查一下寇员外的名字。"

> "寇员外！"阎王打开生死簿，翻了几页。

## ⑦

> "啊，找到了。他两天前死的。他现在在地藏菩萨那里做文书，就在这幽冥界。"

  悟空去了地藏菩萨的玉宇宫。

> "悟空，欢迎，"地藏菩萨说。

> "菩萨好。"猴子行了礼。

## ⑧

> "两天前，我的一个好朋友寇员外在阳间被害。我想请菩萨让他还阳。"

  地藏菩萨挑了挑眉毛。

> "你要他回阳间？"

> "是的，"悟空说，"我正在帮唐僧去西天取经。寇员外对我们非常好。"

## ⑨

  地藏菩萨微笑了。

> "好吧。寇员外可以返回阳间，等到阳寿尽了再回这里来。"

  地藏菩萨带悟空来到一间公房。寇员外正坐在一张大桌前，微笑着审阅文书。他看到悟空，眼中闪出欣喜的光。

## ⑩

> "悟空，见到你真好，"员外说，"你怎么来了？"

> "有个好消息，"猴子说，"你的阳寿还没尽呢，我来带你回阳间。"

  员外一脸困惑，他看了看地藏菩萨。菩萨点了点头。

> "你可以回阳间了。等到阳寿尽了，你再回到这里来上班。"

## ⑪

  员外从桌后走出来，行了一个大礼。

> "感谢菩萨。我在这里很安稳，但我实在想念妻子和亲友们。"

  悟空靠近员外。

> "员外，你马上就能回家了。"

  猴子念了一道咒语，员外便消失了。

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Three: Wukong Returns to the Land of Darkness

## ①

> "The Squire is coming back to life!" said the Tang monk.

  Squire Kou sat up and smiled inside his coffin. Wukong had leaned over the coffin and recited a spell.

  Lady Kou gasped as color returned to her husband's face.

> "It's working!" cried Wujing.

## ②

  Bajie licked his lips.

> "Maybe the Squire will thank us with a big feast!"

  Squire Kou sat up and smiled.

> "Thank you, Wukong."

  He climbed out of the coffin and turned to his wife. Tears filled her eyes, and the two embraced.

## ③

  That night, Squire Kou and Lady Kou held a feast to thank Wukong. And the next morning, they let the travelers leave without any argument.

  *Click-clack, click-clack* — the horse's hooves sounded across the earth.

  The Tang monk and his companions travelled for many more months. Through rain and snow, heat and cold, they slowly continued west.

## ④

  One day, the road led into a beautiful land. There were flowers and magnificent trees. People smiled at the travelers and offered food. The Tang monk stared in amazement.

> "What is this place?"

> "We are in the Western Paradise," said Wukong. "We are very close."

## ⑤

  A woman held out a basket of plums. Bajie scooped up a handful.

> "I love this place!"

> "Look up ahead," said Wujing, pointing to a row of tall buildings. "It's an abbey."

  The road led through a large gate in the abbey wall. At the gate, the monk got down from his horse. A young man greeted them.

## ⑥

> "Are you the Tang monk?" asked the man.

> "Yes," said the monk. He waved towards the rest of the group. "And these are my —"

> "You finally arrived!" the man laughed. "I was starting to think that Bodhisattva Guanyin had tricked me. She told me you would arrive in a year or so. But that was over ten years ago."

## ⑦

  The Tang monk bowed.

> "Forgive me. I wanted to arrive much sooner, but we faced many dangers and delays along the way."

  Bajie snorted.

> "And this place wasn't very easy to find either."

## ⑧

  The man smiled.

> "There's no need to apologize. I'm the Great Immortal of the Golden Summit, and this abbey is my home. Beyond it lies the Western Paradise. Come inside and rest before you continue."

  Servants filled tubs with warm perfumed water, and the travelers took baths.

## ⑨

> "It feels so good to get clean," said Bajie. "I haven't had a bath in months."

  Wukong laughed.

> "Now we won't have to cover our noses when you're near."

  Bajie snorted and splashed water at Wukong. The monkey splashed back. Everyone laughed.

## ⑩

  After their baths, the Tang monk put on the Buddhist robe Guanyin had given them. Then the travelers enjoyed a large meal with the Immortal. Servants brought trays loaded with noodles, vegetables, tofu, and steamed buns.

## ⑪

  In the morning, the Immortal let the group out the back door of the abbey. The road continued west through a land even more beautiful and magical. Birds sang as animals leaped playfully through the flowers. Brilliant light sparkled on everything.

## ⑫

  In the distance stood a huge mountain, its peak hidden by clouds. The Tang monk stared silently at the mountain. Wukong put his hand on the monk's shoulder.

> "That's the Spirit Mountain, Master. We're almost at the end of our journey."

  A smile spread across the monk's face.

## ⑬

  The travelers thanked the Immortal. Filled with energy now, they hurried down the road. The steep slopes of the Spirit Mountain towered over them.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零三章：悟空重归幽冥界

## ①

  "员外还阳了！"唐僧叫道。悟空趴在棺材上念了一道还阳咒。

  寇员外在棺材里坐了起来，脸上露出了笑容。

  寇夫人惊叫着看着丈夫的脸色渐渐红润。

> "生效了！"悟净大喊。

## ②

  八戒舔了舔嘴唇。

> "说不定员外会用一顿大餐来谢谢我们呢！"

  寇员外坐起来，脸上带着笑。

> "悟空，谢谢你。"

  他从棺材里爬出来，转向妻子。寇夫人眼中泪光闪闪，两人紧紧拥抱在一起。

## ③

  那天晚上，寇员外和寇夫人设宴款待，以感谢悟空。第二天一早，他们没再挽留，送行者们上路了。

  *嗒嗒嗒，嗒嗒嗒*——马蹄声响彻大地。

  唐僧师徒又赶了许多个月的路。风雨无阻，寒暑交替，他们继续向西。

## ④

  一天，前方的道路通向了一片美丽的土地。到处是鲜花和奇树异木。人们微笑着向旅人们招手，还送食物给他们。唐僧目瞪口呆。

> "这是什么地方？"

> "我们已到西天了，"悟空说，"极乐世界近在眼前。"

## ⑤

  一个妇人端出一篮李子。八戒伸手抓了一大把。

> "我太喜欢这个地方了！"

> "看前面，"悟净指向一排高大的建筑，"是一座庵院。"

  道路穿过庵院的一扇大门。到了门口，唐僧下了马。一个年轻人出来迎接他们。

## ⑥

> "您就是唐僧吗？"那人问道。

> "是的，"唐僧说。他指向身后一行人。"这是我的——"

> "你们终于到了！"那人大笑起来，"我差点以为观音菩萨骗了我呢。她说你们一年左右就能到。可这已经是十多年前的事了！"

## ⑦

  唐僧鞠躬致歉。

> "请原谅。我本想早些到，但一路上遭遇了许多危险和耽搁。"

  八戒哼了一声。

> "再说了，也不好找啊。"

## ⑧

  那人笑了。

> "不用道歉。我是金顶大仙，这庵院就是我的家。庵院后面就是西天极乐世界了。你们先进来歇息一番再走吧。"

  侍从们端来了温热的香汤，旅人们美美地洗了个澡。

## ⑨

> "洗澡真舒服，"八戒说，"我可有好几个月没洗澡了。"

  悟空笑了笑。

> "这下你走近了我们也不用捂鼻子了。"

  八戒哼了一声，朝悟空泼水。悟空也泼了回去。大家哈哈大笑。

## ⑩

  洗完澡后，唐僧穿上了观音送的锦襕袈裟。旅人们和大仙一起享用了一顿丰盛的饭菜。侍从们端来了面条、蔬菜、豆腐和包子。

## ⑪

  第二天一早，大仙从庵院后门送一行人出去。道路继续向西延伸，沿途的土地更加美丽奇妙。鸟儿歌唱，小动物在花丛中欢蹦乱跳。万物闪耀着灿烂的光芒。

## ⑫

  远处矗立着一座巨大的山，山顶隐在云中。唐僧默默地注视着那座山。悟空把手放到唐僧肩上。

> "那就是灵山，师父。我们的旅程快到终点了。"

  唐僧脸上绽开了笑容。

## ⑬

  旅人们谢过了大仙。他们满怀能量，沿着道路快步赶路。灵山的陡峭山壁巍然矗立在他们面前。

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Four: The Tang Monk and the River

## ①

  Wukong and his companions walked through the Western Paradise. The road wove through a field of flowers and towards the Spirit Mountain.

  Bajie looked up at the huge mountain and shook his head.

> "Will it be easy to climb that?"

  Wukong laughed.

> "Don't ask me to carry you."

## ②

  The travelers soon arrived at a river with a strong current. Waves crashed into jagged rocks, spraying water everywhere.

> "This river looks dangerous," said Wujing. "But we must cross it to get to the Spirit Mountain."

  Bajie sighed.

> "We will never be able to cross this river safely. Let's just go home."

> "Nonsense," said Wukong. "Look over there."

## ③

  The monkey pointed upstream. A thin log lay across the river. It wobbled and shook as the water rushed under it. The Tang monk looked at the log.

> "Don't be silly, Wukong. We can't walk across that log. It's too thin, and it looks quite slippery."

> "But that log is the only way to reach the Spirit Mountain," said Wukong. "You must believe that it's safe. Watch me."

## ④

  The monkey hopped onto the log, ran across the river, and ran back.

> "See?" he said. "It's safe."

  Bajie snorted.

> "You don't weigh much, Wukong. But if I step on that log, it will break."

> "I believe Wukong," said Wujing. "We must walk across the log. Follow me, Master," said Wukong.

## ⑤

  He pulled the Tang monk towards the log. The monk trembled with fear.

> "I'll fall into the river and drown!" said the Tang monk.

> "Let's just fly over the river," suggested Bajie. "We can carry Master and the horse."

> "No," insisted Wukong.

## ⑥

> "The Tang monk must make the entire journey by himself. We're here to protect him, not to carry him. Buddha won't allow Master to have the true scriptures if he doesn't take every step himself. He can't take every step himself..."

## ⑦

  Just then an old man appeared in a boat.

> "I can take you across the river," said the man.

> "Thank you," said the Tang monk.

  He walked to the riverbank.

> "My companion wanted me to walk across that log, but —"

  The monk stopped.

> "There's something wrong with your boat. It has no bottom. Water is flowing right through it."

## ⑧

> "The boat is safe," said the man. "Please climb in. Buddha is waiting."

  With a bit more hesitation, the Tang monk stepped into the boat. He was shocked to find that he didn't sink. He sat on the edge of the boat as Wujing led the horse aboard. Bajie and Wukong followed. The boat glided swiftly across the river.

## ⑨

  Suddenly there was a splash. The Tang monk looked at the water and saw a body floating downstream. He screamed.

> "A man is drowning!"

  Wukong put his hand on the monk's shoulder and smiled.

> "It's you, Master."

## ⑩

> "Who asked?" said the monk. "Me?"

> "Well, Wukong is right!" cried Bajie. "It is you. Look again, Master," said Wujing, smiling.

## ⑪

  The Tang monk looked at the body more carefully. It was wearing the same Buddhist robe that he was wearing.

> "It's me," said the monk quietly. "But how?"

> "You got rid of your mortal body, Master," said Wukong. "You're a spirit now. You're one of us."

  Bajie beamed.

## ⑫

  The boat soon reached the other riverbank and the travelers stepped out. The boat and the old man vanished.

  The Tang monk laughed in amazement.

> "I feel so alive," he said. "I feel like I could run right up this mountain."

> "Good," said Bajie. "Perhaps you could carry me."

  Everybody laughed as they continued up the mountain.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零四章：唐僧与渡河

## ①

  悟空和徒伴们走在西天的路上。小路穿过一片花海，通向灵山。

  八戒抬头望着巨大的山峰，摇了摇头。

> "那山好爬吗？"

  悟空哈哈大笑。

> "可别指望我背你啊。"

## ②

  旅人们很快来到了一条水流湍急的大河边，波浪拍打着嶙峋的巨石，水花四溅。

> "这条河看起来很危险，"悟净说，"但我们必须过了河才能到灵山。"

  八戒叹了口气。

> "我们永远也过不去。还是回家算了。"

> "胡说，"悟空说，"看那边。"

## ③

  猴子朝上游指去。一根细木头横跨在河面上。急流从下面冲过，木头晃晃悠悠。唐僧看了看那根木头。

> "悟净，别开玩笑了。这么细一根木头怎么走得过去？而且看起来滑得很。"

> "但这是通往灵山的唯一道路，"悟空说，"你一定要相信它是安全的。看我走给你看。"

## ④

  猴子跳上木头，跑过了河又跑回来。

> "看到了吧？"他说，"安全得很。"

  八戒哼了一声。

> "你这么轻，没问题的。可我要是一脚踩上去，这根木头就断了。"

> "我相信悟空，"悟净说，"我们必须从这根木头上走过去。"

## ⑤

  他拉着唐僧朝木头走去。唐僧吓得浑身发抖。

> "我会掉进河里淹死的！"唐僧说。

> "我们直接飞过去吧，"八戒提议说，"我们带着师父和马一起飞。"

> "不行，"悟空坚持道。

## ⑥

> "唐僧必须自己走完这全程。我们是来保护他的，不是来背他的。如果师父不自己走完每一步，佛祖是不会让他拿到真经的。"

## ⑦

  就在此时，一位老者驾着一叶小舟出现了。

> "我可以载你们过河，"老者说。

> "谢谢您。"唐僧说着走到了河岸边。

> "我的同伴想让我从那根木头上走过去，可是——"

  唐僧顿住了。

> "你的船没有底啊。水直接从船底穿过来了。"

## ⑧

> "船是安全的，"老者说，"请上来吧。佛祖还在等着呢。"

  唐僧犹豫了一下，踏进了船里。他惊讶地发现自己并没有沉下去。他坐在船边，悟净牵着马上了船。八戒和悟空也跟着上船。小船轻快地滑过了河面。

## ⑨

  突然传来"扑通"一声。唐僧往河里一看，看见一具尸体顺流漂下。他尖叫起来。

> "有人淹死了！"

  悟空把手搭在唐僧肩上，微微笑了。

> "师父，那就是你。"

## ⑩

> "谁呀？"唐僧说，"我？"

> "没错，悟空说得对！"八戒大叫道，"那就是你。师父，您再仔细看看，"悟净笑着说。

## ⑪

  唐僧再仔细一看那具尸体。尸体身上穿的正和他一样的僧袍。

> "真的是我，"唐僧轻声说，"可这是怎么回事？"

> "师父，您已经脱去了凡胎肉体，"悟空说，"您现在是仙体了。和我们一样了。"

  八戒乐开了花。

## ⑫

  小船很快到了对岸，旅人们踏出了小船。小舟和老者都不见了踪影。

  唐僧惊奇地大笑了起来。

> "我感觉身轻如燕，"他说，"我觉得自己能一口气跑上这座山。"

> "那太好了，"八戒说，"说不定您能背我上去。"

  大家哈哈大笑，继续向山上走去。

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Five: The Thunderclap Monastery

## ①

  The travelers walked up the Spirit Mountain. The mountain slopes were covered in pine trees, bamboo, and flowers. Birds sang and small animals ran by.

  The Tang monk stopped walking and turned to his companions.

> "I want to thank you all," said the monk. "You have helped me to reach the Western Paradise. You saved me from demons countless times. I couldn't have gotten here without you."

## ②

  Wukong laughed.

> "You don't need to thank us, Master. We all help each other. You helped me to be good. Now I will earn forgiveness for the evil things I did long ago."

  Wujing nodded.

> "And I will earn forgiveness for breaking that glass vase in heaven."

> "I will earn forgiveness for causing trouble in heaven too," added Bajie. He waved a hand toward the horse. "And remember, that horse is really a dragon."

## ③

> "He accidentally sent rain to his father's palace. He too will earn forgiveness."

  Wujing smiled.

> "See, Master? We are all thankful."

## ④

  They continued up the mountain and were soon surrounded by clouds.

  Bright light shone from the Thunderclap Monastery above. The travelers arrived at a northern gate where two guards stood. Beyond the gate, the Thunderclap Monastery towers and archway sparkled with bright light.

> "Greetings," said the monk to the guards. "I am the Tang monk, and I am here to receive the true scriptures from Buddha."

> "You may enter," said one of the guards.

## ⑤

  The Tang monk and his companions reached a large hall. Buddha sat at the opposite end of the hall. Other Buddhas and bodhisattvas stood behind him. Guanyin was standing next to Buddha and smiling. The travelers bowed.

> "Congratulations," said Buddha. "You have all traveled far and faced many challenges. You have done well."

  Wukong's heart swelled. He wiped tears from his eye.

## ⑥

> "Thank you," said the Tang monk. "It was an honor to make the journey."

  Servants brought a meal to the travelers. When the travelers were done eating, a guard led them to a large room filled with magical light and mist. Wooden chests lined the walls.

## ⑦

> "Marvelous," the Tang monk murmured.

> "The true scriptures are written on these scrolls," said the guard.

  He picked out three scrolls and handed them to the Tang monk. Speechless, the monk gazed at the scrolls. Then he handed them to Wujing and Bajie. The two spirits carefully wrapped the scrolls and placed them in a bag.

## ⑧

  Once again the travelers bowed before Buddha.

> "Take the true scriptures back to the Tang Empire," said Buddha.

> "Another long journey," Bajie murmured.

> "Stop complaining, Bajie," whispered Wukong.

> "Don't tell me what to do," Bajie whispered back.

> "Both of you stop arguing," whispered Wujing.

## ⑨

  Buddha was still talking.

> "The scriptures will teach the people there to be good and to treat each other kindly. But take good care of the scriptures. They are extremely valuable. Once you have delivered them, you shall come back here to receive your awards."

## ⑩

> "Where are you, Buddha?" said Wukong. "We will protect the scriptures with our lives."

  A guard offered to carry the travelers to the Tang Empire.

> "Thank you," said the Tang monk.

> "I'll hold on tight," said Bajie.

  The guard recited a spell and then flew out of the monastery with the travelers.

## ⑪

  Buddha turned to Guanyin.

> "The Tang monk and his companions have done well."

  Guanyin nodded.

> "Wukong especially has learned a lot during the journey. He isn't violent anymore. I believe he is now a good Buddhist."

## ⑫

  Just then a messenger ran into the hall.

> "Bodhisattva!" he cried. "We have a problem."

> "Our problem?" Buddha asked.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零五章：雷音寺

## ①

  旅人们沿着灵山向上攀登。山坡上长满了松树、翠竹和鲜花。鸟儿歌唱，小动物从身边跑过。

  唐僧停下脚步，转向同伴们。

> "我想谢谢你们各位，"唐僧说，"是你们帮我到达了西天。无数次你们从妖怪手中救了我。没有你们，我走不到这里。"

## ②

  悟空笑了。

> "师父，您不必谢我们。我们互相帮助。您帮我向善。如今我要为我早年的恶行赎罪了。"

  悟净点了点头。

> "我也要为打碎天庭琉璃盏的事赎罪。"

> "我也要为在天庭惹的祸赎罪，"八戒补充道。他朝马的方向挥了挥手，"别忘了，那匹马可是一条真龙。"

## ③

> "他不小心把玉帝宫殿的雨水下错了地方。他也该赎罪。"

  悟净微笑了。

> "师父您看吧，我们都很感恩。"

## ④

  他们继续向上攀登，很快被云雾环绕。

  上方雷音寺闪耀着明亮的光芒。旅人来到北门，两位护法站在那里守卫。门内，雷音寺的塔楼和牌坊闪闪发光。

> "两位好，"唐僧向护法说，"我是唐僧，来佛祖这里求取真经。"

> "请进吧，"一位护法说。

## ⑤

  唐僧和同伴们来到了一座大殿。佛祖端坐在大殿尽头，身后站着众佛和菩萨。观音站在佛祖身旁，面带微笑。旅人们鞠躬行礼。

> "恭喜你们，"佛祖说，"你们远道而来，历经千难万险。你们做得很好。"

  悟空心中感慨万千，他抹去了眼中的泪水。

## ⑥

> "感谢佛祖，"唐僧说，"能踏上这段旅程是我的荣幸。"

  侍从给旅人们端来了饭菜。吃完饭后，一位护法把他们领进了一间充满灵光和仙雾的大厅。墙壁上排列着许多木箱。

## ⑦

> "太壮观了，"唐僧喃喃道。

> "真经就是写在这些经卷上的，"护法说。

  他挑出三部经卷，递给了唐僧。唐僧说不出话来，凝望着经卷。然后他接过经卷交给了悟净和八戒。两位仙人小心翼翼地包好经卷，放进了包袱。

## ⑧

  旅人们再次在佛祖面前行礼。

> "把真经带回大唐吧，"佛祖说。

> "又是长途跋涉，"八戒嘟囔着。

> "别抱怨了，八戒，"悟空低声说。

> "你少管我，"八戒回嘴。

> "你们两个别吵了，"悟净低声说。

## ⑨

  佛祖继续讲话。

> "经卷将教导那里的人民向善、彼此友善相处。但你们要好好保护经卷，它们极其珍贵。送到经卷之后，你们再回到这里来接受封号。"

## ⑩

> "佛祖您放一百个心，"悟空说，"我们用性命来保护经卷。"

  一位护法主动提出护送旅人回大唐。

> "谢谢您，"唐僧说。

> "我可抓牢了，"八戒说。

  护法念了一道咒语，便带着旅人们飞出了寺院。

## ⑪

  佛祖转向观音。

> "唐僧师徒做得很好。"

  观音点了点头。

> "特别是悟空一路学到了很多。他不再暴躁了。我相信他现在是个好佛徒了。"

## ⑫

  就在此时，一个信使跑进了大殿。

> "菩萨大人！"他喊道，"出了个问题。"

> "什么问题？"佛祖问道。

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Six: The Question

## ①

  Guanyin looked at the messenger in surprise.

> "What is the problem?" she asked.

> "It's about the Tang monk," said the messenger. "To become a Buddha, he needs to face a hundred challenges. I was just looking at the list of challenges he's faced. There are only ninety-nine challenges on the list. He must face one more challenge to become a Buddha."

## ②

> "We're moving so fast," said the Tang monk, smiling.

  The travelers were flying back east. The guard from the Thunderclap Monastery was using a spell to carry them.

> "I wish the whole journey had been this easy," said Bajie.

> "You couldn't, Master was still mortal before we reached the Western Paradise. He couldn't be carried then," said Wukong.

## ③

  Wukong looked to the horizon.

> "We'll reach the Tang Empire soon."

  Just then, a messenger caught up with them. The messenger whispered something in the guard's ear. The guard glanced quickly at the travelers, then he looked back at the messenger and nodded.

## ④

  Instead of continuing, the spell broke and the travelers fell from the sky. *Bam!* They slammed into the ground next to a wide river.

  Wukong stood up and saw the guard and messenger flying back west. The monkey shook his head.

> "What happened?"

  The Tang monk stood up and brushed mud from his robe.

> "Why did the guard drop us?"

## ⑤

> "I'll tell you why," said Bajie. "He's a villain. He thinks it's funny to drop people."

  The pig waved his fist at the guard, who was now far away.

  "Mild," Wukong turned slowly to the Tang monk.

> "I think I know why he dropped us, Master. You must face a hundred challenges in order to become a Buddha. He probably got to the Western Paradise before you'd faced all of them."

## ⑥

> "Oh no!" the monk trembled. "So other bad things must happen now?"

  Wukong nodded.

> "I hope there won't be too many more problems."

> "The first problem is crossing the river," said Wujing.

## ⑦

> "It looks familiar," said the monk. "We must have crossed it during the journey west."

  Suddenly a large form rose from the river. It was an enormous turtle.

> "Greetings," said the turtle. "Do you remember me?"

  The travelers all smiled.

> "Yes, we do," said the Tang monk. "You carried us over this river many years ago."

## ⑧

> "Yes," said the turtle. "And I will gladly carry you across again. Hop on to my back."

  The travelers climbed on and the turtle started across the river. Wujing and Bajie soon fell asleep while Wukong meditated. The Tang monk stayed awake too, sitting near the turtle's head.

## ⑨

> "Did you reach the Western Paradise?" asked the turtle.

> "Yes," said the Tang monk. "It is a wonderful place. We are now returning to the east so I can deliver the true scriptures."

> "Good," said the turtle. "Did you ask Buddha when I would be reborn as a human?"

## ⑩

  The monk bit his lip. He had forgotten to ask the turtle's question.

> "You are not answering," said the turtle.

> "I'm sorry," said the monk. "I..."

## ⑪

  The turtle suddenly dived under the water. It dumped everyone off his back. Wukong's eyes flew open as he hit the cold water. He leaped into the air. Bajie, Wujing, and the horse quickly flew across the river. But the Tang monk was flailing furiously in the rushing water.

> "Help!" yelped the monk.

## ⑫

  Wukong cast a spell and lifted the monk and the bow from the river. When everyone was on dry land, the monkey turned the bag upside down. Water poured out, followed by the scrolls. They were soaked.

> "The true scriptures!" cried the Tang monk. "They are wet!"

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零六章：一问

## ①

  观音惊讶地看着信使。

> "出了什么问题？"她问道。

> "是关于唐僧的事，"信使说，"要成为佛，他必须经历百难。我刚才查了他经历的劫难清单。清单上只有九十九难。他还必须再经历一难才能成佛。"

## ②

> "我们飞得好快啊，"唐僧微笑着说。

  旅人们正飞回东土。雷音寺的护法施法术载着他们。

> "要是整段旅程都这么轻松就好了，"八戒说。

> "那可不行。没到西天之前师父还是凡胎，不能这样带着他飞的，"悟空说。

## ③

  悟空望向远方。

> "我们马上就到东土大唐了。"

  就在此时，一个信使追上了他们。信使在护法耳边低语了几句。护法快速瞥了一眼旅人们，又看向信使，点了点头。

## ④

  护法停了法术，旅人们从天上掉了下来。*砰！*他们摔在一条宽阔的河边。

  悟空站起来，看到护法和信使正往西天方向飞去。猴子摇了摇头。

> "怎么回事？"

  唐僧站起来，抖掉了袈裟上的泥土。

> "护法为什么把我们丢下来？"

## ⑤

> "我来告诉你为什么，"八戒说，"他是个坏蛋。他觉得把人从天上丢下来很好玩。"

  八戒朝已经飞远的护法的方向挥了挥拳头。

  悟空慢慢转向唐僧。

> "师父，我想我知道他为什么把我们扔下来了。要成佛您得历经百难。大概是护法发现您还差一难没经历。"

## ⑥

> "哎呀！"唐僧浑身发抖，"难道还要再出什么事吗？"

  悟空点了点头。

> "希望别再出太多问题了。"

> "第一个问题就是过河，"悟净说。

## ⑦

> "这河看起来很眼熟，"唐僧说，"我们西行的路上一定走过这里。"

  突然，河面上升起了一个巨大的身影。是一只巨大的乌龟。

> "诸位好，"乌龟说，"还记得我吗？"

  旅人们都笑了。

> "当然记得，"唐僧说，"多年前你驮我们过了这条河。"

## ⑧

> "不错，"乌龟说，"这次我还乐意载你们过去。请上背上来。"

  旅人们爬上龟背，乌龟开始过河。悟净和八戒很快就睡着了，悟空在一旁打坐。唐僧也醒着，坐在乌龟的头旁边。

## ⑨

> "你们到了西天吗？"乌龟问道。

> "到了，"唐僧说，"那是一个神奇的地方。我们现在回东土，我要把真经带回去。"

> "那太好了，"乌龟说，"你帮我问佛祖我没有？我什么时候才能再投胎做人？"

## ⑩

  唐僧咬了咬嘴唇。他已经忘了帮乌龟问了。

> "您怎么不回答？"乌龟说。

> "对不起，"唐僧说，"我……"

## ⑪

  乌龟突然往水下一沉，把背上的所有人都翻了下水。悟空被冷水一激，立刻睁开了眼睛。他纵身飞上了空中。八戒、悟净和白龙马都快速飞过了河。但是唐僧在湍急的河水中拼命挣扎。

> "救命！"唐僧叫道。

## ⑫

  悟空施法将唐僧和经包从河中捞起。众人上了岸，猴子把包袱倒了个底朝天。水哗啦啦流了出来，紧跟着涌出的是经卷。全都被泡透了。

> "真经！"唐僧叫了起来，"全都泡湿了！"

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Seven: Nothing Is Perfect

## ①

  The travelers laid the silk scrolls on some rocks.

> "The sun will dry them out," said Wukong.

  The Tang monk moaned.

> "What if they're ruined?"

  He sat down and put his head in his hand.

> "I wish I'd remembered to ask Buddha the turtle's question."

## ②

  Bajie snorted.

> "Buddha has already forgiven me, and I forgot to turn the turtle's question. That turtle had no right to dump us in the water."

> "Dumping us in the water was rude," Wujing agreed.

  Bajie sighed.

> "The journey back east has been just as difficult as the journey west."

## ③

> "Hello!" came quite a voice.

  The travelers turned and saw a man hurrying toward them.

> "Chen!" said the Tang monk.

  He grasped the man's hands.

> "It's good to see you again."

> "It's good to see all of you," Chen smiled. "Did you reach the Western Paradise?"

## ④

> "Yes," said the Tang monk. "It was magnificent. The land is filled with beauty."

  Chen noticed the scrolls lying on the rocks and his eyes went wide.

> "Are those the true scriptures?" he whispered.

> "Yes," said the monk. "But as you can see, they got wet. A giant turtle dumped us in the river," added Bajie with a sigh.

## ⑤

> "Please come with me," said Chen. "You can dry the true scriptures by my fire. Everyone in the village would be excited to see the travelers who met Buddha."

  Wujing started gathering the wet scriptures.

> "I'll help you," said Bajie.

  The pig grabbed a scroll and pulled — but it was stuck to a rock.

## ⑥

  *Riiip!* The corner of the scroll tore off. The Tang monk gasped.

> "Oh no!"

  Bajie stared at the torn scroll. Wukong smiled.

> "Don't worry, Master."

  The monkey gently picked the rest of the scroll off the rock.

## ⑦

> "This is all I find... But it's ripped!" cried Bajie. He hung his head.

> "Tell me something, Master," said Wukong. "Are you perfect?"

  The monk looked at Wukong, confused.

> "Of course not."

> "Am I perfect?" asked the monkey.

  The Tang monk shook his head.

> "How about Bajie?"

## ⑧

  Wukong smirked.

> "We all know he's not perfect."

  The pig snorted indignantly.

> "Nothing on earth or in heaven is perfect," said Wukong. "So why should the true scriptures be any different? They'll teach the people of the East how to be good and avoid suffering. They will also teach the people that nothing needs to be perfect."

## ⑨

  The travelers finished gathering the scrolls and followed Chen back to the village. People came out of their homes to see the travelers.

> "Welcome back!" called a woman.

> "It's wonderful to see you all again," shouted an old man.

  Soon a crowd was following the Tang monk and his companions to Chen's house. That evening the villagers held a big feast.

## ⑩

  Later that night, Wukong and the Tang monk sat talking.

> "We must leave soon," said the monk. "The villagers will want to see the true scriptures. They'll become jealous that we have them."

> "I agree," said Wukong. He remembered the priest who tried to kill the Tang monk and steal the robe.

## ⑪

> "Let's sneak away now while the villagers are asleep," said Wukong.

  Wukong woke up Bajie and Wujing. The group sneaked out of Chen's house and headed east. It was dark, but the light from the full moon lit up the road.

## ⑫

  Suddenly the guard from the Thunderclap Monastery appeared.

> "And there he goes," said the monk with relief. "I will receive my awards at last."

  The guard recited a summon. Once again the travelers flew toward the east.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零七章：无一是完美

## ①

  旅人们把丝绸经卷铺在几块石头上。

> "太阳会把它们晒干的，"悟空说。

  唐僧唉声叹气。

> "万一毁了怎么办？"

  他坐下来，双手抱头。

> "我当时怎么就忘了帮乌龟问佛祖那句话呢。"

## ②

  八戒哼了一声。

> "佛祖已经宽恕我了，我忘了帮乌龟问那个问题。那只乌龟也没资格把我们翻到水里。"

> "把我们翻进水里也太粗鲁了，"悟净赞同地说。

  八戒叹了口气。

> "这东归之路跟西行一样艰难。"

## ③

> "大家好啊！"传来一声洪亮的招呼。

  旅人们转身，看见一个人朝他们快步走来。

> "是陈澄！"唐僧说。

  他握住那人的手。

> "又见面了，真好。"

> "看到你们真好啊，"陈澄微笑着，"你们到了西天吗？"

## ④

> "到了，"唐僧说，"那里太壮观了。大地充满美丽。"

  陈澄注意到岩石上铺着的经卷，眼珠子都瞪大了。

> "那些就是真经吗？"他轻声问道。

> "是的，"唐僧说，"但你看，全泡湿了。一只大乌龟把我们翻到了河里，"八戒叹着气说。

## ⑤

> "请到我家吧，"陈澄说，"你们可以在我家炉火边烘干经卷。全村人都想见见过佛祖的取经人呢。"

  悟净开始收拾湿了的经卷。

> "我来帮你，"八戒说。

  八戒抓住一卷用力一拉——可是经卷粘在了石头上。

## ⑥

  *嘶啦！*经卷的一角被撕了下来。唐僧倒抽一口冷气。

> "哎呀！"

  八戒盯着被撕坏的经卷。悟空微微笑了。

> "师父，不用担心。"

  猴子小心翼翼地把经卷剩余的部分从石头上揭了下来。

## ⑦

> "这经卷……可是破了呀！"八戒哭丧着脸低下了头。

> "我问你一件事，师父，"悟空说，"您完美吗？"

  唐僧一脸困惑地看着悟空。

> "当然不完美。"

> "那我完美吗？"猴子问道。

  唐僧摇了摇头。

> "那八戒呢？"

## ⑧

  悟空咧嘴一笑。

> "咱们都知道他可不完美。"

  八戒气哼哼地哼了一声。

> "天上人间没有一样东西是完美的，"悟空说，"那真经为啥非得完美呢？它们会教导东土的人民向善、远离苦难。它们也会教导人们——不必事事完美。"

## ⑨

  旅人们收拾好经卷，跟着陈澄回了村子。村民们纷纷走出家门来看望取经人。

> "欢迎回来！"一个女人喊道。

> "太好了，又见到你们了！"一个老汉高声说。

  不一会儿，一大群人跟着唐僧师徒走向陈澄家。那天晚上，村民们举办了盛大的宴会。

## ⑩

  那天夜里，悟空和唐僧坐着聊天。

> "我们得快些走了，"唐僧说，"村民们都想来看真经。他们会因为我们拥有经卷而嫉妒的。"

> "我也这么认为，"悟空说。他想起了那个企图谋杀唐僧、偷走锦襕袈裟的和尚。

## ⑪

> "趁村民们睡着了，我们悄悄走吧，"悟空说。

  悟空叫醒了八戒和悟净。一行人悄悄溜出了陈澄的家，朝东方走去。夜很黑，但皎洁的月光照亮了前方的道路。

## ⑫

  突然，雷音寺的护法出现了。

> "走吧，"唐僧松了一口气，"我最终可以得到封号了。"

  护法念了一道咒语。旅人们再次飞向了东土。

# Journey to the West · Chapter One Hundred and Eight: Rewards

## ①

  The travelers flew through the sky over the Tang Empire. Tears of happiness rolled down the Tang monk's cheeks.

> "I see the Emperor's palace," said the monk.

  "I will wait here while you all deliver the true scriptures," said the guard.

  The Tang monk and his companions went down to earth and entered the palace.

## ②

  The Emperor's eyes lit up.

> "My brother!"

  He embraced the monk.

> "For many years I wondered if I'd ever see you again. Did you get the true scriptures?"

> "Yes," said the monk. "But please forgive me. The journey took much longer than I expected."

> "There's no need to apologize," said the Emperor.

## ③

  Then he noticed the monk's companions.

> "Who are they?"

  Sun Wukong stepped forward.

> "I am Sun Wukong, the Monkey King. I once defeated Heaven's entire army."

> "And I am Zhu Bajie," said the pig.

> "My name is Sha Wujing," said the purple spirit.

## ④

> "They protected me during the journey," the monk explained. "I couldn't have reached the Western Paradise without them."

  The Emperor bowed to Wukong and the others.

> "You don't need a bow," the monkey laughed. "We were happy to help."

  "Well, Wujing and I were," Bajie complained with a snort. "There were a lot of battles that night."

## ⑤

  The pig snorted. The Emperor asked the monk many questions about the journey. He listened in amazement to the monk's stories.

> "I will build a magnificent pagoda," the Emperor declared. "The true scriptures will be kept safe inside it."

  He put his hand on the monk's shoulder.

> "You will always be remembered as the brave monk who traveled to the West. Because of you, our people won't have to suffer anymore."

## ⑥

  After the feast was eaten, the Emperor asked the monk to read from the scriptures. The Tang monk smiled.

> "I would be happy to read from them."

## ⑦

  The monk sat on a platform where the scriptures had been placed in baskets. He unrolled a scroll. Suddenly, light filled the room. The Tang monk and his companions rose into the sky.

> "We should return to the Thunderclap Monastery," said the guard. "Buddha is waiting for you."

> "Yes, let's go," said the monk.

## ⑧

  The travelers were soon bowing before Buddha again. Other Buddhas and bodhisattvas stood behind him. Buddha addressed the horse first.

> "You carried the Tang monk on the journey and earned forgiveness for your crimes. You will now be a golden dragon in heaven."

  Light flashed as a large golden dragon soared into the sky.

## ⑨

> "Sha Wujing," said Buddha. "You too have earned forgiveness for your past crimes. You will now be a golden deity."

  Wujing's body turned gold. The spirit bowed.

> "Thank you, Buddha."

> "You have earned forgiveness, Bajie," said Buddha. "You will be an altar cleaner, an important deity who looks after Buddhist altars."

> "Thank you, Buddha," Bajie said.

## ⑩

  Buddha next turned to the Tang monk.

> "Because of you, the people in the East will never have to suffer again. You made a journey that no other person could make. You are now a Buddha."

  Light glowed around the monk, who bowed before Buddha.

> "Thank you, Buddha," said the monk.

## ⑪

  Finally Buddha turned to the monkey.

> "And you, Wukong," He began. "Your crimes long ago were terrible. But since then you have used your tremendous powers to do good deeds. You too are now a Buddha."

  Wukong bowed.

> "Thank you, Buddha."

## ⑫

  *Hey!* The monkey suddenly noticed that his head felt different. The headband was gone. Buddha smiled.

> "You don't need it anymore."

  Filled with joy, Wukong and the Tang monk joined the other Buddhas and bodhisattvas in the West. They have been in the Western Paradise ever since.

---

# 🇨🇳 第一百零八章：封号

## ①

  旅人们飞越大唐帝国的上空，唐僧激动得热泪盈眶。

> "我看到皇帝的宫殿了，"唐僧说。

> "我在这里等着，你们去送真经吧，"护法说。

  唐僧和徒伴们降落到地面，走进了皇宫。

## ②

  皇帝的双眼亮了起来。

> "御弟！"

  他拥抱了唐僧。

> "这么多年了，我一直在想还能不能再见到你。你取到真经了吗？"

> "取到了，"唐僧说，"但请陛下原谅我。这趟旅程比我预想的长了很多。"

> "不必道歉，"皇帝说。

## ③

  然后他注意到了唐僧身边的三位徒伴。

> "他们是谁？"

  孙悟空走上前来。

> "我是孙悟空，齐天大圣。我当年曾打败天庭千军万马。"

> "我是猪八戒。"八戒说。

> "我叫沙悟净。"悟净说。

## ④

> "这一路上他们保护了我，"唐僧解释道，"没有他们，我到不了西天。"

  皇帝向悟空等人鞠躬。

> "陛下不必行此大礼，"猴子笑道，"能帮上忙，我们很高兴。"

> "哼，悟净和我是很高兴。"八戒嘟囔了一声，"可那些打打杀杀的差事，我可吃了不少苦。"

## ⑤

  八戒哼了一声。皇帝问了唐僧许多关于旅途的问题，听他讲述一路上的故事，惊叹不已。

> "我要修建一座宏伟的宝塔，"皇帝宣布道，"真经将安放在塔中保存。"

  他把手搭在唐僧肩上。

> "你将永远被人们铭记，因为你是一位前往西方取经的英勇僧人。因为有您，我们的百姓再也不必受苦了。"

## ⑥

  盛宴之后，皇帝请唐僧诵读经书。唐僧微笑。

> "我愿意为大家诵读。"

## ⑦

  唐僧坐在讲台上，面前是经卷筐。他展开了一卷经书。突然，光芒充满了整间大殿。唐僧和他的徒伴们升上了天空。

> "我们应该回雷音寺了，"护法说，"佛祖在等着你们受封。"

> "好，走吧，"唐僧说。

## ⑧

  唐僧师徒又跪拜在了佛祖面前。佛祖身后站着众佛和菩萨。佛祖先对白龙马说道：

> "你一路上驮着唐僧取经，为你的罪过赎了罪。如今你将为天庭的一条金龙。"

  金光一闪，一条巨大的金龙飞上了天空。

## ⑨

> "沙悟净，"佛祖说，"你也为过去的罪过赎了罪。你将为天庭的南无八宝金身罗汉菩萨。"

  悟净的全身变得金光闪闪。他行了一个大礼。

> "感谢佛祖。"

> "猪八戒，你也赎了罪，"佛祖说，"你将为净坛使者，负责打扫和守护佛前供品。"

> "感谢佛祖。"八戒说。

## ⑩

  佛祖接下来转向唐僧。

> "因为有您，东土百姓再也不必受苦了。您走了一段无人能及的旅程。您现在是旃檀功德佛。"

  金光照亮了唐僧。他在佛祖面前行礼。

> "感谢佛祖。"唐僧说。

## ⑪

  最后佛祖转向了猴子。

> "悟空，"佛祖说，"你当年的罪行极为严重。但从此之后你用你莫大的法力做了无数善事。你现在是斗战胜佛。"

  悟空行了一个大礼。

> "感谢佛祖。"

## ⑫

  *咦！*猴子突然感觉到头上不一样了。头上的紧箍圈不见了。佛祖微笑了。

> "你不再需要它了。"

  满怀着喜悦，悟空和唐僧与其他佛和菩萨一起留在了西天。从此以后，他们便一直在西天极乐世界。
